There is established a police department for the town, to be composed of a
chief of police and such number of subordinate police officers of such rank as
the town council shall, from time to time, determine. (1987 Code § 2.24.010)
5-1-2: MAYOR TO HEAD DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Mayor To Superintend: The mayor shall be the head of the police
department and shall superintend and direct the police generally and take such
measures as he may deem expedient for the preservation of the peace and good
order and the enforcing of the laws and ordinances in the town.
   B.   Special Police Officers: The mayor shall have power to appoint special
police officers on occasions when an increase in the department is required for
the peace and good order of the town. (1987 Code § 2.24.020)
5-1-3: CHIEF OF POLICE:
The police chief shall be the chief of the acting police and all police
officers shall be in subordination to him, except in cases otherwise provided
for by ordinance. It shall be his duty to cause the public peace to be
preserved and to see that all laws and ordinances are enforced and to perform
such other duties as the council may require of him or that he is required to
do by the town ordinances. (1987 Code § 2.24.030)
5-1-4: OFFICERS:
   A.   Qualifications; Oath: Every person appointed to the office of police
officer shall be at the time of his appointment a citizen of the United States
and, previous to exercising any function of his office, shall take and
subscribe an oath or affirmation that he will faithfully and impartially
discharge the duties of his office according to the best of his knowledge and
ability. (1987 Code § 2.24.040)
   B.   Duties: It shall be the duty of the police officers to aid and assist
the police chief in the execution of his duties. They shall have power and
authority in the town to serve and execute warrants and other processes for the
apprehension and commitment of persons charged with or held for examination or
trial or taken in execution for the commission of any crime or misdemeanor or
violation of any law or ordinance of the town. They shall be vested with and
have all the power and authority conferred upon police officers pursuant to the
laws of the state. (1987 Code § 2.24.050)
   C.   Failure To Perform: Any police officer who neglects or refuses to
perform any duty required of him by the ordinances of the town, or who in the
discharge of his official duties, is guilty of any fraud, extortion,
oppression, partiality, or wilful wrong or injustice, shall be punished
according to the provisions set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1987 Code § 2.24.060)
5-1-5: RECORD KEEPING:
   A.   Police Records: The chief of police shall be and is hereby designated
as "custodian", as defined in Wyoming Statutes section 16-4-201, of all police
records except personnel records, and shall be charged with the keeping of the
records according to the standards which may be set for by the Wyoming state
archives. Such standards shall include, but are not limited to, keeping the
records in a secured, fire safe, water safe and climate controlled environment
and for the storage of historical records in acid free containers.
   B.   Personnel Records: The town clerk, as "official custodian" shall
maintain all personnel records for all employees of the town, including police
personnel, according to the standards set by the Wyoming state archives. (Ord.
14-00, 11-16-2000)
5-1-6: INTERFERING WITH POLICE:
Whoever in the town resists any police officer or member of the police
department in the discharge of his duties or who in any way interferes with or
hinders or prevents him from discharging his duties, and whoever in any manner
assists any person to escape or attempt to escape from custody, or rescues or
attempts to rescue any person in custody of a police officer, shall be punished
according to the provisions set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code. (1987 Code § 2.24.070)
CHAPTER 2
GENERAL OFFENSES
SECTION:
5-2-1: Penalty
5-2-2: Accessory Before The Fact
5-2-3: Attempt To Commit An Offense
5-2-4: Solicitation
5-2-5: Conspiracy
5-2-1: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any section of this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor
and upon conviction thereof shall be punished according to the penalty
provisions prescribed for the underlying offense. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2-2: ACCESSORY BEFORE THE FACT:
   A.   A person who knowingly aids or abets in the commission of an offense,
or who counsels, encourages, hires, commands or procures an offense to be
committed, is an accessory before the fact.
   B.   An accessory before the fact:
      1.   May be indicted, informed against, tried and convicted as if he were
a principal;
      2.   May be indicted, informed against, tried and convicted either before
or after and whether or not the principal offender is indicted, informed
against, tried or convicted; and
      3.   Upon conviction, is subject to the same punishment and penalties as
are prescribed by law for the punishment of the principal. (Ord. 2010-11, 11-4-
2010)
5-2-3: ATTEMPT TO COMMIT AN OFFENSE:
   A.   A person is guilty of an attempt to commit a crime if:
      1.   With the intent to commit the crime, he does any act which is a
substantial step towards commission of the crime. A "substantial step" is
conduct which is strongly corroborative of the firmness of the person's
intention to complete the commission of the crime; or
      2.   He or she intentionally engages in conduct which would constitute
the crime had the attendant circumstances been as the person believes them to
be.
   B.   A person is not liable under this section if, under circumstances
manifesting a voluntary and complete renunciation of his criminal intention, he
avoided the commission of the crime attempted by abandoning his criminal
effort. Within the meaning of this subsection, renunciation of criminal purpose
is not voluntary if it is motivated, in whole or in part, by circumstances, not
present or apparent at the inception of the person's course of conduct, which
increase the probability of detection or apprehension or which make more
difficult the accomplishment of the criminal intention. Renunciation is not
complete if it is motivated by a decision to postpone the criminal conduct
until a more advantageous time or to transfer the criminal effort to another
but similar objective or victim. (Ord. 2010-11, 11-4-2010)
5-2-4: SOLICITATION:
   A.   A person is guilty of solicitation to commit a crime if, with intent
that a crime be committed, he or she commands, encourages or facilitates the
commission of that crime under circumstances strongly corroborative of the
intention that the crime be committed but the solicited crime is not attempted
or committed.
   B.   A person is not liable under this section if, after soliciting another
person to commit a crime, he or she persuaded the other person not to do so or
otherwise prevented the commission of the crime, under circumstances
manifesting a voluntary and complete renunciation of his criminal intention.
(Ord. 2010-11, 11-4-2010)
5-2-5: CONSPIRACY:
   A.   A person is guilty of conspiracy to commit a crime if he or she agrees
with one or more persons that they or one or more of them will commit a crime
and one or more of them does an overt act to effect the objective of the
agreement.
   B.   A person is not liable under this section if after conspiring he or she
withdraws from the conspiracy and thwarts its success under circumstances
manifesting voluntary and complete renunciation of his criminal intention.
   C.   A conspiracy may be prosecuted in the town if the agreement was entered
into or any act evidencing the conspiracy or furthering the purpose took place.
(Ord. 2010-11, 11-4-2010)
ARTICLE A. ALCOHOL
SECTION:
5-2A-1: Furnishing To Minors
5-2A-2: Endangering Welfare Of A Minor
5-2A-3: Purchase And Possession By Minors
5-2A-4: Possession In Vehicle With Intent To Distribute To Minor
5-2A-5: Public Impairment And/Or Intoxication
5-2A-6: Open Containers In Vehicles
5-2A-7: Alcohol On Public Property
5-2A-8: Penalty
5-2A-1: FURNISHING TO MINORS:
   A.   Prohibited: Any person who sells, furnishes, gives or causes to be
sold, furnished or given away any alcoholic liquor or malt beverage to any
person under the age of twenty one (21) years, who is not his legal ward,
medical patient or member of his own immediate family, is guilty of a class A
misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code.
   B.   Exception: This section does not apply to sales by the commission or a
wholesaler to a licensee under this title. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2A-2: ENDANGERING WELFARE OF A MINOR:
   A.   Offense Described: A person who is not the parent or guardian of the
minor, commits the offense of endangering the welfare of a minor if the person
knowingly allows or permits a person under twenty one (21) years of age to:
      1.   Enter or remain in a place under the person's control in which
unlawful activities involving controlled substances or alcohol are maintained
or conducted.
      2.   Consume alcohol or controlled substances in violation of the law in
a place under the person's control.
   B.   In Control Defined: A person is considered to be "in control" of a
place or property when that person is the owner, renter, tenant, keeper,
caretaker or in fact has control over the persons allowed on the premises.
(Ord. 1-95, 4-20-1995)
   C.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class A misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2A-3: PURCHASE AND POSSESSION BY MINORS:
   A.   Prohibited: No person under the age of twenty one (21) years shall buy,
sell, drink, consume, possess, or solicit the sale or purchase of alcoholic
liquor or malt beverage, or be drunk or under the influence of alcoholic liquor
or malt beverage or a controlled substance in the town. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-
2013)
   B.   Exception: This subsection does not apply to possession and/or
consumption of alcoholic or malt beverages by a person under the age of twenty
one (21) years under the following conditions:
      1.   When making a delivery of alcoholic or malt beverages pursuant to
his employment;
      2.   When the consumption has occurred in the physical presence of, and
with consent of, the parent or legal guardian;
      3.   When licensed under this title; or
      4.   When serving alcoholic or malt beverages pursuant to his employment
in a restaurant which holds a license to serve alcoholic or malt beverages, if
the person is at least eighteen (18) years of age. (Ord. 3-97, 6-19-1997)
   C.   False Identification: No person under the age of twenty one (21) years
shall attempt in any manner to purchase alcoholic or malt beverages, nor
falsify any identification nor use any false identification or identification
of another in order to obtain alcoholic or malt beverages.
   D.   Prima Facie Evidence Of Age And Identity: A motor vehicle driver's
license, a registration certificate issued under the federal selective service
act, an identification card issued to a member of the armed forces or an
identification card issued by the department of revenue is prima facie evidence
of the age and identity of a person. Proof that a licensee or his employee or
agent demanded, was shown and acted in reasonable reliance upon the information
contained in any one of the above documents as identification is a defense to
any criminal prosecution or action for the suspension or revocation of a
license.
   E.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2A-4: POSSESSION IN VEHICLE WITH INTENT TO DISTRIBUTE TO MINOR:
   A.   Prohibited: No person who is at least twenty one (21) years of age
shall transport, or have in his possession or control, any alcoholic liquor or
malt beverage, with the intent of furnishing the same to any person under the
age of twenty one (21) years, while operating or occupying a motor vehicle.
(1987 Code § 9.04.030)
   B.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class A misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2A-5: PUBLIC IMPAIRMENT AND/OR INTOXICATION:
   A.   No person who is or remains in any public place or public gathering,
shall drink or otherwise consume any intoxicating liquor, malt liquor,
intoxicating substance, intoxicating compound(s) or illegal controlled
substances of any kind, or any inhale glue, paint or other intoxicating
substance(s).
   B.   No person who is or remains in any public place or public gathering,
shall be impaired, drunk, intoxicated or under the influence from drinking or
consuming intoxicating liquor, intoxicating malt liquor, intoxicating substance
(s) or intoxicating compound(s), illegal controlled substances of any kind, nor
be intoxicated from inhaling inhale glue, paint or other intoxicating substance
(s) so used for the purpose of becoming intoxicated; nor be intoxicated from
the overuse and/or misuse of any legally prescribed controlled substance(s).
   C.   A person in violation of this section is guilty of a class A
misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2016-07, 7-7-2016)
5-2A-6: OPEN CONTAINERS IN VEHICLES:
   A.   Definition: For the purposes of this section, an "open container" is
any glass, cup, bottle, can or other receptacle used for drinking which is not
sealed or capped.
   B.   Consumption Or Possession Prohibited: It is unlawful to consume or to
possess alcoholic or malt beverages in an open container while operating a
motor vehicle.
   C.   Open Container Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to consume or
to carry in an open container any alcoholic or malt beverage while upon a
public street, sidewalk, curb or other public area, except areas designated by
the town council for the consumption of such beverages, and areas licensed by a
twenty four (24) hour malt beverage or catering permit in accordance with
section
3-2-3-12 of this code. (1987 Code § 9.04.050)
   D.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2A-7: ALCOHOL ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
No person shall possess an open container or keg of alcoholic liquor or malt
beverage, nor imbibe, drink, consume, distribute, give, furnish, sell or cause
to be sold, given or distributed any alcoholic liquor or malt beverage on any
town property or public place without a valid permit or license granted
pursuant to and within the scope of title 3, chapter 2 of this code. (Ord.
2012-04, 5-3-2012)
5-2A-8: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE B. OFFENSES BY OR AGAINST PUBLIC OFFICERS AND GOVERNMENT
SECTION:
5-2B-1: Impersonating An Officer
5-2B-2: Interference With Town Officials
5-2B-3: Duty To Assist An Officer
5-2B-4: Interference With Fire Alarm System
5-2B-5: Interference With Fire Hydrants Or Water Mains
5-2B-6: Failure To Appear In Court
5-2B-7: Failure To Pay
5-2B-8: Penalty
5-2B-1: IMPERSONATING AN OFFICER:
It is unlawful to impersonate any law enforcement officer in the town. (1987
Code § 9.08.010)
5-2B-2: INTERFERENCE WITH TOWN OFFICIALS:
No person in the town shall resist any town officers in the discharge of their
duties, or in any way interfere with or hinder or prevent them from discharging
their duties. (1987 Code § 9.08.020)
5-2B-3: DUTY TO ASSIST AN OFFICER:
It shall be the duty of all persons within the town, when called upon by any
police officer, to promptly aid and assist him in the execution of his duties.
(1987 Code § 9.08.030)
5-2B-4: INTERFERENCE WITH FIRE ALARM SYSTEM:
No person shall interfere with any part of the fire alarm system unless so
authorized by the fire chief. (1987 Code § 9.08.040)
5-2B-5: INTERFERENCE WITH FIRE HYDRANTS OR WATER MAINS:
No person shall shut off or turn on or interfere in any way with any fire
hydrant, valve or water main in the town unless so authorized by the governing
body. (1987 Code § 9.08.050)
5-2B-6: FAILURE TO APPEAR IN COURT:
   A.   Any person who fails to appear in response to any summons, citation,
information or subpoena served on such person shall be guilty of a violation of
this section.
   B.   Upon a finding by the court that a person has failed to appear in
response to a summons, personally signed citation, information or subpoena
served on such person, the court may issue a warrant for the arrest of said
person. (Ord. 8-2004, 9-16-2004)
5-2B-7: FAILURE TO PAY:
   A.   Guilty Of Violation: Any person who fails to pay any fines, costs,
fees, restitution or other money ordered to be paid by the municipal court of
the town of Lyman in the time and manner ordered shall be guilty of a violation
of this article.
   B.   Issuance Of Summons, Citation Or Warrant: Upon a finding by the court
that a person has failed to pay as directed by the court in a valid order, the
court may issue a summons commanding the appearance of that person, order law
enforcement officers of the town of Lyman to issue a citation to that person,
or issue a warrant for the arrest of that person. (Ord. 2007-02, 2-15-2007)
   C.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2B-8: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE C. OFFENSES AGAINST THE PERSON
SECTION:
5-2C-1: Assault
5-2C-2: Assault And Battery
5-2C-3: Dangerous Airtight Containers
5-2C-4: Domestic Abuse
5-2C-5: Penalty
5-2C-1: ASSAULT:
Whoever, having the present ability to do so, unlawfully attempts to commit a
violent injury on the person of another, is guilty of assault. (1987 Code §
9.12.010)
5-2C-2: ASSAULT AND BATTERY:
   A.   A person is guilty of battery if that person intentionally, knowingly
or recklessly causes bodily injury to another person by use of physical force.
Battery constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code.
   B.   A person is guilty of unlawful contact if that person touches another
person in a rude, insolent or angry manner without intentionally using
sufficient physical force to cause bodily injury to another. Unlawful contact
constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2C-3: DANGEROUS AIRTIGHT CONTAINERS:
It is unlawful for any person to leave or permit to remain outside of any
dwelling, building or other structure, or within any unoccupied or abandoned
building, dwelling or other structure under his control, in a place accessible
to children, any abandoned, unattended or discarded icebox, refrigerator or
other container which has an airtight door or lid, snap lock or other locking
device which may not be released from the inside, without first removing said
door or lid, snap lock or other locking device from the icebox, refrigerator or
container. A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2C-4: DOMESTIC ABUSE:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    ADULT: A person who is sixteen (16) years of age or older or legally
married.
   BODILY INJURY: Physical pain, injury, illness or any impairment of physical
condition.
   DOMESTIC ABUSE: Physical abuse, threats of physical abuse or acts which
unreasonably restrain the personal liberty of any household member by any other
household member.
   DOMESTIC DISPUTE: Any verbal or physical argument or confrontation between
household members.
   HOUSEHOLD MEMBER:
      1.   Persons married to each other;
      2.   Persons living with each other as if married;
      3.   Persons formerly married to each other;
      4.   Persons formerly living together as if married;
      5.   Parents and their adult children;
      6.   Other adults sharing common living quarters; and
      7.   Persons who are the parents of a child but who are not living with
each other.
   PHYSICAL ABUSE: Touching another in a rude, insolent or angry manner, or
attempting or threatening to cause bodily injury to another while having the
present ability to do so.
   B.   Prohibited: Any person who inflicts or causes physical abuse of a
household member during a domestic dispute is guilty of a crime. (Ord. 1-2002,
3-21-2002)
5-2C-5: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE D. OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC DECENCY
SECTION:
5-2D-1: Gambling
5-2D-2: Indecent Behavior
5-2D-3: Public Nudity
5-2D-4: Prostitution
5-2D-5: Voyeurism
5-2D-6: Marijuana
5-2D-7: Hypnotics And Narcotics
5-2D-8: Drug Paraphernalia
5-2D-9: Lewd And Lascivious Behavior
5-2D-10: Penalty
5-2D-1: GAMBLING:
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall play, deal, carry on or conduct any game of
chance for remuneration whatsoever or any plan, scheme or device for money,
checks, credits, goods, chattels or anything of value by means of cards, dice,
wheels, slot machines, pinball machines, vending devices, tops, punchboards,
lotteries, raffles or any contrivance, means, device or machine of any
denomination or name whatsoever within the town unless said game is expressly
authorized by Wyoming law. (Ord. 2014-04, 11-20-2014)
   B.   Allowing: No person shall knowingly permit subsection A of this section
to be violated in or upon the premises owned, managed, or controlled by him.
(1987 Code § 9.16.020)
   C.   Confiscation Of Devices: It shall be the duty of the chief of police to
seize any game, device, cards, tools and implements or other articles or things
designed for the purpose of gambling, employed or used by or in the possession
of parties arrested for gambling, and, upon conviction of the parties so
arrested and upon order of the judge, to confiscate and destroy them. (1987
Code § 9.16.030)
   D.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2D-2: INDECENT BEHAVIOR:
No person shall appear in any public place within the town in a state of nudity
or indecent dress, or make any indecent exposure of his or her person, or be
guilty of any lewd or indecent behavior, or exhibit, sell or offer to sell any
obscene books or materials, or perform any indecent, immoral or lewd act. (1987
Code § 9.16.040)
5-2D-3: PUBLIC NUDITY:
It is unlawful for any person to appear in a state of nudity in any public
place. For the purposes of this section, "nudity" means the showing of the
human male or female genitals or pubic area or female breasts with less than a
fully opaque covering. (1987 Code § 9.16.050)
5-2D-4: PROSTITUTION:
   A.   House Of Prostitution: No person shall keep, set up, maintain or
operate any place, structure, building or conveyance for the purpose of
prostitution, or with knowledge or reasonable cause to know that the same is or
is to be used for such purpose, or receive or offer to agree to receive any
person in any place, structure, building or conveyance for the purpose of
prostitution or permit any person to remain therein for such purpose.
   B.   Transport: No person shall direct, take, transport or offer or agree to
take or transport any person to any place, structure or building or to any
other person with knowledge or reasonable cause to know that the purpose of
such directing, taking or transporting is prostitution.
   C.   Reside, Enter Or Remain: No person shall reside in, enter or remain in
any place, structure or building, or enter or remain in any conveyance for the
purpose of prostitution.
   D.   Engage In Or Solicit Prostitution: No person shall engage in or solicit
prostitution or aid or abet prostitution, by solicitation or by any means
whatsoever. (1987 Code § 9.16.060)
5-2D-5: VOYEURISM:
No person shall, without consent of the person being viewed, look, peer or peep
into any window, restroom, bath, shower, dressing or fitting room, tanning
booth and/or any other enclosed area where the person viewed has a reasonable
expectation of privacy. The misdemeanor of voyeurism includes peering or
peeping by means of electronic, video, mechanical, physical means and/or any
method of recording and/or transmission of images. Voyeurism is a class A
misdemeanor pursuant to subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2016-10, 10-20-2016)
5-2D-6: MARIJUANA:
Any person who knowingly or intentionally uses or is under the influence of
marijuana within the corporate limits of the town is guilty of a misdemeanor.
(1987 Code § 9.16.080)
5-2D-7: HYPNOTICS AND NARCOTICS:
   A.   Hypnotics:
      1.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person, except as provided in
subsection A2 of this section, to possess, transport, sell, manufacture,
compound, furnish, administer or give away any hypnotic drug, including, but
not limited to, the following:
         a.   Acetyluria derivatives, lysergic acid, "LSD" (lysergic acid
diethylamide) and "DMT" (N-N-dimethyltryptamine), including their salts and
derivatives, or any compounds, mixtures or preparations which are chemically
identical with such substances.
         b.   Barbituric acid or its derivatives, chloral, paraldehyde,
sulfomethane derivatives, amphetamine or its optical isomers or their salts, or
any compounds, mixtures or preparations that may be used for producing hypnotic
effects.
      2.   Exceptions: Subsection A1 of this section shall not apply to a
physician, dentist, veterinarian or other person licensed in the state to
prescribe or administer drugs; or to employees of physicians, dentists,
veterinarians or other persons licensed in the state to prescribe or administer
drugs, or pharmacies, hospitals, clinics or public health agencies, or
manufacturers, compounders, processors, wholesale druggists, common or contract
carriers or law enforcement officials acting in the scope of their respective
employments; or to any person who has obtained such drug upon a valid
prescription of physician, dentist, veterinarian or other person licensed in
the state to prescribe or administer drugs, so long as such drugs are held in
the original containers in which such drugs were delivered. (1987 Code §
9.16.090)
   B.   Narcotics: It is further unlawful for any person, not so authorized by
law, to be in possession of, use, sell, barter, give away or in any manner
distribute marijuana, cocaine, opium, chloral hydrate, methylene dioxy
pyrrolidin ketone, synthetic cannabinoids (including, but not limited to,
cannabicyclohexanol, JWH-018, JWH-073, and HU-210) or any other narcotic,
opiate or drug or derivatives of any of them, or any product the effect of
which is to induce sleep or delirium. Any person who shall be the owner or
occupant of any building, place or premises, who shall knowingly permit on such
premises any of the products, drugs or derivatives referred to in this section
as not authorized by law is guilty of violation of this section. (Ord. 2010-13,
12-16-2010)
5-2D-8: DRUG PARAPHERNALIA:
   A.   Definition: "Drug paraphernalia" as used in this section means all
equipment, products and materials of any kind which are used, intended for use
or designed for use in planting, propagating, cultivating, growing, harvesting,
manufacturing, compounding, converting, producing, processing, preparing,
testing, analyzing, packaging, repackaging, storing, containing, concealing,
injecting, ingesting, inhaling or otherwise introducing into the human body a
"controlled substance" as defined by the Wyoming controlled substances act of
1971 1 , hereinafter referred to as the "act". Such act by this reference is
hereby incorporated in this section as if fully set forth. "Drug paraphernalia"
includes, but is not limited to:
      1.   Kits used, intended for use or designed for use in planting,
propagating, cultivating, growing or harvesting of any species of plant which
is a controlled substance or from which a controlled substance can be derived.
      2.   Kits used, intended for use or designed for use in manufacturing,
compounding, converting, producing, processing or preparing controlled
substances.
      3.   Isomerization devices used, intended for use or designed for use in
increasing the potency of any species of plant which is a controlled substance.
      4.   Testing equipment used, intended for use or designed for use in
identifying or in analyzing the strength, effectiveness or purity of controlled
substances.
      5.   Scales and balances used, intended for use or designed for use in
weighing or measuring controlled substances.
      6.   Dilutents and adulterants, such as quinine hydrochloride, mannitol,
mannite, dextrose and lactose, used, intended for use or designed for use in
cutting controlled substances.
      7.   Separation gins and sifters used, intended for use or designed for
use in removing twigs and seeds from, or in otherwise cleaning or refining,
marijuana.
      8.   Blenders, bowls, containers, spoons and mixing devices used,
intended for use or designed for use in compounding controlled substances.
      9.   Capsules, balloons, envelopes and other containers used, intended
for use or designed for use in packaging small quantities of controlled
substances.
      10.   Containers and other objects used, intended for use or designed for
use in storing or concealing controlled substances.
      11.   Hypodermic syringes, needles and other objects used, intended for
use or designed for use in parenterally injecting controlled substances into
the human body. (1987 Code § 9.16.100)
      12.   Objects used, intended for use or designed for use in ingesting,
inhaling or otherwise introducing marijuana or other controlled substance into
the human body, such as: (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
         a.   Metal, wooden, acrylic, glass, stone, plastic, ceramic pipes,
with or without screens, permanent screens, hashish heads or punctured metal
bowls.
         b.   Water pipes.
         c.   Carburetion tubes and devices.
         d.   Smoking and carburetion masks.
         e.   "Roach clips", meaning objects used to hold burning material,
such as a marijuana cigarette, that has become too small or too short to be
held in the hand.
         f.   Miniature cocaine spoons and cocaine vials.
         g.   Chamber pipes.
         h.   Carburetor pipes.
         i.   Electric pipes.
         j.   Air driven pipes.
         k.   Chillums.
         l.   Bongs.
         m.   Ice pipes or chillers.
   B.   Determination: In determining whether an object is drug paraphernalia,
a court or other authority should consider, in addition to all other logically
relevant factors, the following:
      1.   Statements by an owner or by anyone in control of the object
concerning its use.
      2.   Prior convictions, if any, of an owner or of anyone in control of
the object, under any state or federal law relating to any controlled
substance.
      3.   The proximity of the object, in time and space, to a direct
violation of the act.
      4.   The proximity of the object to controlled substances.
      5.   The existence of any residue of controlled substances on the object.
      6.   Direct or circumstantial evidence of the intent of the owner, or of
anyone in control of the object, to deliver it to persons whom he knows, or
should reasonably know, intend to use the object to facilitate a violation of
the act. The innocence of the owner, or of anyone in control of the object, as
to a direct violation of the act shall not prevent a finding that the object is
intended for use or designated for use as drug paraphernalia.
      7.   Instruction, oral or written, provided with the object concerning
its use.
      8.   Descriptive materials accompanying the object which explain or
depict its use.
      9.   National and local advertising concerning its use.
      10.   The manner in which the object is displayed for sale.
      11.   Whether the owner or anyone in control of the object is a
legitimate supplier of like or related items to the community, such as a
licensed distributor or dealer of tobacco products.
      12.   Direct or circumstantial evidence of the ratio of sales of the
object to the total sales of the business enterprise.
      13.   The existence and scope of legitimate uses for the object in the
community.
      14.   Expert testimony concerning its use.
   C.   Possession: It is unlawful for any person to use, or to possess with
intent to use, "drug paraphernalia" as defined in this section, to plant,
propagate, cultivate, grow, harvest, manufacture, compound, convert, produce,
process, prepare, test, analyze, pack, repack, store, contain, conceal, inject,
ingest, inhale or otherwise introduce into the human body a controlled
substance in violation of the act.
   D.   Manufacture Or Delivery: It is unlawful for any person to deliver,
possess with intent to deliver or manufacture with intent to deliver drug
paraphernalia, knowing, or under circumstances where one reasonably should
know, that it will be used to plant, propagate, cultivate, grow, harvest,
manufacture, compound, store, contain, conceal, inject, ingest, inhale or
otherwise introduce into the human body a controlled substance in violation of
the act.
   E.   Advertisement: It is unlawful for any person to place in any newspaper,
magazine, handbill or other publication any advertisement, knowing, or under
circumstances where one reasonably should know, that the purpose of the
advertisement, in whole or in part, is to promote the sale of objects designed
or intended for use as drug paraphernalia.
   F.   Civil Forfeiture And Seizures; Property Subject To Forfeiture: The
following are subject to forfeiture: all "drug paraphernalia" as defined by
this section.
   G.   Seizure Of Property Subject To Forfeiture: Property subject to
forfeiture under subsection F of this section may be seized by any law
enforcement officer of the state upon process issued by any court having
jurisdiction over the property. Seizure without process may be made if:
      1.   The seizure is incident to an arrest or a search warrant.
      2.   The property subject to seizure has been the subject of a prior
judgment in favor of the state in a criminal injunction or forfeiture
proceedings based upon the act.
   H.   Prompt Institution Of Proceedings: In the event of seizure pursuant to
subsection G of this section, proceedings under subsection I of this section
shall be instituted promptly.
   I.   Seized Property Not Repleviable; Sealing Or Removal Of Seized Property:
Property taken or detained under this section shall not be subject to replevin
but is deemed to be in the custody of the town, subject only to the orders and
decrees of the court having jurisdiction over the forfeiture proceedings. When
property is seized under this section, the law enforcement officer may:
      1.   Place the property under seal;
      2.   Remove the property to a place designated by him; or
      3.   Remove it to an appropriate location for disposition in accordance
with the law.
   J.   Disposition Of Forfeited Property: When property is forfeited under
this section, the law enforcement officer may:
      1.   Retain it for official use, in which case it shall become the
property of the town;
      2.   Sell any such property which is not required to be destroyed by law
and which is not harmful to the public. The proceeds shall be used for payment
of all proper expenses of the proceedings for forfeiture and sale, including
expenses of seizure, maintenance of custody, advertising and court costs;
      3.   Remove it for disposition in accordance with law; or
      4.   Transfer ownership and control of the property to the state or any
political subdivision of the state for its official use.
   K.   Severability: If any provision of this section or the application
thereof to any person or circumstances is held invalid, the invalidity does not
affect other provisions or applications of this section which can be given
effect without the invalid provision or application, and to this end the
provisions of this section are severable. (1987 Code § 9.16.100)
 
Notes
1 1. WS, 1977, §§ 35-7-1001 to 35-7-1057, as amended.
5-2D-9: LEWD AND LASCIVIOUS BEHAVIOR:
   A.   A person is guilty of lewd and lascivious behavior if a person performs
any of the following acts in a public place or under circumstances which the
person knows or should know will likely cause affront or alarm to, on, or in
the presence of another:
      1.   An act of sexual intrusion or contact, as defined by Wyoming
Statutes section 6-2-301;
      2.   Exposes his or her genitals, buttocks, anus, pubic area or the
female breast below the top of the areola;
      3.   Masturbates or manipulates his or her genitals, buttocks, anus,
pubic area or the female breast below the top of the areola in a manner
intended or likely to cause sexual arousal in the actor or others;
      4.   Verbally or visually describing, enticing, propositioning or
graphically referencing any act of sexual intrusion or contact, as defined by
Wyoming Statutes section 6-2-301, in a place or manner observed, or likely to
be observed, by the general public; or
      5.   Any other lewd or lascivious behavior.
   B.   A woman breast feeding, including breast feeding in any location where
the woman otherwise may rightfully be, does not constitute a lewd and
lascivious act, irrespective of whether or not the breast is covered during or
incidental to feeding. (Ord. 2012-06, 9-20-2012)
5-2D-10: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE E. OFFENSES AGAINST PUBLIC PEACE
SECTION:
5-2E-1: Disorderly Conduct
5-2E-2: Disturbing Assemblages
5-2E-3: False Alarm Or Report
5-2E-4: Loitering
5-2E-5: Noise
5-2E-6: Penalty
5-2E-1: DISORDERLY CONDUCT:
   A.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to be guilty of disorderly
conduct.
   B.   Acts Enumerated: A person shall be deemed guilty of disorderly conduct
if he wilfully:
      1.   Commits an act in a violent and tumultuous manner toward another
whereby the property of any person is placed in danger of being destroyed or
damaged.
      2.   Causes, provokes or engages in any fight, brawl or riotous conduct
so as to endanger the life, limb, health or property of another.
      3.   Incites, attempts to incite, or is involved in attempting to incite
a riot. For the purposes of this section, "riot" means a tumultuous disturbance
of the peace by persons assembled and acting with a common intent to the terror
of the people of the municipality, either in executing a lawful enterprise in a
violent or turbulent manner or in executing an unlawful enterprise in a violent
or turbulent manner.
      4.   Obstructs, either singly or together with other persons, the flow of
vehicular or pedestrian traffic and refuses to clear such public way when
ordered to do so by the police or other lawful authority known to be such.
      5.   Damages, befouls or disturbs public property or the property of
another so as to create a hazardous, unhealthy or physically offensive
condition.
      6.   Fails to obey a lawful order to disperse by a police officer, when
known to be such an official, where one or more persons are committing acts of
disorderly conduct in the immediate vicinity, and the public health and safety
is imminently threatened.
      7.   Resists or obstructs the performance of duties by police or any
other authorized official of the town, when known to be such an official.
      8.   Commits an act in a violent and tumultuous manner toward another
whereby that other is placed in danger of his life, limb or health.
      9.   Interferes with another's pursuit of a lawful occupation by acts of
violence.
      10.   Uses abusive, profane or obscene language in any public place.
(1987 Code § 9.20.010)
5-2E-2: DISTURBING ASSEMBLAGES:
   A.   Lawful Assemblage: No person shall disturb any lawful assemblage of
people in the town by rude, boisterous or indecent behavior or otherwise.
   B.   Religious Congregation Or Assembly: No person shall annoy or disturb
any congregation or assembly, gathered together for religious worship in the
town, by making a noise, by rude or indecent behavior or profane discourse
within the place of worship or so near the same as to be heard by the persons
so assembled or to disturb the order or solemnity of the meeting. (1987 Code §
9.20.020)
5-2E-3: FALSE ALARM OR REPORT:
No person in the town shall intentionally make, turn in or give a false alarm
of fire or of need for police or ambulance assistance or aid or abet in the
commission of such an act, nor shall any person make to or file with the chief
of police or town attorney any false, misleading or unfounded statement or
report concerning the commission or alleged commission of any crime occurring
within the town. (1987 Code § 9.20.030)
5-2E-4: LOITERING:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    LOITERING: Remaining idle in essentially one location and includes the
concepts of spending time idly, loafing, or walking about aimlessly, and also
includes the colloquial expression "hanging around".
   PUBLIC PLACE: Includes any place of business which is open to the public.
   B.   Offense Described: No person shall loiter in a public place in such a
manner as to:
      1.   Create or cause to be created a danger of a breach of the peace.
      2.   Create or cause to be created any disturbance or annoyance to the
comfort and repose of any person.
      3.   Obstruct the free passage of pedestrians or vehicles.
      4.   Obstruct, molest or interfere with any person lawfully in any public
place.
      5.   Obstruct, molest or interfere with the operation of any lawful
business in the town.
   C.   Unsolicited Remarks: This section includes the making of unsolicited
remarks of an offensive, disgusting or insulting nature or which are calculated
to annoy or disturb the person to or within whose hearing they are made, or
which cause persons to avoid patronizing a place of business.
   D.   Order To Leave: Whenever the presence of any person in any public place
is causing or is likely to cause any of the conditions enumerated above, any
police officer may order that person to leave that place. Any person who shall
refuse to leave after being ordered to do so by a police officer is guilty of a
violation of this section. (1987 Code § 9.20.040)
5-2E-5: NOISE:
No person in the town shall make or cause to be made or continued any excessive
or unusually loud noise as to disturb the peace, quiet and comfort of any
reasonable person of normal sensitivity residing in the same vicinity,
neighborhood, trailer or mobile home park, apartment house or apartment
complex. A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2E-6: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE F. OFFENSES AGAINST PROPERTY
SECTION:
5-2F-1: Vandalism
5-2F-2: Malicious Mischief
5-2F-3: Shoplifting
5-2F-4: Larceny And Petty Larceny
5-2F-5: Criminal Trespass
5-2F-6: Criminal Entry
5-2F-7: Fraud By Check
5-2F-8: Possession Of Stolen Property
5-2F-9: Penalty
5-2F-1: VANDALISM:
   A.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to wilfully or wantonly or
recklessly break, deface, injure or destroy any public property or any private
property without the consent of the owner thereof. Public property includes,
but is not limited to, all tangible items under the care, custody and control
of the town.
   B.   Consent Required: It is unlawful for any person to wilfully or wantonly
or recklessly break, injure, destroy or deface any public property or any
private property, whether said injury, destruction or defacing be eradicable or
permanent, without the consent of the owner. (Ord. 6-00, 5-18-2000)
5-2F-2: MALICIOUS MISCHIEF:
It shall be unlawful for any person to intentionally or recklessly drive upon,
break, destroy or deface in any manner, or to displace any property or item of
another or the town. Such property shall include, but is not limited to, snow
plowed to the middle of town streets during snow removal operations, and items
placed by the town or other government or public or private entity for safety
or comfort such as gravel, signs, traffic and parking cones or devices. (Ord.
2-2002, 3-21-2002)
5-2F-3: SHOPLIFTING:
   A.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to wilfully conceal or take
possession of any goods offered for sale by wholesale or retail stores or other
mercantile establishments, without the knowledge or consent of the owner
thereof and with intent to convert the goods to his own use without paying the
purchase price.
   B.   Detention; Interrogation: Any officer, merchant or merchant's employee
who has reasonable cause for believing that a person has committed the crime of
shoplifting as described in subsection A of this section, may detain and
interrogate such person in regard thereto in a reasonable manner and for a
reasonable time.
   C.   Defense To Civil Action: When a police officer, merchant or merchant's
employee, with reasonable cause for believing that a person has committed the
crime of shoplifting as described in subsection A of this section, detains and
interrogates such person in regard thereto, and such person thereafter brings
action for slander, false arrest, false imprisonment, assault, battery or
wrongful detention based upon the detention and interrogation, such reasonable
cause shall be a defense to the action if the detention and interrogation were
done in a reasonable manner and for a reasonable time. (1987 Code § 9.24.020)
5-2F-4: LARCENY AND PETTY LARCENY:
A person who steals, takes and carries, leads or drives away property of
another with intent to deprive the owner or lawful possessor, or a bailee or
any other person entrusted with the control, care or custody of any money or
other property, who with the intent to steal or deprive the owner of the
property converts the property to his or another's use, is guilty of a class A
misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2F-5: CRIMINAL TRESPASS:
A person is guilty of criminal trespass if he enters or remains on or in the
land or premises of another person, knowing he is not authorized to do so or
after being notified to depart or to not trespass. Notice is given by personal
communication to the person by the owner or occupant, or his agent, or by a
peace officer or by posting of signs reasonably likely to come to the attention
of the intruders. (1987 Code § 9.24.040)
5-2F-6: CRIMINAL ENTRY:
   A.   Offense Described: A person is guilty of criminal entry if, without
authority, he knowingly enters a building, occupied structure, vehicle or cargo
portion of a truck or trailer, or a separately secured or occupied position of
those enclosures.
   B.   Affirmative Defenses: It is an affirmative defense to prosecution under
this section that:
      1.   The entry was made because of a mistake of fact or to preserve life
or property in an emergency;
      2.   The enclosure was abandoned;
      3.   The enclosure was at the time open to the public and the person
complied with all lawful conditions imposed on access to or remaining in the
enclosure; or
      4.   The person believed that the owner of the enclosure, or other person
empowered to licensed access to the enclosure, would have authorized him to
enter. (1987 Code § 9.24.050)
5-2F-7: FRAUD BY CHECK:
   A.   Statute To Apply: For purposes of this section, the definitions of
Wyoming Statutes section 6-3-701, 1988, as amended, shall apply.
   B.   Offense Described: Any person who knowingly issues a check which is not
paid because the drawer has insufficient funds or credit with the drawee has
issued a fraudulent check and commits misdemeanor fraud by check, if the check
was for a sum less than five hundred dollars ($500.00).
   C.   Restitution: Upon sentencing, the court may require any person
convicted of check fraud to make restitution in an amount not to exceed twice
the amount of the dishonored check in addition to any other punishment imposed
under this section.
   D.   Prima Facie Evidence: Any of the following is prima facie evidence that
the person, at the time he issued the check or other order for the payment of
money, intended that it should not be paid:
      1.   Proof that, at the time of issuance, he did not have an account with
the drawee;
      2.   Proof that, at the time of issuance, he did not have sufficient
funds with the drawee and that he failed to pay the check or other order within
five (5) days after receiving notice of nonpayment or dishonor, personally
given or sent to the address shown on the check or other order; or
      3.   Proof that, when presentment was made in a reasonable time, the
issuer did not have sufficient funds with the drawee and he failed to pay the
check or other order within five (5) days after receiving notice of nonpayment
or dishonor, personally given or sent to the address shown on the check or
other order.
   E.   Proof Of Knowledge: Proof the drawer opened an account with the drawee
on a certain date shall be considered evidence of the drawer's knowledge of the
account balance on that date. (1987 Code § 9.24.060)
   F.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2F-8: POSSESSION OF STOLEN PROPERTY:
   A.   Prohibited: A person who possesses, buys, receives, conceals or
disposes of property which he or she knows, believes or has reasonable cause to
believe was obtained in violation of law is guilty of a misdemeanor.
   B.   Venue: A person may be charged and convicted under this section even if
the property was unlawfully obtained in another jurisdiction. (Ord. 2008-21, 1-
6-2009)
5-2F-9: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE G. OFFENSES BY OR AGAINST MINORS
SECTION:
5-2G-1: Contributing To Delinquency
5-2G-2: Curfew
5-2G-3: False Statement Of Age
5-2G-4: Tobacco Sales
5-2G-1: CONTRIBUTING TO DELINQUENCY:
It is unlawful for any person to cause or encourage any person under the age of
nineteen (19) years to violate any law of the United States, the State or the
Town, or to knowingly commit any immoral, indecent or obscene act in the
presence of such person, or to entice any minor of either sex to enter into any
place for the purpose of practicing fornication or adultery, or to cause any
child to be guilty of any vicious or immoral conduct. A violation of this
section constitutes a Class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
5-2G-2: CURFEW:
It is unlawful for any person under the age of sixteen (16) years to be found
loitering about or in or upon any of the streets, alleys, public or private
places in the Town, between the hours of nine thirty o'clock (9:30) P.M. and
dawn of the next succeeding day during the months of November through March,
and between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and dawn of the next
succeeding day during the months of April through October, unless such person
is traveling to or from any school or church activity, or is engaged in
necessary business or employment, or in works of charity, necessity or mercy.
(1987 Code § 9.28.020)
5-2G-3: FALSE STATEMENT OF AGE:
It is unlawful for any minor in the Town to make false statements or to
furnish, present or exhibit any fictitious or false registration card,
identification card, or note or other document, or to furnish, present or
exhibit such document or documents issued to a person other than the one
presenting the same, for the purpose of gaining admission to prohibited places
or for the purpose of procuring the sale, gift, or delivery of prohibited
articles. (1987 Code § 9.28.030)
5-2G-4: TOBACCO SALES:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
 
                  Means any substance containing tobacco leaf, including, but
                  not limited to, cigarettes, cigars, pipe tobacco, snuff,
                  chewing tobacco or dipping tobacco. It also includes any
                  electronic cigarette, pipe, hookah, vaporizer, personal
                  vaporizer or other device designed to introduce a smoke,
TOBACCO PRODUCTS: vapor or aerosol into a person for recreational purposes. The
                  definition of tobacco products, herein, does not include any
                  scheduled controlled substance, and nothing in these
                  Ordinances shall be read as authorizing the use of or
                  decriminalization of such substances without a valid and
                  authorized prescription by a duly licensed Wyoming Physician
                  taken in the manner prescribed by said physician.
                  Any mechanical, electric or electronic self-service device
VENDING MACHINE:  which, upon insertion of money, tokens or any other form of
                  payment, dispenses tobacco products.
 
   B.   Prohibited Sales Or Delivery:
      1.   Prohibited: No person shall sell, offer for sale, give away or
deliver tobacco products to any person under the age of twenty-one (21) years.
      2.   Defense to Prosecution: It is a defense to a prosecution under
subsection B1 of this section if, in the case of a sale, the person who sold
the tobacco product was presented with, and reasonably relied upon, an
identification card which identified the person buying or receiving the tobacco
product as being over twenty-one (21) years of age.
   C.   Posted Notice Required; Location Of Vending Machines:
      1.   Sign Required: Any person who sells tobacco products shall post
signs informing the public of the age restrictions provided in this section at
or near every display of tobacco products and on or upon every vending machine
which offers tobacco products for sale. Each sign shall be plainly visible and
shall state:
      THE SALE OF TOBACCO PRODUCTS TO PERSONS UNDER TWENTY-ONE YEARS OF AGE IS
PROHIBITED BY LAW
      2.   Location Of Vending Machines: No person shall sell or offer tobacco
products for sale by use of a vending machine unless the vending machine is
located in a business premises where alcoholic or malt beverages are sold or
dispensed and where entry by individuals under twenty-one (21) is prohibited.
   D.   Purchase By Minors Prohibited: No person under the age of twenty-one
(21) years shall purchase tobacco products, or misrepresent his identity or
age, or use any false or altered identification for the purpose of purchasing
tobacco products.
   E.   Possession Or Use By Persons Under Twenty-One (21): It is unlawful for
any person under the age of twenty-one (21) years to possess or use any tobacco
products. (Ord. 2008-20, 10-16-2008; amd. Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013; Ord. 2018-
02, 4-5-2018; Ord. 2020-05, 8-20-2020)
ARTICLE H. WEAPONS
SECTION:
5-2H-1: Concealing Or Displaying
5-2H-2: Possessing Or Discharging
5-2H-3: Exceptions
5-2H-4: Penalty
5-2H-1: CONCEALING OR DISPLAYING:
   A.   Prohibited: No person in the town shall wear under his clothes or
conceal about his person or display in a threatening manner any dangerous
weapon, including, but not limited to, any pistol, revolver, slingshot, brass
knuckles, bowie knife or switchblade.
   B.   Exceptions: This section shall not prohibit firearms in the possession
of:
      1.   A peace officer as defined by Wyoming Statutes section 7-2-101(a)
(iv);
      2.   A person who possesses a valid concealed weapon permit pursuant to
Wyoming Statutes section 6-8-104;
      3.   Any person who possesses a permit as described in Wyoming Statutes
section 6-8-104(a)(iii);
so long as said persons are in compliance with all provisions of Wyoming
Statutes section 6-8-104, including the prohibitions included in section 6-8-
104(t). (Ord. 2009-02, 7-16-2009)
5-2H-2: POSSESSING OR DISCHARGING:
   A.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any person to use or discharge any
firearm, BB gun, or any other gun, slingshot, bow or other dangerous weapon
except in a shooting gallery or range approved by the town council or in
compliance with section
5-2H-3 of this article. (Ord. 4-2002, 3-21-2002; amd. Res. 2009-08, 3-5-2009)
   B.   Law Enforcement Officers: The prohibition of subsection A of this
section shall not be construed to forbid law enforcement officers from carrying
or using while on duty such weapons as shall be necessary in the proper
discharge of their duties. (Ord. 4-2002, 3-21-2002)
5-2H-3: EXCEPTIONS:
   A.   Any citizen may erect and use an archery range within the town of Lyman
so long as:
      1.   The range is entirely contained on the land owned by the prospective
range user, and
      2.   The range is equipped only with manufacturer's recommended targets
and sufficient backstops appropriate for the archery equipment used and the
surrounding environs, as determined by the town's chief of police or his
assigned agent, and
      3.   The prospective range owner submits a statement indemnifying the
town for any and all injuries arising from the use or misuse of the archery
range, and that the range will only be used for private, noncommercial
purposes, and
      4.   The prospective range owner pays a forty dollar ($40.00) application
fee to recompense the town for the processing time and review by town
employees. (Res. 2009-08, 3-5-2009)
5-2H-4: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class A misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 3
ANIMAL CONTROL
ARTICLE A. CARE, CONTROL AND REGULATION
SECTION:
5-3A-1: Definitions
5-3A-2: Keeping Of Animals
5-3A-3: Keeper Considered Owner
5-3A-4: Running At Large
5-3A-5: Impoundment
5-3A-6: Dead Animal Disposal
5-3A-7: Animal Excrement
5-3A-8: Noisy Animals
5-3A-9: Biting And Vicious Animals
5-3A-10: Animals Left In Streets
5-3A-11: Licensing Of Dogs And Cats
5-3A-12: Vaccination
5-3A-13: Cruelty To Animals
5-3A-14: Keeping Of Chickens
5-3A-15: Dangerous Animals
5-3A-99: Penalty
5-3A-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this article, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ALTERED: An animal that has been spayed or neutered.
ANIMAL: Any mammal, bird, or reptile.
AT LARGE: Off the premises of the owner and not under immediate restraint by a
competent person.
BITING ANIMAL: Any animal that bites a person, or other animal, in a way that
breaks the skin or causes bodily injury.
BODILY INJURY: Physical pain, bruising, bleeding, or any impairment of physical
condition is a bodily injury.
OWNER: Any person or persons, firm, association or corporation owning, keeping
or harboring an animal.
RESTRAINT: The animal is controlled by a leash, or similar device, or in the
immediate company of a competent person and obedient to that person's command,
or in a vehicle.
UNCONFINED: Any animal which is not securely confined indoors or confined in a
securely enclosed and locked pen or structure upon the premises of the owner of
such animal. Such pen or structure shall have secure sides and a secure top. If
the pen or structure has no bottom secured to the sides, the sides shall be
embedded into the ground no less than one foot (1').
VICIOUS ANIMAL: Any animal with a known propensity, tendency or disposition to
attack unprovoked, to cause injury to or otherwise endanger the safety of
humans or other domestic animals; or any animal which attacks a human being or
other domestic animal without provocation. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997; amd. Ord. 6-
2004, 9-16-2004)
5-3A-2: KEEPING OF ANIMALS:
The keeping of any animal shall be in compliance with town ordinances,
including section
12-7-9, "Animal Grazing Permits", of this code; article B, "Multiple Animal
Permits", of this chapter; and title 4, chapter 1, "Nuisances", of this code.
(Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
5-3A-3: KEEPER CONSIDERED OWNER:
Any person who shall keep or harbor any animal or permit the same to habitually
remain or be fed in or upon or about his premises shall be considered and held
to be the owner of such animal and responsible therefor under the terms of this
article. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
5-3A-4: RUNNING AT LARGE:
   A.   Prohibited: No person owning or having custody of an animal shall fail
to take adequate and necessary steps to prevent said animal from being at large
within the corporate limits of the town. (Ord. 2016-02, 2-18-2016)
   B.   Destruction Or Relocation Of Animals At Large: It shall be the duty of
the chief of police and/or municipal court judge to destroy, relocate, or have
the same accomplished, any animal found running at large contrary to the
provisions of this article if the treatment of such animal is the only manner
of preventing such animal from running at large. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
5-3A-5: IMPOUNDMENT:
   A.   Duty To Apprehend And Impound: If any animal is found running at large,
it shall be the duty of the chief of police or other designated public official
of the town to apprehend and impound such animal in a secure pen, pound or
other place provided for that purpose.
   B.   Registry: The chief of police or other designated official, upon
receiving any animal, shall make a registry entering the breed, color and sex
of such animal and whether licensed or unlicensed. If licensed, he shall enter
the name and address of the owner and the number of the license tag.
   C.   Notice Of Impoundment: No later than forty eight (48) hours after the
impounding of any animal, the owner shall be notified, or if the owner is
unknown, written notice shall be posted for not less than two (2) days at one
conspicuous place in the town describing the animal and the place and time of
taking. The owner of any animal so impounded may redeem such animal upon
payment of the established impound fee and license, if required. (Ord. 7-96, 1-
9-1997)
   D.   Impound Fees: The fees to be paid to the town for impounding any animal
shall be set by resolution of the town council. (Ord. 2009-5, 7-16-2009)
   E.   Payment Required For Release: No animal so impounded shall be released
until the owner shall pay such sum as the governing body has determined to be a
just and suitable fee for the impoundment and care of the type of animal so
impounded. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
   F.   Shelter Abandonment:
      1.   Prohibited: An owner of an animal who wilfully fails or refuses to
redeem and retrieve an impounded animal as provided herein within five (5) days
after having been given notice or having actual notice of said impoundment as
provided in subsection C of this section is guilty of a crime. (Ord. 2011-09,
6-2-2011)
      2.   Penalty: A person found guilty of this section shall be punished as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this code and, in addition, is subject to all other remedies,
penalties, and fees described herein including those described in subsections G
and H of this section and subsection
5-3A-11E of this article. (Ord. 6-2002, 3-21-2002)
   G.   Sale Of Unredeemed Animals:
      1.   Authority; Notice Of Sale: At the discretion of the chief of police
or other designated official the town may sell at public auction any animal so
impounded, upon giving five (5) days' previous notice to the owner or person in
charge of the impounded animal, if known, of the time and place of such sale,
which notice shall describe the animal with reasonable accuracy; provided, that
any such animal may be redeemed at any time before the sale by payment of the
fees and charges provided for in subsection D of this section and subsection
5-3A-11E of this article.
      2.   Excess Funds: In case any animal sold pursuant to the provisions of
this section, shall be sold for more than an amount sufficient to pay the fees
and charges required pursuant to subsection D of this section and subsection
5-3A-11E of this article, the excess shall be deposited with the treasurer of
the town. Such excess shall be paid to the owner of such animal or to the
person entitled to the possession of such animal, upon claim and proper proof
presented by such person. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
   H.   Treatment Of Unclaimed Animals: It shall be the duty of the chief of
police to keep all animals so impounded for a period of seventy two (72) hours.
At the expiration of seventy two (72) hours from the date of notice or proof of
actual notice to the owner or the posting of notice, any animal which shall not
have been reclaimed may be forthwith destroyed, adopted or relocated. (Ord.
2011-09, 6-2-2011)
   I.   Breaking Open Pound: No person shall, directly or indirectly, break
open or assist in breaking open any pen or enclosure with the intention of
releasing any animal confined therein pursuant to this article. (Ord. 7-96, 1-
9-1997)
5-3A-6: DEAD ANIMAL DISPOSAL:
It shall be the duty of the owner of any animal found dead within the town to
remove such animal beyond the corporate limits of the town and to bury such
animal; provided, that if the town has designated a particular area for the
burial of dead animals, the owner of any dead animal shall remove the dead
animal to such designated area and bury the dead animal therein. (Ord. 7-96, 1-
9-1997)
5-3A-7: ANIMAL EXCREMENT:
   A.   Prohibited: It is unlawful for any animal owner to encourage, permit,
allow, or fail to prevent their animal from:
      1.   Urinating: Urinating on public or private property not under the
control of the animal owner.
      2.   Defecating: Defecating on public or private property not under the
control of the animal owner without removing said excrement promptly.
      3.   Exceptions: Exceptions to this section apply to use of the
designated rodeo area of the town recreation complex and organized drives or
parades wherein livestock passes upon and through the streets of town. (Ord. 7-
96, 1-9-1997)
5-3A-8: NOISY ANIMALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor within the limits of the
town any animal if that animal makes noise which disturbs the quiet of any
neighborhood or person. It shall be the duty of the chief of police and/or
municipal court judge to destroy or relocate or have destroyed or relocated any
noisy animal if the treatment of such animal is the only manner of preventing
such animal from making excessive noise. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
5-3A-9: BITING AND VICIOUS ANIMALS:
   A.   Owner Prevention: No person who owns, possesses, keeps or exercises
control over any animal shall fail to:
      1.   Prevent the animal from attacking, rushing, snapping at, growling,
snarling, biting or causing any bodily injury to any person, livestock or
domestic animal not on the premises of such owner, possessor or keeper.
      2.   Prevent the animal from attacking, rushing, snapping at, growling,
snarling, biting or causing any bodily injury to any person, livestock or
domestic animal lawfully present upon the premises of the residence of such
owner, possessor or keeper.
         a.   It is an affirmative defense to this subsection A.2., if such
premises have previously posted warning signs about the animal:
            (1)   At each entrance;
            (2)   With a prominent and conspicuous sign; and
            (3)   With lettering not less than two inches (2") in height.
         b.   It is also an affirmative defense to this subsection A.2. if the
bite or bodily injury caused by the animal was necessary to prevent or
apprehend a person engaged in committing an act of violence, robbery or theft
on the property.
      3.   Prevent the animal from attacking, rushing, snapping at, growling,
snarling, biting or causing any bodily injury to any person or domestic animal
upon the premises of any business establishment that is open to the public.
         a.   It is an affirmative defense to this subsection A.3. if the bite
or bodily injury caused by the animal was necessary to prevent or apprehend a
person engaged in committing an act of violence, robbery or theft on the
property.
      4.   The provisions of this section shall not apply to any law
enforcement officer who uses an animal while engaged in law enforcement
activities, nor to any owner, possessor or keeper of any animal which attacks,
bites or causes bodily injury to a person engaged in physically attacking or
striking such owner, possessor or keeper.
   B.   Biting Animal Impoundment: Any animal which bites a human being (or
another animal) so as to break the skin, may be immediately impounded for up to
ten (10) days as an examination period to determine whether the animal is
infected with rabies. The owner, possessor or keeper shall pay a seventy five
dollar ($75.00) rabies impound fee at the time, or before, the animal is
released.
      1.   Any human being, or parent or guardian of any human being, who has
been bitten by any animal may make application to the chief of police to
destroy that animal in order to determine if that animal has rabies, if that
animal has not been vaccinated against rabies within thirty six (36) months
prior to the bite occurring. It shall be at the sole discretion of the chief of
police whether such request shall be granted.
   C.   Ownership: No person shall own, keep or harbor any vicious animal or
any animal that may manifest a disposition to bite anyone, without having such
animal properly secured and muzzled at all times.
   D.   Vicious Animals Off Premises: The owner of a vicious animal shall not
suffer or permit such animal to go beyond the premises of such person unless
such animal is securely leashed and muzzled or otherwise securely restrained
and muzzled.
   E.   Unconfined Vicious Animals: The owner of a vicious animal shall not
permit such animal to go unconfined.
   F.   Destruction Or Relocation Of Vicious Animals: It shall be the duty of
the chief of police and/or municipal court judge to destroy, relocate, or have
the same accomplished, any animal found to be vicious contrary to the
provisions of this article if the treatment of such animal is the only manner
of preventing such animal from biting or acting viciously. (Ord. 6-2004, 9-16-
2004; amd. Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011; Ord. 2021-10, 1-20-2022)
5-3A-10: ANIMALS LEFT IN STREETS:
   A.   Fastening Required: No person shall leave any animal in any street or
alley within the limits of the town without securely fastening such animal.
   B.   Tying To Trees Or Fences: No person shall tie any animal to any growing
tree within the limits of the town, without the permission of the owner of such
tree, nor shall any animal be tied to any fence or otherwise so as to obstruct
any sidewalk within the town limits. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
5-3A-11: LICENSING OF DOGS AND CATS:
   A.   Licensing Required: Any person owning, harboring or caring for a dog or
cat within the Town may be permitted to do so by obtaining an annual license
from the town clerk or other officer appointed by the town. Any person owning,
harboring or caring for a dog or cat which was born in the Town and continually
maintained in the Town may be permitted to do so by obtaining an annual license
from the Town Clerk or other Officer appointed by the Town on or before the
date the animal reaches ninety (90) days old.
   B.   Vaccination Certificate Required: The license shall be issued after the
owner, harborer, or keeper provides a certificate of vaccination showing the
dog or cat is currently vaccinated against rabies and parvo, and paying a
license fee as set forth in subsection E of this section. Should a license be
issued for an animal less than six (6) months old, that animal’s owner,
harborer or keeper shall submit proof of such vaccination upon the animal
reaching the age of six (6) months.
   C.   Term: The license shall be valid for one year from the date of
issuance.
   D.   Collar And Tag: It shall be the duty of the owner of such dog or cat so
licensed to provide such dog or cat with a suitable collar to attach the
license tag issued by the town clerk, or in lieu of a collar, provide other
suitable identification recognized by the chief of police. Any dog or cat
licensed but not collared and tagged or identified as aforesaid found running
at large will be impounded and the owner subject to the same penalty as the
owner for an unlicensed dog or cat. Any dog or cat impounded under this section
shall be well housed, well fed and well watered. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
   E.   Annual License Fees: The fees to be paid to the town for licensing any
dog or cat will be set by resolution of the town council.
   F.   Exceptions: The provisions of this section shall not apply to dogs and
cats whose owners are nonresidents temporarily within the town, nor to seeing
eye dogs when such dogs are actually being used by blind persons, nor to dogs
and cats licensed under a multiple animal permit as provided in article B of
this chapter. For purposes of this subsection, "temporarily within the town"
shall mean any person who does not own, lease or control property within the
town, and/or resides within the town less than one month per year,
cumulatively, and/or one week per occasion. In calculating said time periods,
brief absences from the town shall not be considered. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011;
amd. Ord. 2023-03, 10-5-2023)
5-3A-12: VACCINATION:
Any person owning, harboring or desiring to keep a dog or cat, over the age of
six (6) months, within the Town must have proof of current certification,
subscribed by a doctor of veterinary medicine, or the serial number of self-
administered parvo vaccination that the dog or cat owned, harbored, kept or to
be kept has been vaccinated against rabies and parvo. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
5-3A-13: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this chapter, the following terms shall have
the meanings indicated:
 
                                   All costs incurred by the impounding entity
                                   in providing necessary food and water,
COSTS OF THE ANIMAL'S IMPOUNDMENT: veterinary attention and treatment for any
                                   animal which is the subject of a violation
                                   of this Code.
                                   Any privately owned dog, cat, rabbit, guinea
                                   pig, hamster, mouse, gerbil, ferret, bird,
                                   fish, reptile, amphibian, invertebrate or
HOUSEHOLD PET:                     any other species of domesticated animal
                                   sold, transferred or retained for the
                                   purpose of being kept as a pet in or near a
                                   house. "Household pet" shall not include any
                                   livestock;
                                   Horses, mules and asses, rabbits, llamas,
                                   cattle, swine, sheep, goats, poultry, or
                                   other animal generally used for food or in
                                   the production of food or fiber, working
LIVESTOCK:                         animals and guard animals actively engaged
                                   in the protection or management of
                                   livestock. Bison are considered livestock
                                   unless otherwise designated by the Wyoming
                                   livestock board and the Wyoming game and
                                   fish commission.
 
   B.   Animal abuse.
      1.   A person commits animal abuse if the person:
         a.   Knowingly overrides an animal or drives an animal when
overloaded;
         b.   Intentionally or knowingly, unnecessarily injures or beats an
animal;
         c.   Knowingly carries an animal in a manner that poses undue risk of
injury or death;
         d.   Has the charge and custody of any animal and under circumstances
which manifest extreme indifference to the animal's safety, health or life:
            (1)   Fails to provide it with proper food, drink or protection
from the weather adequate for the species;
            (2)   Abandons the animal. Relinquishment of an animal to a public
or private animal shelter or like facility is not a violation of this
subparagraph;
            (3)   In the case of immediate, obvious, serious illness or injury
to the animal, fails to provide the animal with appropriate care; or
            (4)   Keeps any household pet in a manner that results in chronic
or repeated serious physical harm to the household pet.
         e.   Owns, possesses, keeps or trains fowls or dogs with the intent to
allow the dog or fowl to engage in an exhibition of fighting with another dog
or fowl;
         f.   For gain causes or allows any dog to fight with another dog or
any fowl to fight with another fowl;
         g.   Promotes any dog or fowl fighting;
         h.   Knowingly permits any act prohibited under paragraphs (a) through
(g) of this subsection on any premises under the person's charge or control.
   C.   Willful killing of domestic animals. No person in the town shall
willfully kill, maim, or disfigure any horse, dog or other domestic animal or
administer poison to any such animal, or expose any poisonous substance with
the intent that it shall be taken by any such animal except in the exercise of
a lawful business or in discharge of an official duty. This Ordinance shall not
prevent the humane killing of a terminally injured or ill animal by law
enforcement, animal control officer a veterinarian or owner of said animal.
   D.   Other Abuse Misdemeanors
      1.   A person shall not destroy an animal by the use of a high?altitude
decompression chamber or a carbon monoxide gas chamber utilizing a gasoline
engine.
      2.   A person is guilty of a misdemeanor if he knowingly is present at
any place where an exhibition of fighting of fowls or dogs is occurring for
amusement or gain.
      3.   A person is guilty of a misdemeanor if he keeps a household pet
confined in conditions which constitute a public health hazard.
   E.   Exemptions
      1.   Nothing in this Chapter may be construed to prohibit:
         a.   A person humanely destroying an animal, including livestock;
         b.   The use of industry accepted agricultural and livestock practices
on livestock or another animal used in the practice of agriculture;
