         c.   Rodeo events, training for rodeo events or participating in rodeo
events, whether the event is performed in a rodeo, fair, jackpot, agricultural
exhibition or other similar event;
         d.   The use of dogs in the management of livestock by the owner of
the livestock, his employees or agents or other persons in lawful custody of
the livestock;
         e.   The use of dogs or raptors in hunting;
         f.   The training of dogs or raptors or the use of equipment in the
training of dogs or raptors for any purpose not prohibited by law;
         g.   The hunting, capture, killing or destruction of any predatory
animal, pest or other wildlife in any manner not otherwise prohibited by law.
   F.   Penalty.
      1.   Any prohibited act under this Chapter is a misdemeanor punishable by
imprisonment for not more than six (6) months, a fine of not more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00), or both.
      2.   Additionally, the Municipal Court Judge may order any or all of the
following:
         a.   If the defendant is the owner of the animal, require the
defendant to forfeit ownership of the animal. This paragraph shall not affect
the interest of any secured party or other person who has not participated in
the offense;
         b.   Require the defendant to pay all reasonable costs of the animal's
impoundment, if the animal has been impounded;
         c.   Impose continuing prohibitions or limitations on the defendant's
ownership, possession or custody of any animal.
      3.   Each animal affected by the defendant's conduct may constitute a
separate count for the purposes of prosecution, conviction, sentencing and
penalties under this article. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011; amd. Ord. 2021-07, 8-5-
2021)
5-3A-14: KEEPING OF CHICKENS:
   A.   Chickens Permitted: So long as the owners and keepers are in compliance
with all other provisions herein and in this Code, the keeping of chickens
shall be allowed within Town limits. The maximum number of chickens allowed
pursuant to this section is six (6) without a conditional use permit, and such
chickens shall not be included in the number of animals calculated in article B
of this chapter. (Ord. 2017-07, 5-4-2017)
   B.   Roosters And Other Poultry: No rooster over one (1) month in age or any
other poultry shall be kept in Town without an applicable and active
conditional use permit.
   C.   Containment: All chickens must be maintained in an appropriately fenced
area contained completely on the one (1) lot. Any chicken found outside the
property of any owner or keeper shall constitute a nuisance and may be treated
as such pursuant to title 4, chapter 1 of this Code. Additionally, such animal
may be considered at large as regulated by section
5-3A-4 of this article.
   D.   Clean And Orderly: All areas accessible by chickens shall be maintained
in a clean and orderly manner, and any keeping of chickens in a manner which is
likely to spread odor, noise or disease, such as salmonella is prohibited. The
failure to do so may constitute a separate offense for nuisance prosecutable
under title 4, chapter 1 of this Code.
   E.   Business Prohibited: No chicken or product thereof, including meat and
eggs, may be sold or exchanged for goods or services without the owner or
keeper first obtaining an applicable conditional use and business permit.
Nothing in this provision shall prohibit the sharing, without remuneration, of
such products. (Ord. 2013-03, 9-19-2013)
   F.   Exemption: Except for the sections regarding chickens running at large
and maintaining a clean premises, no restriction herein shall be applicable in
R-A Zones. (Ord. 2017-07, 5-4-2017)
5-3A-15: DANGEROUS ANIMALS:
The Chief of Police and or their designee is authorized to immediately remove
and/or destroy an animal which presents a clear and immediate danger to the
public, property and/or other animals and when such removal is the only means
by which public safety can be reasonably assured. (Ord. 2019-08, 10-3-2019)
5-3A-99: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a Class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. Additionally, restitution may include the expenses for
care incurred by the Town or other party, including, but not limited to,
medical care, veterinary care and impound fees. Further, no cat or dog whose
residence is in the Town shall be released from impoundment unless that animal
is properly licensed and vaccinated pursuant to Town ordinances. (Ord. 2012-11,
1-17-2013; amd. Ord. 2013-03, 9-19-2013)
ARTICLE B. MULTIPLE ANIMAL PERMITS
SECTION:
5-3B-1: License Required; Zoning Compliance
5-3B-2: License Fees
5-3B-3: Inspections
5-3B-4: Standards
5-3B-5: Effective Date
5-3B-6: Penalty
5-3B-1: LICENSE REQUIRED; ZONING COMPLIANCE:
No person or persons may own, rent, lease or otherwise occupy premises where a
combination of six (6) or more adult (over 12 weeks of age) animals, no more
than three (3) of which are canines, are kept without an annual multiple animal
permit. For dogs and cats, a multiple animal permit will be in lieu of
individual licenses. Possessors of a multiple animal permit must comply with
all applicable town zoning laws and maintain proof of current rabies and parvo
vaccination for each dog or cat over six (6) months of age. A conditional use
permit, as described in title 12, chapter 12 of this code, must first be
obtained from the town planning and zoning commission before a multiple animal
permit may be granted. Animals that are commonly intended to be constantly
maintained in a small, self-contained enclosure, such as caged birds and fish,
are exempt from this article. Animals commonly intended to be kept as
livestock, such as horses, sheep and cattle, are exempt from this article in
premises located in R-A and R-1-A zones. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
5-3B-2: LICENSE FEES:
   A.   Annual Fees: The annual fee for a multiple animal permit shall be
according to a schedule set by resolution of the town council.
   B.   Exception: No multiple animal fee shall be required of any veterinary
hospital, humane society or municipal animal control facility. (Ord. 2011-09,
6-2-2011)
5-3B-3: INSPECTIONS:
It shall be a condition of issuance of a multiple animal permit that the
appropriate town officials are permitted to inspect all animals and the
premises where animals are kept. Such inspections shall be conducted during
daylight hours upon reasonable suspicion of a violation of the multiple animal
permit or other animal control regulation. Additionally, the appropriate town
officials may conduct random inspections during daylight hours no more
frequently than once every three (3) months. If permission for an inspection is
refused, the license shall be revoked and all animals impounded. (Ord. 2011-09,
6-2-2011)
5-3B-4: STANDARDS:
All holders of multiple animal permits shall, in addition to the other
requirements of this title, comply with the minimum standards of this section.
Failure to meet these standards shall be grounds to deny or revoke the multiple
animal permit, and such failure shall be unlawful:
   A.   Enclosures: Secure animal enclosures must be provided which shall allow
adequate protection against weather extremes. (Ord. 2011-09, 6-2-2011)
   B.   Maintenance: All animal quarters and runs are to be kept clean and in
sanitary condition.
   C.   Food And Water: All food and water shall be free from contamination,
wholesome, palatable and of sufficient quantity and nutritive value to meet the
normal daily requirements for the conditions and size of the animal.
   D.   Space: Each animal shall have a sufficient and reasonable amount of
space unto itself to stand up, lie down and turn around without touching the
sides or tops of enclosures. Runs shall provide an adequate exercise area and
protection from the weather. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
5-3B-5: EFFECTIVE DATE:
The provisions of this chapter shall take effect on April 1, 1997. Only animal
owners subject to the provisions of this article, who register with the Lyman
police department prior to March 31, 1997, will be considered nonconforming
uses as described in title 12, chapter 10 of this code. (Ord. 7-96, 1-9-1997)
5-3B-6: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
ARTICLE C. BEES
SECTION:
5-3C-1: Keeping Of Bees
5-3C-2: Applicability; Effective Date
5-3C-3: Penalty
5-3C-1: KEEPING OF BEES:
No person shall establish any hive or box where bees are kept, or keep any bees
on the premises within three hundred feet (300') of any dwelling (except the
dwelling of the owner of such bees) or within one hundred feet (100') of any
exterior boundary of the property on which the hive or box is located, except:
a) when the bees are stored in containers from which they cannot escape; or b)
when the owner of the property upon which the bees are kept first obtains a
conditional use permit pursuant to title 12, chapter 12 of this code. (Ord. 1-
99, 3-4-1999)
5-3C-2: APPLICABILITY; EFFECTIVE DATE:
This article shall apply to all persons keeping bees within the municipal
limits of the town of Lyman, Wyoming, effective May 1, 1999. (Ord. 1-99, 3-4-
1999)
5-3C-3: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this article, any violation of the provisions of
this article constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 4
UNCLAIMED PROPERTY
SECTION:
5-4-1: Authority To Sell
5-4-2: Records Required
5-4-3: Time Of Sale
5-4-4: Notice Of Sale
5-4-5: Proceeds Of Sale
5-4-1: AUTHORITY TO SELL:
The chief of police shall sell at public auction any bicycles, automobiles,
guns, revolvers, watches or any other personal items of property or parts
thereof which may have been entrusted to the care of the police department or
come into its possession in the course of official police department duties
which may not have been redeemed or claimed. (1987 Code § 2.40.010)
5-4-2: RECORDS REQUIRED:
A record shall be kept of all articles received by the police department giving
the date, the origin of receipt, the name of the owner, if known, the purpose
for which held and any other information that may be available, including the
date such articles were sold and to whom sold. (1987 Code § 2.40.020)
5-4-3: TIME OF SALE:
Sales under this chapter may be conducted at intervals of three (3) months or
semiannually as may be deemed advisable, but in no case may an article be sold
that has been in the possession of the police department for a period of less
than thirty (30) days. (1987 Code § 2.40.030)
5-4-4: NOTICE OF SALE:
When a sale of any article is to be held, notice of the time and place of the
sale shall be given at least ten (10) days prior to the date of sale in one of
the following ways:
   A.   Posting: By posting a notice of such sale in three (3) public places in
the town.
   B.   Publication: By one publication thereof in some newspaper of general
circulation published in the town.
   C.   Mail: By mailing a written notice to the owners of the various articles
to be sold at their last known or given address. (1987 Code § 2.40.040)
5-4-5: PROCEEDS OF SALE:
   A.   Disposition: In case any article is sold for more than a sufficient
amount to make recompense on the purpose for which it was held or to pay any
necessary charges of the police department, plus incidental expense for
advertising or notification, etc., such excess shall be deposited with the town
treasurer and, upon order of the town council, paid to the person entitled to
the possession of same, provided claim and proper proof is made before the town
council.
   B.   Unclaimed Proceeds: In the event no claim for the proceeds of any
article offered for sale is made within thirty (30) days after such sale, the
proceeds thereof shall be listed as "Sale of Personal Property", and remitted
to the town treasurer as a part of the police department receipts. (1987 Code §
2.40.050)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Undefined Words
6-1-2: General Definitions
6-1-1: UNDEFINED WORDS:
Words or phrases used in this title and not defined by this chapter but defined
in section 31-5-102 of the Wyoming Statutes shall have the meanings set out in
section 31-5-102 of the Wyoming Statutes. (1987 Code § 10.04.010; amd. 2004
Code)
6-1-2: GENERAL DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this title, the words and phrases set out in this chapter
shall have the meanings respectively ascribed to them:
AUTHORIZED EMERGENCY VEHICLES: Vehicles of the fire department, police
vehicles, and such ambulances and emergency vehicles of municipal departments
or public service corporations as are designated or authorized by the chief of
police of the municipality. Private ambulances, wreckers and funeral cars are
emergency vehicles if they are so authorized by the chief of police in writing.
BUS: Every motor vehicle designed for carrying more than ten (10) passengers
and used for the transportation of persons, and every motor vehicle, other than
a taxicab, designed and used for the transportation of persons for
compensation.
BUSINESS DISTRICT: The territory contiguous to, and including, a street when
within any six hundred feet (600') along such street where there are buildings
in use for business or industrial purposes, including, but not limited to,
hotels, banks, or office buildings, railroad stations and public buildings
which occupy at least three hundred feet (300') of frontage on one side or
three hundred feet (300') collectively on both sides of the street.
CONTROLLED ACCESS ROADWAY: Every street or roadway in respect to which owners
or occupants of abutting lands and other persons have no legal right of access
to or from the same except at such points only and in such manner as may be
determined by the public authority having jurisdiction over such street or
roadway.
CROSSWALK: That part of a roadway at an intersection included within the
connections of the lateral lines of the sidewalks on opposite sides of the
street measured from the curbs or, in the absence of curbs, from the edges of
the traversable roadway; any portion of a street at an intersection or
elsewhere distinctly indicated for pedestrian crossing by lines or other
markings on the surface.
DISABLED MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle which is self-propelled and is in such
state of condition that it cannot be safely operated, and particularly, cars
which have had the motor or tires removed, the rear end dismantled, or any part
missing, so as to be incapable of operating under its own power for any reason
whatever.
DRIVER: Every person who drives or is in actual physical control of a vehicle.
EXPLOSIVES: Any chemical compound or mechanical mixture that is commonly used
or intended for the purpose of producing an explosion and which contains any
oxidizing and combustive units or other ingredients in such proportions,
quantities or packing that an ignition by fire, by friction, by concussion, by
percussion or by detonator of any part of the compound or mixture may cause
such a sudden generation of highly heated gases that the resultant gaseous
pressures are capable of producing destructive effects on contiguous objects or
of destroying life or limb.
FARM TRACTOR: Every motor vehicle designed and used primarily as a farm
implement for drawing plows, mowing machines and other implements of husbandry.
FLAMMABLE LIQUID: Any liquid which has a flash point below one hundred degrees
Fahrenheit (100°F), and has a vapor pressure not exceeding forty (40) pounds
per square inch (absolute) at one hundred degrees Fahrenheit (100°F).
INTERSECTION:
   A.   The area embraced within the prolongation or connection of the lateral
curb lines, or, if none, the lateral boundary lines of the roadways of two (2)
streets which join one another at, or approximately at, right angles, or the
area within which vehicles traveling upon different streets joining at any
other angle may come in conflict.
   B.   Where a street includes two (2) roadways thirty feet (30') or more
apart, then every crossing of each roadway of such divided street by an
intersecting street shall be regarded as a separate intersection. In the event
such intersecting street also includes two (2) roadways thirty feet (30') or
more apart, then every crossing of two (2) roadways of such street shall be
regarded as a separate intersection.
LANED ROADWAY: A roadway which is divided into two (2) or more clearly marked
lanes for vehicular traffic.
MOTOR DRIVEN CYCLE: Every motorcycle, including every motor scooter, with a
motor which produces not more than five (5) horsepower and every bicycle with
motor attached.
MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle which is self-propelled and every vehicle which is
propelled by electric power obtained from overhead trolley wires, but not
operated upon rails.
MOTORCYCLE: Every motor vehicle having a seat or saddle for the use of the
rider and designed to travel on no more than three (3) wheels in contact with
the ground, but excluding a tractor.
OFFICIAL TRAFFIC CONTROL DEVICES: All signs, signals, markings and devices not
inconsistent with the provisions of this title placed or erected by the
governing body or by an official with proper authority of the governing body
for the purpose of regulating, warning or guiding traffic.
OFF-ROAD RECREATIONAL VEHICLE PER WYOMING STATUTE § 31-1-101(K):
   A.   Type 1 - Any recreational vehicle primarily designed for off-road use
which has an unladen weight of one thousand one hundred (1,100) pounds or less;
   B.   Type 2 - Any unlicensed motorcycle which has an unladen weight of six
hundred (600) pounds or less and is designed to be ridden off-road with the
operator astride upon a seat or saddle and travels on two (2) tires; and
   C.   Type 3 - Any multi-wheeled motorized vehicle not required by law to be
licensed and is designed for cross-country travel on or over land, sand, snow,
ice or other natural terrain and has an unladen weight of more than nine
hundred (900) pounds.
OPERATOR: Every person who operates or is in actual physical control of the
operation of an off-road vehicle.
OWNER: A person who holds the legal title of a vehicle or, in the event a
vehicle is the subject of an agreement for the conditional sale or lease
thereof with the right of purchase upon performance of the conditions stated in
the agreement and with an immediate right of possession vested in the
conditional vendee or lessee or in the event a mortgagor of a vehicle is
entitled to possession, such conditional vendee or lessee or mortgagor.
PARK: The standing of a vehicle, whether occupied or not, otherwise than
temporarily for the purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or
unloading.
PEDESTRIAN: Any person afoot.
POLICE OFFICER: Every officer authorized to direct or regulate traffic or to
make arrests for violation of traffic regulations.
PRIVATE ROAD OR DRIVEWAY: Every way or place in private ownership and used for
vehicular travel by the owner and those having express or implied permission
from the owner, but not by other persons.
RAILROAD: A carrier of persons or property upon cars, other than streetcars,
operated upon stationary rails.
RAILROAD SIGN OR SIGNAL: Any sign, signal or device erected by authority of a
public body or official or by a railroad and intended to give notice of the
presence of railroad tracks or the approach of a railroad train.
RAILROAD TRAIN: A steam engine, electric or other motor, with or without cars
coupled thereto, operated upon rails, except streetcars.
RESIDENCE DISTRICT: The territory contiguous to and including a street not
comprising a business district when the property on such street for a distance
of three hundred feet (300') or more is in the main improved with residences or
residences and buildings in use for business.
RIGHT OF WAY: The right of one vehicle or pedestrian to proceed in a lawful
manner in preference to another vehicle or pedestrian approaching under such
circumstances of direction, speed and proximity as to give rise to danger of
collision unless one grants precedence to the other.
ROAD TRACTOR: Every motor vehicle designed and used for drawing other vehicles
and not so constructed as to carry any load thereon either independently or any
part of the weight of a vehicle or load so drawn.
ROADWAY: That portion of a street improved, designed or ordinarily used for
vehicular travel, exclusive of the berm or shoulder. In the event a street
includes two (2) or more separate roadways, the term "roadway" shall refer to
any such roadway separately but not to all such roadways collectively.
SAFETY ZONE: The area or space officially set apart within a roadway for the
exclusive use of pedestrians and which is protected or is so marked or
indicated by adequate signs as to be plainly visible at all times while set
apart as a safety zone.
SCHOOL BUS: Every motor vehicle that complies with the color and identification
requirements set forth in the most recent edition of "Minimum Standards For
School Buses" and is used to transport children to or from school or in
connection with school activities, but not including buses operated by common
carriers in urban transportation of school children.
SEMITRAILER: Every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole
trailer, designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a
motor vehicle and so constructed that some part of its weight and that of its
load rests upon or is carried by another vehicle.
SIDEWALK: That portion of a street between curb lines, or the lateral lines of
a roadway, and the adjacent property lines, intended for use of pedestrians.
STOP: Complete cessation from movement.
STOP, STOPPING OR STANDING: When prohibited, means any stopping or standing of
a vehicle, whether occupied or not, except when necessary to avoid conflict
with other traffic or in compliance with the directions of a police officer or
traffic control sign or signal.
STREET: The entire width between the boundary lines of every way publicly
maintained when any part thereof is open to the use of the public for purposes
of vehicular travel.
THROUGH STREET: Every street or portion thereof on which vehicular traffic is
given preferential right of way, and at the entrances to which vehicular
traffic from intersecting streets is required by law to yield the right of way
to vehicles on such through highway in obedience to a stop sign, yield sign or
other official traffic control devices, when such signs or devices are properly
erected.
TRAFFIC: Pedestrians, ridden or herded animals, vehicles and other conveyances
either singly or together while using any street for purposes of travel.
TRAFFIC CONTROL SIGNAL: Any device, whether manually, electrically or
mechanically operated, by which traffic is alternately directed to stop and
permitted to proceed.
TRAILER: Every vehicle with or without motive power, other than a pole trailer,
designed for carrying persons or property and for being drawn by a motor
vehicle and so constructed that no part of its weight and that of its load
rests upon or is carried by another vehicle.
TRUCK: Every motor vehicle designed, used or maintained primarily for the
transportation of property.
TRUCK TRACTOR: Every motor vehicle designed and used primarily for drawing
other vehicles and not so constructed as to carry a load other than a part of
the weight of the vehicle and load so drawn.
URBAN DISTRICT: The territory contiguous to and including any public street
which is built up with structures devoted to business, industry or dwelling
houses situated at intervals of less than one hundred feet (100') for a
distance of a quarter of a mile or more.
VEHICLE: Every device, in, upon or by which any person or property is or may be
transported or drawn upon a street, except devices moved by human power or used
exclusively upon stationary rails or tracks. (1987 Code §§ 10.04.010 –
10.04.430; amd. Ord. 7-94, 1-19-1995; 2004 Code; Ord. 2021-03, 5-6-2021)
CHAPTER 2
STATE PROVISIONS ADOPTED
SECTION:
6-2-1: Adopted State Provisions Designated
6-2-1: ADOPTED STATE PROVISIONS DESIGNATED:
   A.   Sections Adopted: Sections 31-5-101 through and including 31-5-1214,
31-7-404 and 31-5-1402 of the Wyoming Statutes and all subsequent amendments
thereto, being the uniform act regulating traffic on highways, except such
sections of said act as are specifically deleted therefrom by subsection B of
this section, are adopted by reference and incorporated as a part of this
section as fully as if completely set out herein. (Ord. 2017-01, 2-2-2017; amd.
Ord. 202-08, 1-21-2021)
   B.   Sections Deleted Or Excepted: The following sections of the uniform act
regulating traffic on highways, and all amendments thereto, are specifically
deleted and excepted therefrom before adoption by the governing body of the
town: sections 31-5-111, 31-5-120, 31-5-225, 31-5-227, 31-5-228, 31-5-133, 31-
5-301, 31-5-501, 31-5-502, 31-5-801, 31-5-1107 through 31-5-1113, 31-5-1115,
31-5-1116, and 31-5-1201. (Ord. 2009-07, 8-20-2009)
   C.   Copy On File: One copy of such provisions shall be kept on file in the
office of the town clerk, where it shall be available for inspection by the
public during the normal office hours of the town clerk. (1987 Code §
10.08.010)
   D.   Violations: Any violations of the provisions of this chapter shall be
punished pursuant to the state statute prohibiting such an act. (Ord. 2012-11,
1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 3
LICENSING AND REGISTRATION
SECTION:
6-3-1: Driver's License Required
6-3-2: Minimum Age Of Operator
6-3-3: Registration And License Plates
6-3-4: Driving While License Canceled, Suspended Or Revoked
6-3-5: Operating A Motor Vehicle Without Insurance
6-3-6: Operating A Motor Vehicle Without Proof Of Insurance
6-3-1: DRIVER'S LICENSE REQUIRED:
It is unlawful for any person to operate a motor vehicle, motorcycle or power
cycle in the town unless he or she is in possession of a valid driver's license
or permit issued by the licensing authority of the state. (1987 Code §
10.12.010)
6-3-2: MINIMUM AGE OF OPERATOR:
Any person under fifteen (15) years of age who operates a motor vehicle, and
any owner, dealer or manufacturer who authorizes or permits a person under
fifteen (15) years of age to operate a motor vehicle, and any owner, dealer or
manufacturer who authorizes or permits a person who is not licensed for the
type or class of vehicle to be driven to operate a motor vehicle shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor and shall be punished as provided in this title
for violation of this title. (1987 Code § 10.12.020)
6-3-3: REGISTRATION AND LICENSE PLATES:
   A.   Required: No person shall operate, nor shall an owner knowingly permit
to be operated within the town any vehicle required to be registered unless
there is attached thereto and displayed thereon when and as required by Wyoming
Statutes 31-4-101 through 31-4-104, a valid registration plate or plates issued
therefor by the motor vehicle division of the state or county treasurer for the
current registration year, except as otherwise expressly permitted by Wyoming
Statutes 31-4-101 through 31-4-104. (1987 Code § 10.12.030; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Improper Use: No person shall lend to another any license or
registration number of plates, special number of plate or permit issued to him
if the person desiring to borrow the same would not be entitled to the use
thereof, nor shall any person knowingly permit the use of any of the same by
one not entitled thereto, nor shall any person display upon a vehicle any
registration number plate, special number plate or permit not issued for such
vehicle, or not lawfully used thereon under this section. (1987 Code §
10.12.030)
6-3-4: DRIVING WHILE LICENSE CANCELED, SUSPENDED OR REVOKED:
   A.   Misdemeanor: Any person who drives a motor vehicle on any public road
in this town at a time when his driver's license, from this or any other
jurisdiction, or nonresident operating privileges are canceled, suspended or
revoked under this act or any other law is guilty of a misdemeanor.
   B.   Additional One Year Suspension: Upon receiving a record of the
conviction of any person upon a charge of driving a vehicle while the license
of the person was suspended, revoked or canceled, the department of motor
vehicles shall suspend, revoke or cancel the license or nonresident operating
privileges for an additional period of one year. (1987 Code § 10.12.040)
6-3-5: OPERATING A MOTOR VEHICLE WITHOUT INSURANCE:
   A.   Requirements: No owner of a motor vehicle required to be registered
shall operate or permit the operation of his motor vehicle without having in
full force and effect a motor vehicle liability policy in amounts provided by
Wyoming Statutes 31-9-405(b) or a bond in amounts provided by Wyoming Statutes
31-9-102(a)(xi).
No person shall operate a motor vehicle that is required to be registered
without having in full force and effect a motor vehicle liability policy in
amounts provided by Wyoming Statutes 31-9-405(b) or a bond in amounts provided
by Wyoming Statutes 31-9-102(a)(xi). (Ord. 7-2004, 9-16-2004)
   B.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. Additionally, in the event of a second or subsequent
violation of this section, the judge may require the defendant to deliver the
registration and license plates of the vehicle involved to the county treasurer
for the county where the citation was issued, and the registration and license
plates shall be held by the county treasurer until such time as the judge
determines that the defendant has met all obligations imposed by law. (Ord.
2012-11, 1-17-2013)
   C.   Defense: Excusable neglect or mistake by another is a defense for any
violation of this section. If evidence of excusable neglect or mistake by
another is presented and the defendant is convicted, the court may consider
this evidence in imposing a penalty under this section. The judge may suspend
part or all of the sentence under this section and place the defendant on
probation subject to conditions imposed by the judge which may include a
condition that the defendant shall deliver the registration and license plates
of the vehicle involved to the county treasurer for the county where the
citation was issued.
   D.   Exemptions: This section does not apply to:
      1.   Self-insurers pursuant to Wyoming Statutes 31-9-414;
      2.   A vehicle owned by the United States government, any state or
political subdivision thereof which is self-insured;
      3.   A vehicle meeting the requirements of Wyoming Statutes 31-9-408 and
31-9-409;
      4.   A commercial vehicle registered or proportionally registered in this
and any other jurisdiction provided the vehicle is covered by a vehicle
insurance policy complying with the laws of any other jurisdiction in which it
is registered;
      5.   A vehicle owned by a nonresident and registered in a state requiring
insurance if a vehicle insurance policy meeting requirements of the laws and
regulations of that state is in effect or unless it otherwise complies with the
laws of that state concerning compulsory financial responsibility. The
department shall report any violation of this section to the motor vehicle
administrator in the state wherein the vehicle is registered. A vehicle owned
by a nonresident and registered in a state not requiring insurance is exempt
from this section. (Ord. 7-2004, 9-16-2004)
6-3-6: OPERATING A MOTOR VEHICLE WITHOUT PROOF OF INSURANCE:
   A.   No operator of a motor vehicle requiring insurance pursuant to section
6-3-5 of this chapter shall operate said vehicle without having proof of said
insurance in his or her possession at the time of the vehicle's operation. If
the operator has an insurance card issued by an insurer licensed in the state
of Wyoming facially in effect at the time of the vehicle stop in his or her
possession and presents said card to the officer at the time of the operator's
stop, this shall create a rebuttable presumption of proof of insurance for
purposes of probable cause.
   B.   If an operator or owner of a vehicle involved in a violation of this
section presents proof to the court clerk or his or her designee that the
vehicle carries insurance as required by section
6-3-5 of this chapter within ten (10) business days after the issuance of a
citation or receipt of a summons pursuant to this section, the case will be
immediately dismissed against the operator.
   C.   The court clerk or his or her designee is hereby authorized to dismiss
any citation pursuant to subsection B of this section by writing on the face of
the citation "dismissed - proof given" and signing and dating that writing.
   D.   This section is deemed to be a lesser included offense of section
6-3-5 of this chapter. (Ord. 2007-6, 3-15-2007)
CHAPTER 4
DRIVING RULES
SECTION:
6-4-1: Care And Prudence Generally
6-4-2: Reckless Driving
6-4-3: Speed Limits
6-4-4: Speed Or Acceleration Contests
6-4-5: Slade Park And Lyman Recreation Complex
6-4-6: Eluding Police Officers
6-4-7: Driving Under Influence
6-4-8: Flatbed Trucks And Trailers
6-4-9: Right Of Way In Crosswalks
6-4-10: Inattentive Driving
6-4-11: Clinging To Moving Vehicles
6-4-12: Off-Road Recreational Vehicles
6-4-13: Incidental Operation
6-4-1: CARE AND PRUDENCE GENERALLY:
Every person operating a vehicle on the streets or highways under the
jurisdiction of the town shall drive the same in a careful and prudent manner,
having regard for the width, grade, curves, corners, traffic and use of these
streets and all other attendant circumstances so as not to endanger the life,
limb or property of any person. (1987 Code § 10.16.010)
6-4-2: RECKLESS DRIVING:
Any person who drives any vehicle in wilful or wanton disregard for the safety
of persons or property is guilty of a class A misdemeanor punishable as set
forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
6-4-3: SPEED LIMITS:
   A.   Basic Rule: No person shall drive a vehicle on a street at a speed
greater than is reasonable and prudent under the conditions and having regard
to the actual and potential hazards then existing.
   B.   Maximum Lawful Speeds: Except when a special hazard exists that
requires lower speed, the limits posted on any street or highway, including
periodic lower speed limits around school zones, shall be maximum lawful
speeds, and no person shall drive a vehicle on a street at a speed in excess of
such maximum limits. (Ord. 2009-07, 8-20-2009)
6-4-4: SPEED OR ACCELERATION CONTESTS:
No person shall engage in, aid, or abet any motor vehicle speed or acceleration
contest, or exhibition of speed or acceleration, on any street or highway
within the corporate limits of the town without the prior written approval of
the mayor or town council. (1987 Code § 10.16.040)
6-4-5: SLADE PARK AND LYMAN RECREATION COMPLEX:
All motor vehicles, including "motorcycles" and "motor driven cycles", as
defined in this title, shall be driven only upon the designated roadways of
Slade Park and the Lyman Recreation Complex. (1987 Code § 10.16.050)
6-4-6: ELUDING POLICE OFFICERS:
   A.   Prohibited: Any driver of a motor vehicle who wilfully fails or refuses
to bring his vehicle to a stop, or who otherwise flees or attempts to elude a
pursuing police vehicle, when given visual or audible signal to bring the
vehicle to a stop, is guilty of a misdemeanor. The signal by the police officer
may be by hand, voice, emergency light or siren. The officer giving such signal
shall be in uniform, prominently displaying his badge of office, and his
vehicle shall be appropriately marked showing it to be an official police
vehicle.
   B.   Misdemeanor: Whoever knowingly or wilfully fails or refuses to stop or
who otherwise flees or attempts to elude a pursuing police officer when given
an audible or visual signal to stop is guilty of a misdemeanor. (1987 Code §
10.16.060)
   C.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class A misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
6-4-7: DRIVING UNDER INFLUENCE:
   A.   Definitions: As used in this section, the following words and terms
shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection:
    ALCOHOL CONCENTRATION:
      1.   The number of grams of alcohol per one hundred milliliters (100 ml)
of blood;
      2.   The number of grams of alcohol per two hundred ten liters (210 l) of
breath; or
      3.   The number of grams of alcohol per seventy five milliliters (75 ml)
of urine.
   CONTROLLED SUBSTANCE: A drug, substance, or immediate precursor in Wyoming
Statutes schedules I through V of article III 1 .
   CONVICTION: A final conviction and shall include:
      1.   An unvacated adjudication of guilt or a determination of a violation
in a court of original jurisdiction or an administrative proceeding;
      2.   An unvacated forfeiture of bail or collateral deposited to secure
the person's appearance in court;
      3.   A plea of guilty or nolo contendere accepted by the court;
      4.   The payment of a fine or court cost; or
      5.   Violation of a condition of release without bail, regardless of
whether the penalty is rebated, suspended or probated.
   DRIVER'S LICENSE: As defined in Wyoming Statutes subsection 31-7-102(a)
(viii) and includes nonresident operating privileges as defined in Wyoming
Statutes subsection 31-7-102(a)(xiii).
   OTHER LAW PROHIBITING DRIVING WHILE UNDER THE INFLUENCE: A statute of
another state, the United States or a territory or district of the United
States or an ordinance of a governmental entity of this or another state or of
an Indian tribe which prohibits driving while under the influence of
intoxicating liquor, alcohol, controlled substances or drugs.
   B.   Driving Or Actual Physical Control Prohibited: No person shall drive or
have actual physical control of any vehicle within the town if the person:
(1987 Code § 10.16.070)
      1.   Has an alcohol concentration of eight one-hundredths of one percent
(0.08%) or more; or (Ord. 2-03, 8-15-2003)
      2.   To a degree which renders him incapable of safely driving:
         a.   Is under the influence of alcohol;
         b.   Is under the influence of a controlled substance; or
         c.   Is under the influence of a combination of any of the elements
named in subsections B2a and B2b of this section.
   C.   Presumptions From Chemical Analysis: Upon the trial of any criminal
action or proceeding arising out of the acts alleged to have been committed by
any person while driving or being in actual physical control of a vehicle while
under the influence of alcohol, the amount of alcohol in the person's blood at
the time alleged as shown by chemical analysis of the person's blood, urine,
breath, or other bodily substance shall give rise to the following
presumptions:
      1.   If there was at that time an alcohol concentration of five one-
hundredths of one percent (0.05%) or less, it shall be presumed that the person
was not under the influence of alcohol. (1987 Code § 10.16.070)
      2.   If there was at that time an alcohol concentration of more than five
one-hundredths of one percent (0.05%) and less than eight one-hundredths of one
percent (0.08%), that fact shall not give rise to any presumption that the
person was or was not under the influence of alcohol, but it may be considered
with other competent evidence in determining whether the person was under the
influence of alcohol to a degree which renders him incapable of safely driving
a motor vehicle. (1987 Code § 10.16.070; amd. Ord. 2-03, 8-15-2003)
   D.   Other Competent Evidence: Subsection C of this section shall not be
construed as limiting the introduction of any other competent evidence bearing
upon the question of whether the person was under the influence of alcohol,
including tests obtained more than three (3) hours after the alleged violation.
The fact that any person charged with a violation of subsection B of this
section is or has been entitled to use the controlled substance under the laws
of this state shall not constitute a defense against any charge under
subsection B of this section. (1987 Code § 10.16.070)
   E.   Penalty: Any person convicted under this section shall be punished
pursuant to Wyoming Statutes sections 31-5-233(e) and (f). (Ord. 2016-05, 4-7-
2016)
   F.   License Suspension Or Revocation: Any person convicted under this
section shall, in addition to the penalty imposed, have his driver's license
suspended or revoked pursuant to Wyoming Statutes section 31-7-127 or 31-7-128.
The court shall forward to the Wyoming state department of motor vehicles, a
copy of the record pertaining to disposition of the arrest or citation.
   G.   Release For Employment Or Education: The court may, upon pronouncement
of any jail sentence under subsection E of this section, provide in the
sentence that the defendant may be permitted, if he is employed or enrolled in
school and can continue his employment or education, to continue such
employment or education for not more than the time necessary as certified by
his employer or school administrator, and the remaining day, days or parts of
days shall be spent in jail until the sentence is served. He shall be allowed
out of jail only long enough to complete his actual hours of employment or
education and a reasonable time to travel to and from his place of employment
or school.
   H.   Prosecution: Any person charged under this section shall be prosecuted
under this section and not under a reduced charge or dismissed, unless the
prosecuting attorney, in open court, moves or files a statement to reduce the
charge or dismiss, with supporting facts, stating that there is insufficient
evidence to sustain the charge. (1987 Code § 10.16.070)
   I.   Chemical Analysis: Chemical analysis of a person's blood, breath or
urine to determine alcohol concentration or controlled substance content shall
be performed in accordance with Wyoming Statutes section 31-6-105, including
subsection (d). (Ord. 2013-05, 11-21-2013)
 
Notes
1 1. WS § 35-7-1011 et seq.
6-4-8: FLATBED TRUCKS AND TRAILERS:
No person shall operate a flatbed truck or trailer carrying property on a
street in the town unless the truck or trailer is equipped with sideboards or
walls of such size as to contain a load to prevent spillage, or the load is
fastened to the truck or trailer bed. (1987 Code § 10.16.080)
6-4-9: RIGHT OF WAY IN CROSSWALKS:
   A.   When traffic control signals are not in place or not in operation, the
driver of a vehicle shall yield the right of way by stopping to yield to any
pedestrian within or entering a crosswalk at either edge of the roadway.
   B.   No pedestrian shall suddenly leave a curb or other place of safety and
walk or run into the path of a vehicle which is so close as to constitute an
immediate hazard.
   C.   Whenever any vehicle is stopped at a marked crosswalk or at any
unmarked crosswalk at an intersection to permit a pedestrian to cross the
roadway, the driver of any other vehicle approaching from the rear shall not
overtake and pass the stopped vehicle. (Ord. 2007-04, 3-1-2007)
6-4-10: INATTENTIVE DRIVING:
No person shall operate or have physical control of a motor vehicle in a manner
which evidences a lack of that degree of attentiveness required to safely
operate the vehicle under the prevailing conditions. (Ord. 2010-08, 8-19-2010)
6-4-11: CLINGING TO MOVING VEHICLES:
   A.   No person shall attach himself to the exterior of any vehicle,
including fenders and running boards, while being operated upon a roadway, nor
shall any person ride upon any bicycle, coaster, roller skates, skateboard,
sled, toy vehicle or other device or object attached to a vehicle while being
operated upon a roadway.
   B.   No person shall knowingly or recklessly operate a vehicle on a roadway
while another person has attached himself to the exterior of any vehicle,
including fenders and running boards, nor while another person rides any
bicycle, coaster, roller skates, skateboard, sled, toy vehicle or other device
or object attached to a vehicle.
   C.   This section does not prohibit attaching a bicycle trailer or bicycle
semitrailer to a bicycle if the trailer or semitrailer was designed for the
attachment, nor to a commercial vehicle or a vehicle operated by or for a
political subdivision of this state designed to permit a passenger to ride on a
fender or running board, such as a fire department or trash collection truck.
(Ord. 2016-01, 2-18-2016)
6-4-12: OFF-ROAD RECREATIONAL VEHICLES:
Off-road recreational vehicles may be operated on the streets, roads and travel
routes under the control of the Town of Lyman subject to compliance with the
following requirements:
   A.   The off-road recreational vehicle shall display the current State of
Wyoming off-road recreational vehicle registration decal;
   B.   The operator must have a valid driver's license;
   C.   Crossings of main-travelled roadways by the off-road recreational
vehicle shall be made at right angles to the roadway or as nearly as
practicable, but in any case, yielding the right-of-way to all traffic in the
main-travelled roadway;
   D.   When operating at any time from one-half (1/2) hour after sunset to
one-half (1/2) hour before sunrise, the off-road recreational vehicle shall be
equipped with a use lighted lamp and illuminating devices in accordance with
Wyoming Statues § 31-5-910 through 31-5-940;
   E.    The off-road recreational vehicle shall be equipped with an adequate
braking device that may be operated either by hand or foot; and
   F.    The off-road recreational vehicle shall be equipped with a noise
muffler which produces a propulsion noise level of not more than one hundred
two (102) decibels at twenty (20) inches in a stationary test. (Ord. 2021-03,
5-6-2021)
6-4-13: INCIDENTAL OPERATION:
The occasional incidental operation of off-road recreational vehicles for non-
recreation purposes shall be permitted on town streets subject to requirement
set forth in Town Ordinance
6-4-12, but in addition, wherever practicable, the off-road recreational
vehicle shall be operated off the main-travelled portion of the Town street.
(Ord. 2021-03, 5-6-2021)
CHAPTER 5
PARKING
SECTION:
6-5-1: Prohibited Parking Locations
6-5-2: Obstruction Of Streets And Alleys
6-5-3: Proximity To Intersection
6-5-4: Double Parking
6-5-5: Distance From Fire Apparatus
6-5-6: Crosswalk And Curb Markings
6-5-7: Designated Parking Lines
6-5-8: Loading Zone
6-5-9: Wrong Direction
6-5-10: Permit Parking
6-5-11: Certain Trucks And Trailers Restricted
6-5-12: Parking On Street To Repair
6-5-13: Inoperable Motor Vehicles On Public Streets
6-5-14: Storage Of Vehicles
6-5-15: Keys In Ignition
6-5-16: Parades, Authority To Prohibit Parking
6-5-17: Registered Owner's Responsibility
6-5-18: Parking Tickets
6-5-19: Handicapped Parking
6-5-1: PROHIBITED PARKING LOCATIONS:
   A.   Locations Designated: No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle,
except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic or in compliance
with law, or the directions of a police officer or traffic control device in
any of the following places:
      1.   On a sidewalk.
      2.   In front of a public or private driveway.
      3.   Within an intersection.
      4.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure, street or within a
street tunnel.
      5.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping.
      6.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
      7.   On Highway U.S. 305 in the town, unless such vehicle is parallel to
the curb or curb line and not more than one foot (1') therefrom and not within
twenty feet (20') of any intersecting streets.
   B.   Moving Into Prohibited Area: No person shall move a vehicle not
lawfully under his control into any such prohibited area, or away from a curb
such distance as is unlawful.
   C.   Authority To Remove Vehicle: Whenever any police officer finds a
vehicle unattended in any such prohibited area, such officer is authorized to
provide for the removal of such vehicle to the nearest garage or other place of
safety at the expense of the owner of the vehicle. (1987 Code § 10.20.010)
6-5-2: OBSTRUCTION OF STREETS AND ALLEYS:
   A.   Prohibited; Responsibility: No person shall park or place in the
streets or alleys any vehicles or other thing obstructing or tending to
obstruct the free use of the streets and alleys, nor shall the owner,
proprietor or occupant of any premises within the town permit or allow the
streets and alleys abutting his property to be obstructed. In case the owner of
any unoccupied premises shall be a nonresident of the town or absent from the
town, any resident agent who shall have charge of such premises shall comply
with the requirements of this section.
   B.   Unattended Vehicle; Exception: It is unlawful for any operator to stop,
stand or park or leave unattended any vehicle in such a manner or under such
conditions as to leave available less than twenty feet (20') of the width of
the roadway for free movement of vehicular traffic; except that this provision
shall not apply to a necessary stop and obedience to traffic regulations or
traffic signs or signals of a police officer. (1987 Code § 10.20.020)
6-5-3: PROXIMITY TO INTERSECTION:
No person shall park, or leave standing, any vehicle within fifteen feet (15')
of any street intersection, whether posted or not posted. (Ord. 2015-07, 12-3-
2015)
6-5-4: DOUBLE PARKING:
It is unlawful for any vehicle to double park, that is, park the same between a
car properly parked at the curb and the center of the street whether the driver
physically is or is not in the vehicle. (1987 Code § 10.20.040)
6-5-5: DISTANCE FROM FIRE APPARATUS:
The driver of any vehicle other than one of official business shall not follow
any fire apparatus traveling in response to a fire alarm closer than five
hundred feet (500') or drive into or park such vehicle within the block where
fire apparatus has stopped in answer to a fire alarm. (1987 Code § 10.20.050)
6-5-6: CROSSWALK AND CURB MARKINGS:
No person shall stop, stand or park a vehicle, except when necessary to avoid
conflict with other traffic or in compliance with law or the directions of a
police officer or traffic control device in any of the following places:
   A.   Red Curb: At any place where the curb has been painted red; and
   B.   Pedestrian Crosswalk: Within any area designated in any manner as a
pedestrian crosswalk. (1987 Code § 10.20.060)
6-5-7: DESIGNATED PARKING LINES:
Every vehicle parked within areas set out by designated painted lines shall be
parked within those lines as defined in this chapter. It is unlawful to park
any vehicle contrary to the provisions of this section. (1987 Code § 10.20.090)
6-5-8: LOADING ZONE:
   A.   Private Driveway: It is unlawful for the operator of a vehicle to stop
or park such vehicle in front of a private driveway except temporarily for the
purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading passengers and in
no case shall such vehicle be left, even momentarily, unattended. (1987 Code §
10.20.080; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Passenger Zones: It is unlawful for the operator of a vehicle to stop,
stand or park such vehicle for a period of time longer than is necessary for
the actual loading or unloading of passengers in any place marked as a
passenger zone.
   C.   Loading Zones: It is unlawful for the operator of a vehicle to stop,
stand or park such vehicle for a period of time longer than is necessary for
the actual loading or unloading of passengers or for the loading and delivery
or pick up and loading of materials in any place marked as a loading zone.
   D.   Authority To Determine Zones: The chief of police shall have the
authority to determine the location of passenger zones and loading zones as
described in this section and shall erect and maintain appropriate signs
indicating the same. (1987 Code § 10.20.080)
6-5-9: WRONG DIRECTION:
Except when necessary in obedience to traffic regulations or traffic signs or
signals, the operator of a vehicle shall not stop, stand or park such vehicle
in a roadway other than parallel to the edge of the roadway, headed in the
direction of traffic and with the curb side wheels of the vehicle within twelve
inches (12") of the edge of the roadway and within the area designated by the
markings on the roadway; except, upon those streets which have been marked or
signed for angle parking, vehicles shall be parked at the angle to the curb
indicated by such marks or signs. (1987 Code § 10.20.110)
6-5-10: PERMIT PARKING:
   A.   Authority To Issue Permits: The chief of police is authorized to issue
to any owner of a vehicle used to transport merchandise or materials a special
permit, renewable annually and stating therein the terms and conditions
thereof, allowing the operator of such vehicle the privilege of loading or
unloading while the vehicle is backed against the curb if, in the opinion of
the governing body, such privilege is reasonably necessary in the conduct of
the owner's business and will not seriously interfere with traffic.
   B.   Restrictions On Parking: In places where and at hours when stopping for
the loading or unloading of merchandise or materials is permitted, vehicles
used for the transportation of merchandise or materials may back against the
curb to take on or discharge loads when the owner of such vehicle holds a
permit granting him such special privilege.
   C.   Permits In Possession; Decal: Such permits shall be either in the
possession of the operator, affixed by decal in a conspicuous place on the
vehicle at the time such vehicle is backed against the curb to take on or
discharge a load.
   D.   Violation: It is unlawful for any owner or operator to violate any of
the special terms or conditions of any special permit. (1987 Code § 10.20.100)
6-5-11: CERTAIN TRUCKS AND TRAILERS RESTRICTED:
   A.   Truck-Tractors And Trucks: The following are prohibited from parking in
all residential zoning districts of the town, except off street parking in R-
A zones:
      1.   Truck-tractors;
      2.   Trucks of two (2) ton capacity and larger;
      3.   Trucks having three (3) or more axles; or
      4.   Truck-tractors when connected with trailer and/or semitrailer in
truck trailer combination unit, are used, designed or maintained for
transportation of persons for hire, compensation or profit, or used, designed
or maintained primarily for the transportation of property for gain or profit.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/451a7fe2ce7093dd22169ecf11a0856268fb1c1b/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1631.jpg]
 
(The diagrams are for illustration purposes only and not intended to be all
inclusive to all makes and models of trucks and truck-tractors and
combinations.)
   B.   Affirmative Defense: It shall be an affirmative defense to subsection A
of this section if the said vehicle (truck-tractor only) is parked on a
driveway or other similarly improved property of the owner or operator, and the
vehicle is not left running or operating to thereby produce noise or emissions
while parked.
   C.   Trailers And Semitrailers: The following are prohibited from parking in
all residential zoning districts in town, except off street parking in R-
A zones:
      1.   Trailers and/or semitrailers exceeding thirty feet (30') in length;
      2.   Trailers and/or semitrailers having three (3) or more axles;
      3.   Trailers and/or semitrailers used, designed or maintained for
transportation of persons for hire, compensation or profit, or used, designed
or maintained primarily for the transportation of property for gain or profit.
[https://export.amlegal.com/media/451a7fe2ce7093dd22169ecf11a0856268fb1c1b/
IMAGES/0-0-0-1633.jpg]
 
(The diagrams are for illustration purposes only and not intended to be all
inclusive to all makes and models of trucks and truck-tractors and
combinations.)
   D.   Exception:
      1.   This section shall not prevent parking for brief periods of time
while the vehicle and/or trailer is attended for the loading and unloading of
goods and materials.
      2.   This section shall not prohibit the parking of said vehicles owned
or operated by the town, public utilities, contractors, or material men or
delivery trucks while making deliveries or while engaged in the repair,
maintenance or construction of streets, street improvements or utilities within
the town. (Ord. 2015-02, 5-21-2015)
6-5-12: PARKING ON STREET TO REPAIR:
It shall be unlawful for any garage, service station, mechanic, repairman or
owner to park any vehicle upon any public street when the vehicle is in
possession and custody of the garage, service station, mechanic, repairman or
owner for the purpose of repairing, improving, restoring or servicing the
vehicle. (Ord. 7-94, 1-19-1995)
6-5-13: INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLES ON PUBLIC STREETS 1 :
It shall be unlawful for owner, keeper and/or user of any inoperable motor
vehicle to use, operate or park the same on any public street, alley, highway,
sidewalk or parking area within the Town. (Ord. 2017-02, 2-2-2017)
 
Notes
1 1. See also chapter 8 of this title.
6-5-14: STORAGE OF VEHICLES:
   A.   Five Day Limit: It is unlawful for any person to store or park a travel
trailer, tent trailer, boat, boat trailer, snow vehicle, snow vehicle trailer,
ATV trailer, cycle trailer, utility trailer, horse trailer, pickup camper, or
similar vehicle on a Town street or alleyway for a period exceeding five (5)
consecutive days. Moving such a vehicle from one location to another on a Town
street or alley or from one Town street or alley to another shall not excuse a
violation of this section and shall not toll the five (5) day limit.
   B.   Removal After Notice: Provided, however, a person shall not be in
violation of this section if the person removes the vehicle from the Town
streets within twenty four (24) hours after notice of the violation has been
posted or attached to the vehicle.
   C.   Removal For Street Cleaning Or Snow Removal 1 : Any such vehicle parked
on the Town streets for periods of time long enough to hamper or make
impossible street cleaning or snow removal from said portion of the street
shall be, by notification of the owner by the Police Department, removed by the
owner to a location that will make cleaning and snow removal possible within
twenty four (24) hours of said notice.
   D.   Declared Nuisance: In addition, any vehicle found to be in violation of
this section shall be deemed a public nuisance and the Police Department is
hereby authorized to remove the vehicle to the nearest garage or other place of
safety at the expense of the owner. (Ord. 4-2001, 12-6-2001; amd. 2004 Code)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  8-1-10 of this Code.
6-5-15: KEYS IN IGNITION:
No person driving or in charge of a motor vehicle shall permit it to stand
unattended without first stopping the engine, locking the ignition, removing
the key and effectively setting the brake thereon and, when standing upon any
grade, turning the front wheels to the curb or side of the highway. (1987 Code
§ 10.20.070)
6-5-16: PARADES, AUTHORITY TO PROHIBIT PARKING:
The Chief of Police is authorized to prohibit parking by vehicles in zones and
areas during the time set aside by him for the purpose of parades. (1987 Code §
10.20.140)
6-5-17: REGISTERED OWNER'S RESPONSIBILITY:
Every registered owner of a vehicle shall be responsible for its operation by
every employee and other person using such vehicle with the consent, authority
or acquiescence of the owner. The violation of any part of this section by a
person other than the owner of such vehicle shall be and be deemed to be in
violation of this chapter by the registered owner of such vehicle and it shall
not be a defense to any charge made under this chapter that the owner of the
vehicle is not driving, operating or parking or having parked the same at the
time the violation occurred. (1987 Code § 10.20.120)
6-5-18: PARKING TICKETS:
   A.   Duty To Issue: It shall be the duty of every police officer, upon
finding a vehicle parked in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter,
to forthwith issue and affix to or deposit in such vehicle a parking ticket,
giving notice to the owner or operator of such vehicle of the parking
violation.
   B.   Required Information: Such parking ticket shall contain the following:
      1.   Name of owner or operator, if known, and if not known, notice shall
be directed to the owner or operator.
      2.   Vehicle make and license number of the offending vehicle.
      3.   Description of the violation by reference to the portion of this
chapter alleged to have been violated.
      4.   Date and time of the alleged violation.
      5.   Location of the alleged violation.
      6.   The reason indicated for the violation.
      7.   Summons directing the owner or operator of the offending vehicle to
appear before the municipal judge at the Lyman municipal court upon a date and
time certain to answer the alleged violation and be dealt with according to
law. (1987 Code § 10.20.130)
6-5-19: HANDICAPPED PARKING:
   A.   Prohibited: No person shall wilfully park a vehicle in violation of the
restrictions, regulations and prohibitions stated on signs specified under
Wyoming Statutes 31-5-501 and 31-5-111 unless that person or his/her passenger
has been issued and displays a distinctive handicapped license plate or
transferable handicapped placard by this or another state pursuant to Wyoming
Statutes 31-2-213 or its equivalent from another state.
   B.   Defined: "Park", as prohibited by this section, shall mean the standing
of a vehicle, whether occupied or not, and whether its engine is running or
not.
   C.   Violation: A violation of this section shall be considered a class B
misdemeanor pursuant to subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2015-01, 4-7-2015)
CHAPTER 6
SNOWMOBILES
SECTION:
6-6-1: Definition
6-6-2: Compliance Required
6-6-3: Prohibited Types
6-6-4: Roadway And Sidewalk Operation
6-6-5: Operator's License Required
6-6-6: Registration
6-6-7: Towing
6-6-8: Number Of Occupants Restricted
6-6-9: Safety Equipment
6-6-10: Mufflers
6-6-11: Brakes
6-6-12: Inspections
6-6-13: Hours Of Operation
6-6-14: Rules Of The Road
6-6-1: DEFINITION:
"Snowmobile" means any mechanically driven vehicle of a type which utilizes
sleet type runners, or skis or any endless belt tread or combination of these,
designed primarily for operation over snow. (1987 Code § 10.24.010; amd. 2004
Code)
6-6-2: COMPLIANCE REQUIRED:
No snowmobile shall be operated within the incorporated limits of the town
except upon compliance with this chapter. (1987 Code § 10.24.010; amd. 2004
Code)
6-6-3: PROHIBITED TYPES:
No snowmobile shall be operated within the incorporated limits which are
propeller driven or which have tracks capable of damaging road surfaces. (1987
Code § 10.24.020; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-4: ROADWAY AND SIDEWALK OPERATION:
Snowmobiles shall operate over designated roadways when the same are snowpacked
only, and such vehicles shall not be permitted to operate on the sidewalks.
(1987 Code § 10.24.030; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-5: OPERATOR'S LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall operate any snowmobile upon the streets and alleys of the town
unless such person shall first have obtained and have in his possession a motor
vehicle driver's license, a motor vehicle instruction permit or a power cycle
operator's permit. (1987 Code § 10.24.040; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-6: REGISTRATION:
No snowmobile shall be operated without a proper and valid registration from
the state. It is not the intent of this chapter to in any way limit the state's
control of snowmobiles while operated within the town. (1987 Code § 10.24.050;
amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-7: TOWING:
No snowmobile shall pull any skier, sled, or other combination vehicle by rope,
or flexible coupling. All sleighs or cutters shall be safely and securely
affixed to the snowmobile by direct coupling, solid tongue, or triangular tow
bar not to exceed forty inches (40") in length, being securely affixed to two
(2) points on the sleigh or cutter with one flexible joint at the center of the
snowmobile. (1987 Code § 10.24.060; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-8: NUMBER OF OCCUPANTS RESTRICTED:
No snowmobile shall be operated within the town while occupied by more than two
(2) persons and if a snowmobile is so operated, each occupant thereof is in
violation of this chapter. (1987 Code § 10.24.070; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-9: SAFETY EQUIPMENT:
It is a misdemeanor for any person to drive or move, or for the owner to cause
or knowingly permit to be driven or moved, on any roadway, any snowmobile or
combination of vehicles which is in such unsafe condition as to endanger any
persons or property, or which is not at all times equipped with such equipment
in proper condition and adjustment as required by this chapter, or which is
equipped in any manner in violation thereof. (1987 Code § 10.24.080; amd. 2004
Code)
6-6-10: MUFFLERS:
Every snowmobile shall be at all times equipped with a muffler in good working
order and in constant operation to prevent excessive or unusual noise and
annoying smoke. (1987 Code § 10.24.090; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-11: BRAKES:
Every snowmobile shall be equipped with brakes adequate to control the movement
of and to stop and hold such vehicle. (1987 Code § 10.24.100; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-12: INSPECTIONS:
   A.   Authority To Inspect: The chief of police, members of the state highway
patrol, and county law enforcement officers, upon reasonable cause to believe
that a snowmobile is unsafe or not equipped as required by this chapter, or
that its equipment is not in proper adjustment or repair, may require the
driver of such vehicle to stop and submit such vehicle to an inspection and
test.
   B.   Notice Of Defects: If the vehicle is found to be unsafe or improperly
or defectively equipped, notice of such defects shall be given to the driver of
the vehicle. No person shall operate any vehicle after receiving notice of
defects as above provided, except as may be necessary to return such vehicle to
the residence or place of business of the owner or driver or to a garage, until
the vehicle and its equipment have been placed in proper repair and adjustment
and otherwise made to conform to the requirements of this chapter. (1987 Code §
10.24.110; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-13: HOURS OF OPERATION:
No snowmobile shall be operated within the town between the hours of nine
thirty o'clock (9:30) P.M. and one-half (1/2) hour before sunrise. (1987 Code §
10.24.120; amd. 2004 Code)
6-6-14: RULES OF THE ROAD:
Every operator of a snowmobile shall observe all rules of the road and
ordinances of the town pertaining to the operation of vehicles, to the extent
that they are not in conflict with this chapter. In addition, every operator of
a snowmobile shall observe the following rules in operating the vehicle:
   A.   Yield Right Of Way: All snowmobiles shall yield the right of way to
motor vehicles.
   B.   Stopping: All snowmobiles shall come to a complete stop at each and
every intersection, when emerging from an alley or private property, and before
crossing any street.
   C.   Main Street: Snowmobiles shall not be operated on or along Main Street
except to cross said street at intersections.
   D.   Speed: No operator shall drive a snowmobile at a greater speed than is
reasonable and prudent under the conditions and having regard to the actual and
potential hazards then existing, and under no circumstances shall an operator
drive such vehicle at a speed in excess of fifteen (15) miles per hour on or
along any street or alley in the town. (1987 Code § 10.24.130; amd. 2004 Code)
CHAPTER 7
CHILD SAFETY RESTRAINT SYSTEMS
SECTION:
6-7-1: Definitions
6-7-2: Use Required
6-7-3: Penalty
6-7-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
CHILD SAFETY RESTRAINT SYSTEM: Any device which is designed to protect, hold or
restrain a child in a privately owned, leased or rented noncommercial passenger
car in such a way as to prevent or minimize injury to the child in the event of
a motor vehicle accident or sudden stop and which conforms to the standards
prescribed by 49 CFR 571.213 or to the applicable federal motor vehicle safety
standards in effect at the time of manufacture.
COMMERCIAL VEHICLE: Any vehicle or vehicle combination used for the
transportation of persons for hire, compensation or profit, or designed or used
primarily for the transportation of property for gain or profit.
EMERGENCY VEHICLE: Any fire department vehicle, police, sheriff's department or
highway patrol vehicle, civil defense vehicle, ambulance, hearse or other
vehicle used primarily for emergency purposes.
MOTOR VEHICLE: Every vehicle which is self-propelled.
PASSENGER CAR: A motor vehicle designed to carry eleven (11) persons or less
and primarily used to transport persons, excluding emergency vehicles,
motorcycles, motor homes, vans, pickups, church and school buses.
SCHOOL BUS: A motor vehicle that is owned by or leased to or registered to a
public school district or private school or church that is used to transport
children to or from school or church or in connection with school or church
activities and is designed for and capable of carrying twelve (12) or more
passengers.
SEATING POSITION: Any motor vehicle interior space intended by the motor
vehicle manufacturer to provide seating accommodation while the motor vehicle
is in motion. (1987 Code § 10.28.010)
6-7-2: USE REQUIRED:
   A.   Required: Except as otherwise provided in subsection B of this section,
no person shall operate a passenger vehicle in this state unless each child who
is a passenger in that vehicle and who has not reached his or her ninth
birthday is properly secured in a child safety restraint system in a seat of
the vehicle.
   B.   Exceptions: Any child who is within the age requirements specified in
subsection A of this section need not be properly secured in a child safety
restraint system if a licensed physician has determined that the physical or
medical condition of the child requires that the child not be secured in such a
system. The person operating a passenger car transporting such a child shall
carry in the car the physician's signed statement certifying that the child
should not be secured in a child restraint system. (Ord. 2015-08, 12-3-2015)
6-7-3: PENALTY:
   A.   Fine:
      1.   First Violation: Any person who violates this chapter shall be
issued a citation and fined not more than twenty five dollars ($25.00) for the
first offense; provided, that the fine shall be waived by the court upon
receipt of proof by the court that the offender has purchased, leased or
otherwise acquired a child safety restraint system which meets the requirements
of this chapter.
      2.   Second Or Subsequent Violation: For a second or subsequent violation
of this chapter, the offender shall be fined not more than one hundred dollars
($100.00).
   B.   Use Not In Accordance With Manufacturer's Instructions: Any person who
uses a child safety restraint system in a manner other than in accordance with
the manufacturer's instructions is guilty of a violation of this chapter and
shall be fined as provided in subsection A of this section. (1987 Code §
10.28.030)
   C.   Effect Limited: Violation of this chapter does not constitute evidence
of negligence or recklessness and does not constitute a basis for criminal
prosecution except as set forth in this chapter. (1987 Code § 10.28.040)
CHAPTER 8
INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLES 1
SECTION:
6-8-1: Definitions
6-8-2: Keeping Of Inoperable Vehicles
6-8-3: Keeper Considered Owner
6-8-4: One Inoperable Vehicle Permitted
6-8-5: Two Inoperable Vehicles
6-8-6: Three Or More Inoperable Vehicles
6-8-7: Exemptions
6-8-8: Effective Date; Compliance
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  12-12-5 of this code.
6-8-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter unless the context otherwise indicates:
ADJACENT PROPERTY OWNERS: The owners of property that are immediately abutting
the subject property, excluding streets and rights of way.
ADMINISTRATIVE PERMIT: Special authorization granted from the chief of police
or his designated representative for the purpose of keeping more than one, but
no more than two (2) inoperable vehicles.
COVERED: The vehicle has securely attached to it some form of material or tarp
so as to hide, shield or otherwise protect the vehicle from view and accidents,
and the covering is maintained in a state of good repair.
INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLE: A vehicle that is, without alteration, unable to
legally and safely be operated on a public street or highway, including the
possession of applicable current registration and valid proof of insurance.
REAR OR SIDE YARD: That portion of the yard behind the front line of the house
extended to each side property line.
SAFE CONDITION: A motor vehicle kept in such condition including, but not
limited to, the following:
   A.   The vehicle must be removed from jacks or other blocking materials that
would otherwise permit the vehicle to fall.
   B.   The vehicle does not create a condition where a person or animal could
become trapped inside or underneath.
   C.   There be no sharp metal or glass where one may be easily cut, punctured
or otherwise injured. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998; amd. Ord. 2006-11, 7-20-2006; Ord.
2017-02, 2-2-2017)
6-8-2: KEEPING OF INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
The keeping of inoperable vehicles shall be permitted within all zones in the
town on private property in accordance with town ordinances, including this
chapter, chapter 5 of this title and title 4, chapter 1 of this code. (Ord. 6-
97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-3: KEEPER CONSIDERED OWNER:
Any person who shall keep, place or permit any inoperable motor vehicle on or
about his premises shall be considered and held to be the owner of such
inoperable motor vehicle and responsible therefor under the terms of this
chapter. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-4: ONE INOPERABLE VEHICLE PERMITTED:
Any property owner within any zone in the town may keep one inoperable motor
vehicle; provided, that such one vehicle is kept in the rear or side yard and
in a safe condition. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-5: TWO INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   Administrative Permit Required: Any property owner within any zone in
the town may keep two (2) inoperable motor vehicles; provided, that an
administrative permit is first obtained from the chief of police or his
designated representative. The chief or his representative shall first ensure
that:
      1.   All inoperable vehicles shall be kept in the rear or side yard;
      2.   All inoperable vehicles are kept in a safe condition; and
      3.   All surrounding property owners are notified and do not have
unreasonable objections to the subject property owner keeping two (2)
inoperable motor vehicles.
   B.   Signatures Of Surrounding Property Owners:
      1.   Required: Notification shall be made by the applicant obtaining
signatures from the surrounding property owners on a form prepared by the chief
of police or his designated representative.
      2.   Form: Said form shall include the names and addresses of all
surrounding property owners, a signature line for each property owner to sign
in favor or in opposition, and the details of the request being made, including
any conditions imposed by ordinance or by the chief or his representative. Upon
the applicant obtaining signatures in favor of the permit, the chief shall
issue the administrative permit.
   C.   Additional Conditions: The chief or his representative may also require
any other reasonable conditions that will ensure that keeping the two (2)
inoperable vehicles will not be detrimental to the subject property,
surrounding properties, or the town. Such reasonable conditions may include
time limits, location requirements, coverings, etc.
   D.   Denial; Appeal: If the applicant for an administrative permit is
denied, the applicant may appeal to the planning and zoning commission for a
conditional use permit as specified in title 12, chapter 12 of this code.
   E.   Fee: The fee for an administrative permit to keep two (2) inoperable
vehicles shall be determined by the town council. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-6: THREE OR MORE INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   Criteria For Requiring Conditional Use Permit: Any one of the following
criteria shall cause the applicant property owner to obtain a conditional use
permit:
      1.   A signature of objection on the notification form for surrounding
property owners applying for an administrative permit for two (2) inoperable
vehicles;
      2.   A denied application for an administrative permit; or
      3.   Failure to comply with any conditions required in section
6-8-4 or
6-8-5 of this chapter.
   B.   Permit Required: Any property owner within any zone in the town may
keep three (3) or more inoperable motor vehicles; provided, that they first
obtain a conditional use permit from the planning and zoning commission. (Ord.
6-97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-7: EXEMPTIONS:
The requirements of this chapter shall not apply to:
   A.   Inoperable vehicles kept in an enclosed garage or storage building; or
   B.   Persons licensed in accordance with Wyoming Statutes section 31-13-114.
(Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998)
6-8-8: EFFECTIVE DATE; COMPLIANCE:
The provisions of this chapter shall take effect on June 1, 1998. All property
owners in the town will be subject to the provisions of this chapter. There
will be no nonconforming uses regarding keeping inoperable motor vehicles. All
property owners will have until June 1, 1998, to conform with the provisions of
this chapter. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998)
CHAPTER 9
PENALTY
SECTION:
6-9-1: Violation; Penalty
6-9-1: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any violation of the provisions of this title constitutes a class B misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code, except the following which constitute a class A
misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code:
   A.   Driving under the influence pursuant to Wyoming Statutes section 31-5-
233 through 234 and/or section
6-4-7 of this title.
   B.   Eluding a police officer pursuant to Wyoming Statutes section 31-5-225
and/or section
6-4-6 of this title.
   C.   Reckless driving pursuant to Wyoming Statutes section 31-5-229 and/or
section
6-4-2 of this title.
   D.   Operating a motor vehicle without a required interlock device pursuant
to Wyoming Statutes section 31-7-404.
   E.   Operating a motor vehicle without insurance pursuant to section
6-3-5 of this title.
   F.   Operating a motor vehicle while a license is canceled, suspended or
revoked pursuant to section
6-3-4 of this title. (Ord. 2017-03, 2-2-2017)
TITLE 7
FIRE REGULATIONS 1
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
7-1-1: Established
7-1-2: Organization
7-1-3: Officers
7-1-4: Duties
7-1-5: Police Authority
7-1-6: Records; Reports
7-1-7: Loaning Apparatus
7-1-8: Alarms Outside Town Limits
7-1-9: Indebtedness
7-1-10: Interfering With Fire Department
7-1-11: Inspections
7-1-12: Right Of Entry
7-1-13: Water Department Cooperation
7-1-14: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  9-2-5 of this code for adoption of the uniform fire code.
7-1-1: ESTABLISHED:
There is created the fire department of the town, whose duties it shall be to
prevent and extinguish fires, to educate the public in all matters pertaining
to fires and fire prevention, to care for all fire apparatus and other town
property in its charge and perform such other duties as may be assigned to it
by the mayor or town council. (1987 Code § 2.20.010)
7-1-2: ORGANIZATION:
