   A.   Fire Companies: The fire department may consist of a hose company, a
ladder company, a salvage company and such additional companies as may be
authorized by vote of a majority of the members of the fire department, subject
to the approval of the town council.
   B.   Bylaws: The fire department shall adopt suitable bylaws for the
government of the department, such as are not in conflict with town ordinances
or state and national laws, subject to the approval of the town council. These
bylaws and all fire prevention ordinances shall be posted and maintained in a
conspicuous place in each fire station and filed with the town clerk, together
with any revisions and additions. (1987 Code § 2.20.020)
7-1-3: OFFICERS:
   A.   Designated: Officers of the fire department may include chief,
assistant chief, secretary, treasurer, and for each organized company, a
captain and a lieutenant, and such other officers as may be provided for in the
bylaws of the fire department. Officers and members shall be selected as
provided for in the bylaws.
   B.   Chief; Assistant Chief: No member shall assume the office of chief or
assistant chief whose entire time, both day and night, is not habitually spent
within the town limits, and who has not been a member of the fire department
for at least two (2) years, except when less than five (5) members are thus
qualified. (1987 Code § 2.20.030)
7-1-4: DUTIES:
   A.   Obey Superiors: It shall be the duty of each officer and member of the
fire department to obey without question the orders of his superior officers at
all times while in the fire station or at or going to or returning from fires.
   B.   Wear Uniform Or Insignia: Each member of the fire department shall wear
at all times when on duty such distinctive uniform or insignia as shall be
prescribed in the bylaws.
   C.   Chief's Duties:
      1.   Discipline, Good Order And Proper Conduct: The chief of the fire
department shall be responsible for the discipline, good order and proper
conduct of the whole fire department, for the enforcement of all ordinances and
regulations pertaining thereto, and for the care and condition of the hoses,
fire apparatus, and all other property of the department or in its charge.
      2.   Command And Control: The chief shall have command and control of all
officers and members of the department, and of all hoses, fire apparatus and
other property of the department or in its charge.
      3.   Summon Able Bodied Persons To Assist: The chief likewise shall have
control of all persons present at fires and shall have power, if need be, to
summon any and all able bodied persons present to aid in extinguishing any
fire, in removing property from any burning and exposed building and in
guarding the same, and any able bodied person refusing to obey such summons
shall be liable to the penalties as provided in section
7-2-5 of this title.
   D.   Absence Of Chief: In the absence of the chief when responding to
alarms, the assistant chief, captain, lieutenant or senior member present, in
order of rank and seniority, shall assume the duties and full authority of the
chief until the arrival of a superior officer.
   E.   Leaving Scene Of Fire: After responding to an alarm, no member shall
leave the scene of the fire or the apparatus until the fire shall have been
extinguished and the apparatus returned to the station and properly cared for,
except by permission of the commanding officer. (1987 Code § 2.20.040)
7-1-5: POLICE AUTHORITY:
   A.   Authority: The fire chief and members acting under his order shall have
full and complete police powers and authority within the fire station, as to
all matters pertaining to the fire department and shall also have authority to
make arrests for violations of all town ordinances, the enforcement of which is
under his jurisdiction. The chief of police and all members of the police
department shall cooperate with him in the enforcement of the above mentioned
ordinances.
   B.   Limits At Fires: The chief of the fire department may prescribe limits
at fires within which no person shall be admitted except by this order. (1987
Code § 2.20.050)
7-1-6: RECORDS; REPORTS:
   A.   Record Of Activities; Report To Council: The fire chief shall keep or
cause to be kept a complete record of the activities of the fire department and
shall make a thorough investigation of each fire and report to the mayor and
town council at least quarterly, giving in detail the following information in
regard to each, if available: cause, location, time, owner, tenant, occupancy,
type of building, insurance carried, insurance paid, building loss, contents
loss, how extinguished, apparatus used, firemen present, adequacy of water
supply and pressure, and any other information of value.
   B.   Inventory Of Property: The fire chief, immediately after assuming
office and annually thereafter, shall make an inventory of all property owned
by the fire department or in its charge, noting the condition of each article,
which shall be submitted to the mayor and town council, together with
recommendations for the purchase of additional equipment needed and any other
recommendations he may desire to submit affecting the fire department.
   C.   Inspection Of Fire Hydrants: The fire chief shall inspect or cause to
be inspected by members of the fire department, at least twice annually and
more often if needed, all fire hydrants and shall list those needing attention
in his next report to the council.
   D.   Membership List: The chief shall also maintain in the office of the
town clerk an accurate list of the members of the fire department and shall
report promptly any additions or withdrawals from the membership.
   E.   Loss Or Damage To Equipment; Accidents: Loss of or damage to equipment
and accidents involving members of the fire department in the performance of
their duties shall be reported immediately to the mayor and council by the fire
chief. (1987 Code § 2.20.060)
7-1-7: LOANING APPARATUS:
Fire apparatus and other town property in charge of the fire department shall
not be loaned or rented except by permission of the fire chief and with the
approval of a majority of the membership of the fire department. (1987 Code §
2.20.070)
7-1-8: ALARMS OUTSIDE TOWN LIMITS:
The fire department shall not respond to alarms outside of the corporate
limits, leaving the town unprotected, except that not more than one-half (1/2)
of the membership may respond to such alarms with reserve equipment, only when
authorized to do so by the fire chief. (1987 Code § 2.20.080)
7-1-9: INDEBTEDNESS:
No member of the fire department or other person shall contract any
indebtedness on behalf of the fire department. (1987 Code § 2.20.090)
7-1-10: INTERFERING WITH FIRE DEPARTMENT:
   A.   Entering Fire Station: No person shall be allowed to enter the fire
station unless accompanied by a member of the fire department.
   B.   Performance Of Duties: No person shall interfere in any way with the
fire department in the performance of its duties.
   C.   Use Of Apparatus: No person not a member of the fire department shall
use any of the fire apparatus at fires or otherwise unless acting under orders
of the commanding officer.
   D.   Drivers Hearing Alarm: Upon hearing an alarm of fire all drivers of
vehicles shall take due warning and upon the approach of fire apparatus shall
move promptly to the right curb and stop in order to leave clear the center of
the street.
   E.   Following Fire Apparatus: Vehicles shall not follow fire apparatus
nearer than one full block and shall not proceed to any point within one full
block of the fire.
   F.   Driving Over Fire Hose: Vehicles shall not be driven over the fire hose
or other apparatus.
   G.   Prohibited Parking: Vehicles shall not be parked within fifteen feet
(15') of any fire hydrant or before the entrance of any theater, hall, or other
building in which large public assemblages are held.
   H.   False Alarm: No person shall knowingly give a false alarm other than
those for test purposes given by the fire chief.
   I.   Interfering With Alarm System: No person shall interfere with any part
of the fire alarm system unless so authorized by the fire chief of the fire
department. (1987 Code § 2.20.100)
   J.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class A misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
7-1-11: INSPECTIONS:
   A.   Duty To Inspect: It shall be the duty of the fire chief to inspect or
cause to be inspected by the fire department officers or members, as often as
may be necessary, but not less than twice a year in outlying districts and four
(4) times a year in the closely built portions of the town, all buildings,
premises and public thoroughfares, except the interiors of private dwellings,
for the purpose of ascertaining and causing to be corrected any conditions
liable to cause fire, or any violations of the provisions or intent of any
ordinance of the town affecting the fire hazard.
   B.   Order To Remove Or Remedy: Whenever any officer or member shall find in
any building, or upon any premises or other place, combustible or explosive
matter or dangerous accumulation of rubbish or unnecessary accumulation of
waste paper, boxes, shavings or any other highly inflammable materials
especially liable to fire, and which is so situated as to endanger property, or
shall find obstruction to fire escapes, stairs, passageways, doors or windows
liable to interfere with the operations of the fire department, or egress of
occupants, in case of fire, or shall find any other conditions dangerous to
life or property by reason of the fire hazard, he shall order the same to be
removed or remedied, and such order shall forthwith be complied with by the
owner or occupant of such premises or buildings, subject to appeal within
twenty four (24) hours to the mayor, who shall, within ten (10) days, review
such order and file his decision thereon, and unless the order is revoked or
modified, it shall remain in full force and be obeyed by such owner or
occupant.
   C.   Failure To Comply: Any owner or occupant failing to comply with such
order within ten (10) days after said appeal shall have been determined, or if
no appeal is taken, then within ten (10) days after the service of the said
order, shall be liable to a penalty as stated in section
1-4-1 of this code.
   D.   Authority Of Fire Chief: The fire chief shall have authority to order
the immediate discontinuance of the use of any stove, stovepipe, flue, furnace,
electric wiring or other hazardous device, pending the result of the appeal.
(1987 Code § 2.20.110)
7-1-12: RIGHT OF ENTRY:
The fire chief and members acting under his orders shall have authority to
enter any building in the proper performance of their duties. (1987 Code §
2.20.120)
7-1-13: WATER DEPARTMENT COOPERATION:
The water department shall cooperate with the fire department in every way
possible to provide an adequate supply of water at pressures suitable for
firefighting and shall supply the fire department one or more accurate maps of
the distributing system, showing the size and location of all mains, valves and
fire hydrants, which shall be posted and maintained in a conspicuous place in
each fire station, and shall report promptly to the fire department the opening
and closing of all valves in street mains and any other information relative to
the water supply to any and all parts of town, which information shall also be
posted for the information of the firemen and others. (1987 Code § 2.20.130)
7-1-14: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE AND EXPLOSION HAZARDS
SECTION:
7-2-1: Burning
7-2-2: Trash, Rags And Ash Accumulations
7-2-3: Explosives
7-2-4: Fireworks
7-2-5: Penalty
7-2-1: BURNING:
   A.   Permission Required: It is unlawful for any person to burn or cause to
be burned any garbage, waste, trash, weeds or other materials, within the
corporate limits of the town, without having first obtained written permission
from the fire chief. The fire chief may grant such permission if, in his
opinion, the burning of the materials described in this section can be
accomplished without danger to adjoining property or undue contamination to the
air or offense to others in the vicinity.
   B.   Liability: The town shall not be held to assume any liability by reason
of having granted permission to burn any of the materials mentioned in this
section if such burning should cause damage to another person's property.
   C.   Term Of Permission: The permission granted shall be valid for only
forty eight (48) hours from the time of issuance. (1987 Code § 8.08.010)
7-2-2: TRASH, RAGS AND ASH ACCUMULATIONS:
   A.   Combustible Materials: No person or persons shall allow to remain
longer than thirty six (36) hours, or overnight, in any alley, or on any
sidewalk or premises, within thirty feet (30') of any building, empty boxes,
wastepaper, rubbish, trash, or other combustible materials.
   B.   Ashes:
      1.   Prohibited: No person or persons shall be allowed to place ashes
within any building in any box or other wooden vessel or upon any wooden vessel
or floor.
      2.   Receptacle; Ash Pit: No ashes shall be kept or deposited in any part
of the town unless the same shall be kept in a secure incombustible container,
and every owner of property where ashes are kept or deposited shall erect upon
the premises a secured incombustible receptacle or ash pit for that purpose, so
located as not to endanger walls, fences and other combustible material.
   C.   Oily Waste; Oily Rags: No person shall keep or permit to be kept on the
premises any oily waste or oily rags, unless at all times when not actually in
use such oily waste and oily rags are kept in a metal can with self-closing
cover and riveted joints, standing on metal legs which raise the bottom of the
container at least five inches (5") above the floor. (1987 Code § 8.08.020)
7-2-3: EXPLOSIVES:
   A.   Prohibited Explosives; Exception: It is unlawful to store or keep any
dynamite, nitroglycerin or other explosives other than gunpowder in any
storeroom or building or on any premises within the town limits. A limit of
five (5) pounds of gunpowder may be stored in sealed metal containers.
   B.   Gunpowder, Permit Required: Any person, firm or corporation who sells
or stores gunpowder shall obtain a permit from the fire chief, who shall
inspect the place where the gunpowder is kept. (1987 Code § 8.08.050)
   C.   Penalty: A violation of this section constitutes a class A misdemeanor
punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A1 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
7-2-4: FIREWORKS:
   A.   Definition: For purposes of this section, "fireworks" includes any item
which may be sold or offered for sale under federal law as contained within 15
United States Code section 1261; 21 United States Code section 371; and 16 CFR,
commercial practices, part 1507 and/or any article, device or substance
prepared for the primary purpose of producing a visual or auditory sensation by
combustion, explosion, deflagration or detonation including, without
limitation, the following articles and devices commonly known and used as
fireworks:
      1.   Toy cannons or toy canes in which explosives are used;
      2.   Blank cartridges;
      3.   Firecrackers;
      4.   Bottle rockets;
      5.   Squibs or other crackers;
      6.   Torpedoes;
      7.   Skyrockets; and
      8.   Roman candles.
   B.   Prohibitions:
      1.   Discharge; Detonation: Unless otherwise authorized by the Town
Council, the discharge or detonation of any fireworks at any time within the
limits of the Town is strictly prohibited.
      2.   Minors: Individuals under the age of majority shall not sell, buy,
detonate or discharge any approved fireworks, unless they are accompanied by an
adult.
      3.   Penalty: Violations of this subsection B shall, upon conviction, be
punished pursuant to subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. The detonation or discharge of each firework may
constitute a separate violation.
   C.   Exceptions:
      1.   Power To Ban: The Town Council, Chief of Police, and/or Fire Chief,
at their discretion, may put a ban on the discharge of fireworks at any time,
including the type and/or the approved period by resolution or proclamation.
Any ban of the sale or discharge of fireworks in or adjacent to the Town by an
authorized State, Federal or County official shall constitute a ban within the
Town. (Ord. 2016-09, 9-15-2016)
      2.   Discharge; Detonation Allowed: The detonation or discharge of
fireworks within the Town shall be allowed each year as follows:
         a.   From nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. until twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight on July 4. (Ord. 2018-07, 8-16-2018)
         b.   From nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. until twelve o'clock (12:00)
midnight on the day (Saturday) of the official Town Pioneer Days celebration.
         c.   From five o'clock (5:00) P.M. on December 31 until two o'clock
(2:00) A.M. on January 1.
      3.   Public Display: The Mayor or Town Council may authorize the public
display of fireworks by properly qualified individuals; provided, that such
display or displays shall be of such character and so located, discharged or
fired, as in the opinion of the Fire Chief, they shall not be hazardous to
surrounding property or endanger any person or persons.
   D.   Licensing:
      1.   Transient Merchant: Any transient merchant desiring to sell
fireworks must also comply with title 3, chapter 4 of this Code.
      2.   Inspection; Approval Required: Prior to the issuance of a business
license, the Fire Chief must inspect and approve sales and storage areas. Said
approval must be in writing and delivered to the Town Clerk prior to the
issuance of a business license.
   E.   Removal: The Fire Chief may, at his own discretion, remove or have
removed, at the owner's expense, all stocks of fireworks, or other combustibles
exposed for sale or held in stock, in violation of this section.
(Ord. 2016-09, 9-15-2016; amd. Ord. 2024-03, 9-4-2024)
7-2-5: PENALTY:
   A.   Penalty: Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of
this chapter constitutes a Class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
   B.   Members Of Fire Department: Members of the Fire Department, when acting
as such, violating this chapter or chapter 1 of this title shall be dealt with
in accordance with the bylaws of the Fire Department.
   C.   Enforced Removal: The application of the penalty set forth in
subsections A and B of this section shall not be held to prevent the enforced
removal of prohibited conditions and the imposition of one penalty for any
violation of this chapter or chapter 1 of this title shall not excuse the
violation, or permit it to continue.
   D.   Required To Correct Or Remedy Violations: All persons convicted thereof
shall be required to correct or remedy such violations or defects within a
reasonable time. (1987 Code § 8.08.050)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
USE AND CLOSURE GENERALLY
SECTION:
8-1-1: Barricading Of Excavations
8-1-2: Tearing Up Pavement
8-1-3: Damaging Street Signs
8-1-4: Placing Materials On Public Way
8-1-5: Erecting Posts Or Poles
8-1-6: Deposit Of Petroleum Products
8-1-7: Cellar Doors; Subterraneous Openings
8-1-8: Closing Streets
8-1-9: Duty Of The Town Concerning Snow Removal
8-1-10: Removal Of Vehicles For Snowplowing And Removal
8-1-11: Ice And Snow Accumulations
8-1-99: Penalty
8-1-1: BARRICADING OF EXCAVATIONS:
When any street in the Town must be excavated, including any Town property,
extending from any private property line to another property line, the earth
shall be deposited in a manner that will occasion the least inconvenience to
the public and provide for the passage of water along the gutters. No person
shall make any excavations or dig any hole, drain or ditch in any street or
alley within the Town without providing a temporary fence or barricade around
the same in order to prevent persons, animals, or vehicles from falling into
the same. (1987 Code § 12.04.010)
8-1-2: TEARING UP PAVEMENT 1 :
No person shall tear up or injure any pavement including curb or gutter or
sidewalk within the Town without authority, in writing, from the Town. (1987
Code § 12.04.020)
 
Notes
1 1. See also chapter 3 of this title.
8-1-3: DAMAGING STREET SIGNS:
It is unlawful for any person to deface, mar or damage any street signs within
the Town. (1987 Code § 12.04.030)
8-1-4: PLACING MATERIALS ON PUBLIC WAY:
It is unlawful for any person to cause or permit any building materials,
machinery, sand, dirt, or other object to be in or upon the streets, alleys, or
sidewalks of the Municipality without first obtaining a permit from the Town
for such use of streets, alleys, or sidewalks; provided, that whenever a permit
is issued, such permit shall carry the right to place materials, machinery or
other objects upon the streets, alleys, or sidewalks, subject to the conditions
as are deemed necessary for the safety of persons on or about such streets,
alleys or sidewalks and which are set forth in such permit. (1987 Code §
12.04.040)
8-1-5: ERECTING POSTS OR POLES:
No person shall encroach into or upon any of the sidewalks, streets, or alleys
of the Town by erecting or maintaining thereon a pole, post or other structure
used in the transmission of electric current by wire, including electric light,
telegraph or telephone poles, or attach or maintain upon such poles, posts or
other structures any wire for any purpose whatsoever, except in accordance with
the rights conferred by the Governing Body. (1987 Code § 12.04.050)
8-1-6: DEPOSIT OF PETROLEUM PRODUCTS:
No person shall drain or deposit upon any street, sidewalk, alley, park or
public place or into any sump, gutter, catch basin, manhole, conduit, sewer,
lake or waterway in the Municipality any tar, asphaltum, gasoline, lubricating
oil, greases, waste oil from automobile or truck crank cases, or any byproduct
of petroleum. (1987 Code § 12.04.060)
8-1-7: CELLAR DOORS; SUBTERRANEOUS OPENINGS:
No person shall allow any cellar door, pit, vault or other subterraneous
opening on or adjacent to any highway or sidewalk to be left or kept open or in
an unsecured condition so that passersby will be in danger of falling into such
cellar, pit, vault or other subterraneous opening. (1987 Code § 12.04.070)
8-1-8: CLOSING STREETS:
The Chief of Police is authorized to temporarily close any street, alley or
public way or portion thereof, while such street, alley or public way is
undergoing construction, alteration or repair or being involved in special
work. In closing such street, alley or public way, the Chief of Police shall
cause to be erected appropriate barricades, signs and warnings sufficient to
fairly apprise the public thereof. (1987 Code § 12.04.080)
8-1-9: DUTY OF THE TOWN CONCERNING SNOW REMOVAL:
It shall be the duty of the Town to promptly address the clearing of the
roadways in the Town when there is an accumulation of snow, ice and/or other
debris upon a public street, alley, or right-of-way. The Town shall prioritize
health and safety in determining the schedule and manner of the plowing of
streets and removing of snow, as well as clearing sidewalks adjacent to Town
owned properties and keeping melted runoff flowing into storm drains and other
water-clearing channels. The removal of accumulations may be superseded by
other Town emergencies, such as water line breaks or other emergency response,
as well as the employment status and hours worked of Town employees. The Mayor
may approve the temporary emergency hiring of employees, contractors and/or
equipment to address emergencies in extreme situations. Nothing in this section
is intended to, nor is to be read as creating a cause of action for any person
for failure of the Town to remove accumulations to their desired specifications
or schedule. (Ord. 2019-04, 5-2-2019)
8-1-10: REMOVAL OF VEHICLES FOR SNOWPLOWING AND REMOVAL:
It shall be the duty of all persons owning vehicles, trailers or other
apparatus parked upon the streets of the Town, to remove such vehicles,
trailers or other apparatus from the streets from the hours of six o'clock (6:
00) P.M. until nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. on each night between October 31st
until April 30th of the following year. Nothing in this section shall be read
to supersede or interfere with the Town's additional ability to have vehicles
removed pursuant to subsection
6-5-14C of this Code. In addition to the remedies contained within section
8-1-99 of this chapter, the Public Works Director and/or law enforcement may
have any vehicle violating this section towed at the owner's expense. (Ord.
2019-04, 5-2-2019)
8-1-11: ICE AND SNOW ACCUMULATIONS:
No person shall cause or permit snow, ice and/or other debris to be deposited
upon a public street, alley, or right-of-way, except snow removed from street
adjacent sidewalks and gutters may be deposited on top of accumulated snow
placed on the street by the Town and/or its designee or assign. Should any
deposit of snow on top of snow moved or placed by the Town and/or its designee
or assign become a hazard as determined by an official representative of the
Town, the State Department of Transportation and/or law enforcement, the
adjacent land owner may be required to immediately remove or alter said
deposit. Any deposit of snow and/or ice not in conformity to this section shall
be prima facie evidence that it was so placed by the owner, occupant or manager
of the adjacent tenements or grounds. (Ord. 2019-04, 5-2-2019)
8-1-99: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a Class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013; amd. Ord. 2019-04, 5-2-2019)
CHAPTER 2
SIDEWALKS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Duty To Clean
8-2-2: Penalty
8-2-1: DUTY TO CLEAN:
All persons shall keep the sidewalks and gutters in front of and adjacent to
the tenements or ground owned, occupied or managed by them clear of ice, mud,
dirt, rubbish, filth, leaves, plants, tree limbs, roots, vegetation or other
obstructions. All trees, bushes, shrubs, and plants within the Town of Lyman
shall be maintained by the landowners, occupiers or managers in such a manner
as to prevent encroachment into the space above the said sidewalks. All owners,
occupiers and managers shall edge their lawns in such a manner as to prevent
vegetation from encroaching upon adjacent sidewalks. After any fall of snow,
said persons shall cause the snow to be immediately removed from such sidewalks
and gutters. (Ord. 2007-12, 9-6-2007; amd. Ord. 2023-04, 11-2-2023)
8-2-2: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 3
CONSTRUCTION, REPAIR AND EXCAVATIONS 1
SECTION:
8-3-1: Excavation License
8-3-2: Driveway And Parking Strip Permit
8-3-3: Breaking Through Pavement
8-3-4: Piling Excavated Materials
8-3-5: Cleanup
8-3-6: Maintaining Gutter Flow
8-3-7: Disposal Of Mud And Runoff
8-3-8: Backfilling
8-3-9: Restoration Of Surface
8-3-10: Penalty
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  9-3-1 of this code.
8-3-1: EXCAVATION LICENSE:
   A.   Required: A license shall be required prior to any person commencing
work upon any excavation, construction or repair of water and/or sewer lines,
cables, poles, or lines located in or on any street, alleyway and easement of
the town. (1987 Code § 12.12.010)
   B.   Form Of License: The license required in subsection A of this section
shall be in the following form:
   TOWN OF LYMAN, WYOMING
   LICENSE
The Town of Lyman, Wyoming (hereinafter called the "Town"), hereby grants a
license to                                     (hereinafter called the
"Licensee") to install and operate (hereinafter called the "Utility"), upon the
property of the Town of Lyman in the locations and positions shown or printed
on the reverse side, marked Exhibit "A" and in strict accordance with the "Town
of Lyman, Wyoming Standards and Specifications".
The foregoing license is subject to the following conditions:
FIRST: The work of installing the utility shall be commenced by the Licensee
only after the execution of this agreement by the parties hereto. Further, the
Town Clerk shall be notified immediately prior to the time of commencement.
SECOND: The Licensee shall perform all necessary work on the installation of
the utility and the cost of such work shall be borne by the Licensee. The work
to be performed by the Licensee shall include the following:
   (a) Sub-excavation of all unstable material and compaction of all backfill
or special backfill to a density of ninety five percent (95%).
   (b) All backfill shall be placed to the top of the subgrade and the surface
course or courses shall be replaced by materials presently composing the
surface course or courses.
   (c) Furnish, provide, erect and maintain all necessary precautions for the
protection of the work and safety of the public at the installation area.
THIRD: In case settlement or failure occurs after Licensee has completed
backfilling and resurfacing utility cut, the Town will correct such settlement,
or failure, and all labor, material and equipment required to make such
correction will be billed to the Licensee.
(1987 Code § 12.12.020)
8-3-2: DRIVEWAY AND PARKING STRIP PERMIT:
Except where included in a building permit, no person shall commence work on
the construction, alteration, repair or removal of any driveway or the paving
of any parking strip on any street, alley or other public place in the town
without a written permit first having been obtained from the town clerk. (1987
Code § 12.12.030)
8-3-3: BREAKING THROUGH PAVEMENT:
The following provisions shall be applicable where any excavation requires
breaking through pavement:
   A.   Heavy Duty Pavement Breakers: Heavy duty pavement breakers may be
prohibited by the administrative official when the use endangers existing
substructures or other property.
   B.   Saw Cutting: Saw cutting of cement concrete may be required by the
administrative official when the nature of the job or the condition of the
street warrants.
   C.   Cutting Ahead Of Excavation: Approved cutting of bituminous pavement
surface ahead of excavations may be required by the administrative official to
confine pavement damage to the limits of the trench.
   D.   Removal Of Sidewalk Sections: Sections of sidewalks shall be removed to
the nearest score line or saw-cut edge.
   E.   Unstable Pavement: Unstable pavement shall be removed over caveout and
overbreaks and the subgrade shall be treated as the main trench.
   F.   Pavement Edges: Pavement edges shall be trimmed to a vertical face and
nearly aligned with the centerline of the trench.
   G.   Cutouts: Cutouts outside of the trench line must be normal or parallel
to the trench line.
   H.   Boring: Boring or other methods to prevent cutting of new pavement may
be required by the administrative official.
   I.   Preexisting Damage: A permittee under this chapter shall not be
required to repair damage existing prior to excavation done by him unless his
cut results in small floating sections which may be unstable, in which case the
permittee shall remove and pave the area. (1987 Code § 12.12.040)
   J.   Cash Bond Required: Prior to the commencement of excavation under this
chapter, wherein the breaking through of pavement is contemplated by the person
performing the construction, the person shall furnish to the town a cash bond
in the bid amount prior to breaking any pavement located within any street,
sidewalk, curb or gutter. The bond provided herein shall be held by the town
for a period of not more than one year thereafter and shall be returned to the
person placing said bond at the expiration of the one year period if, in the
opinion of the town, the pavement has been satisfactorily replaced. However,
if, in the opinion of the town, the excavated area has not been satisfactorily
replaced, the town, in its discretion, may apply whatever amount of the bond,
in whole or in part, towards restoration of the area to the condition prior to
excavation. Any remaining bond balance shall be refunded to the person placing
the bond. (1987 Code § 12.12.040; amd. 2004 Code)
8-3-4: PILING EXCAVATED MATERIALS:
All material excavated from trenches and piled adjacent to the trench or in any
street shall be piled and maintained in such a manner as not to endanger those
working in the trench, pedestrians or other users of the streets and so that as
little inconvenience as possible is caused to those using streets or adjoining
property. Where the confines of the area being excavated are too narrow to
permit the piling of excavated material beside the trench, the administrative
official shall have the power to require that the permittee under this chapter
haul the excavated material to a storage site and then rehaul it to the trench
site at the time of backfilling. (1987 Code § 12.12.050)
8-3-5: CLEANUP:
   A.   Required: As excavation work progresses, all streets, sidewalks and
alleys shall be thoroughly cleaned of all rubbish, excess earth, rock and other
debris resulting from such work.
   B.   Cost: All cleanup operations at the location of such excavation shall
be accomplished at the expense of the permittee.
   C.   Cleanup After Completion: All cleanup shall be completed to the
satisfaction of the administrative official and immediately after completion of
such work, the permittee shall, at his own expense, clean up and remove all
refuse and unused materials of any kind resulting from such work. (1987 Code §
12.12.060)
8-3-6: MAINTAINING GUTTER FLOW:
A permittee under this chapter shall maintain all gutters free and unobstructed
for the full depth of the adjacent curb and for at least one foot (1') in width
from the base of such curb at the gutter line. (1987 Code § 12.12.070)
8-3-7: DISPOSAL OF MUD AND RUNOFF:
A permittee under this chapter shall make provisions to dispose of all surplus
water, muck, silt, slickings or other runoff pumped from excavations or
resulting from sluicing or other operations and shall be responsible for any
damage resulting from its failure to so provide. (1987 Code § 12.12.080)
8-3-8: BACKFILLING:
Fine materials free from lumps and stone shall be thoroughly compacted around
and above the substructure to the upper level of the substructure. Above the
upper level of the substructure, backfill material shall be placed to the
subgrade of the pavement in lifts consistent with the type of soil involved and
the method of consolidation being used. Broken pavement, large stones, roots
and other debris shall not be used in the backfill. Each lift shall be rolled
or tamped or a combination of these methods shall be used, depending upon the
type of soil involved, to compact the backfill materials. Such backfill shall
be done in a manner that will permit the restoration of the surface to a
condition equivalent to that in which it was prior to excavation. (1987 Code §
12.12.090)
8-3-9: RESTORATION OF SURFACE:
   A.   Resurfacing: Resurfacing of excavation shall be done with such
materials and in such manner as to restore the surface to a condition at least
as good as the surface was prior to the commencement of the excavation.
   B.   Temporary Surfacings: Temporary surfacings may be required by the
administrative official where the backfill is likely to settle. The temporary
surface shall be replaced with permanent resurfacing when the backfill has
ceased to settle.
   C.   Conformance Required: All surfaces and subsurfaces shall conform to the
method of construction of the street, sidewalk or alley in which the excavation
was made.
   D.   Settling: If any trench settles within one year, then in such event,
the contractor shall reexcavate and resurface the affected area. (1987 Code §
12.12.100)
8-3-10: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 4
INTERSECTION VIEW OBSTRUCTION
SECTION:
8-4-1: View Obstructing Structures Prohibited
8-4-2: Building Permit Required
8-4-3: Height; Setback
8-4-4: Nuisance
8-4-5: Penalty
8-4-1: VIEW OBSTRUCTING STRUCTURES PROHIBITED:
   A.   Restricted Sight Triangle Defined: A triangular shaped zone, the sides
of which are determined by measuring the distance from the intersection of two
(2) connected street curb lines or the outer adjacent edge of any private
driveway and any street curb line, and the hypotenuse of which is determined by
a connecting line between the said sides. The combined length of the two (2)
sides must be a minimum of forty feet (40'), with no side's length being less
than fifteen feet (15') from the point of the sides' intersection. (Ord. 2008-
9, 5-15-2008)
   B.   Prohibition: No structure, sign, opaque fence, tree, plant, shrubbery,
or other thing shall be permitted to be placed within a restricted sight
triangle if any portion of the said item is more than thirty six inches (36")
above the level of any street adjacent to the restricted sight triangle. All
vegetation within a restricted sight triangle shall be trimmed and maintained
in such a way to ensure that said vegetation complies with this section. (Ord.
2012-11, 1-17-2013)
8-4-2: BUILDING PERMIT REQUIRED:
All persons desiring to place or maintain any view obstructing fence,
billboard, other advertising device or structure, or shrubs or trees at or near
any intersection in the town shall first apply for and secure a building
permit. (1987 Code § 12.16.020)
8-4-3: HEIGHT; SETBACK:
No view obstructing fence, billboard, other advertising device or structure, or
shrubs or trees, shall be built or maintained nearer than fifteen feet (15')
from the front line or side line of the lot. Such fences, structures and
devices shall be so constructed as to have either the bottom thereof at least
eight feet (8') above, or the top thereof not more than three and one- half
feet (31/2') above the level of the adjacent streets. They shall conform in all
other respects to the codes and regulations of the town. (1987 Code §
12.16.030)
8-4-4: NUISANCE:
Whenever the building inspector or town council finds that any poster board,
billboard, bulletin board, signboard or other advertising device or structure,
fence, shrub or tree in the town is in an unsafe condition, or in any manner
fails to conform to the provisions of this chapter, the council may declare it
a nuisance which shall be abated according to the provisions set forth in title
4, chapter 1 of this code. (1987 Code § 12.16.040)
8-4-5: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
CHAPTER 5
PARKS
SECTION:
8-5-1: Closure
8-5-2: Park Use Permit
8-5-3: Posted Signs
8-5-4: Penalty
8-5-1: CLOSURE:
Any park or recreation complex, in whole or in part, may be declared closed to
the public by the administrative official at any time and for any interval of
time, either temporarily or at regular and stated intervals (daily or
otherwise) and either entirely or merely to certain uses as the administrative
official shall find reasonably necessary. (Ord. 2017-12, 8-17-2017)
8-5-2: PARK USE PERMIT:
   A.   Required: Any nonprofit group of more than twenty five (25) individuals
desiring to use parks and related facilities for organized activities shall
make application to the administrative official for a permit at least thirty
(30) days prior to the date and hour for which such permit is desired. (1987
Code § 12.20.020)
   B.   Application: The application shall state:
      1.   The name and address of the applicant.
      2.   The name and address of the person sponsoring the activity, if any.
      3.   The day and hours for which the permit is desired.
      4.   The particular park, complex or portion thereof for which such
permit is desired.
      5.   An estimate of the anticipated attendance.
      6.   Whether or not the applicant wishes to consume alcoholic beverages
during the time specified in the permit application and in the area specified
in such application.
      7.   Whether or not the applicant wishes to authorize concession vendors
during the time specified in the permit application and in the area specified
in such application.
      8.   An affirmative statement by the applicant that he, she or the
applicant organization is in fact a nonprofit organization.
      9.   Any other information which the administrative official shall find
reasonably necessary to a fair determination as to whether a permit should be
issued under this chapter. (1987 Code § 12.20.030)
   C.   Standards For Issuance: The administrative official shall issue a
permit hereunder when he finds that:
      1.   The proposed activity or use, including the proposed consumption of
alcoholic beverages where such is to be engaged in, of the park or complex will
not unreasonably interfere with or detract from the general public's enjoyment
of the park or complex; and provided, however, the applicant otherwise complies
with the provisions of section
3-2-3-12 of this Code.
      2.   The proposed activity and use will not unreasonably interfere with
or detract from the promotion of public health, welfare, safety and recreation.
      3.   The proposed activity or use is not reasonably anticipated to incite
violence, crime or disorderly conduct.
      4.   The proposed activity will not entail unusual or extraordinary or
burdensome expense or police operation by the Municipality.
      5.   The facilities desired have not been reserved for other use at the
day and hour requested in the application.
      6.   The proposed activity is consistent with the public park,
recreational, playground, pleasure, educational, historical and amusement
purposes for which parks are dedicated and is not for commercial gain or
profit. (1987 Code § 12.20.040)
   D.   Damage Deposit:
      1.   Amount Required: The administrative official shall collect the
following damage deposits from groups of one hundred (100) persons or more:
         a.   One hundred (100) to two hundred fifty (250) persons, fifty
dollars ($50.00).
         b.   Over two hundred fifty (250) persons, seventy five dollars
($75.00).
         c.   The administrative official shall collect a damage deposit of
seventy five dollars ($75.00) for a group of any size whenever a permit for the
consumption of alcoholic beverages has been granted.
      2.   Inspection For Damage: Within twenty four (24) hours after the event
has concluded, the administrative official shall cause an inspection to be made
of the area used, and shall determine, in his sole and absolute discretion, the
extent of any damage to park property which has occurred as a result of such
use and shall thereafter and forthwith assess and retain that portion of the
deposit necessary to restore the damaged property and return the balance of the
deposit to the person from whom it was acquired.
      3.   Liability Of Permittee: Nothing herein contained shall relieve the
permittee from the liability imposed by subsection F of this section, and any
amounts withheld by the administrative official pursuant to this section shall
be held as an offset against the total liability of the permittee. (1987 Code §
12.20.050)
   E.   Permit Denial; Appeals: Within fifteen (15) days after receipt of an
application, the administrative official shall issue the permit or shall
apprise the applicant, in writing, of his reasons for refusing the permit. Any
aggrieved person shall have the right to appeal, in writing, to the Governing
Body within fifteen (15) days after the date of such refusal, which shall
consider the application under the standards set forth in subsection C of this
section, and sustain or overrule the administrative official's decision within
fifteen (15) days after receipt of the notice of appeal. The decision of the
Governing Body shall be final. (1987 Code § 12.20.060)
   F.   Liability Of Permittee: The person to whom a permit is issued shall be
liable for any loss, damage or injury sustained by any person whomsoever by
reason of the negligence of the person, his agents or vendors authorized by
said permittee, to whom such permit shall have been issued. Upon being granted
the issuance of a permit, the person to whom the permit is issued, his agents
and concession vendors, shall hold harmless the Town from any accident or
injury, danger or damage to any person during such time such permit remains in
effect. (1987 Code § 12.20.070)
   G.   Revocation: The administrative official shall have the authority to
revoke a permit upon a finding of violation of any rule, ordinance or standard
outlined in subsection C of this section. The Chief of Police or his authorized
representative shall have the authority to revoke a permit upon a finding of
such a violation. (1987 Code § 12.20.080)
8-5-3: POSTED SIGNS:
No person or entity shall willfully, knowingly or recklessly violate or disobey
any sign, written instruction or rule posted by the Town. (Ord. 2017-13, 8-17-
2017)
8-5-4: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this chapter, any violation of the provisions of
this chapter constitutes a Class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in
subsection
1-4-1A2 of this Code. (Ord. 2017-13, 8-17-2017)
CHAPTER 6
CEMETERY
SECTION:
8-6-1: Fees
8-6-2: Perpetual Care
8-6-3: Donations
8-6-4: Abandonment
8-6-5: Fees Nonrefundable
8-6-1: FEES:
The following fee schedule shall be and is hereby adopted on behalf of the
Lyman cemetery:
   A.   New Gravesite: The purchase of a new gravesite shall be fifty dollars
($50.00) per site.
   B.   Open/Close Gravesite:
      1.   Weekdays: The fee to open/close a casket gravesite on weekdays
(Monday through Friday) shall be one hundred twenty five dollars ($125.00). The
fee for opening and closing for an urn burial shall be fifty dollars ($50.00).
      2.   Weekend; Holiday: The fee to open/close a casket gravesite on
weekends (Saturday or Sunday) or holidays shall be one hundred seventy five
dollars ($175.00). The fee for opening and closing for an urn burial shall be
seventy five dollars ($75.00).
      3.   Maintenance Personnel Employee: Only the town of Lyman maintenance
personnel employees may open or close any burial site.
   C.   Annual Maintenance Fee: The annual maintenance fee for a previously
purchased but unoccupied gravesite shall be ten dollars ($10.00) per gravesite
per year.
   D.   Perpetual Care:
      1.   Occupied Sites: For all previously purchased and occupied gravesites
(prior to January 1, 2000), there shall be a onetime assessment for perpetual
care of fifty dollars ($50.00) per gravesite.
      2.   New Purchases: The onetime perpetual care fee shall be three hundred
dollars ($300.00) per gravesite.
   E.   Urn Burial Sites:
      1.   Two (2) urns may be buried on one gravesite. Each urn burial site
shall be five feet (5') wide by five feet (5') wide by three feet (3') deep and
shall not overlap.
      2.   All sites containing an urn shall have a monument designating the
deceased which is:
         a.   A monument with a flat concrete border of no less than two feet
(2') wide at ground level; or
         b.   A flat headstone at ground level. (Ord. 5-2007, 3-1-2007)
8-6-2: PERPETUAL CARE:
   A.   Fund Established: A perpetual care fund shall be established for the
upkeep and maintenance of the gravesites which may include, but is not limited
to: mowing, weeding, trimming; the payment of utilities such as water and
electric; and snow removal. The town may continue to subsidize the Lyman
cemetery for the purpose of maintenance, utility payments, capital improvements
and other labor costs until such time as the perpetual care fund may be self-
sustaining and/or the governing body determines that such subsidies are no
longer necessary.
   B.   New Purchases: As of January 1, 2000, all persons wishing to purchase a
new gravesite at the Lyman cemetery shall be assessed a onetime fee of three
hundred dollars ($300.00) for the perpetual care of the gravesite at the time
of purchase or may elect to pay the perpetual care fee at a later date, but the
fee (and all monies owed under the annual maintenance program) must be paid
before the gravesite is opened. If the fee for perpetual care is not paid at
the time of purchase, the owner must participate in the annual maintenance
program until the fee is paid. (Ord. 5-2005, 9-15-2005)
8-6-3: DONATIONS:
The Lyman cemetery may accept cash donations as gifts for the perpetual care
fund or the donation of unoccupied gravesites back to the cemetery as a gift or
in lieu of maintenance fees which may be in arrears. (Ord. 7-99, 12-16-1999)
8-6-4: ABANDONMENT:
If any fees associated with a purchased but unoccupied gravesite remain unpaid
for a period of two (2) years or more, the gravesite may be declared abandoned
by the director of public works and available for purchase by another. Notice
of the impending abandonment shall be attempted, by regular U.S. mail, no less
than fifteen (15) days before such a declaration may be made. (Ord. 2010-03, 4-
1-2010)
8-6-5: FEES NONREFUNDABLE:
No fee imposed in this chapter shall be refundable without prior approval of
the director of public works. (Ord. 2010-03, 4-1-2010)
TITLE 9
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
BUILDING PERMITS
SECTION:
9-1-1: Building Permit Required
9-1-2: Building And Setup Fees
9-1-1: BUILDING PERMIT REQUIRED:
   A.   Permit Required: Except as specified in the Building Code, it is
unlawful for any person, firm, partnership, corporation or other business
entity, to construct, add to, alter, move or demolish any building or structure
within the Town without first obtaining a permit thereof.
   B.   Requirements Prior To Issuance: The permit shall not issue without
first obtaining the following:
      1.   A drawing, plan or sketch showing a site plan which conforms to
existing Town zoning laws;
      2.   A blueprint or plans of the structure with the builder's and/or
owner's certification that the building meets or will comply with the Building
Code; and
      3.   A written application and the appropriate fee.
   C.   Mobile Home, Manufactured Home, Modular Home Or Prefabricated Home Not
Meeting Building Code Standards 1 : Any mobile home, manufactured home, modular
home or other prefabricated home which does not or cannot meet the standards
set forth in the Building Code shall secure a setup permit and shall comply
with the provisions set forth in title 12 of this Code. All other work as
defined above shall require a building permit. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-
1-2001)
   D.   Term: Any permit obtained under this section shall be valid for a
period of one year from the date of issuance. Permittees who have exceeded the
building permit term may be granted one automatic six (6) month extension if
applied for and pay a fifty dollar ($50.00) extension fee. Any subsequent
extensions must be approved by the Planning and Zoning Commission and ratified
by the Town Council with an additional extension fee and further required
progress benchmarks. Permits which exceed any nonextended time period shall be
considered null and void. A null and void building permit may be renewed only
by the initiation of a new building permit application with all associated fees
and costs, and must comply with any new building standards adopted in this
Code.
   E.   Nuisance: Construction or placement of a building within the Town
without obtaining a building permit or after the expiration of a building
permit, or allowing the continued placement or accumulation of construction
materials on a lot for more than two (2) weeks absent an active building permit
shall constitute a misdemeanor punishable by not more than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00). Each day or continued placement or accumulation may
constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 2012-02, 5-3-2012)
   F.   Small accessory buildings: Accessory buildings with a footprint less
than 200 square feet and without electricity and/or plumbing are not required
to have a building permit. The exemption herein does not exempt the accessory
building from compliance with all other sections of the Town Code.
   G.   Commercial Remodel: In addition to the requirements above, any
modification of a commercial property and/or transformation of an existing
property to a commercial purpose, requiring construction, removal, or
alteration of the load-bearing walls, plumbing, foundations, and/or electrical
wiring requires approval by the Town Council. In granting such a permit, the
Council may require any lawful contingent condition on the granting of such a
building permit.
   H.   Exemptions: The following structures are exempt from the requirement of
having a building permit before construction and/or remodeling:
      1.   Accessory buildings with a footprint less than five hundred (500)
square feet unless said building has permanent plumbing and/or electricity.
      2.   Greenhouses after submission of a site plan demonstrating intended
compliance with easement and setbacks.
      3.   Unroofed decks less than thirty-six (36) inches off the ground.
      The exemption herein does not exempt the accessory building from
compliance with all other sections of the Town Code. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000,
eff. 1-1-2001; Ord. 2012-02, 5-3-2012; Ord. 2018-06, 7-5-2018; Ord. 2019-07,
10-3-2019; Res. 2020-16, 8-6-2020; Ord. 2022-05, 10-20-2022)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  12-2-1 of this Code for definitions of "mobile home" and "modular home".
9-1-2: BUILDING AND SETUP FEES:
The fee to be charged for any permit, including, but not limited to, building
and setup fees, shall be established by a resolution of the Town Council. These
fees are not refundable and not concurrent with any and all other fees charged
in the construction permitting process. (Ord. 2011-06, 4-7-2011)
CHAPTER 2
REGULATORY CODES
SECTION:
9-2-1: Building Code Adopted
9-2-2: Building Official
9-2-3: Building Inspector
9-2-4: Enforcement
9-2-5: Universal Ordinance Application
9-2-6: Copies On File
9-2-1: BUILDING CODE ADOPTED:
There is adopted by the town for the purpose of prescribing regulations for the
minimum standards to safeguard life, health, property and public welfare, that
certain suggested code known as the International Building Code (IBC), along
with all incorporated codes contained by reference in the IBC being
particularly the most recent edition of the code available to the general
public, and the whole thereof, save and except such portions as are modified,
deleted, added or amended pursuant to resolution by the Town Council. The IBC
and the codes incorporated by reference within the IBC are incorporated in this
section as fully as if set out in length in this section, and the provisions
thereof shall be controlling within the town unless specifically excepted by
Resolution. (Ord. 2010-09, 10-7-2010; amd. Ord. 2019-06, 10-3-2019)
9-2-2: BUILDING OFFICIAL:
The director of public works for the town of Lyman, or his or her designee in
whole or in part, shall act as the building official for the town of Lyman
whenever that term is used within the international building code. (Ord. 2010-
09, 10-7-2010)
9-2-3: BUILDING INSPECTOR:
To the extent that the international building code requires actions by a
licensed building inspector, such requirements are to be met pursuant to
chapter 7 of this title. Additionally, the director of public works may require
that any inspection be conducted pursuant to the international building code by
a neutral licensed building inspector at the builder's or owner's expense.
(Ord. 2010-09, 10-7-2010)
9-2-4: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   Any person who violates any provision of the international building
code or this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction thereof
shall be punished according to the provisions set forth in sections
1-4-1 through
1-4-4 of this code.
   B.   In addition to enforcement by officials and officers of the town of
Lyman, members of the Uinta County fire protection and emergency services joint
powers board may enforce any provision of the international fire code, which is
incorporated by reference into the international building code. (Ord. 2010-09,
10-7-2010)
9-2-5: UNIVERSAL ORDINANCE APPLICATION:
Any and all references to a building code adopted by the town of Lyman within
the town code, including any reference to the uniform building code, shall be
read as the international building code. (Ord. 2010-09, 10-7-2010)
9-2-6: COPIES ON FILE:
   A.   Codes: At least one copy of each code adopted in this chapter and any
ordinance and resolution providing for amendments, modifications, additions or
deletions in such codes shall be maintained on file in the office of the town
clerk where they shall be available for public inspection during the normal
office hours of the Town Clerk. In lieu of having a physical copy of each Code,
the office of the Town Clerk may provide information directing the public to
the on-line location of the adopted Codes.
   B.   Amendments; Modifications: One copy of each ordinance and resolution
amending or modifying each code shall be kept with each copy of the code. (1987
Code § 15.08.060; amd. Ord. 2010-09, 10-7-2010; Ord. 2019-06, 10-3-2019)
CHAPTER 3
MISCELLANEOUS SAFETY REQUIREMENTS
SECTION:
9-3-1: Protection Of Excavations
9-3-2: Exits In Public Buildings
9-3-1: PROTECTION OF EXCAVATIONS 1 :
It is unlawful for any person to dig or maintain any cellars, pits or other
excavation without providing adequate protection to persons and property in the
form of barricades and warning devices. (1987 Code § 15.12.010)
 
Notes
1 1. See title 8, chapter 3 of this code.
9-3-2: EXITS IN PUBLIC BUILDINGS:
It is unlawful for any person, firm or corporation owning or having the control
or management of any public building, resorted to or occupied by a considerable
number of persons, to fail to provide the same with sufficient and safe means
of speedy escape in case of accident or fire. All doors and exits of the
buildings used for public assemblage shall during the continuance of the
gathering be kept unlocked, and in a condition to permit the speedy exit of the
audience. (1987 Code § 15.12.020)
CHAPTER 4
SOLAR ACCESS
SECTION:
9-4-1: Statutory Authority
9-4-2: Purpose
9-4-3: Definitions
9-4-4: Shading And Location Of Solar Collectors
9-4-5: Prior Nonconforming Uses
9-4-6: Variances
9-4-7: Solar Permit
9-4-8: Enforcement
9-4-1: STATUTORY AUTHORITY:
Authorization for these regulations is contained in Wyoming Statutes sections
34-22-101 through 34-22-106. (1987 Code § 15.16.010)
9-4-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect the health, safety, and general
welfare of the town by encouraging the use of solar energy systems. It is the
intent of this chapter to provide a means of protection for the use of solar
collectors without causing undue hardships on the rights of adjacent property
owners and to establish solar collectors as a permitted use in all zoning or
land use districts. (1987 Code § 15.16.020)
9-4-3: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
SOLAR COLLECTOR: One of the following which is capable of collecting, storing
or transmitting at least twenty five thousand (25,000) BTUs on a clear winter
solstice day:
   A.   A wall, clerestory or skylight window designed to transmit solar energy
into a structure for heating purposes;
   B.   A greenhouse attached to another structure and designed to provide part
or all of the heating load for the structure to which it is attached;
   C.   A trombe wall, drum wall or other wall or roof structural element
designed to collect and transmit solar energy into a structure;
   D.   A photovoltaic collector designed to convert solar energy into electric
energy;
   E.   A plate type collector designed to use solar energy to heat air, water
or other fluids for use in hot water or space heating or other applications;
   F.   A massive structural element designed to collect solar energy and
transmit it to internal spaces for heating; or
   G.   Other devices or combination of devices that rely upon sunshine as an
energy source.
SOLAR RIGHT: A property right to an unobstructed line of sight path from a
solar collector to the sun which permits radiation from the sun to impinge
directly on the solar collector. The extent of the solar right shall be
described by that illumination provided by the path of the sun on the winter
solstice day which is put to a beneficial use or otherwise limited by this
chapter.
WINTER SOLSTICE DAY: The solstice on or about December 21 which marks the
beginning of winter in the northern hemisphere and the time when the sun
reaches its southernmost point. (1987 Code § 15.16.030)
9-4-4: SHADING AND LOCATION OF SOLAR COLLECTORS:
   A.   Shading Prohibited: Except as otherwise provided by this chapter, it is
unlawful for any person to erect a building or other structure, or to allow a
tree, shrub or other vegetation to cast a shadow upon a solar collector which
is greater than the shadow cast by a hypothetical ten foot (10') high wall
located along the property lines, between the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M.
and three o'clock (3:00) P.M., MST, on the winter solstice day.
   B.   Location: Solar collectors shall be located on the solar user's
property so as not to unreasonably or unnecessarily restrict the uses of
neighboring property. (1987 Code § 15.16.040)
9-4-5: PRIOR NONCONFORMING USES:
Structures or vegetation which existed prior to the time of installation of the
solar energy collection system or the effective date hereof shall not be
subject to the requirements of section
9-4-4 of this chapter. (1987 Code § 15.16.050)
9-4-6: VARIANCES:
Any person desiring to erect any structure, or increase the height of any
structure, or permit the growth of any tree or other vegetation, or otherwise
use his/her property, not in conformance with this chapter, may apply for a
variance from the planning and zoning commission. A variance shall not be
approved by the commission unless it finds the literal enforcement or
application of these regulations would result in unnecessary hardship. (1987
Code § 15.16.060)
9-4-7: SOLAR PERMIT:
   A.   Required:
      1.   A solar permit shall be granted before a solar right may be
established.
      2.   A solar permit shall be granted for any proposed or existing solar
collector which complies with the requirements of this chapter.
      3.   The solar right vests on the date the solar permit is granted. The
solar collector shall be put to beneficial use within two (2) years, except
additional time may be granted for good cause. The building inspector or other
administrative official shall certify the right and its beneficial use within
two (2) years.
      4.   Existing solar collector users shall apply for permits within five
(5) years after the date hereof.
      5.   A solar right which is not applied to a beneficial use for a period
of five (5) years or more shall be deemed abandoned and without priority. (1987
Code § 15.16.070)
   B.   Application:
      1.   Any person who desires to obtain a solar right shall first make
application to the building inspector or other administrative official for a
solar access permit.
      2.   The application for a permit along with the required fee, shall be
filed on a form furnished for that purpose. Information adequate to determine
compliance with these regulations shall accompany the application.
      3.   The building inspector or other administrative official after review
of the application shall grant a solar access permit for any proposed or
existing solar collector which complies with this chapter. (1987 Code §
15.16.080)
   C.   Recording Or Solar Rights And Permits: A copy of the solar permit shall
be recorded with the county clerk by the person receiving the solar permit. The
solar permit shall include a description of the collector surface, or that
portion of the collector surface to which the permit is granted. The
description shall include the dimensions of the collector surface, the
direction of orientation, the height above ground level, the location of the
collector on the solar user's property and the date the solar permit was
granted. (1987 Code § 15.16.090)
9-4-8: ENFORCEMENT:
The building inspector or other administrative official shall enforce this
chapter and bring to the attention of the town attorney any violations or lack
of compliance. (1987 Code § 15.16.100)
CHAPTER 5
TRAILER AND MOBILE HOME PLUMBING
SECTION:
9-5-1: Definition
9-5-2: Protection From Freezing
9-5-3: Allowing Water To Run
9-5-1: DEFINITION:
For the purpose of this chapter the terms "trailer" and "mobile home" mean a
unit more than eight and one-half feet (81/2') in width which is designed,
constructed and equipped as a dwelling place, living abode or place of business
to which wheels may be attached for movement upon streets and highways, except
a unit used primarily as a mobile laboratory or mobile office. The terms
"trailer" and "mobile home" shall not include the connection of two (2) single
wide, unisectioned mobile home units, not manufactured, constructed and
intended expressly for the purpose of joining single sections together to
provide one continuous living space. (1987 Code § 15.20.010)
9-5-2: PROTECTION FROM FREEZING:
It is unlawful for any person to maintain, use, occupy, or permit to be
occupied any trailer or mobile home within the town without first protecting
the plumbing of the trailer or mobile home from freezing by placing the trailer
or mobile home on a permanent foundation or by installation of suitable
skirting material around the entire perimeter of the trailer or mobile home,
and, in addition, by installation of electrical heating tapes or similar
heating devices along and around any exposed water pipe which is not heated by
the principal heating unit of the trailer or mobile home. (1987 Code §
15.20.020)
9-5-3: ALLOWING WATER TO RUN:
It is unlawful for any person occupying, maintaining, using or permitting the
use of a trailer or mobile home on property owned or controlled by the person,
to prevent the plumbing of the trailer or mobile home from freezing by
permitting or allowing water to run continuously from any tap or faucet in, on
or about the trailer or mobile home. (1987 Code § 15.20.030)
CHAPTER 6
HOUSING REHABILITATION
SECTION:
9-6-1: Applicability
9-6-2: Rehabilitation Site And Neighborhood
9-6-3: Access To Dwelling Units
9-6-4: Structural Soundness
9-6-5: Lead Based Paint
9-6-6: Water Supply
9-6-7: Interior Air Quality
9-6-8: Illumination And Electricity
9-6-9: Heating And Cooling; Insulation And Weatherstripping
9-6-10: Sanitary Facilities
9-6-11: Space And Security
9-6-12: Food Preparation; Refuse Disposal
9-6-13: Sanitary Conditions
9-6-14: Congregate Housing
9-6-1: APPLICABILITY:
   A.   Federal Guidelines Adopted: In order to comply with federal guidelines
for the community development block grant housing rehabilitation project, the
following rehabilitation, construction renovation guidelines for building
sites, neighborhoods and the interior/exterior of dwellings designated for
rehabilitation are adopted and established.
   B.   Limitations: The guidelines set out in this chapter are expressly
limited to neighborhoods, building rehabilitation sites or interior/exterior of
dwellings designated for housing rehabilitation by the town.
   C.   New Construction Codes: This chapter shall not be construed as,
substituted for, or abate or relieve construction requirements promulgated by
the uniform building, plumbing or electrical codes for new construction, as
adopted by the town. (1987 Code § 15.24.010)
9-6-2: REHABILITATION SITE AND NEIGHBORHOOD:
   A.   Unacceptable Environmental Conditions: The rehabilitation site and
surrounding neighborhood shall be, to the extent possible, reasonably free from
disturbing noises, reverberations and other hazards to the health, safety and
general welfare of the occupants, and shall not be subject to serious manmade
or natural adverse environmental conditions such as:
      1.   Dangerous or unstable walkways or steps;
      2.   Flooding, poor drainage, septic tank backflows, sewage hazards or
mud slides;
      3.   Abnormal smoke, dust or air pollution;
      4.   Excessive noise, vibrations or vehicular traffic;
      5.   Excessive trash accumulations;
      6.   Vermin or rodent infestation; or
      7.   Fire hazards.
   B.   Measures To Correct: Measures to correct the conditions described in
subsection A of this section shall include the following:
      1.   All steps and walkways should be level, provided with sufficient
pitch to prevent water accumulation, and be free from dangerous cracks,
crumbling or breakage.
      2.   The lot should have positive drainage away from the dwelling's
foundation to prevent standing water.
      3.   Any material which accumulates on the property should be screened or
arranged in a manner so as to minimize visual impact and not detract from the
appearance of the surrounding neighborhood.
      4.   The rehabilitation site should be kept free from fire hazards such
as storage of highly flammable materials. (1987 Code § 15.24.020)
9-6-3: ACCESS TO DWELLING UNITS:
   A.   Requirements: The dwelling unit shall have adequate entrance and exit
access for the occupants:
      1.   It shall be usable and capable of being maintained without
unauthorized use of other private property.
      2.   The building shall provide alternate means of egress in case of fire
such as fire stairs or egress through windows.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with the conditions described in
subsection A of this section shall include the following: the property should
be adjacent to an access street or road. (1987 Code § 15.24.030)
9-6-4: STRUCTURAL SOUNDNESS:
   A.   Required Conditions: The dwelling unit shall be structurally sound so
as to not pose any threat to the health and safety of the occupants as well as
protect the occupants from their environment.
      1.   Ceilings, Walls And Floors: Ceilings, walls and floors shall be free
from defects such as severe bulging, leaning, large holes, loose surface
materials, severe buckling or noticeable movement under walking stress, missing
parts or other serious damage.
      2.   Roof: The roof structure and roofing shall be firm and weathertight.
      3.   Walls: Exterior wall structures and interior wall surfaces shall not
have any serious defects such as leaning, buckling, sagging, cracks or holes,
loose siding or other serious damage.
      4.   Stairways, Halls, Porches, Walkways, Etc.: The condition and
equipment of interior and exterior stairways, halls, porches, walkways, etc.,
shall be such as not to present a danger of tripping or falling.
      5.   Elevators: Elevators, if present, shall be maintained in a safe
operating condition.
      6.   Anchoring: Mobile or manufactured homes shall be securely anchored
by a tie down device which distributes and transfers the unit's weight to
appropriate ground anchors so as to resist overturning and shifting.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with the conditions described in
subsection A of this section include:
      1.   First Floor Structural Wood Members: In crawl spaces or basements,
all first floor structural wood members including floor joists, plates, piers
and pilings should be inspected for cracked, broken, rotten or otherwise
damaged conditions. Damaged members should be accordingly repaired or replaced.
Exterior walls should be weathertight and prevent heat loss.
      2.   Roof: The roof structure should be firm and all roof framing members
free from cracks and rot. Roof sheathing should be solid and free from sagging,
buckling, etc. If the roof appears well worn, it should be replaced entirely.
If more than two (2) layers of shingles are on the roof, both layers of
shingles should be stripped to the sheathing, and a new covering applied. Any
extensions through the roof, such as chimneys or vents, shall be properly
flashed.
      3.   Foundations, Piers And Pilings; Chimneys: Concrete block or brick
foundations, piers and pilings should be inspected for loose mortar joints. All
empty or cracked mortar joints should be tuck pointed in an acceptable manner
to match the rest of the structure. The chimney should be inspected for loose
mortar joints and proper height. All empty or cracked mortar joints should be
tuck pointed in an acceptable manner and the joints should be recessed.
      4.   Steps, Walkways And Porches; Interior Stairways: All exterior steps,
walkways and porches should be free of tripping hazards. Crumbling, cracked or
uneven conditions should be repaired or replaced as necessary. Interior
stairway conditions should avoid presenting a danger of falling or tripping and
handrails should be installed on all stairways.
      5.   Termites: The property should be inspected for and, if necessary,
treated for termites.
      6.   Other Buildings: All other buildings, such as garages, should be
repaired to a usable condition or removed from the property. The general
appearance of the exterior structure and lot, after rehabilitation, should be
such that the property makes a significant contribution to the general
appearance of the neighborhood. (1987 Code § 15.24.040)
9-6-5: LEAD BASED PAINT:
   A.   Requirements: The dwelling unit shall comply with HUD lead based paint
regulations.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with this requirement shall
include:
      1.   Compliance with 24 CFR part 35, issued pursuant to the lead based
paint poisoning prevention act, 42 United States Code 4801.
      2.   Owner shall provide certification that the dwelling is in accordance
with said HUD regulations.
      3.   If the dwelling was constructed prior to 1950, the family shall be
furnished with a notice required by HUD lead based paint regulations and the
procedures regarding the hazards of lead based paint poisonings, the symptoms
and treatment of lead poisoning and the precautions to be taken against lead
poisoning.
   C.   Actions To Comply: To comply with the lead based paint regulations, the
following actions are required:
      1.   Notification to occupants that the property (if constructed prior to
1950) may contain lead based paints and the hazards, symptoms and treatment of
such poisoning.
      2.   The contracts shall include language prohibiting the use of lead
based paint.
      3.   The inspection for and elimination of "immediate hazards", defined
as chipping, peeling, cracking or loosening of any paint in a structure built
prior to 1950. (1987 Code § 15.24.050)
9-6-6: WATER SUPPLY:
   A.   Requirements: The dwelling's water supply shall be free from
contamination and shall be served by an approved public or private sanitary
water supply.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with the requirements set out in
subsection A of this section shall include:
      1.   Hot Water Heater: The unit should have a hot water heater with a
capacity to serve current and future residents.
      2.   Hot And Cold Running Water: Hot and cold running water should be
supplied to at least the kitchen and bath.
      3.   Protection From Freezing: All water lines should be protected from
freezing. (1987 Code § 15.24.060)
9-6-7: INTERIOR AIR QUALITY:
   A.   Requirements: The dwelling unit shall be free from pollutants in the
air at levels which threaten the health of the occupants. The dwelling unit
shall be free from dangerous levels of air pollution from carbon monoxide,
sewer gas, fuel, gas, dust and other harmful air pollutants. Air circulation
shall be adequate throughout. Bathroom area shall have at least one operable
window or other adequate exhaust ventilation.
   B.   Measures To Correct: Measures to correct the conditions described in
subsection A of this section include:
      1.   Venting: All oil fired or gas fired appliances should have proper
venting to the outside of the dwelling unit for combustion gases.
      2.   Windows: All windows designed to open should be operable and
provided with screens.
      3.   Kitchen Areas: Kitchen areas should also have proper ventilation.
(1987 Code § 15.24.070)
9-6-8: ILLUMINATION AND ELECTRICITY:
   A.   Requirements:
      1.   Illumination: Each room shall have adequate natural or artificial
illumination to permit normal indoor activities and to support the health and
safety of occupants.
      2.   Electrical Sources: Sufficient electrical sources shall be provided
to permit use of essential electrical appliances while assuring safety from
fire.
      3.   Windows: Living and sleeping rooms shall include at least one
window.
      4.   Light Fixture: A ceiling or wall light fixture shall be present and
operable in the kitchen and bathroom.
      5.   Electrical Outlets: At least two (2) electrical outlets, one of
which may be an overhead light, shall be present and operable in the living
area, kitchen and each bedroom.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with the requirements set out in
subsection A of this section shall include:
      1.   Windows: Living rooms and bedrooms shall include at least one
window.
      2.   Light Fixtures: A ceiling or wall light fixture operated by a wall
switch should be present in the kitchen, bathroom and in hallways.
      3.   Outlets: All outlets installed as a result of rehabilitation should
be properly grounded.
      4.   Electrical Service:
         a.   Requirements: Each unit should be provided with at least 100-
ampere service and a sufficient number of circuits to service present and
future use of the dwelling.
            1.   There should be separate circuits for air conditioning,
furnaces, dryers and stoves.
            2.   There should be a separate 20-ampere circuit for the heavy
workload area of the kitchen.
            3.   The main service box should be provided with circuit breakers.
            4.   Connection at the main service to the unit should be in an
acceptable manner.
            5.   Placement of the connection should be out of children's reach.
            6.   Proper anchoring should be used.
            7.   All defective exposed "knob and tube" wiring should be
removed.
         b.   Hazardous Conditions: All hazardous conditions such as broken
switches or outlets, bare wiring or fixtures not properly anchored should be
repaired in an acceptable manner. (1987 Code § 15.24.080)
9-6-9: HEATING AND COOLING; INSULATION AND WEATHERSTRIPPING:
   A.   Requirements: The dwelling unit shall have, and be capable of
maintaining, a thermal environment healthy for the human body. The unit shall
contain safe heating and/or cooling facilities which are in proper operating
condition and provide adequate heat and/or cooling to each room in the dwelling
unit appropriate for the climate. Unvented room heaters which burn gas, oil or
kerosene are unacceptable.
   B.   Measures To Comply: Measures to comply with the requirements set out in
subsection A of this section include:
      1.   Venting System: All parts of the venting system for central units
