than two hundred milligrams per liter (200 mg/l) and a suspended solids
concentration of not more than two hundred fifty milligrams per liter (250 mg/
l).
OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE: Those functions that result in expenditures during
the useful life of the treatment works for materials, labor, utilities and
other items which are necessary for managing and for which such works were
designed and constructed. The term "operation and maintenance" includes
"replacement" as defined herein.
REPLACEMENT: Expenditures for obtaining and installing equipment, accessories
or appurtenances which are necessary during the useful life of the treatment
works to maintain the capacity and performance for which such works were
designed and constructed.
RESIDENTIAL USER: Any contributor to the town's treatment works whose lot,
parcel or real estate, or building is used for domestic dwelling purposes only.
SEPTAGE: The liquid and solid material pumped from a septic tank or cesspool
during cleaning.
SEPTIC TANK: A sewage disposal tank in which waste material is collected and
decomposed by anaerobic bacteria.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS (SS): Solids that either float on the surface of or are in
suspension in water, sewage, or other liquids and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
TREATMENT WORKS: Any devices and systems for the storage, treatment, recycling
and reclamation of municipal sewage, domestic sewage or liquid industrial
wastes. These include intercepting sewers, outfall sewers, sewage collection
systems, pumping, power, and other equipment and their appurtenances;
extensions improvement, remodeling, additions and alterations thereof; elements
essential to provide a reliable recycled supply such as standby treatment units
and clear well facilities; and any works, including site acquisition of the
land that will be an integral part of the treatment process or is used for
ultimate disposal of residues resulting from such treatment (including land for
composting sludge, temporary storage of such compost and land used for the
storage of treated wastewater in land treatment systems before land
applications); or any other method or system for preventing, abating, reducing,
storing, treating, separating or disposing of municipal waste or industrial
waste, including waste in combined storm water and sanitary sewer systems.
USER CHARGE: That portion of the total wastewater service charge which is
levied in a proportional and adequate manner for the cost of operation,
maintenance and replacement of the wastewater treatment works.
WATER METER: A water volume measuring and recording device, furnished and/or
installed by a user or the town of Lyman and approved by the town of Lyman.
(Ord. 9-92, 6-17-1993; amd. Ord. 2006-9, 7-20-2006)
10-3-3: SEWER CONNECTIONS; PERMITS, FEES:
   A.   Permit Required: Any person desiring to connect to the sewer system
owned by the town shall apply to the town clerk for a permit. Only one
residence or building shall be covered by each permit.
   B.   Fee: The fee for issuance of a permit to connect to town sewer is five
hundred dollars ($500.00). The permit fee shall also include the cost for the
inspections.
   C.   Sewer Line: The sewer line from the facility to the connection with the
town sewer shall be provided by the person connecting with the sewer and shall
be done in a good and workmanlike manner with proper sewer pipe and to the
satisfaction of the town public works director or other officer designated to
inspect such connecting in and the connection with the town sewer. (Ord. 9-92,
6-17-1993)
10-3-4: TOTAL ANNUAL COST OF OPERATION AND MAINTENANCE:
The town shall determine the total annual costs of capital, operation and
maintenance of the wastewater system which are necessary to maintain the
capacity and performance, during the service life of the treatment works, for
which such works were designed and constructed. The total annual cost of
operation and maintenance shall include, but not be limited to, capital
replacement, labor, repairs, equipment and replacement, maintenance, necessary
modifications, power, sampling, laboratory tests, and a reasonable contingency
fund. (See section
10-3-11 of this chapter.) (Ord. 9-92, 6-17-1993)
10-3-5: WASTEWATER CONTRIBUTION:
   A.   Residential User Calculation: The town of Lyman shall determine for
each residential user or user class the average monthly volume of wastewater
discharged to the wastewater system, by using winter water consumption volumes
determined by reading meters for October through April and then dividing total
winter volume by seven (7) months.
   B.   New Services: New services without a prior year's volume to base rates
will be charged according to average residential or nonresidential rates. (Ord.
2006-9, 7-20-2006)
10-3-6: WASTEWATER SERVICE CHARGE:
   A.   Basis For Monthly User Charge: For residential users, monthly user
charges will be based on actual winter water usage. If a user has a consumptive
use of water or in some other manner uses water which is not discharged into
the wastewater collection system, the user charge for that contributor may be
based on readings of wastewater meter(s) or separate water meter(s) installed
and maintained at the user's expense. For nonresidential users, monthly user
charges will be based on actual monthly water usage throughout the year.
   B.   Classification As Residential: The governing body may classify
institutional, religious, industrial, commercial, and other nonresidential
establishments as a residential user; provided, that the wastes from these
establishments are equivalent to the wastes from the average residential user
with respect to volume, strength, and delivery flow rate characteristics (see
section
10-3-13 of this chapter).
   C.   Rates Established: Rates for wastewater service from the town municipal
system shall be established and/or amended by resolution of the town council.
Said rates set by said resolution(s) may include a flat base rate with monthly
base rates and/or graduated usage rates for wastewater usage beyond a specified
base rate. The town may also set, by resolution, additional rates and/or fees
for residential and nonresidential users whose wastewater has a greater
strength than normal domestic sewage, which surcharge is in addition to the
normal user charge that will be collected.
   D.   Septage Waste Haulers: Each septage waste hauler shall be assessed a
user charge rate to be set by resolution of the town council, including an
additional rate for septage of greater strength than is typically charged.
Nothing in this section shall require the town to accept septage into the
town's wastewater system.
   E.   Toxic Pollutants: Any user which discharges any toxic pollutants (see
chapter 2 of this title) which cause an increase in the cost of managing the
treatment works, or any user which discharges any substance which singly or by
interaction with other substances causes identifiable increases in the cost of
operation, maintenance or replacement of the treatment works, shall pay for
such increased costs. The charge to each such user shall be as determined by
the appropriate financial personnel and approved by the town governing body.
   F.   Rates: All rates in effect at the enactment of this section shall
continue until amended by resolution of the town council. (Ord. 2017-05, 2-2-
2017)
10-3-7: WASTEWATER FACILITIES REPLACEMENT FUND:
A reserve fund called the wastewater facilities replacement fund is hereby
established within the wastewater utility fund for the purpose of providing
sufficient funds to be expended for obtaining and installing equipment,
accessories and appurtenances during the useful life (20 years) of the
wastewater treatment facilities necessary to maintain the capacity and
performance for which such facilities were designed and constructed. This fund
shall also be sufficient at the end of the useful life of the treatment
facility to replace facilities as necessary. Such an annual cost shall be
determined as outlined under "equipment replacement" in section
10-3-11 of this chapter. (Ord. 9-92, 6-17-1993)
10-3-8: BILLING AND DELINQUENT ACCOUNTS:
   A.   Billing: Wastewater service charges for use of the town of Lyman
wastewater system shall be due and payable monthly, on or before the end of
each month. The town clerk shall prepare and mail a statement of the wastewater
service charge to each user. This statement may be combined with the water rent
charges pursuant to section
10-1-5 of this title. All charges shall be paid to the town clerk at his office
in the town hall. There shall be no discount allowed. (Ord. 2007-01, 2-15-2007)
   B.   Deemed Delinquent: If the sewer user fails, refuses or neglects to pay
the wastewater charges within thirty (30) days of the mailing of notice of the
due charges, the bill shall become delinquent and may be collected by action or
fine for violation of this chapter in the municipal court, and the sewer access
may be immediately shut off.
   C.   Collection Policy: A collection policy for delinquent accounts shall be
adopted by resolution, which prescribes periods and practices for sending late
notices, hanging turnoff notice tags, turning off wastewater access, late
penalty fees, etc. (Ord. 2011-12, 9-1-2011)
   D.   Restoration Of Service: Before the wastewater service shall be
restored, all delinquent charges for the premises must be paid with an
additional fee, as established by policy, for restoring the service. (Ord.
2007-01, 2-15-2007)
   E.   Misdemeanor: Failure to pay delinquent water charges, as set out in
subsection A of this section, shall constitute a misdemeanor punishable by up
to seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) in addition to any and all arrearages,
if, after no less than thirty (30) days, and after a minimum of fifteen (15)
days after written notice. Notice shall be considered sufficient if said notice
is attached to the residence. (Ord. 2011-12, 9-1-2011)
10-3-9: REVIEW OF SERVICE CHARGE:
   A.   Annual Review: The town shall review the total annual cost of operation
and maintenance as well as each user's wastewater contribution not less often
than every year and will revise the system as necessary to assure equity of the
service charge system established herein and to assure that sufficient funds
are obtained to adequately operate and maintain the wastewater treatment works.
   B.   Excess Revenues: After two (2) consecutive years of collecting excess
revenues, the town shall apply those revenues to the costs of operation and
maintenance for the next year and adjust the rates accordingly. If a
significant user, such as a business, has completed in house modifications
which would change that user's wastewater contribution, the user can present to
the town staff such factual information and the town shall then determine if
the user's wastewater contribution is to be changed.
   C.   Request For Review: Any user who feels his user charge is unjust and
inequitable may make written application to the town requesting a review of his
user charge.
   D.   Review Of Request: Review of the request shall be made by the town as
soon as is reasonable, and, if substantiated, the user charges for that user
shall be recomputed based upon the revised flow and/or strength data and the
new charges shall be applicable to the next billing cycle/period.
   E.   Fiscal Year End Balances: Fiscal year end balances in the operation,
maintenance, and replacement fund shall be used for no other purposes than
those designated. Monies which have been transferred from other sources to meet
temporary shortages in the operation, maintenance and replacement fund shall be
returned to their respective accounts upon appropriate adjustment of the user
charge rates for operation, maintenance, and replacement. The user charge rate
(s) shall be adjusted such that the transferred monies will be returned to
their respective accounts within six (6) months of the fiscal year in which the
monies were borrowed. (Ord. 9-92, 6-17-1993)
10-3-10: NOTIFICATION:
Each user will be notified, at least annually, in conjunction with a regular
bill, of the rate and that portion of the user charges which are attributable
to wastewater treatment services. (Ord. 9-92, 6-17-1993)

CHAPTER 4
RELOCATION OF UTILITY FIXTURES
SECTION:
10-4-1: Notice To Relocate
10-4-2: Cost Responsibility
10-4-3: Assurance Of Subexcavation And Backfill
10-4-4: Maintaining Public Safety Precautions
10-4-5: Failure To Comply
10-4-6: Suspension Of License
10-4-1: NOTICE TO RELOCATE:
Upon actual written notice by the town, transmitted by any reasonable means of
communication to the business address of any licensed utility company providing
utility services in the town, including, but not limited to, the Bridger Valley
Electric Association, Mountain Fuel Supply Company, Union Telephone Company and
Western Wyoming Cablevision Corporation, such utility company shall thence
forthwith and within twenty (20) days of receiving written notice commence to
effectively remove and relocate cables, lines, poles, pipes and/or other of its
fixtures as the town directs and deems reasonably necessary, and when in the
opinion of the town, the public's use of streets, roads, alleys and sidewalks
requires the reasonable protection of the health and safety of the public for
and during periods of repair, reconstruction, replacement of any street, road,
alley or sidewalk within the town limits, subsequent to written notice as
aforesaid by the town to each respective licensed utility company affected, and
each such licensed utility company shall replace said cables, lines, poles,
pipes and other of its fixtures upon the express direction by the town. In
cases of emergency, the town shall be relieved of giving the twenty (20) day
written notice requirement when an immediate threat presents itself to the
health or safety of the public. In such event, immediate actual notice shall be
provided the licensed utility company by the town. (1987 Code § 13.12.010)
10-4-2: COST RESPONSIBILITY:
Each licensed utility affected herein shall perform all work identified to each
project episode in the construction, removal, repair, reconstruction and
replacement of the cables, lines, poles, pipes and fixtures involved and assume
all costs incident thereto. (1987 Code § 13.12.020)
10-4-3: ASSURANCE OF SUBEXCAVATION AND BACKFILL:
Each licensed utility, upon direction of the town, may be required, upon demand
by the town, to assure subexcavation and backfill work commensurate with
current licensing standards of the town. (1987 Code § 13.12.030)
10-4-4: MAINTAINING PUBLIC SAFETY PRECAUTIONS:
During times and places of repair, reconstruction or replacement, each licensed
utility affected in this chapter shall furnish, provide, erect and maintain all
ordinary and necessary construction precautions for the protection of the work
and safety of the public. (1987 Code § 13.12.040)
10-4-5: FAILURE TO COMPLY:
In the event any licensed utility affected by any of the provisions or
directives of this chapter shall fail to comply with this chapter, the town may
take whatever corrective action deemed reasonably necessary and bill for
collection the respective utility company or association involved for any and
all costs incurred. (1987 Code § 13.12.050)
10-4-6: SUSPENSION OF LICENSE:
Failure to comply with the provisions of this chapter by any utility company,
corporation or association affected by this chapter may be considered by the
town as the basis of just cause for the suspension of any license granted the
affected company, corporation or association as provided by ordinance or law.
(1987 Code § 13.12.060)
CHAPTER 5
PENALTY
SECTION:
10-5-1: Violations; Penalty
10-5-1: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this title, any violation of this title
constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
TITLE 11
SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
11-1-1: Purpose
11-1-2: Conformance With Provisions
11-1-3: Applicability
11-1-4: Street Access Required
11-1-5: Costs
11-1-1: PURPOSE:
   A.   Design: This title is designed to promote the public health, safety,
morals and general welfare in the incorporated areas of the town by:
      1.   Providing for the orderly subdivision of property into lots, sites
or tracts that are established by standards including minimum width and depth;
      2.   Encouraging proper arrangements of streets, roads, alleys, rights of
way and easements in relation to existing or planned public access patterns;
      3.   Ensuring that subdivision developments conform to the comprehensive
plan for area control and development;
      4.   Protecting the environment;
      5.   Providing for adequate and convenient open spaces;
      6.   Providing for community use facilities; and
      7.   Regulating such other matters as the planning and zoning commission
and town council deem necessary in order to protect the best interests of the
public.
   B.   Purposes: This title, by its nature, will also serve the following
specific purposes:
      1.   Each subdivider will know in advance what general subdivision design
is expected, will be able to use established principles of development for his
subdivision and will know what improvements will be necessary.
      2.   Adjoining landowners should have assurance that at a later date
their property can be subdivided without conflict with present plats and should
be protected against poor practices which would destroy values along their
property boundaries.
      3.   Future property owners should be able to purchase sites in newly
subdivided areas with the knowledge that legal descriptions are accurate and
that desirable features have been used in the subdivisions.
      4.   All taxpayers should save money by coordinated, logical street right
of way and utility extensions, and by assurance that improvements are made to
specified standards, and should be able to secure necessary land for public
purposes in advance of high values. (1987 Code § 16.04.010)
11-1-2: CONFORMANCE WITH PROVISIONS:
Under the authority vested in the town council and the planning and zoning
commission to protect the public health, safety and welfare, no final plat of
land subdivision shall be approved and accepted unless it conforms to the
provisions of this title. No annexation shall occur for more than one
previously or contemporaneously divided parcels unless the standards set forth
in this title have been or are contemporaneously applied in a manner which
allows the annexed parcel to be incorporated into town as a subdivision. (Ord.
2012-03, 3-1-2012)
11-1-3: APPLICABILITY:
   A.   Division Into Three Lots, Plats, Etc.: The division of a lot, tract or
parcel of land into three (3) or more lots, plats, sites or other divisions of
land for the purpose, whether immediate or future, of sale or building
development, shall make the transaction subject to the provisions of this title
whether a plat is recorded or not.
   B.   Filed And Recorded After Review And Approval: All plats of a
subdivision of land within the town shall be filed and recorded only after
having been reviewed and approved by the planning and zoning commission and
accepted and signed by the town council.
   C.   Incorporated Land Within Town: This title is applicable to the
incorporated land within the town. (1987 Code § 16.04.030)
11-1-4: STREET ACCESS REQUIRED:
No building shall be erected on any lot nor shall a building permit be issued
for a building unless the street giving access to the lot upon which such
building is proposed to be placed has been approved by the planning and zoning
commission and accepted by the town council as a part of an official
subdivision where the land is subject to section
11-1-1 of this chapter. Dead end streets which are terminated due to natural or
preexisting manmade barriers or which form a continuous loop without any
intersecting street, private or public, may be retained in private ownership,
however a building permit shall only be issued if approved by the Planning and
Zoning Commission and a recordable document is created or produced absolving
the town from maintaining, improving, or upgrading the street. (1987 Code §
16.04.040; amd. Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
11-1-5: COSTS:
Unless otherwise explicitly agreed by resolution of the town council, all costs
and fees associated with or stemming from the processes governed by this title
shall be borne by the land owner or subdivider, including required amended
plats and engineering services. (Ord. 2016-04, 2-18-2016)
CHAPTER 2
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
11-2-1: General Definitions
11-2-1: GENERAL DEFINITIONS: The definitions set out in this chapter apply in
this title:
ALLEY: A public or private way at the rear or side of property permanently
reserved as a means of secondary vehicular access to the abutting property,
generally having less width than a street.
BLOCK: An area of land within a subdivision which area is entirely bounded by
streets or highways, or the exterior boundary or boundaries of the subdivision.
COLLECTOR STREET: A thoroughfare ultimately designed for the movement of one or
more lanes of traffic in each direction, and designated as a secondary street
by the comprehensive plan.
COMPREHENSIVE PLAN: The plan which may be prepared and adopted by the planning
and zoning commission for future growth, protection and development.
CUL-DE-SAC: A dead end street which permanently terminates at a point where a
vehicular turnaround point is provided.
EASEMENT: A right to use a specified space on a lot or parcel of land for
specified purposes such as for public utilities or other public uses.
FRONT LOT: The narrowest lot boundary abutting a street.
FRONTAGE: The line where a lot abuts a dedicated street or highway right of
way. Frontage is expressed in linear feet and is measured along the right of
way.
HALF STREET: A street normally parallel and contiguous to a property line and
of lesser right of way than ultimately required.
IMPROVEMENT: Such work to occur and utilities, paving, traffic controls,
landscaping or other betterments to be installed where agreed to be installed
by the subdivider on the land dedicated or to be dedicated for streets,
highways, public ways and easements or on existing public streets bordering on
the land of the subdivider or on nonpublic lands within or near the subdivision
as are necessary for general use of the lot or subdivision.
LOCAL STREET: A street intended wholly or principally for local neighborhood
traffic.
LOT:
   A.   A parcel of real property with a separate and distinct number or other
designation shown on a plat recorded in the office of the county recorder; or
B. A parcel of real property containing not less lot area than required by the
zone in which it is located, abutting at least one public street, and held
under separate ownership from adjacent property prior to the effective date of
the Lyman zoning ordinance.
LOT LINE ADJUSTMENTS: A change or series of changes to the lot line or lines of
an existing subdivision that do not constitute a division of an existing parcel
or parcels into three (3) or more parcels, lots or building sites.
MAJOR ARTERIAL STREET: A thoroughfare ultimately designed for the movement of
two (2) or more lanes of traffic moving in each direction, and designated as a
major street by the comprehensive plan.
MINOR SUBDIVISION: Any real property, improved or unimproved, or a portion
thereof, shown on the last preceding tax roll as a unit or as contiguous units,
which is divided and/or the lot lines thereof are altered and has the following
features:
   A.   All resulting lots in the minor subdivision have existing access to the
town water and wastewater systems without further construction and/or addition
by the town;
   B.   All resulting lots have frontage on a public street or highway;
   C.   All resulting lots comply with Town Ordinances regarding size,
setbacks, length of frontage and other applicable ordinances;
   D.   The minor subdivision is not created by or in conjunction with an
annexation into town; and
   E.   The minor subdivision results in the creation of three (3) or fewer
lots.
Nothing in this definition shall prevent the Town Planning and Zoning
Commission from declaring a proposed minor subdivision as too complicated and/
or problematic, and therefore requiring the minor subdivision to be processed
as if it is a subdivision.
PERFORMANCE GUARANTEE: Any security which may be accepted by the town council
in lieu of a requirement that certain improvements be made by the subdivider
before the plat is approved, including performance bonds, escrow agreements and
other similar collateral or surety agreements.
PERMANENT MONUMENT: Any structure of masonry, steel or metal permanently placed
on or in the ground, including those expressly placed for surveying.
SERVICE ROAD: A street paralleling and abutting major streets or limited access
highways to provide access to abutting properties.
STREET: Any public right of way dedicated for the purpose of moving vehicular
traffic.
STUB STREET: A street which temporarily terminates at a boundary of the
subdivision with no permanent vehicular turnaround area.
SUBDIVIDER: Refers to a person, firm, corporation, partnership or association
who causes land to be divided into a subdivision for himself or for others.
SUBDIVISION: Any real property, improved or unimproved, or a portion thereof,
shown on the last preceding tax roll as a unit or as contiguous units, which is
divided into four (4) or more parcels, lots or building sites and which does
not qualify under the definition of a minor subdivision herein. Any use of the
word "Subdivision" that does not conflict with Chapter 5 of this Title shall
include Minor Subdivision in their interpretation and application.
THROUGH LOT: Those lots which have street frontage on two (2) opposite ends of
the lot. (1987 Code, chapter 16.08; amd. 2004 Code; Ord. 2011-03, 2-17-2011;
Ord. 2012-03, 3-1-2012; Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
CHAPTER 3
PRELIMINARY PLAT
SECTION:
11-3-1: Basic Considerations
11-3-2: Procedural Outline
11-3-3: Preliminary Sketch
11-3-4: Contents And Filing Of Plat
11-3-5: Supporting Data
11-3-6: Distribution
11-3-7: Review
11-3-8: Hearing
11-3-9: Conditions On Approval
11-3-10: Expiration; Approval
11-3-1: BASIC CONSIDERATIONS:
   A.   Good Counsel Essential: A successful subdivision involves coordination
and understanding of many factors related to law, engineering, marketing,
financing and planning. Because of the need for thorough analysis, an
individual considering the platting of a parcel of land is advised to contact
his attorney, an engineer or surveyor, a real estate or marketing firm, a
financial lending institution and a land planning specialist. While certain
shortcuts may be possible, good counsel on all phases of a proposed subdivision
is essential at an early stage. Through this review, the subdivider may be able
to save time, avoid unnecessary mistakes and make the most of his
opportunities.
   B.   Questions To Be Considered: Some of the questions which should be
considered by both the subdivider and the planning and zoning commission at the
onset are as follows:
      1.   Is there a need for additional residential sites in the area?
      2.   What type and price homes are likely to be built?
      3.   What lot sizes would be most appropriate? (Lot sizes should conform
to zoning ordinance.)
      4.   Should areas be reserved for business or industrial use?
      5.   Does the tract include special scenic locations or areas of
historical importance which need to be reserved?
      6.   Will school and/or playground sites be required?
      7.   If the plat abuts a major street or expressway, will additional
right of way or limited access features be necessary?
      8.   Are portions of the area subject to flooding?
      9.   Are soil conditions favorable for construction purposes?
      10.   How can water, sanitary sewer, storm sewer, electrical and gas
utility services be provided?
      11.   Can the subdivision be designed as part of an existing
neighborhood?
      12.   Should the planned unit development concept be considered?
      13.   Can any of the land adjacent to the site be included?
      14.   Will the site be adversely affected by its surrounding environment
or will the proposed usage adversely affect the environment?
      15.   What legal or tax problems are likely to be encountered?
      16.   Does the proposed usage meet the requirements of the comprehensive
plan and zoning regulations? (1987 Code § 16.12.010)
11-3-2: PROCEDURAL OUTLINE:
The following outline is included as a guide for the subdivider to use in
obtaining systematic review and approval or disapproval of a proposed
subdivision. The planning and zoning commission may delegate the initial
contact and review responsibilities to an authorized representative:
   A.   Obtain Lyman subdivision and zoning information.
   B.   Analyze proposed development concepts for conformity.
   C.   Prepare preliminary sketch (optional).
   D.   Prepare preliminary plat with a vicinity map (unless the subdivision is
a minor subdivision.
   E.   Submit preliminary plat to planning and zoning commission no less than
fourteen (14) days before the next scheduled planning and zoning meeting.
   F.   Meet with Town Public Works Supervisor or designee to determine
placement of utilities, including the possible installation the entire length
of the subdivision or lots.
   G.   Prepare final plat.
   H.   Obtain required specifications, dedications, etc.
   I.   Submit final plat to planning and zoning commission.
   J.   Submit final plat to town council.
   K.   Record approved and signed final plat with accompanying Resolution of
the Town Council.
(1987 Code § 16.12.020; amd. Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
11-3-3: PRELIMINARY SKETCH:
If the subdivider chooses, he may submit a sketch map to the planning and
zoning commission (or their designated representative) for their review and
comments prior to making application for planning and zoning commission review
of the preliminary plat. The sketch map should be prepared in a manner which
generally defines the layout of the streets, lots and location of any public
uses, such as schools and parks. It is the purpose of the sketch map to resolve
any major points of disagreement with the planning and zoning commission before
the subdivider goes to the expense of designing and drawing the preliminary
plat. No action is required of the planning and zoning commission other than to
review the sketch plan and offer comments appropriate to the subdivider. (1987
Code § 16.12.030)
11-3-4: CONTENTS AND FILING OF PLAT:
   A.   Filing Of Preliminary Plat:
      1.   Filing With Planning And Zoning Commission: The first official step
which must be taken by a subdivider in order to obtain approval of any proposed
subdivision is the filing of a preliminary plat with the planning and zoning
commission or designated representative.
      2.   Number Of Copies Required: Each subdivider shall file with the
planning and zoning commission a minimum of ten (10) prints. The planning and
zoning commission may require more if necessary for distribution.
      3.   Time Of Filing: The preliminary plat shall be filed no later than
fourteen (14) days prior to the commission's next regular meeting for staff or
agency review. If properly submitted, as required in this section, the matter
shall be placed on the agenda of the next regular meeting following the
fourteen (14) day review period.
   B.   Specifications; Required Information: The preliminary plat shall be
clearly and legibly drawn and shall have the following information. The scale
of the map shall not be smaller than one inch equals one hundred feet (1" =
100') for subdivisions less than one hundred sixty (160) acres, and one inch
equals two hundred feet (1" = 200') for areas more than one hundred sixty (160)
acres. The following information shall be contained on the preliminary plat:
      1.   The name of the tract.
      2.   Name and address of record owner or owners.
      3.   Name and address of the subdivider.
      4.   Name and business address of the designer of the subdivision.
      5.   The location, names and existing widths of existing streets,
highways, easements and recorded section lines.
      6.   The locations, names and existing widths of existing and proposed
streets, highways and easements.
      7.   Approximate lot layout and approximate dimensions of each lot.
      8.   Approximate boundaries of areas subject to the inundation of storm
water overflow.
      9.   Existing contours at two foot (2') intervals for predominant ground
slopes within the tract between level and five percent (5%) grade and five foot
(5') contours for predominant ground slopes within the tract over five percent
(5%) grade.
      10.   State of improvements and public utilities to be made or installed,
including the location of designated street lighting poles, wires and lights.
      11.   Approximate location of all tree clusters, natural features or
permanent significant manmade structures standing within the boundaries of the
proposed subdivision.
      12.   Total acreage of the subdivision.
      13.   Approximate boundary of subdivision.
      14.   The date, north arrow and scale of the map.
      15.   The vicinity or key map (smaller scale) which indicates all
existing subdivisions, streets and boundary lines, or other tracts within one-
eighth (1/8) mile in each direction of the proposed preliminary plat.
      16.   Existing and/or proposed zoning classifications of the land
proposed for subdivision and zoning of the land adjacent to the proposed
subdivision.
      17.   Legal description by township, range and section.
      18.   Adjacent property owners.
   C.   All plats, both preliminary and final, submitted to the Planning and
Zoning Commission shall be filed with the Town no less than fourteen (14) days
before the Planning and Zoning Commission meeting considering the submission to
allow time for review. (1987 Code § 16.12.040; amd. Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
11-3-5: SUPPORTING DATA:
In addition to the preliminary plat, the following data, if applicable, shall
be submitted with the application:
   A.   Water: Method of providing water and estimated gallons per day of water
requirements if a distribution system is proposed.
   B.   Sewage: Estimated total number of gallons per day of sewage to be
treated and added to the town system.
   C.   Storm Drainage: An analysis of preliminary storm drainage problems and
methods for caring for storm runoffs.
   D.   Utility Companies: A letter from all utility companies involved
addressed to the planning and zoning commission setting forth any comments they
may have concerning the design of the plat as it affects their utility service.
   E.   Soils, Geologic And Ground Water Analysis: A soils, geologic and ground
water analysis is desirable, but is optional at this stage unless specifically
requested by the planning and zoning commission or town council. (1987 Code §
16.12.050)
11-3-6: DISTRIBUTION:
   A.   Distribution By Commission: The planning and zoning commission or its
authorized representatives shall, upon receipt and acceptance of a complete
preliminary plat application, distribute copies of prints of the plat provided
by the subdivider as follows:
      1.   To the appropriate school district.
      2.   To other agencies as may be deemed desirable by the planning and
zoning commission.
   B.   Response: The agencies listed in subsection A of this section shall
respond to the planning and zoning commission prior to or at the hearing upon
the proposed subdivision. Failure to respond at that time shall constitute a
waiver of any agency's right to make recommendations. (1987 Code § 16.12.060)
11-3-7: REVIEW:
The planning and zoning commission shall approve or disapprove the preliminary
plat within thirty one (31) days after their initial review of the request at a
regular meeting. Otherwise, such plat shall be deemed to have been approved,
and a certificate to that effect shall be issued by the planning and zoning
commission by demand. The applicant may, however, agree to waive this thirty
one (31) day requirement with the consent of the planning and zoning
commission, and extend it to such a date mutually agreed upon by both parties.
If the preliminary plat is disapproved, the planning and zoning commission
shall state the reasons for such denial. (1987 Code § 16.12.070)
11-3-8: HEARING:
   A.   Required: No plat shall be acted on the by planning and zoning
commission without first reviewing the matter at a regularly established
meeting of the commission.
   B.   Notice: Notice shall be sent to the address of the subdivider by first
class mail stating the time and place of such meeting. Similar notice shall be
mailed to the owners of the land immediately adjoining the platted land as
their names and addresses appear on the tax records of the county. The names
and addresses shall be provided by the applicant with the certification that
they are correct to the best of the applicant's knowledge.
   C.   Conditional Approval: If the plat is approved conditionally or subject
to modifications, the nature of the required modifications shall be stated in
the records of the planning and zoning commission and a letter defining them
mailed to the applicant. (1987 Code § 16.12.080)
11-3-9: CONDITIONS ON APPROVAL:
The planning and zoning commission shall have the power to agree with the
applicant upon the use, height, area or bulk requirements or restrictions
governing buildings and premises within the subdivision, provided such
requirements or restrictions do not authorize the violation of the then
effective zoning ordinance of the town. Zoning variances may only occur when
the subdivision is filed as a planned unit development. Such requirements or
restrictions shall be stated upon the plat prior to the approval and recording
of the plat and shall have the same force by law and be enforceable in the same
manner and with the same sanctions and penalties and subject to the same powers
of amendment or repeal as though set out as a part of the zoning ordinance or
map of the town. No action under this section shall be binding for any purpose
until the action has been approved by the town council. (1987 Code § 16.12.090)
11-3-10: EXPIRATION; APPROVAL:
   A.   Time Limitation: Within eighteen (18) months after the date of approval
or conditional approval of the preliminary plat by the planning and zoning
commission, the subdivider shall cause the subdivision to be accurately
surveyed and the final map thereof to be prepared in accordance with the
preliminary plat for at least the first phase, with any and all alterations and
changes required thereto. In the event this eighteen (18) month time limit
expires prior to submission of the final plat, the original approval is deemed
void.
   B.   Request For Extension: Prior to the date on which the preliminary plat
becomes void, the subdivider may request the planning and zoning commission to
extend the time limit not to exceed one additional year. (1987 Code § 1.12.100)
CHAPTER 4
FINAL PLAT
SECTION:
11-4-1: Contents
11-4-2: Supporting Documents
11-4-3: Planning And Zoning Commission Action
11-4-4: Town Council Action; Recording
11-4-5: Street Dedications And Permits
11-4-6: Changes After Approval
11-4-7: Copy Of Plat As Recorded
11-4-8: As Built Improvement Drawings
11-4-1: CONTENTS:
Prior to the expiration of the preliminary plat, the final plat shall be
submitted to the planning and zoning commission. The following is required of
and on the final plat:
   A.   Specifications: The final plat shall be clearly and legibly drawn in
black, waterproof India ink or produced by photographic process upon tracing
cloth or other acceptable, stable based material. Affidavits, certificates and
acknowledgements may be legibly stamped, printed or photographed upon the map
in opaque ink. Signatures shall be in opaque black ink. The size of each sheet
to be recorded shall conform to Wyoming Statutes. The scale of the plat shall
be large enough to show all details clearly and enough sheets shall be used to
accomplish this end. The scale shall not be smaller than one inch equals one
hundred feet (1" = 100'), except that when all of the lots are one acre or
larger, the scale may be not smaller than one inch equals two hundred feet (1"
= 200'). The particular number of the sheet and the total number of the sheets
comprising the plat shall be stated on each of the sheets, and the relation of
each adjoining sheet shall be clearly shown by key maps and match lines.
   B.   Preparation And Certification By Surveyor: The plat shall be prepared
and certification made as to its accuracy by a registered land surveyor
licensed to do such work according to the state. A workmanlike execution of the
plat shall be made in every detail. The accuracy of the field survey and of the
plat dimensions and closures shall be one in five thousand (1:5,000).
   C.   Point Of Beginning: The point of beginning shall be indicated, and
proper reference to the monumented perimeter survey shall be delineated on the
drawing.
   D.   Bearings And Distances: All bearings and distances of the boundary
shall be indicated outside the boundary line, not inside with the lot
dimensions.
   E.   Blocks; Lots: All blocks, and all lots within each block, shall be
consecutively numbered.
   F.   Curved Boundaries: On curved boundaries and all curves on the plat,
sufficient data should be given to enable the reestablishment of the curves.
This curve data should include the following:
      1.   Points of curvature.
      2.   Points of tangency.
      3.   Radius of curve.
      4.   Arc length, chord length and bearing.
      5.   Central angle.
   G.   Streets, Walkways, Easements And Alleys: All streets, walkways,
easements and alleys shall be designated as such and named. Bearings and
dimensions shall be given.
   H.   Irregularly Shaped Lots: All dimensions of irregularly shaped lots
shall be indicated in each lot.
   I.   Lot Lines: Bearings shall be given for all lot lines except that
bearings need not be given for each lot in a series that are similar. In this
instance, only the end lots shall be so designated with bearings.
   J.   Uncontiguous Parcels; Multiple Plats: Parcels not contiguous shall not
be included in one plat nor shall more than one plat be made on the same sheet.
   K.   Other Information: Other information required on the plat is as
follows:
      1.   Name of subdivision, true north point, and date.
      2.   Name and address of owner or owners of record.
      3.   Total acreage of tract and number of lots.
      4.   Township, range, section and quarter section, block and lot numbers.
      5.   Graphic scale.
      6.   Certification of title showing that the applicant is the landowner.
      7.   Legal description of the property included within the subdivision
contained in a statement by the owner dedicating streets, rights of way and any
sites for public use. The description and statement shall be in the form
prescribed by Wyoming Statutes.
      8.   Certification showing approval by town engineer.
      9.   Certification showing approval by the planning and zoning
commission.
      10.   Under the title of each plat, the following words: "In the Town of
Lyman, County of Uinta, State of Wyoming".
      11.   Mayor's certification showing acceptance of the plat by the town
council. The certificate shall show the ordinance number and date of
acceptance. (1987 Code § 16.16.010)
11-4-2: SUPPORTING DOCUMENTS:
   A.   Drawings: The following documents shall be submitted with the final
plat drawing and be considered a part of the final plat submission. Drawings
showing layout of the following:
      1.   Utilities: All utilities, including the location of street lighting
poles, wires and lights, plus statements from utility companies (water, sewer,
electric, gas, telephone, etc.) as applicable, that service will be provided to
the development, and that the utility company or subdivider will provide
necessary on site and off site improvements.
      2.   Roads And Bridges: Profile and typical cross section drawings of
roads and bridges.
      3.   Grading And Drainage Plan: The proposed grading plan shall be
indicated by dashed line contours superimposed on solid line contours of
existing topography for the area of the final plat. Such contours shall be at
one foot (1') intervals for predominant ground slopes within the tract between
level and five percent (5%) grade and two foot (2') contours for predominant
ground slopes within the tract over five percent (5%) grade.
   B.   Utility And Street Drawings: All utility and street drawings shall meet
the requirements contained in the "Town Of Lyman, Wyoming, Standards And
Specifications". These drawings shall be prepared by a registered land
surveyor, as required by the laws of the state, who is licensed to do such work
in the state. An exact copy of a certificate of a reputable title insurance or
abstract company or attorney which shall set forth the names of all owners of
property shall be included on the plat. This shall also include a list of all
mortgages, judgments, liens, easements, contracts and agreements of record in
the county, which shall affect the property covered by such plats. If the
opinion of title discloses any of the above, the holders or owners of such
mortgages, judgments, liens, easements, contracts or agreements shall be
required to join in and approve the application before the plat shall be acted
upon by the town council.
   C.   Public Improvements: The subdivider shall be required to submit
construction drawings and details for all public improvements proposed or
required by the planning and zoning commission or this title, including cost
estimated for the installation and construction of these improvements. The
planning and zoning commission and town council may review these plans or have
them reviewed by the town engineer to check compliance with local standards.
(1987 Code § 16.16.020)
11-4-3: PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION ACTION:
   A.   Submittal; Placement On Agenda: The subdivider shall submit five (5)
copies of the final plat and utility drawings to the town engineer at least
fourteen (14) days prior to the meeting at which such plat is to be considered.
If properly submitted in full compliance with these regulations, the matter
shall be placed on the agenda of the next regular meeting of the planning and
zoning commission after the fourteen (14) day review period. (1987 Code §
16.16.030; amd. 2004 Code)
   B.   Commission Action: Within thirty one (31) days after the review of the
final plat, at a regular meeting, the planning and zoning commission shall
approve, disapprove or approve subject to modifications, the final plat. Such
action shall be recorded in the records of the planning and zoning commission.
   C.   Basis For Rejection: The only basis for rejection of a plat shall be
its nonconformance to adopted rules, regulations and ordinances concurrently in
force and affecting the land and its development in the town, and its lack of
conformance with the approved preliminary plat. (1987 Code § 16.16.030)
11-4-4: TOWN COUNCIL ACTION; RECORDING:
   A.   Submittal; Performance Guarantee: After the approval of the final plat
by the planning and zoning commission, the original and one copy of the plat
shall be presented to the town council for its review and approval and
acceptance of all dedications which may be provided on the final plat for
public use. Approval of the final plat is granted only when public improvements
have been installed in accordance with the plans, or if a performance guarantee
in the form of surety bonds or other suitable means (in a form acceptable to
the town's legal advisor) has been secured with the subdivider for those
improvements not yet installed. The amount of the performance guarantee shall
be established by the town council.
   B.   Recording; Term: A soon as possible after approval of the map and
dedications, the final plat shall be recorded by the county clerk, unless the
subdivider requests a delay. If the final plat has not been recorded within
ninety (90) days after the approval of the town council, the approving actions
shall be deemed void. (1987 Code § 16.16.040)
11-4-5: STREET DEDICATIONS AND PERMITS:
   A.   Proof Of Dedication: Where a portion of an existing easement is
contiguous to a proposed easement or right of way within the subdivision, proof
of the dedication of the existing easement or right of way acceptable to the
town council must be submitted when requested.
   B.   State Highway Permit: When a new street will intersect with a state
highway, a copy of the state highway permit shall be submitted. (1987 Code §
16.16.050)
11-4-6: CHANGES AFTER APPROVAL:
In no case shall additions, corrections or modifications of any kind be made to
the final plat other than signatures required after the final plat has been
approved by the town council. (1987 Code § 16.16.060)
11-4-7: COPY OF PLAT AS RECORDED:
After recording of the final plat, the subdivider shall furnish the town
engineer (or other authority designated by the planning and zoning commission)
with one reproducible map and one print of the final plat, as officially
recorded. (1987 Code § 16.16.070)
11-4-8: AS BUILT IMPROVEMENT DRAWINGS:
After all public utilities and improvements are in place, as built construction
drawings and details shall be filed with the town engineer or other
representative designated by the town council. (1987 Code § 16.16.080)
CHAPTER 5
RESUBDIVISIONS AND LOT LINE ADJUSTMENTS
SECTION:
11-5-1: Resubdivision Procedure
11-5-1: RESUBDIVISION PROCEDURE:
Minor subdivisions shall follow all procedures of a subdivision as outlined
above, except that a minor subdivision shall not be required to:
   A.   Prepare or submit a preliminary sketch;
   B.   Prepare or submit a preliminary plat with a vicinity map; or
   C.   Submit a preliminary plat to the planning and zoning commission.
(Ord. 2017-14, 9-21-2017; amd. Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
CHAPTER 6
MOUNTAIN SUBDIVISIONS
SECTION:
11-6-1: Permitted Deviations; Redesign Or Denial
11-6-2: Determination Of Mountainous Character
11-6-3: Special Problems
11-6-1: PERMITTED DEVIATIONS; REDESIGN OR DENIAL:
   A.   Permitted Deviations: If, in the opinion of the planning and zoning
commission, the topography of a proposed subdivision has sufficient slope to be
considered mountainous, minor deviations may be made from the standards of this
title, if, in the opinion of the planning and zoning commission, such
deviations will not materially affect the general health, safety or welfare of
future or adjacent residents.
   B.   Redesign Or Denial: If significant deviations are necessary to make the
project feasible, it may be determined that the topography simply is not
conducive to residential purposes. In this instance, the project may require
redesign or denial. (1987 Code § 16.24.010)
11-6-2: DETERMINATION OF MOUNTAINOUS CHARACTER:
For the purpose of determining if the area is considered mountainous, the
applicant should submit plans for a preliminary review by the planning and
zoning commission. General agreement as to basic design principles could occur
at that time. The planning and zoning commission, however, is under no
obligation to commit themselves until all of the submittal requirements of the
preliminary plat are filed. (1987 Code § 16.24.020)
11-6-3: SPECIAL PROBLEMS:
In addition to normal subdivision problems, the planning and zoning commission
will be concerned with geologic hazards, grades of proposed streets, method of
handling slash materials and other problems created by mountainous development.
(1987 Code § 16.24.030)
CHAPTER 7
PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT
SECTION:
11-7-1: Purpose
11-7-2: Application And Procedure
11-7-1: PURPOSE:
The planned unit development concept is being used to encourage more creative
and flexible use of land and to provide greater flexibility in land
development. This type of development can occur by relaxing the minimum and
maximum requirements of zoning/subdivision regulations and by permitting the
combination of a variety of housing types with open space, recreation
facilities and community facilities with the ultimate result being better
living environments. (1987 Code § 16.28.010)
11-7-2: APPLICATION AND PROCEDURE:
If a planned unit development is proposed, variances to the requirements of
this title may be authorized. The procedures for application shall meet all of
the requirements of submittal, review and approval as defined in title 12 of
this code. Preliminary and final plats would be submitted at their appropriate
times with the PUD application items for concurrent review as required for
subdivision. (1987 Code § 16.28.020)
CHAPTER 8
DESIGN STANDARDS
SECTION:
11-8-1: Generally
11-8-2: Preservation Of Natural Features
11-8-3: Streets
11-8-4: Easements
11-8-5: Blocks
11-8-6: Lots
11-8-7: Dedications For Public Purposes (Rep. by Ord. 2019-02, 3-21-2019)
11-8-8: Required Improvements
11-8-9: Official Standards
11-8-1: GENERALLY:
The general location and alignment of streets and lot size shall conform to the
comprehensive plan and zoning requirements for the Town. Efforts should be made
to encourage good design practices, incorporating new ideas, improving planning
techniques which vary from the typical grid street pattern now commonly found
in many older subdivisions. The topography and other natural features of the
site should be taken into consideration and plans developed in such a manner
that these natural features benefit the total development. This may be done by
a curvilinear pattern, open spaces for recreation or pedestrian movements, or
it may be accomplished by increasing cluster or townhouse developments which
permit greater use of open space and greater preservation of natural
topographic and environmental features. The design standards set out in this
chapter shall apply to all subdivisions. (1987 Code § 16.32.010)
11-8-2: PRESERVATION OF NATURAL FEATURES:
The design and development of subdivisions shall preserve, insofar as possible,
the natural terrain, natural drainage, existing topsoil and trees. (1987 Code §
16.32.020)
11-8-3: STREETS:
   A.   Local Streets: Local streets shall be designed in such a manner that
through traffic within the subdivision will be discouraged.
   B.   Intersections: Streets shall be laid out so as to intersect as nearly
as possible at right angles.
   C.   Cul-De-Sacs: A system of cul-de-sac streets is encouraged; however, the
maximum length of the cul-de-sac shall not exceed six hundred feet (600'),
unless the lots adjoining such streets are one acre or larger and special
permission is granted by the Planning and Zoning Commission to have the street
extended an additional length. The turnaround area shall have a minimum radius
of fifty feet (50') of right-of-way and a curb or pavement edge radius of forty
two feet (42'), or some other suitable turning area approved by the Town
Council.
   D.   Minimum Width: The minimum width of streets shall be as shown in the
"Town of Lyman, Wyoming, Standards and Specifications".
   E.   Names: Street names shall not duplicate an existing street name unless
the street is an extension of the existing street. Street names shall be
subject to the approval of the Planning and Zoning Commission.
   F.   Centerline Curve Radius: The minimum centerline curve radius permitted
on streets shall be as follows:
      1.   Major arterial street: One thousand feet (1,000').
      2.   Collector street: Six hundred feet (600').
      3.   Local street: One hundred fifty feet (150').
   G.   Alleys: Alleys shall be provided only if required by the Planning and
Zoning Commission. The minimum width of the alley shall be sixteen feet (16').
Dead end alleys shall be avoided whenever possible. If unavoidable, a
turnaround area shall be provided at the end of the alley.
   H.   Conformance With Comprehensive Plan: All streets shall conform to the
location as may be defined by the Lyman comprehensive plan when the plan is
adopted.
   I.   Stub Streets: Stub streets may be used as a means to allow for future
connections. Stub streets of over two hundred feet (200') in length shall
provide a temporary turnaround area.
   J.   Intersections With Major Streets: Intersections of local streets with
major streets shall be kept at minimum.
   K.   Half Streets: Half streets shall not be permitted except to complete a
half street already in existence.
   L.   Streets Intersecting From Opposite Sides: Two (2) streets intersecting
from opposite sides shall intersect at the extension of their centerline, or
their centerlines shall be offset at least one hundred fifty feet (150').
   M.   Sight Distance: To ensure adequate sight distances, when street roadway
lines deflect more than one degree (1°), connection shall be made by horizontal
curves.
   N.   Vertical Curves: Vertical curves shall be used at changes of grade
exceeding one percent (1%) and shall be designed to provide, at a minimum, a
sight distance of two hundred feet (200') for local streets and three hundred
feet (300') for all other streets (arterial and collector streets shall be
determined by the current specifications of the American Association of State
Highway Officials and as may be required by the Town Engineer).
   O.   Service Roads: Service roads or other design solutions to limited
access may be required when the subdivision abuts a major street, highway or
freeway.
   P.   Driveways: Driveways shall not be permitted to have direct access to
major streets. (1987 Code § 16.32.030)
11-8-4: EASEMENTS:
Easements shall be provided for all utilities, drainageways, channels or
streams which traverse across or serve the subdivision. (1987 Code § 16.32.040)
11-8-5: BLOCKS:
The length, width and shapes of blocks shall be determined by the type of use,
zoning requirements, needs for convenient access, circulation and safety of
street traffic and limitations and opportunities of topography. Unless unusual
circumstances exist, block length will not exceed one thousand two hundred feet
(1,200') or be less than three hundred feet (300'). (1987 Code § 16.32.050)
11-8-6: LOTS:
   A.   Minimum Width: The minimum width of lots shall conform to the
applicable zoning standards.
      1.   On cul-de-sac streets or curved streets, the lot width required
shall, at a minimum, apply at the building setback line as defined by the zone
in which the property is located.
      2.   Through lots with frontage at opposite ends should be generally
avoided, except where it is essential to provide a separation of residential
development from major arterial highways.
   B.   Side Lot Lines: Side lot lines shall be at substantially right angles
or radial to street lines.
   C.   Street Frontage: All residential lots in a subdivision shall front on a
public street. (1987 Code § 16.32.060)
11-8-7: DEDICATIONS FOR PUBLIC PURPOSES:
(Rep. by Ord. 2019-02, 3-21-2019)
11-8-8: REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS:
Improvements which the subdivider shall make or agree to make at the cost of
the subdivider prior to acceptance and approval for the final plat by the Town
Council shall be:
   A.   Grading, Curbs And Gutters: Grading, concrete curbs and gutters, cross
gutters, drainage and drainage structures necessary to the proper use, safety
and drainage of streets and highways.
   B.   Pavement: Pavement material and thickness (including base) as
determined by a soils test and approved by the Town Engineer, the test to be
performed by a qualified soils engineer.
   C.   Sidewalks: Concrete sidewalks shall be provided not less than four feet
(4') wide. Wider sidewalks may be required along major and collector highways
or for streets abutting Commercial or Industrially zoned land. In areas where
lots are consistently wider than ninety feet (90'), sidewalks may be waived by
the Town Council.
   D.   Trees: (Rep. by Ord. 2019-01, 3-21-2019)
   E.   Water Mains; Fire Hydrants: Water mains and fire hydrants of a size,
type and at a location designated by the Town Engineer.
   F.   Sanitary Sewer Facilities: Sanitary sewer facilities and connections
for each lot shall be provided. Stubs from public utilities where provided and
from sanitary sewers shall be made available for each lot in such manner as
will obviate the necessity for disturbing the street pavement, gutter, culvert
and curb when sewer line connections are made.
   G.   Street Name Signs: Street name signs shall be installed at all street
intersections. The subdivider shall bear the total expense in the purchasing
and installation of all required street name signs.
   H.   Traffic Islands: Traffic islands shall be provided where they are
required to control the movement of traffic.
   I.   Barricades And Reflectors: Barricades and reflectors shall be provided
along the ends of all dead end or without turnaround streets, and at the ends
of culverts and other dangerous areas.
   J.   Subdivider To Perform Work: The subdivider shall perform all work
required by the Town Engineer in connection with the demolition, moving,
altering or converting of any structure or facility, including underground
facilities, either wholly or partially within the subdivision or affected
thereby.
   K.   Survey Monuments: Permanent survey monuments as described in chapter 9
of this title shall be set at all subdivision boundary corners.
   L.   Other Improvements: The subdivider shall make such other improvements
as needed when deemed necessary by the Town Council to preserve the public
health, safety or welfare.
   M.   Sewer And Water Line Extensions: If sewer and water facilities are not
available adjacent to the proposed subdivision, it shall be the responsibility
of the subdivider to extend such lines in a manner satisfactory to the Town
Council. Where such lines may benefit existing developments, the Town Council
can make such a determination and, if deemed necessary, partially finance or
make other arrangements as needed to assist in such construction.
   N.   Lights: The subdivider shall install light poles and luminaries of the
same size and brand as other poles and luminaries in the area and as approved
by the engineer. The pole and luminaire shall be supplied with electricity and
the luminaire shall be attached so as to illuminate and not obscure the area of
intended illumination. Such light poles and luminaries shall be installed at
each intersection and/or at minimum intervals equal to the interval of and
corresponding with the number and placement of fire hydrants in the
subdivision. (1987 Code § 16.32.080; amd. Ord. 2019-01, 3-21-2019; Ord. 2021-
05, 6-3-2021)
11-8-9: OFFICIAL STANDARDS:
The "Town of Lyman, Wyoming, Standards and Specifications" shall be the
"Official Development Standards", as an appendix to the ordinance codified in
this title. These standards shall be used as an administrative guide for the
Town Engineer as he deals with public improvements relating to subdivisions.
(1987 Code § 16.32.090)
CHAPTER 9
MONUMENTATION
SECTION:
11-9-1: Boundary Control
11-9-2: Required Monumentation
11-9-3: Monument Construction
11-9-4: Markings
11-9-1: BOUNDARY CONTROL:
   A.   Section Lines Or Section Subdivision Lines Form Boundaries: Where
section lines or section subdivision lines form part of the boundaries of a
subdivision, these lines should be legally established and monumented as per
the 1947 bureau of land management "Manual Of Instruction For The Survey Of
Public Lands Of The United States", and the pertinent detailed information
should be shown on the plat.
   B.   Perimeter Subdivision Lines: Perimeter subdivision lines should be
accurately related by distance and bearing to established street lines, block
corners and other recognized permanent monuments and surveys.
   C.   Boundary Control Points: Boundary control points should be
appropriately named on both the plat and the monument, and angle points shall
be numbered.
   D.   Planimetric Features: Planimetric features such as rivers, lakes,
canals, cliffs, etc., that become a part of the boundaries of the exterior or
the interior of the subdivision should be shown and monumented with sufficient
detail so that the intent of the subdivider will be clear; and so that the
points and boundaries can be reestablished economically.
   E.   Witness Corners: Witness corners should be set or accessory ties made
to block and boundary corners that are apt to be destroyed or become
inaccessible. Both offset monuments and witness corners, when set on the
original surveys, should be so noted on the monument and on the plat.
   F.   PC And PT On Curves: The PC and PT on all curves should be monumented
in the field.
   G.   Property Corners: All property corners shall be surveyed, monumented
and identified.
   H.   Distances And Bearings: Distances and bearings shall be shown
sufficiently to ensure closure and prevent any possibility of wrong
interpretation.
   I.   Differences Between Distances And Bearings: Any difference between
bearings and distances on this survey and recorded distances and bearings of
other adjoining surveys should be noted.
   J.   Monument Descriptions: Descriptions of all monuments set should be
noted.
   K.   Recovered Monuments: The descriptions of existing recovered monuments
should be given.
   L.   Perimeter To Be Surveyed: The entire perimeter of the subdivision
should be surveyed and balanced to ensure accuracy of survey and to provide a
basis for restoration of lost corners.
   M.   Elevations: Elevations shall be referred to as USGS datum and at least
one bench mark established on each subdivision. (1987 Code § 16.36.010)
11-9-2: REQUIRED MONUMENTATION:
   A.   Outside Angle Points: All outside angle points should be monumented
with stamped and marked brass caps that are set either in concrete or on pipe
of sufficient length to allow permanency. If the original outside boundary
monumentation is in a location likely to be obliterated, i.e., street, alley,
etc., it should then be adequately witnessed with the above mentioned
monuments.
   B.   Other Points On Map: All points other than outside perimeter points
which are shown on the map should be monumented with a monument which can be
marked and identified without question. (1987 Code § 16.36.020)
11-9-3: MONUMENT CONSTRUCTION:
   A.   Perimeter And Block Monuments:
      1.   Firm Soil: Two and one-half inches (21/2") nominal iron pipe or
equivalent thirty inches (30") long with metal cap at least one and three-
eighths inches (13/8") in diameter or metal tags.
      2.   Solid Rock: One and three-eighths inch (13/8") diameter metal tablet
with a one and one-half inch (11/2") long shank countersunk in rock and grouted
with "Por-Rok," epoxy cement or equal.
      3.   Loose Soil, Sand, Marsh, Etc.: Monuments shall not be set, but shall
be witnessed.
      4.   Monuments Within Streets Or Roads:
         a.   Three-fourths inch (3/4") nominal iron pipe or no. 5 rebar twenty
four inches (24") long with metal cap at least one and three-eighths inches
(13/8") in diameter. Monuments set within roadway areas shall be placed so that
their tops are six (6) to eight inches (8") below the final road surface.
         b.   Perimeter or block monuments which shall have to be moved for
road or street construction shall be referenced and shall be reset from these
reference marks as soon as practicable after road or street earthwork is
completed and preferably before paving.
   B.   Lot Markers And Reference Marks:
      1.   Firm Soil: No. 5 steel rebar eighteen (18) to twenty four inches
(24") long with metal caps or tags identifying the corner.
      2.   Concrete Walks Or Curbs: Three-fourths inch (3/4") diameter blind
rivet with one-fourth inch (1/4") diameter shank one-half inch (1/2") long.
      3.   Solid Rock: Blind rivet as in subsection B2 of this section, or one-
fourth inch (1/4") diameter by three inch (3") long iron bar grouted in drilled
hole two inches (2") deep.
   C.   Bench Marks: Upon completion of construction, bench marks shall be
established on fire hydrants or other permanent items agreeable to the town
engineer.
   D.   Minimum Construction Standards: Construction standards given in this
section are minimum. More massive and durable monuments are, of course,
permitted. (1987 Code § 16.36.030)
11-9-4: MARKINGS:
   A.   Surveyor's Registration Number: All monuments, markers and bench marks
shall have affixed securely to the top thereof the registration number of the
land surveyor responsible for the establishment of such monument, marker or
bench mark.
   B.   Aliquot Corners: Aliquot corners within the public land survey system
shall be marked with the bureau of land management designation pursuant to
chapter IV of the "Manual Of Instructions For The Survey Of The Public Lands Of
The United States", 1947, except that the date may be omitted.
   C.   Bench Marks: Bench marks shall be stamped with the letters "B.M." and
the elevation. (1987 Code § 16.36.040)
CHAPTER 10
LAND RESERVATION
SECTION:
11-10-1: School Sites
11-10-1: SCHOOL SITES:
Prior to approval of the preliminary plat, the subdivider shall inform the
school district of his intentions to subdivide and, if deemed necessary by the
district, reserve land suitable for future school usage. (1987 Code §
16.40.010)
