CHAPTER 12
ADMINISTRATION
SECTION:
11-12-1: Interpretation
11-12-2: Variances
11-12-3: Filing Fee
11-12-4: Repealed
11-12-5: Amendment
11-12-1: INTERPRETATION:
In the interpretation and application of the provisions of this title, the
following regulations shall govern:
   A.   Provisions And Minimum Requirements: In their interpretation and
application, the provisions of this title shall be regarded as the minimum
requirements for the protection of the public health, safety, comfort,
convenience, prosperity and welfare of the inhabitants of Lyman. This title
shall therefore be regarded as remedial, and shall be liberally construed to
further its underlying purposes.
   B.   Application Of Overlapping Regulations: Whenever both provisions of
this title or any provision in any other law, ordinance, resolution, rule or
regulation of any kind contain any restrictions covering any of the same
subject matter, whichever restrictions are more restrictive or impose higher
standards or requirements shall govern.
   C.   Existing Permits And Private Agreements: This title is not intended to
abrogate or annul:
      1.   Any permits issued before the effective date of this chapter; or
      2.   Any easement, covenant or any other private agreement. (1987 Code §
16.48.010)
11-12-2: VARIANCES:
The town council may authorize variances from this title in cases where, due to
exceptional topographical conditions or other conditions peculiar to the site,
an unnecessary hardship is placed on the subdivider. Such variance shall not be
granted if it would be detrimental to the public good or impair the intent and
purpose of this chapter. The conditions of any variance authorized shall be
stated in writing in the minutes of the planning and zoning commission with the
justifications set forth. (1987 Code § 16.48.020)
11-12-3: FILING FEE:
A filing fee for review and processing of the preliminary and final plat or PUD
shall be paid to the town clerk in accordance with the latest fee schedule
established by resolution of the town council. The fee is in addition to the
county filing fee and shall cover the cost of checking the plats, drawings and
inspection. (1987 Code § 16.48.030)
11-12-4: REPEALED:
(Repealed by Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
11-12-5: AMENDMENT:
From time to time, the town council may amend this title. Any such amendment
shall not be made or become effective unless the same has been either proposed
by or submitted to the planning and zoning commission for approval, disapproval
or recommendations. If such amendment is disapproved by the planning and zoning
commission within thirty (30) days after submission, the amendment, to become
effective, must receive the favorable vote of not less than a majority of the
entire membership of the town council. Before finally adopting any such
amendment, the town council shall hold a public hearing thereon, and at least
thirty (30) days notice of the time and place of the hearing shall be given by
at least one publication in a newspaper of general circulation in Uinta County.
(1987 Code § 16.48.050)
CHAPTER 13
ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
11-13-1: Enforcement Authority
11-13-2: Unapproved Subdivisions
11-13-3: Penalty
11-13-1: ENFORCEMENT AUTHORITY:
Town law enforcement officers, the town attorney and other duly authorized
enforcement officials are empowered to enforce the provisions of this title.
(1987 Code § 16.52.010)
11-13-2: UNAPPROVED SUBDIVISIONS:
   A.   Sale Or Transfer Of Lots: Any owner or agent of an owner who sells,
transfers, agrees to sell or negotiates to sell land in an unapproved
subdivision shall be punished according to the provisions set forth in section
1-4-1 of this code for each lot so sold, transferred or agreed or negotiated to
be sold.
   B.   Metes And Bounds Description: Description of the lots in the unapproved
subdivision by metes and bounds in the transfer shall not exempt the owner from
being punished.
   C.   Injunction: The town may enjoin any transfer or sale of such land by
injunction and may recover the penalty in a civil action in a court of
competent jurisdiction. (1987 Code § 16.52.020)
11-13-3: PENALTY:
Unless specifically set out in this title, any violation of this title
constitutes a class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. A violation shall not be construed to include a
subdivision in existence before January 1, 1977. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
TITLE 12
ZONING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL PROVISIONS
SECTION:
12-1-1: Purpose
12-1-2: Interpretation
12-1-1: PURPOSE:
This title is adopted to promote the public health, safety, comfort, morals and
general welfare of the town by:
   A.   Encouraging and facilitating orderly growth and development in
accordance with standards deemed beneficial to the interest and general welfare
of the people.
   B.   Establishing population densities to reduce congestion and to secure
economy in the cost of providing water supply and sewage systems, streets and
highways, fire and police protection, schools, parks and recreation facilities.
   C.   Securing safety from fire, floods and other dangers.
   D.   Preventing overcrowding of land or buildings, avoiding undue
concentrations of population, and fostering industry and agriculture in
appropriate locations.
   E.   Conserving the value of buildings and enhancing the value of land
throughout the town. (1987 Code § 17.04.010)
12-1-2: INTERPRETATION:
The provisions of this title shall be held to be minimum requirements. Where
this title imposes a greater restriction than is imposed by the state or by
other provisions, the provisions of this title shall prevail. (1987 Code §
17.04.020)
CHAPTER 2
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
12-2-1: General Definitions
12-2-1: GENERAL DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this title, certain words, terms and phrases are defined to
have the same meaning as set forth in this chapter:
ACCESSORY USE OR BUILDING: A use or building customarily incidental to, and
located on the same lot occupied by, the main use or building. "Accessory
building" may include a private garage, garden shed or barn, a private
playhouse, private greenhouse, and a swimming pool in accordance with the
provisions of this title.
APARTMENT: A room or suite of two (2) or more rooms in a multiple dwelling,
occupied or suitable for occupancy as a residence of one family. Kitchens and
baths shall not be considered rooms for the purpose of this definition.
APARTMENT HOUSE: A building or portion thereof designed or used for three (3)
or more dwelling units and six (6) or more guestrooms or suites of rooms.
BASEMENT: A space wholly or partly underground and having more than one-half
(1/2) of its height, measuring from its floor to its ceiling, below the average
adjoining grade; if the finished floor level directly above a basement is more
than six feet (6') above grade at any point, such basement shall be considered
a story.
BUILDING: A structure designed, built or occupied as a shelter or roofed
enclosure for persons, animals or property, including tents, lunch wagons,
dining cars, camp cars, mobile homes, and other roofed structures on wheels or
other supports used for residential, business, mercantile, storage, commercial,
industrial, institutional, assembly, educational, or recreational purposes. For
the purposes of this definition, "roof" includes an awning or other similar
covering, whether or not permanent in nature.
BUILDING HEIGHT: The vertical distance measured from the average level of the
highest and lowest point of that portion of the lot covered by the building to
the highest point of the building.
BUILDING PERMIT: A written warrant or license granting a landowner approval,
for proposed construction, reconstruction or alteration of buildings or
structures.
CAMPER UNITS: All dependent or independent recreational trailers not otherwise
defined as a "mobile home" in this title, and truck campers, tent trailers,
tents, etc.
CAMPGROUND: An area of land used to temporarily accommodate two (2) or more
camping parties or camping units.
CHURCH: A permanently located building commonly used for religious worship
fully enclosed with walls (including windows and doors) and having a roof
(canvas and fabric excluded) and conforming to applicable legal requirements
affecting design and construction.
CONDITIONAL USE PERMIT: A permit which may permit those uses as described in
this title under special conditions granted after review by the planning and
zoning commission. Those conditions attached to the use must have a reasonable
and valid relationship to the use and compatibility of surrounding property.
CORNER LOT: A lot located at the junction of two (2) intersecting streets.
Frontage and side setbacks of primary and accessory buildings closest to the
street are to be uniform for both frontage streets.
CROP AND GARDEN USES: Land which shall be used for agriculture, horticulture,
grazing or cropland within the town limits.
DAYCARE CENTER: A facility established to provide care for children from
families during normal working hours of the day to enable the parent or parents
to pursue employment.
DEPENDENT TRAVEL TRAILER OR TRUCK CAMPER: A travel trailer, converted bus, or
truck camper which does not have a flush toilet, bath or shower.
DRIVEWAY: An accessory to a required off street parking facility, which shall
be open and unencumbered to a height of not less than eight feet (8'). It shall
be safe and usable.
DUPLEX: A building designed to contain two (2) separate residences without
common areas with separate and individual entrances and exits.
EDUCATIONAL INSTITUTIONS:
   A.   Includes: Public, parochial and other nonprofit institutions conducting
regular academic instruction at kindergarten, elementary, secondary and
collegiate levels and including graduate schools, universities and nonprofit
research institutions. Such institutions must either:
      1.   Offer general academic instruction equivalent to the standards
prescribed by the state board of education; or
      2.   Confer degrees such as college or university graduate or
undergraduate standing; or
      3.   Conduct research.
   B.   Does not include: Schools, academies or institutes, incorporated or
otherwise, which operate for a profit, nor does it include commercial or trade
schools.
FENCE: Any device forming a physical barrier between two (2) areas. This
includes wire mesh, steel mesh, chainlink, louver, stake, masonry, and lumber
and other similar materials. A fence is considered a structure.
FLOOR AREA: The total horizontal living area of a building, measured on the
outside walls of each story.
FRONT YARD: An open, unoccupied space on the same lot with a building situated
between the nearest roofed portion of the building and the front lot line of
the lot and extending from side lot line to side lot line.
FRONT YARD SETBACK LINE: The line which defines the depth of the required front
yard. The setback line is parallel with the sidewalk line which is the furthest
distance from the street or, when established by the master plan of streets and
highways, with the highway right of way line, or by the provisions of this
title, removed therefrom by the perpendicular distance prescribed for the front
yard in the zone.
FRONTAGE: The narrowest dimension of the lot which abuts on a dedicated street
or highway right of way line. Frontage is expressed in linear feet and is
measured along the right of way line. Where a future street or highway right of
way line has been established on the general or master plan or other official
plan, frontage shall be measured along that line.
GAMING: Risking any property for gain contingent in whole or in part upon lot,
chance, the operation of a gaming device, or the happening or outcome of an
event, including a sporting event, over which the person taking the risk has no
control.
GAMING DEVICE: Any device, machine, paraphernalia or equipment used in the act
of gaming.
GAMING ESTABLISHMENT: Any building, room, enclosure, vehicle, vessel or other
place, whether open or enclosed, used or intended to be used for gambling
having one or more gaming devices.
HEIGHT OF A STRUCTURE: The vertical distance derived from the average finished
grade at the foundation corners of the building or structure, to the highest
point of the building or structure, excluding a chimney or other similar
structures.
HOME OCCUPATION OR SMALL HOME BUSINESS: Limited industry, light manufacturing,
or selling of goods or services which may be conducted from a family residence
or out of buildings occupying the same general area or premises as a family
residence.
HOME PROFESSIONAL OFFICE: Any business or home occupation in which not more
than two (2) persons are employed who are not members of the family, and in
which the office shall be in the main building and shall not occupy more than
the equivalent of one-half (1/2) of the floor area of the building. The home
professional office of a physician shall not include a biological or other
medical testing laboratory. The home in which such home professional office is
located shall maintain a residential character and quality.
HOSPITAL: A building used for the diagnosis, treatment or other care of human
ailments, unless otherwise specified. "Hospital" includes a sanitarium,
sanatorium, clinic, convalescent home, nursing home, rest home or other
building with an equivalent appellation. A hospital shall not include care and
treatment of mental patients, liquor or drug addicts, except incidentally.
IMPROVED LOT: A lot that is connected to a public water system, sewer system
or, in the absence of such a system, other sanitary methods which meet with the
approval of the planning and zoning commission.
INDUSTRIAL PARK: A group of nonnuisance industrial plants on a single parcel of
land, or on separate parcels contiguously arranged so as to form a planned
development of industrial sites, building or buildings.
INDUSTRY: The manufacture, fabrication, processing, reduction or destruction of
any article, substance or commodity, or any other treatment thereof in such a
manner as to change the form, character or appearance thereof, and including
storage elevators, truck storage yards, warehouses, wholesale storage and other
similar types of enterprise.
LOT AREA: The total horizontal area included within lot lines.
LOT WIDTH: The mean dimension measured at substantially right angles to the
depth of the lot.
MAIN BUILDING: A building in which is conducted a principal use of the lot or
parcel of land upon which it is situated. Where a permissible use involves more
than one building designed or used for a primary purpose, each such building on
the building site shall be defined as a main building.
MANUFACTURED HOME: See definition of Mobile Home.
MINERAL EXPLORATION: The search for coal, minerals or ore by:
   A.   Geological surveys;
   B.   Geophysical prospecting;
   C.   Bore holes and trial pits; and
   D.   Surface or underground headings, drifts or tunnels.
MINING: The process of obtaining useful minerals from the earth's crust,
including both underground excavations and surface workings.
MOBILE HOME: A transportable structure built on a chassis and designed to be
used with or without a permanent foundation as a dwelling unit when connected
to public utility facilities and which is built in a factory in accordance with
specifications set forth by the U.S. department of housing and urban
development. Motorized homes, trailers or other camping or recreational
vehicles are not considered mobile homes.
MOBILE HOME PARK: An area specifically designed for and occupied by six (6) or
more mobile homes. A development consisting of individual ownership of
individual lots is not considered to be a mobile home park. Land that has a
mobile home situated upon it and that is owned by the resident of that mobile
home is not considered to be a mobile home park.
MODULAR HOME: A transportable structure designed to be used with a permanent
foundation to be used for residential, commercial, educational or industrial
purposes when connected to public utility facilities and which is built in a
factory in accordance with all requirements of the uniform building code.
MOTEL: A building containing more than seventy five percent (75%) of the
lodging rooms are for rent to transient persons for a continuous period of less
than thirty (30) days.
MULTIPLE DWELLING: A building arranged, intended or designed to be occupied by
three (3) or more families living independently of each other as separate
housekeeping units.
NATIONAL BUILDING CODE: A national code prescribing regulations governing the
construction, alteration and demolition of buildings and structures (uniform
building code).
NONCONFORMING STRUCTURE: A structure lawfully existing as of the effective date
hereof or any amendment hereto affecting such structure, which does not conform
to the building regulations of this title for the district in which it is
situated, irrespective of the use to which such structure is put.
NONCONFORMING USE: Any use of a building, structure, lot or land, or part
thereof, lawfully existing at the effective date hereof or any amendment hereto
affecting such use, which does not conform to the use regulations of this title
for the district in which it is situated.
OPEN SPACE: Unoccupied space within the incorporated limits set aside for
recreational use.
PARKING SPACE: One off street space available for parking of one motor vehicle
and having an area of not less than two hundred (200) square feet, exclusive of
passageways and driveways, giving access thereto and having direct access to a
street or alley.
PLANNED UNIT DEVELOPMENT: A land area which:
   A.   Consists of two (2) or more principal structures or uses on a single
parcel of land; and
   B.   Is designed and organized to be capable of satisfactory use and
operation as a separate neighborhood or community unit without necessarily
having the participation of other building sites or other common property; the
ownership of the common property may be either public or private.
PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION: The planning commission and/or planning and
zoning commission as appointed by the governing body or the town council.
PRIVATE GARAGE: A detached accessory building or portion of a main building on
the same lot as a dwelling, used for housing vehicles of the occupants of the
dwelling, having a roof and enclosed on not less than four (4) sides. Any such
structure enclosed on three (3) sides or less shall be considered a carport.
PUBLIC FACILITIES AND UTILITIES: Those facilities and utilities necessary to
serve the people with electricity, water, sewage treatment, and other necessary
facilities for which a franchise is granted by the town.
PUBLIC GARAGE: Any premises used exclusively for the storage of vehicles.
PUBLIC NOTICE: Notice of the time and place of a hearing, meeting or proceeding
printed in the official newspaper of the town as required by law.
PUBLIC PARKING AREA: An open area, other than a street, used for parking or
automotive vehicles which is open to the public at large.
REAR YARD: A space on the same lot with a building situated between the nearest
roofed portion of the building and the rear lot line of the lot, and extending
from side lot line to side lot line.
RESIDENCE: A building used, designed or intended to be used as a home or
dwelling.
RESTAURANT: A place which is used for the serving of meals to guests for
compensation and which has suitable kitchen facilities connected therewith,
containing conveniences for cooking an assortment of food which may be required
for ordinary meals. "Meals" means the usual assortment of foods commonly
ordered at various times of the day. The service of such foods and victuals
only as sandwiches or salads does not constitute a "restaurant".
ROOM: An unsubdivided portion of the interior of a building, excluding
bathrooms, closets, hallways, kitchens and service porches.
SANITARY LANDFILL: Land specified by the town council for disposal of garbage,
trash, refuse or waste material of any kind.
SERVICE STATION: A business which services motor vehicles, including tube and
tire repairs, battery charging, storage of merchandise and supplies related to
the servicing of motor vehicles, sale of gasoline and lubricants, automobile
washing (not including mechanical car wash), grease racks, and automobile
repairs.
SIDE YARD: An open, unoccupied space on the same lot with a building situated
between the nearest roofed portion of the building or of any accessory building
and the side lot line of the lot.
SINGLE-FAMILY DWELLING: An individual home designed and used exclusively for
residential occupancy by one family on a lot.
SINGLEWIDE MOBILE HOME: A mobile home that comes as a single section or is less
than twenty feet (20') wide.
SPECIAL USE PERMIT: A use specified in one or more districts, for which the
planning and zoning commission may grant a permit, pursuant to the provisions
of this title (see definition of Conditional Use Permit).
STREET: Any road, highway, avenue, street, parkway, lane or other way, public
or private, set aside and commonly used by the public for street purposes, and
shown upon the town map or upon a filed plat.
STRUCTURE 1 : Anything constructed or built over the height of three feet (3'),
any edifice, building or fence of any kind, or any piece of work artificially
built up or composed of parts joined together in some definite manner, which
requires location on the ground or is attached to something having a location
on the ground, excepting outdoor areas such as uncovered patios, paved areas,
walks, tennis courts, and similar recreation areas.
TWO-FAMILY DWELLING: A building designed and used exclusively for residential
occupancy by two (2) families, including, but not limited to, duplexes.
VARIANCE: A modification of the regulations of this title granted on grounds of
impractical difficulties or unnecessary hardship, not self-imposed, pursuant to
the provisions of this title and the laws of the state.
WALL: Any structure or device forming a physical barrier which is so
constructed that fifty percent (50%) or more of the vertical surface is closed
and prevents the passage of light, air and vision through the surface in a
horizontal plane. This includes concrete, concrete block, wood or other
materials that are solids and are so assembled as to form a solid barrier.
YARD: Any open space, other than a court, on the same lot with a building or
dwelling group, which space is generally open from the ground to the sky. (1987
Code §§ 17.08.010 - 17.08.670; amd. Ord. 6-94, 10-20-1994; Ord. 7-95, 7-20-
1995; Ord. 8-98, 8-20-1998; Ord. 04-00, 4-20-2000; Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff.
1-1-2001; 2004 Code; Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-2006; Ord. 2007-7, 4-5-2007; Ord. 2008-
8, 4-3-2008; Ord. 2015-06, 12-3-2015)
 
Notes
1 1. See section
  9-1-1 of this code for building permit requirements for all structures.
CHAPTER 3
MAP
SECTION:
12-3-1: Adoption
12-3-2: Delineation Of Districts
12-3-3: Uncertainty Of District Boundaries
12-3-1: ADOPTION:
The boundaries of each district or zone are established as shown on the
official zoning map of the town, which accompanies the ordinance codified in
this title and is declared a part of this title. (1987 Code § 17.12.010)
12-3-2: DELINEATION OF DISTRICTS:
The zones established pursuant to this title shall be delineated on the zoning
map of the town. (1987 Code § 17.12.020)
12-3-3: UNCERTAINTY OF DISTRICT BOUNDARIES:
Where uncertainty exists as to the boundaries of any district as shown on any
zoning map or part thereof, the following rules shall apply:
   A.   Follow Street, Alley Or Lot Lines: Where such boundaries are indicated
as approximately following street lines, alley lines, or lot lines, such lines
shall be construed to be such boundaries.
   B.   Unsubdivided Property; Zone Divides Lot: In the case of unsubdivided
property and where a zone boundary divides a lot, the locations of such
boundaries, unless the same are indicated by dimensions, shall be determined by
the use of a scale appearing on such zoning map.
   C.   Vacation Of Street Or Alley: Where a public street or alley is
officially vacated, the zoning regulations applicable to abutting property on
each side of the centerline shall apply up to the centerline of such vacated
street or alley on each respective side thereof.
   D.   Unclassified Streets Or Alleys: Areas of dedicated streets or alleys
other than those designated on the zoning map as being classified in one of the
districts provided in this title shall be deemed unclassified. (1987 Code §
17.12.030)
CHAPTER 4
ZONING DISTRICTS
ARTICLE A. R-0 ZONE
SECTION:
12-4A-1: Purpose
12-4A-2: Permitted Uses
12-4A-3: Conditional Uses
12-4A-4: Minimum Floor Area, Garages And Accessory Buildings
12-4A-5: Minimum Lot Size
12-4A-6: Height Limits
12-4A-7: Setbacks
12-4A-8: Fences And Walls
12-4A-9: Off Street Parking, Drives And Walks
12-4A-10: Signs
12-4A-11: Utilities
12-4A-12: Animals
12-4A-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a low density residential area with lots having a
minimum area of one-half (1/2) acre, with no more than one residential dwelling
per lot. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
0 zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or
enlarged, or land used except for the following purposes:
Public parks, playgrounds, and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings (only 1 per lot). (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the R-0 zone subject to the conditional use
permits are as follows: (Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
Churches.
Golf courses. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-4: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA, GARAGES AND ACCESSORY BUILDINGS:
   A.   Minimum Floor Area: The ground floor of single-story homes in the R-
0 zone, exclusive of porches, decks, and garages, shall be no less than two
thousand (2,000) square feet, and no less than one thousand six hundred (1,600)
square feet for two-story dwellings. The second floor of a two-story dwelling
shall be at least one-half (1/2) the square footage of the first floor. (Ord.
05-2001, 12-20-2001)
   B.   Accessory Buildings; Garages: Garages may be attached or detached,
however a detached garage shall be considered an accessory building. All
accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3'). (Ord. 2014-01, 4-
3-2014)
   C.   Exterior: All structures shall have a minimum of one-third (1/3) of the
exterior siding material composed of brick, stone, or stucco. No metal or
aluminum siding is permitted unless it is of residential grade and design.
   D.   Greenhouses: Greenhouse structures must be premanufactured glass units
and may be attached to either the dwelling or accessory building, however, a
detached greenhouse shall be considered an accessory building. (Ord. 05-2001,
12-20-2001)
12-4A-5: MINIMUM LOT SIZE:
The minimum lot area in the R-0 zone shall be one-half (1/2) acre and the lot
dimensions shall be sufficient to accommodate the minimum setback and yard
requirements set forth in section
12-4A-7 of this article. The building site for any use in the R-0 zone shall be
on an improved lot and connected to town water and sewer systems. (Ord. 05-
2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-6: HEIGHT LIMITS:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. The dwelling structure,
including garage, shall be site built. Modular, mobile, and off site built
structures, including outbuildings, are prohibited. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4A-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-0 zone are as follows: There shall be a minimum
setback of thirty feet (30') along the front of each lot, and twenty feet (20')
along the sides of each lot, and twenty feet (20') along the rear of each lot.
Except for drives and walks, there shall be no structures or buildings located
within the setbacks. Any accessory building shall be located on the one-half
(1/2) of the property located farthest from the street, or if on a corner lot,
the accessory building must be on the farthest back one-fourth (1/4) of the
property. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4A-9: OFF STREET PARKING, DRIVES AND WALKS:
   A.   Off Street Parking: Off street parking requirements for the R-0 zone
shall be those set forth in chapter 8 of this title.
   B.   Drives And Walks: Drives and walks shall be required to all garages,
dwelling entries, and accessory buildings. All drives and walks shall be
concrete, asphalt, stone, or brick. No dirt or graveled drives are permitted.
(Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-10: SIGNS:
Sign requirements for the R-0 zone shall be those set forth in chapter 9 of
this title. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-11: UTILITIES:
All utility lines including, but not limited to, electrical, telephone, cable
television, and telecommunications lines and cables shall be underground.
Except for sewer and water valves, meters, and access covers, all junction,
switching, and access boxes shall be located on the rear one-half (1/2) of each
lot where reasonably possible. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
12-4A-12: ANIMALS:
Outdoor animals shall be limited to one animal per one-half (1/2) acre and
shall be limited to cats and dogs. No animal shall exceed thirty six inches
(36") in height at the shoulder. Animal dwellings shall be maintained, fenced,
and inconspicuous to neighbors. Indoor animals may be maintained at the owner's
discretion. (Ord. 05-2001, 12-20-2001)
ARTICLE B. R-1 ZONE
SECTION:
12-4B-1: Purpose
12-4B-2: Permitted Uses
12-4B-3: Conditional Uses
12-4B-4: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4B-5: Minimum Floor Area
12-4B-6: Lot Requirements
12-4B-7: Height Limit
12-4B-8: Setbacks
12-4B-9: Fences And Walls
12-4B-10: Off Street Parking
12-4B-11: Signs
12-4B-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a low density residential area with lots having a
minimum area of seven thousand (7,000) square feet with not more than one
dwelling on one lot. (1987 Code § 17.16.010)
12-4B-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
1 zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Educational institutions.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings (only 1 per lot). (1987 Code § 17.16.020)
12-4B-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the R-1 zone subject to conditional use permits
are as follows: (Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
Churches.
Daycare centers.
Golf courses.
Planned unit developments, provided such development complies with article L of
this chapter.
Rest and convalescent homes. (1987 Code § 17.16.030)
12-4B-4: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to use a lot
for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a building permit
for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All applicants for
building permits for the R-1 zone must certify, under oath, that the building,
structure or improvement will conform to the town building code as adopted. An
improvement which does not comply with the town adopted building code will not
be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
R-1 zone must be placed on, and permanently attached to, a permanent foundation
on which all of the weight or load is borne primarily by the perimeter
foundation and secondarily by permanent interior foundation support, but not on
jacks or other nonfoundation structure. All foundations must meet town adopted
building code standards.
   C.   New Buildings: Any building moved into the R-1 zone, to be placed on
any lot or space, and to be used with a permanent foundation, shall be new.
Such building may not have been set up for anticipated use, with or without a
foundation, before. (Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-2006)
   D.   Homes Permitted: Only stick built homes or component homes or modular
homes are permitted in the R-1 zone. Component and modular homes are permitted
in an R-1 zone if the home is structurally sound and the joists of that home
are not intended to be supported, in whole or in part, by a metal joist frame,
and the entire structure is intended to be primarily supported by a permanent
foundation under the exterior perimeter of the home. (Ord. 2008-1, 3-20-2008)
12-4B-5: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
The ground floor area of the main structure in the R-1 zone, exclusive of one-
story open porches and garages, shall not be less than one thousand two hundred
(1,200) square feet for one dwelling, nor less than one thousand (1,000) square
feet for a dwelling of more than one story. (Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-2006)
12-4B-6: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-1 zone shall be seven thousand
(7,000) square feet.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot width in the R-1 zone is seventy feet
(70') for interior lots. Corner lots must be large enough to accommodate
setback and side yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the R-1 zone shall be
on an improved lot. (1987 Code § 17.16.050)
12-4B-7: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4B-8: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-1 zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-1 zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no
structures located in a required front yard or in a required side yard abutting
a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted to dismantle, repair or keep
any inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor side yard abutting a street or
driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than twelve feet (12') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10'). (1987 Code § 17.16.070)
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted
only to the extent necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted
in this zone. Accessory buildings are not used for residential purposes. All
accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3').
         ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET

      1.    No accessory building may encroach into the front yard beyond the

Yard intrusions as provided in section
12-7-5 of this title shall not be considered to apply to accessory buildings of
two hundred (200) square feet or less and portable in nature in residential
zones. (Ord. 2014-01, 4-3-2014)
12-4B-9: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4B-10: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the R-1 zone, see chapter 8 of this
title. (1987 Code § 17.16.090)
12-4B-11: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the R-1 zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987 Code
§ 17.16.100)
ARTICLE C. R-1-A ZONE
SECTION:
12-4C-1: Purpose
12-4C-2: Permitted Uses
12-4C-3: Conditional Uses
12-4C-4: Prohibited Uses

12-4C-6: Minimum Floor Area
12-4C-7: Lot Requirements

12-4C-14: Sanitation
12-4C-15: Reserved
12-4C-16: Qualifications For Zone
12-4C-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this zone is to provide low density, residential development
where animals may be kept for pleasure. Because the main purpose of the zoning
is residential development, no animals shall be kept on any lot unless the
single-family dwelling is built and occupied. (1987 Code § 17.18.010)
12-4C-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-1-
A Zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings.
Animals for pleasure.
Gardens for personal use.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings (only 1 per lot). (1987 Code § 17.18.020)
12-4C-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the R-1-A Zone subject to conditional use
permits are as follows:
Churches.
Golf courses and playing fields.
Hospitals and clinics.
Planned unit developments.
Public and private elementary and secondary schools.
Public facilities. (1987 Code § 17.18.030; amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
12-4C-4: PROHIBITED USES:
Uses which are not permitted in the R-1-A Zone are as follows:
Commercial feedlots.
Storage of commercial goods or materials. (1987 Code § 17.18.040)
12-4C-5: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to use a lot
for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a building permit
for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All applicants for
building permits for the R-1-A Zone must certify, under oath, that the
building, structure or improvement will conform to the Building Code as
adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the Building Code will not
be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
R-1-A zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks or in
the center of the structure. All foundations must meet building code standards.
(Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4C-6: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
The ground floor area of the main structure in the R-1-A zone, exclusive of
one-story open porches and garages shall not be less than one thousand two
hundred (1,200) square feet nor less than one thousand (1,000) square feet for
a dwelling of more than one story. (1987 Code § 17.18.050)
12-4C-7: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Minimum Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-1-A zone shall be
twenty one thousand five hundred (21,500) square feet.
   B.   Minimum Lot Width: The minimum lot width in the R-1-A zone shall be one
hundred feet (100') for interior lots. Corner lots must be at least one hundred
feet (100') wide or larger to accommodate setback and side yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: All lots shall be improved lots, and shall be connected
to town water and sewer systems. Animal wastes (excretions) will not be allowed
in the town sewer system. (1987 Code § 17.18.060)
12-4C-8: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4C-9: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-1-A zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-1-A zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty five feet (25') nor more than fifty feet (50'). Except for drives
and walks, there shall be no structures located in a required front yard or in
a required side yard abutting a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted
to dismantle, repair or keep any inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor
side yard abutting a street or driveway. No animals as defined in section
12-4C-13 of this article shall be allowed or kept in the required front yard or
in required side yard abutting a street.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than fifteen feet (15') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard. Animals shall not be kept in a required side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10'). (1987 Code § 17.18.080)
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted
only to the extent necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted
in this zone. Accessory buildings are not used for residential purposes. All
accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3').
      ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET
Portable Accessory Buildings (Easily Moved By Sliding)
Building Square Feet Front Side Yard Side Yard Corner Lot Rear Yard
Portable Accessory Buildings (Easily Moved By Sliding)
Building Square Feet Front Side Yard Side Yard Corner Lot Rear Yard

121 - 250            251   5         15                   5
Permanent Accessory Buildings
With Foundation Or Concrete Floor
Building Square Feet Front Side Yard Side Yard Corner Lot Rear Yard
0 or more            251   10        15                   10
 
Note:
      1.    No accessory building may encroach into the front yard beyond the
main structure.
   (Ord. 2014-01, 4-3-2014)
   C.   Structures To House Animals: Structures intended to house or protect
animals may be considered additional to the allowed accessory buildings. They
will, however, be subject to the height and setback requirements for accessory
buildings established in this article. Such structures shall be constructed of
a similar material and finished to be aesthetically similar to the main
dwelling. Any exceptions shall be approved by the planning and zoning
commission. The size of buildings to house or protect animals shall not exceed
three hundred (300) square feet per allowed animal unit as defined herein.
(1987 Code § 17.18.080)
12-4C-10: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4C-11: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the R-1-A zone, see chapter 8 of this
title. (1987 Code § 17.18.100)
12-4C-12: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the R-1-A zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987
Code § 17.18.110)
12-4C-13: KEEPING OF DOMESTIC ANIMALS:
The keeping and maintenance of animals and fowl permitted in the R-1-A zone
shall be limited to the following animal units:
   A.   Unit 1; Horse, Mule, Pony Or Cattle: There shall be no more than one
such animal per twenty one thousand five hundred (21,500) square feet of land;
or
   B.   Unit 2; Llamas, Sheep And Goats: There shall be no more than two (2)
animals per twenty one thousand five hundred (21,500) square feet of land; or
   C.   Unit 3; Poultry, Rabbits, Chinchillas: There shall be no more than ten
(10) such animals per twenty one thousand five hundred (21,500) square feet of
land. These poultry, rabbits or chinchillas shall be penned and shall not be
allowed to run free.
   D.   Types Of Animals Restricted: Any animals not specifically mentioned in
subsection A, B or C of this section shall be deemed excluded. Any exceptions
shall be specifically approved by the planning and zoning commission. The
keeping of swine is prohibited.
   E.   Combinations And Tradeoffs: In lieu of one llama, sheep or goat in
animal unit 2 of subsection B of this section, five (5) animals from unit 3 of
subsection C of this section may be kept per twenty one thousand five hundred
(21,500) square feet of land.
   F.   Wild Animals: Nothing in this chapter shall be construed as authorizing
the keeping of wild animals or animals capable of inflicting harm or
endangering the health and safety of any person or property.
   G.   Distance From Main Structure: Animals as specified in this section
shall not be kept closer than ten feet (10') from the main structure. (1987
Code § 17.18.120)
12-4C-14: SANITATION:
   A.   Drainage: Lots shall be graded and adequately drained to alleviate any
potential health or safety problem.
   B.   Insect And Rodent Control: In order to provide adequate insect and
rodent control, lots shall be kept free of rubbish and maintained in sanitary
condition at all times. All harborage for insects and rodents shall be
eliminated and prevented. Flies and mosquitoes shall be controlled.
   C.   Manure; Animal Refuse: Manure and other animal refuse shall not be
allowed to accumulate nor will such material be stockpiled or accumulated for
future use.
   D.   Nuisance: Animals shall be kept in such a manner as not to constitute a
nuisance (title 4, chapter 1 of this Code) with respect to neighboring
properties. (1987 Code § 17.18.130)
12-4C-15: RESERVED:
(Ord. 2017-08, 5-4-2017)
12-4C-16: QUALIFICATIONS FOR ZONE:
In order for property to be considered for R-1-A zoning, it must meet the
following criteria:
   A.   Must be currently zoned A, L-I, H-I or adjacent property outside the
incorporated limits of the Town; and
   B.   Must have adjacent properties on two (2) sides currently zoned A, L-I,
H-I or property outside the incorporated limits of the Town; and
   C.   Must not have more than three (3) developed residential properties
(with residences) within sixty feet (60') from the property (lot) boundary in
any direction. (1987 Code § 17.18.140)
ARTICLE D. R-A ZONE
SECTION:

12-4D-2: Permitted Uses

12-4D-16: Variance
12-4D-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this zone is to provide low density, residential development
where a higher density of animals may be kept for pleasure. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-
1999)
12-4D-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
A zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings.
Animals for pleasure.
Gardens for personal use.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings (only 1 per lot). (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the R-A zone subject to conditional use permits
are as follows:
Churches.
Golf courses and playing fields.
Hospitals and clinics.
Planned unit developments.
Public and private elementary and secondary schools.
Public facilities. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999; amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
12-4D-4: PROHIBITED USES:
Uses which are not permitted in the R-A zone are as follows:
Commercial feedlots.
Storage of commercial goods or materials. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-5: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Uniform Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to
use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the R-A zone must certify, under oath, that
the building, structure or improvement will conform to the uniform building
code, as adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the uniform
building code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
R-A zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks or in
the center of the structure. All foundations must meet uniform building code
standards. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4D-6: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
The ground area of the main structure in the R-A zone, exclusive of one-story
open porches and garages, shall not be less than one thousand two hundred
(1,200) square feet nor less than one thousand (1,000) square feet for a
dwelling of more than one story. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-7: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Minimum Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-A zone shall be forty
three thousand five hundred (43,500) square feet.
   B.   Minimum Lot Width: The minimum lot width in the R-A zone shall be one
hundred feet (100') for interior lots. Corner lots must be at least one hundred
twenty feet (120') wide or larger to accommodate setback and side yard
requirements.
   C.   Building Site: All lots shall be improved lots, and shall be connected
to town water and sewer systems. Animal wastes (excretions) will not be allowed
in the town sewer system. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-8: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4D-9: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-A zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-A zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty five feet (25'), nor more than fifty feet (50'). Except for drives
and walks, there shall be no structures located in a required front yard or in
a required side yard abutting a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted
to dismantle, repair or keep any inoperative vehicles in the front yard nor
side yard abutting a street or driveway. No "animals" as defined in section
12-4D-13 of this article shall be allowed or kept in the required front yard or
in a required side yard abutting a street.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than fifteen feet (15') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard. Animals shall not be kept in the side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10'). (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
   B.   Accessory Buildings:
      1.   Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted only to the extent
necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted in this zone.
Accessory buildings are not used for residential purposes. All accessory
buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be separated from the
main building by at least three feet (3').
      ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET
 
Building Square Feet Front Side Yard Side Yard Corner Lot Rear Yard
0 - 120              251   3         5                    3
121 - 250            251   5         10                   5
251 or more2         251   10        15                   10
 
   Notes:
      1.   No accessory building may encroach into the front yard beyond the
main structure.
      2.   Allowed only on permanent accessory buildings with foundation or
concrete floor.
   C.   Structure To House Animals: Structures intended to house or protect
animals may be considered additional to the allowed accessory buildings. They
will, however, be subject to the height and setback requirements for accessory
buildings established in this article. Such structures shall be constructed of
a similar material and shall be finished to be aesthetically similar to the
main dwelling. Any exceptions shall be approved by the planning and zoning
commission. (Ord. 2014-01, 4-3-2014)
12-4D-10: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4D-11: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the R-A zone, see chapter 8 of this
title. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-12: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the R-A zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (Ord. 5-99,
11-18-1999)
12-4D-13: KEEPING OF DOMESTIC ANIMALS:
The keeping and maintenance of animals and fowl permitted in the R-A zone shall
be limited to the following animal units:
   A.   Unit 1; Horse, Mule, Pony Or Cattle: There shall be no more than one
such animal per ten thousand (10,000) square feet of land; or
   B.   Unit 2; Llamas, Sheep And Goats: There shall be no more than two (2)
animals per ten thousand (10,000) square feet of land; or
   C.   Unit 3; Poultry, Rabbits, Chinchillas: There shall be no more than ten
(10) such animals per ten thousand (10,000) square feet of land. These poultry,
rabbits or chinchillas shall be penned and shall not be allowed to run free.
   D.   Types Of Animals Restricted: Any animals not specifically mentioned in
subsection A, B or C of this section shall be deemed excluded. Any exceptions
shall be specifically approved by the planning and zoning commission. The
keeping of swine is allowed by special permit of the planning and zoning
commission only during a 4-H project season (approximately February through
August of any year). Each swine kept during such time shall be considered one
animal unit (1 swine per 10,000 square feet).
   E.   Combinations And Tradeoffs: In lieu of one llama, sheep or goat in
animal unit 2 of subsection B of this section, five (5) animals from unit 3 of
subsection C of this section may be kept per ten thousand (10,000) square feet
of land.
   F.   Wild Animals: Nothing herein shall be construed as authorizing the
keeping of wild animals or animals capable of inflicting harm or endangering
the health and safety of any person or property.
   G.   Distance From Main Structure: Animals specified in this section shall
not be kept closer than ten feet (10') from the main structure. (Ord. 5-99, 11-
18-1999)
12-4D-14: SANITATION:
   A.   Drainage: Lots shall be graded and adequately drained to alleviate any
potential health or safety problem.
   B.   Insect And Rodent Control: In order to provide adequate insect and
rodent control, lots shall be kept free of rubbish and maintained in a sanitary
condition at all times. All harborage for insects and rodents shall be
eliminated and prevented. Flies and mosquitos shall be controlled.
   C.   Manure; Animal Refuse: Manure and other animal refuse shall not be
allowed to accumulate nor will such material be stockpiled or accumulated for
future use.
   D.   Nuisance: Animals shall be kept in such a manner as not to constitute a
nuisance (title 4, chapter 1 of this code) with respect to neighboring
properties. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-15: QUALIFICATIONS FOR ZONE:
In order for property to be considered for R-A zoning it must meet the
following criteria:
   A.   The property must be currently zoned as A, L-I, H-I, or as adjacent
property outside the incorporated limits of the town; and
   B.   The property must have adjacent properties on at least two (2) sides
which are currently zoned as A, L-I, H-I, R-A, or as property outside the
incorporated limits of the town; and
   C.   The property must not have more than two (2) developed residential
properties (with residences) within one hundred feet (100') from the property
(lot) boundary in any direction. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-1999)
12-4D-16: VARIANCE:
Properties which do not qualify for the R-A zone, but which none the less wish
to be considered for the R-A zone, may petition the planning and zoning
commission for the zone designation. If the planning and zoning commission
determines that the petitioning property is currently surrounded by an existing
R-A zone and that there will be no detrimental effect to the area or the
health, safety and welfare of the inhabitants, the planning and zoning
commission may, at their discretion, grant the variance. (Ord. 5-99, 11-18-
1999)
ARTICLE E. R-2 ZONE
SECTION:
12-4E-1: Purpose
12-4E-2: Permitted Uses
12-4E-3: Conditional Uses
12-4E-4: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4E-5: Minimum Floor Area
12-4E-6: Lot Requirements
12-4E-7: Height Limit And Construction
12-4E-8: Setbacks
12-4E-9: Fences And Walls
12-4E-10: Off Street Parking
12-4E-11: Signs
12-4E-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a medium density residential area with lots having
minimum area of seven thousand (7,000) square feet with not more than one
dwelling on one lot. (1987 Code § 17.20.010)
12-4E-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
2 zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered, or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Educational institutions.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings.
Two-family dwellings. (1987 Code § 17.20.020)
12-4E-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the R-2 zone subject to conditional use permits
are as follows:
Apartment buildings, but no more than two (2) dwelling units per seven thousand
(7,000) square feet of lot area.
Churches.
Daycare centers.
Funeral homes.
Planned unit developments, provided such development complies with article L of
this chapter. (Ord. 2013-02, 9-19-2013)
12-4E-4: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to use a lot
for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a building permit
for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All applicants for
building permits for the R-2 zone must certify, under oath, that the building,
structure or improvement will conform to the town building code as adopted. An
improvement which does not comply with the town adopted building code will not
be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
R-2 zone must be placed on, and permanently attached to, a permanent foundation
on which all of the weight or load is borne primarily by the perimeter
foundation and secondarily by permanent interior foundation support, but not on
jacks or other nonfoundation structure. All foundations must meet town adopted
building code standards.
   C.   New Buildings: Any building moved into the R-2 zone, to be placed on
any lot or space, and to be used with a permanent foundation, shall be new.
Such building may not have been set up for anticipated use, with or without a
foundation, before.
   D.   Singlewide Manufactured Homes Prohibited: No singlewide manufactured
homes shall be allowed in the R-2 zone. (Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-2006)
12-4E-5: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
The ground floor area of the main structure in the R-2 zone, exclusive of one-
story open porches and garages shall not be less than one thousand two hundred
(1,200) square feet for one dwelling, nor less than one thousand (1,000) square
feet for a dwelling of more than one story. Multi-family units shall have a
minimum area of eight hundred (800) square feet per unit. (Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-
2006)
12-4E-6: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-2 zone shall be seven thousand
(7,000) square feet.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot width in the R-2 zone shall be sixty
feet (60') for interior lots. Corner lots must be large enough to accommodate
setback and side yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the R-2 zone shall be
on an improved lot. (1987 Code § 17.20.050)
12-4E-7: HEIGHT LIMIT AND CONSTRUCTION:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4E-8: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-2 zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-2 zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no
structures located in a required front yard or in a required side yard abutting
a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted to dismantle, repair or keep
any inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor side yard abutting a street or
driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than twelve feet (12') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth of not less than ten feet (10'). (1987 Code § 17.20.070)
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted
only to the extent necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted
in this zone. Accessory buildings are not used for residential purposes. All
accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3').
      ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET
Portable Accessory Buildings (Easily Moved By Sliding)

With Foundation Or Concrete Floor

Note:
      1.    No accessory building may encroach into the front yard beyond the
main structure.
Yard intrusions as provided in section
12-7-5 of this title shall not be considered to apply to accessory buildings of
two hundred (200) square feet or less and portable in nature in residential
zones. (Ord. 2014-01, 4-3-2014)
12-4E-9: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4E-10: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the R-2 zone, see chapter 8 of this
title. (1987 Code § 17.20.090)
12-4E-11: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the R-2 zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987 Code
§ 17.20.100)
ARTICLE F. R-3 ZONE
SECTION:
12-4F-1: Purpose
12-4F-2: Permitted Uses
12-4F-3: Conditional Uses
12-4F-4: Exemptions; Restrictions
12-4F-5: Minimum Floor Area
12-4F-6: Lot Requirements
12-4F-7: Height Limit And Construction
12-4F-8: Setbacks
12-4F-9: Fences And Walls
12-4F-10: Off Street Parking
12-4F-11: Signs
12-4F-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a high density residential area with lots having a
minimum area of six thousand (6,000) square feet with not more than one
dwelling on one lot. (1987 Code § 17.24.010)
12-4F-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
3 zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered, or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Educational institutions.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings.
Two-family dwellings. (1987 Code § 17.24.020)
12-4F-3: CONDITIONAL USES 1 :
Uses which may be permitted in the R-3 zone subject to conditional use permits
are as follows:
Churches.
Daycare centers.
Funeral homes.
Multi-family dwellings, but no more than four (4) dwelling units per six
thousand (6,000) square feet of lot area.
Planned unit developments, provided such development complies with article L of
this chapter. (1987 Code § 17.24.030; amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
 
Notes
1 1. See also subsection 12-4K-2B of this chapter.
12-4F-4: EXEMPTIONS; RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Exemptions: All residential buildings located within the R-3 zone shall
be exempt from the provisions of this code that requires uniform building code
requirements, except as may be required by the department of housing and urban
development.
   B.   Restrictions: All buildings which shall be built, placed or moved into
the R-3 zone after January 1, 2001, shall be certified by the manufacturer and
the owners that they are in compliance with all standards set forth by the
department of housing and urban development. No permit shall be issued by the
town of Lyman without said certifications. (Ord. 15-2004, 11-18-2004)
12-4F-5: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
Each dwelling unit in the R-3 zone shall have a minimum size of seven hundred
(700) square feet, exclusive of one-story open porches and garages. (1987 Code
§ 17.24.040)
12-4F-6: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-3 zone shall be six thousand
(6,000) square feet.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot width in the R-3 zone shall be sixty
feet (60') for interior lots. Corner lots must be large enough to accommodate
setback and yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the R-3 zone shall be
on an improved lot. (1987 Code § 17.24.050)
12-4F-7: HEIGHT LIMIT AND CONSTRUCTION:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than the height of the dwelling structure
actually on the lot. Building height is measured from the highest point on the
lot. If the dwelling structure is less than twenty feet (20') in height, any
accessory building designed primarily to be storage for a vehicle shall not be
required to be less than twenty feet (20') in height. The roof pitch of all
buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a four
inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4F-8: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-3 zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-3 zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no
structures located in a required front yard or in a required side yard abutting
a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted to dismantle, repair, or keep
any inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor side yard abutting a street or
driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot,
extending from the front yard, of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than twelve feet (12') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10'). (1987 Code § 17.24.070)
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted
only to the extent necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted
in this zone. Accessory buildings are not used for residential purposes. All
accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3').
      ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET

main structure.
Yard intrusions as provided in section

12-4F-9: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4F-10: OFF STREET PARKING:

For sign requirements in the R-3 zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987 Code
§ 17.24.100)
ARTICLE G. C ZONE
SECTION:
12-4G-1: Purpose
12-4G-2: Permitted Uses
12-4G-3: Conditional Uses
12-4G-4: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4G-5: Lot Requirements
12-4G-6: Height Limit
12-4G-7: Setbacks
12-4G-8: Fences And Walls
12-4G-9: Off Street Parking
12-4G-10: Signs
12-4G-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended to provide for commercial locations within the town,
convenient to residential areas, agricultural areas and the general public for
the purpose of buying, selling and trading goods and services, and allowing for
pedestrian as well as automotive traffic. (1987 Code § 17.28.010)
12-4G-2: PERMITTED USES:
The primary objective of this zone is to provide locations for people
collectively or individually to conduct a wide variety of retail or wholesale
business ventures and entrepreneurship conducive to free enterprise and a free
market system. Buildings and structures erected, altered or enlarged and land
used for any business transactions shall comply with codes, permits,
allowances, restrictions, etc., as provided by the laws and ordinances of the
town code. Examples of permitted uses are as follows:
Agricultural implements and sales.
Antique shops and stores.
Apparel and accessory stores.
Automobile accessory and supply stores.
Automobile and truck sales and service.
Automobile parking lots.
Bakery and pastry shops.
Banks and financial institutions.
Barbershops and beauty shops.
Bars and cocktail lounges.
Book and stationery stores.
Bowling alleys.
Bus passenger stations.
Car washes.
Churches.
Commercial enterprises.
Convenience food markets.
Department stores and shopping centers.
Drive-in or walk-in eating places.
Drugstores and prescription shops.
Dry cleaning and laundry establishments.
Dry goods and notions stores.
Dwellings on floors other than the ground floor.
Electric and telephone substations.
Fix it shops (radios, televisions and small household appliances).
Florist and gift shops.
Furniture and home furnishings stores.
Government and public buildings:
Fire stations, police stations, jails, public administration buildings.
Libraries and museums (public).
Parks, playgrounds and community buildings owned and operated by a public
agency.
Postal terminals.
Grocery, fruit, vegetable and meat stores.
Hardware, glass and paint stores.
Hotels.
Household and appliance stores.
Jewelry and craft stores and shops.
Laundry and launderettes.
Mail order catalog stores.
Medical, dental and health clinics.
Membership clubs and recreation centers.
Mobile home sales and service.
Music stores and studios.
Offices and office buildings.
Opticians, and optometrists' shops.
Package liquor stores.
Pet shops.
Photo shops.
Print shops.
Restaurants.
Shoe stores and shoe repair.
Sporting and athletic goods stores.
Stores and shops similar to the uses listed in this section.
Taverns and bars.
Theaters (indoor only).
Utility company offices.
Variety stores. (1987 Code § 17.28.020)
12-4G-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in the commercial zone subject to conditional use
permits are as follows:
Convenience stores that dispense gasoline.
Gaming establishments.
Mini-storage units.
Repair garages for automobiles, motorcycles, and boats. (Ord. 6-94, 10-20-1994;
amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004; Ord. 12-2004, 10-7-2004)
12-4G-4: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Prohibited Businesses And Uses: Businesses and uses that should be
located in an industrial zone as provided for in article H of this chapter may
not permitted in a C zone.
   B.   Uniform Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to
use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the C zone must certify, under oath, that
the building, structure or improvement will conform to the uniform building
code as adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the uniform building
code will not be permitted.
   C.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in a C
zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks or in
the center of the structure. All foundations must meet uniform building code
