standards. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4G-5: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
Lots of record on the effective date hereof whose area or dimensions are less
than those required in this zone, may be occupied by uses permitted, subject to
all other property development standards of the C zone.
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area shall be five thousand (5,000) square
feet.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot dimensions shall be: Minimum lot width,
fifty feet (50'). (1987 Code § 17.28.040)
12-4G-6: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building or structural height in the C zone shall be thirty five
feet (35'); provided, that a greater height may be allowed on obtaining a
conditional use permit; and provided, that when the zone abuts a residential
zone, then the maximum building or structural height shall not be greater than
thirty five feet (35') for a distance of fifty feet (50') from the zone
boundary abutting the residential zone. (1987 Code § 17.28.050)
12-4G-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the C zone are as follows:
   A.   Front Yard: Structures may be constructed on the front property line.
However, no structure may be constructed closer than forty feet (40') from the
centerline of the street.
   B.   Side Yard:
      1.   No side yard is required between commercial structures.
      2.   When abutting a residential zone, there shall be a side yard of not
less than ten feet (10') in width on that side of the property abutting the
residential zone.
   C.   Rear Yard:
      1.   No rear yard is required when property abuts property in a
commercial zone.
      2.   When abutting a residential zone, the required rear yard shall be
ten feet (10'). (1987 Code § 17.28.060)
12-4G-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4G-9: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the C zone, see chapter 8 of this title.
(1987 Code § 17.28.080)
12-4G-10: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the C zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987 Code §
17.28.090)
ARTICLE H. L-I AND H-I ZONES
SECTION:
12-4H-1: L-I Zone
12-4H-2: H-I Zone
12-4H-3: Administratively Permitted Uses
12-4H-4: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4H-5: Lot Requirements
12-4H-6: Height Limit
12-4H-7: Setbacks
12-4H-8: Fences And Walls
12-4H-9: Off Street Parking
12-4H-10: Signs
12-4H-1: L-I ZONE:
   A.   Established; Purpose: A light industrial (L-I) zone is created to
provide for an area where light industry, as enumerated in this section, may be
established. (1987 Code § 17.32.010)
   B.   Permitted And Conditional Uses: Only the following buildings,
structures and uses conducted either singly or in combination, as provided for
in this section, are permitted in the L-I zone. No building or structure shall
be erected, structurally altered or land used except for the following
purposes:
      1.   Permitted Uses:
Commercial:
Commercial uses customarily incidental and directly related to the services or
operations of the permitted industrial uses:
Administrative offices.
Restaurants and cafes.
Lumberyards (open storage area permitted).
Maintenance services.
Repair garages for automobiles, motorcycles and boats.
Utilities:
Distribution plants and substations.
Service yards.
Wholesaling and warehousing, including miniwarehouses.
Other:
Automobile service stations.
Drugs.
Pest control services.
Printing and publishing.
Research and development.
      2.   Uses Subject To Conditional Use Permit:
Fabrication:
Assembly of electric and electronic equipment.
Fabrication of products from finished rubber.
Metals.
Wood and wood products.
Helicopter landing areas.
Oil and gas wells. (1987 Code § 17.32.020)
12-4H-2: H-I ZONE:
   A.   Established; Purpose: A heavy industrial (H-I) zone is created to
provide for an area where heavy industry, as enumerated in this section, may be
established. (1987 Code § 17.12.030)
   B.   Permitted And Conditional Uses: Only the following buildings,
structures and uses, conducted either singly or in combination, as provided for
under this section, are permitted in the H-I zone. No building or structure
shall be erected, structurally altered or land used except for the following
purposes:
      1.   Permitted Uses:
Commercial:
Commercial uses customarily incidental and directly related to the services or
operations of the permitted industrial uses: administrative offices.
Lumberyards (open storage area permitted).
Maintenance service.
Fabrication:
Assembly of electric and electronic equipment.
Fabrication of products from finished rubber.
Metals.
Wood and wood products.
Manufacturing:
Manufacturing, compounding, assembly or treatment of articles from the
following prepared materials:
Canvas.
Cellophane.
Cloth.
Cork.
Feathers.
Felt and fiber.
Glass.
Metals.
Paper.
Plaster.
Plastics or synthetics.
Putty.
Shells.
Tobacco.
Wax and/or wood.
Novelties manufacture.
Repair garages for automobiles, motorcycles and boats.
Utilities:
Distribution plants and substations.
Service yards.
Wholesaling and warehousing.
Other:
Pest control service.
Railroad services, maintenance and storage.
Research and development.
Trucks, heavy equipment service and storage.
      2.   Uses Subject To Conditional Use Permit:
Helicopter landing areas.
Junkyards.
Miniwarehouses.
Oil and gas refineries and processing plants.
Oil and gas wells.
Sexually oriented businesses. (1987 Code § 17.32.040; amd. Ord. 9-99, 1-5-2000)
12-4H-3: ADMINISTRATIVELY PERMITTED USES:
Other buildings and uses for either the L-I zone or the H-I zone may be
permitted as an administrative act of the planning and zoning commission,
provided a public hearing is held, and the planning commission determines and
finds as a fact that such buildings and uses are similar to those listed in the
sections preceding; and provided further, that such other uses shall not have
any different or detrimental effect upon the adjoining neighborhood area or
zones than such specifically permitted uses and shall not increase the traffic
and noises in the neighborhood or otherwise be more objectionable or obnoxious
than those uses specifically permitted. (1987 Code § 17.32.050)
12-4H-4: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Uniform Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to
use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the L-I and H-I zones must certify, under
oath, that the building, structure or improvement will conform to the uniform
building code as adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the uniform
building code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
L-I and H-I zones must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight
or load bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks
or in the center of the structure. All foundations must meet uniform building
code standards. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4H-5: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
The minimum lot area in either industrial zone shall be five thousand (5,000)
square feet and the minimum lot width shall be fifty feet (50'). (1987 Code §
17.32.060)
12-4H-6: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building or structural height in either industrial zone shall be
six (6) stories, or seventy feet (70'), whichever is the lesser. (1987 Code §
17.32.070)
12-4H-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the L-I and H-I zones are as follows:
   A.   Front Yard: No building shall be erected closer than twenty feet (20')
to the property line fronting on a street or highway.
   B.   Side Yard: When property abuts upon a lot in a residential zone, the
required side yard shall be thirty feet (30'). Otherwise, no side yard is
required.
   C.   Rear Yard: When property abuts any lot in a residential zone, the
required rear yard shall be thirty feet (30'). Otherwise, no rear yard is
required. (1987 Code § 17.32.080)
12-4H-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required in the
L-I and H-I zones. Such fences and walls shall not exceed twelve feet (12') in
height.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences in L-I and H-I zones may be constructed
of chainlink and may have not more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the
top of the chainlink. (1987 Code § 17.32.090)
12-4H-9: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the H-I and L-I zones, see chapter 8 of
this title. (1987 Code § 17.32.100)
12-4H-10: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the H-I and L-I zones, see chapter 9 of this title.
(1987 Code § 17.32.110)
ARTICLE I. A ZONE
SECTION:
12-4I-1: Purpose
12-4I-2: Permitted Uses
12-4I-3: Conditional Uses
12-4I-4: Accessory Buildings And Uses
12-4I-5: Certification; Exemptions
12-4I-6: Setbacks
12-4I-7: Lot Requirements
12-4I-8: Off Street Parking
12-4I-9: Signs
12-4I-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended to provide an area for large farm and ranch operations
with such residential uses as are necessary and subordinate to the primary
purpose of farming and ranching. (1987 Code § 17.36.010)
12-4I-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the A zone.
No buildings and structures shall be erected, structurally altered or enlarged,
or land used, except for the following purposes:
Agriculture and ranching in general, excluding feedlots.
Cemeteries.
Golf courses.
Living quarters used only for housing of persons employed on the premises and
their immediate families (a mobile home may be used); provided, that all living
units meet or exceed state standards for water supply and sewage disposal.
Small animal breeding and raising, including commercial kennels.
Stables and riding academies. (1987 Code § 17.36.020)
12-4I-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in A zones subject to conditional use permits are
as follows:
Campgrounds.
Carnivals, circuses, temporary rodeos, auto and/or motorcycle raceways, and
similar types of outdoor commercial entertainment.
Dairying.
Guest ranches, hunting lodges and commercial recreational facilities.
Helicopter landing areas.
Membership clubs.
Mining and quarrying.
Oil and gas wells.
Rest and convalescent homes, hospitals and clinics.
Sanitary landfills.
Sewage treatment facilities. (1987 Code § 17.36.030; amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-
2004)
12-4I-4: ACCESSORY BUILDINGS AND USES:
Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted only to the extent necessary
and incidental to the types of uses permitted in this zone. (1987 Code §
17.36.040)
12-4I-5: CERTIFICATION; EXEMPTIONS:
   A.   Exemptions: All residential buildings located in the A zone shall be
exempt from the provisions of title 9, chapter 2 of this code except as may be
required by the department of housing and urban development.
   B.   Restrictions: All buildings which shall be built, placed or moved into
the A zone after January 1, 2000, shall be certified by the manufacturer and
the owner that they are in compliance with all standards set forth by the
department of housing and urban development. No permit shall issued by the town
without said certifications. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4I-6: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the A zone are as follows:
   A.   Front Yard: No building fronting on a street or highway shall be
erected closer that fifty feet (50') from the property line.
   B.   Side Yard: No building shall be erected closer than twenty feet (20')
to any side property line.
   C.   Rear Yard: No building shall be erected closer than fifty feet (50') to
the rear property line. (1987 Code § 17.36.050)
12-4I-7: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
The minimum lot area in the A zone shall be fifteen (15) acres. (1987 Code §
17.36.060)
12-4I-8: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the A zone, see chapter 8 of this title.
(1987 Code § 17.36.070)
12-4I-9: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the A zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (1987 Code §
17.36.080)
ARTICLE J. O ZONE
SECTION:
12-4J-1: Purpose
12-4J-2: Permitted Uses
12-4J-3: Conditional Uses
12-4J-4: Accessory Buildings And Uses
12-4J-5: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4J-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as an area of open space within the community which may
be used for outdoor recreational purposes. (1987 Code § 17.40.010)
12-4J-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in O zones. No
buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or land used
except for the following purposes:
Campgrounds.
Fairgrounds.
Outdoor sports arenas, including roping and rodeo.
Parks and playgrounds. (1987 Code § 17.40.020)
12-4J-3: CONDITIONAL USES:
Uses which may be permitted in O zones subject to conditional use permits are
as follows:
Overnight trailer parks.
Power substations or public utility operations facilities.
Recreational services, not service stations, motels or hotels. (1987 Code §
17.40.030; amd. Ord. 10-2004, 10-7-2004)
12-4J-4: ACCESSORY BUILDINGS AND USES:
Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted only to the extent necessary
and normal to the limited types of uses permitted in this zone. Accessory
buildings may only be used for residential purposes for those persons necessary
for the operation of uses permitted in this zone. All residences must have town
approved services. (1987 Code § 17.40.040)
12-4J-5: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Uniform Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to
use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the O zone must certify, under oath, that
the building, structure or improvement will conform to the uniform building
code as adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the uniform building
code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
O zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks or in
the center of the structure. All foundations must meet uniform building code
standards. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
ARTICLE K. M ZONE
SECTION:
12-4K-1: Purpose
12-4K-2: Location Of Mobile Homes
12-4K-3: Compliance With Article
12-4K-4: Certification; Exemptions
12-4K-5: Density; Setbacks
12-4K-6: Access
12-4K-7: Water Supply
12-4K-8: Sewage Disposal
12-4K-9: Lighting
12-4K-10: Utilities; Fire Protection
12-4K-11: Sanitation
12-4K-12: Skirting And Additions
12-4K-13: Mobile Home Maintenance
12-4K-14: Mobile Home Park
12-4K-15: Mobile Homes Outside Mobile Home Parks; Standards
12-4K-16: Camper Parks; Special Standards
12-4K-17: Age Overlay
12-4K-18: Conflicts Between Ordinance And Rules
12-4K-19: License Transfer Or Suspension; Reapplication
12-4K-20: Fences And Walls
12-4K-21: Height Limit
12-4K-22: Permitted Uses
12-4K-1: PURPOSE:
A mobile home park (M) zone is created to provide for an area where mobile
homes can be situated for year round living. Mobile home parks shall be
permitted in the M zone and may be established in R-3 zones with a conditional
use permit; provided, that they comply with all subdivision and zoning
requirements as provided by law. (1987 Code § 17.44.010)
12-4K-2: LOCATION OF MOBILE HOMES:
   A.   Prohibited: Mobile home units are not permitted in C, L-I, or H-
I zones.
   B.   Mobile Home Parks: Mobile home parks are allowed in M zones or in R-
3 zones with a conditional use permit. (Ord. 2006-01, 3-2-2006)
   C.   Singlewide And Doublewide Mobile Homes: Singlewide mobile homes and
doublewide mobile homes on private lots are allowed in R-3 and A zones.
Doublewide mobile homes on private lots are allowed in R-2 zones, singlewide
mobile homes are not allowed in R-1 and R-2 zones. Placement of a mobile home
must comply with all relevant zoning regulations set forth in this code. The
connection of two (2) or more unisectioned mobile home units, not manufactured,
constructed and intended expressly for the purpose of joining single sections
together to provide one continuous living space are strictly prohibited. (Ord.
2008-1, 3-20-2008)
12-4K-3: COMPLIANCE WITH ARTICLE:
   A.   Required: All new and existing mobile home parks and camper parks will
be required to meet all applicable standards as set forth in this article prior
to receiving the town's approval and a business license to operate.
   B.   Existing Mobile Home Parks And Camper Parks: All existing mobile home
parks and camper parks must be licensed within sixty (60) days of the enactment
or revision of this article. Conditions which exist as of the revision of this
article which are contrary to portions hereof will be allowed to remain until
the mobile home unit or camper unit causing the contrary condition is moved.
Any mobile home unit or camper unit then parked or set shall comply to all
conditions herein.
   C.   New Mobile Home Parks And Camper Parks: All new mobile home parks and
camper parks must meet all standards prior to being granted a business license
to operate. (1987 Code § 17.44.030)
12-4K-4: CERTIFICATION; EXEMPTIONS:
   A.   Exemptions: All residential buildings located within the M zone shall
be exempt from the provisions of title 9, chapter 2 of this code except as may
be required by the department of housing and urban development.
   B.   Restrictions: All buildings which shall be built, placed or moved into
the M zone after January 1, 2001, shall be certified by the manufacturer and
the owner that they are in compliance with all standards set forth by the
department of housing and urban development. No permit shall issue by the town
without said certifications. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4K-5: DENSITY; SETBACKS:
   A.   Density:
      1.   Maximum Number Of Spaces: No mobile home park shall have a density
of more than seven (7) spaces per acre.
      2.   Minimum Area Of Each Space: Each space shall have a minimum area of
three thousand two hundred (3,200) square feet and shall not be less than forty
feet (40') in width at the unit's location.
      3.   Unit Boundaries: The boundaries of each unit shall be clearly
defined.
      4.   Occupied Space: The mobile home shall not occupy more than seventy
five percent (75%) of any space.
      5.   Camper Park Spaces: Each camper park unit shall be a minimum of
twenty five feet (25') in width and each unit space shall have a minimum area
of nine hundred (900) square feet. (1987 Code § 17.44.040)
      6.   Number Of Residences Per Lot: No more than one residence shall be
contained on a single lot. (Ord. 2009-06, 7-16-2009)
   B.   Common Areas: Not less than five percent (5%) of the gross site area
shall be designated as common areas.
   C.   Direct Access To Public Streets: For mobile home park spaces having
direct access to public streets, no part of any mobile home or camper unit,
including parts used for towing shall be closer than twenty feet (20') from the
park boundary line abutting the public street or highway. All mobile home and
camper units shall be located at least fifteen feet (15') from any park
boundary abutting upon a public street or highway but not having direct access
to the street or highway. All mobile home and camper units shall be located at
least ten feet (10') from other park boundary lines.
   D.   Distance Between Units: There shall be a minimum distance of fifteen
feet (15') between the mobile home unit or camper unit and abutting park
street.
   E.   Structures On Adjoining Lots: Structures on adjoining lots shall be no
closer than twenty feet (20') apart. Unless attached to another structure on
the same space, all structures on the same lot shall be at least ten feet (10')
apart.
   F.   Distance From Service Buildings: There shall be a minimum of twenty
feet (20') between a mobile home or camper unit and any service building(s).
   G.   Address Display; Space Designation: For mobile home park spaces having
direct access to public streets, each space shall display a street address as
assigned by the town. Each address display shall be readily discernible from
the public street. All mobile home park spaces having direct access to roads
within the park shall discernably display a space number or designation. Such
space designation shall be logically assigned to allow easy location. (1987
Code § 17.44.040)
12-4K-6: ACCESS:
   A.   Roads: All roads in the park shall be a minimum of twenty four feet
(24') in width. All roads shall be improved and brought up to an acceptable
standard to adequately handle the proposed traffic load of the mobile home
court.
   B.   Walkways: All weather walkways of three feet (3') minimum width shall
be provided for each mobile home space. These walkways shall be of a permanent
nature, constructed of concrete or asphalt or some other material acceptable to
the planning and zoning commission. No walkways are required in a camper park.
(1987 Code § 17.44.050)
12-4K-7: WATER SUPPLY:
Water supply for mobile home parks must comply with town and state standards.
(1987 Code § 17.44.060)
12-4K-8: SEWAGE DISPOSAL:
The sewage disposal system for mobile home parks must comply with town and
state standards. (1987 Code § 17.44.070)
12-4K-9: LIGHTING:
Adequate lighting shall be provided for all portions of the mobile home park
and camper park. (1987 Code § 17.44.080)
12-4K-10: UTILITIES; FIRE PROTECTION:
   A.   Standards: All utilities shall meet state and local requirements.
   B.   Fire Protection:
      1.   Required: All mobile home parks shall meet the minimum standards for
fire protection in mobile home parks as set forth by the state department of
fire protection and electrical safety and Wyoming mobile home park and
campground regulations.
      2.   Approved Plan: An approved plan for providing adequate fire
protection to the park shall be presented. Approval shall be by the town fire
department. (1987 Code § 17.44.090)
12-4K-11: SANITATION:
   A.   Drainage: The mobile home court and camper park shall be graded and
adequately drained to alleviate any potential health or safety problems.
   B.   Garbage Disposal: Each mobile home court and camper park shall set
forth a plan on how garbage disposal is to be handled. Each mobile home space,
either individually or as a group, shall be provided or required to provide
adequate garbage containers having tightfitting lids. Refuse shall be collected
and disposed of at least once per week.
   C.   Insect And Rodent Control: In order to provide adequate insect and
rodent control, every mobile home park and camper park shall be kept free of
rubbish and maintained in a sanitary condition at all times. All harborages for
insects and rodents shall be eliminated and prevented. Flies and mosquitoes
shall be controlled. (1987 Code § 17.44.100)
12-4K-12: SKIRTING AND ADDITIONS:
   A.   Skirting: Skirting of all mobile homes shall be required within thirty
(30) days after occupying a space in the mobile home park 1 .
   B.   Additions: Additions to mobile homes such as covered porches,
additions, etc., with the exception of open steps of less than forty (40)
square feet per landing, shall be prohibited, unless they are provided for in
the approved plan of the mobile home park. The connection of two (2) single
wide, unisectioned mobile home units, not manufactured, constructed, and
intended expressly for the purpose of joining single sections together to
provide one continuous living space shall be strictly prohibited in mobile home
parks. (1987 Code § 17.44.110)
 
Notes
1 1. See also section
  12-6-5 of this title.
12-4K-13: MOBILE HOME MAINTENANCE:
   A.   The integrity of each mobile home occupying a space in a mobile home
park shall be maintained. That is, doors shall be capable of being locked and
shall be secured at all times when unoccupied, glass windows shall be intact
and any broken glass shall be replaced at once, any exterior surface or siding
shall be maintained and kept in place and the general appearance of the mobile
home shall be maintained at all times.
   B.   Any mobile home or motor home occupying a space in a mobile home park
that is not used as a residence or is otherwise unoccupied for a period of four
(4) months or more must be removed by the owner of said mobile home park.
   C.   Failure to comply with the provisions of this section constitutes a
misdemeanor punishable by not more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00)
in fines. Each day of continuing violation may constitute a separate offense.
Either the owner of the mobile or motor home may be charged, or the mobile home
park owner or both. A misdemeanor herein shall not bar any other remedy by the
town under law or equity, including the initiation of abatement proceedings.
(Ord. 2012-10, 12-20-2012)
12-4K-14: MOBILE HOME PARK:
   A.   Business License Requirements:
      1.   Application: Each mobile home park owner or camper park owner shall
make application with the town for a mobile home park business license.
      2.   Plans, Drawings And Specifications: Each application for a new
mobile home park or camper park business license shall be accompanied by the
necessary plans, drawings and specifications to show that the proposed park
will meet all of the necessary standards as set forth in this chapter.
      3.   Transmittal To State Agencies: Sufficient copies of drawings and
specifications must be provided along with letters of transmittal to the
necessary state agencies for approval, or copies of letters of transmittal to
the necessary state agencies requesting their review and requesting copies of
their review be forwarded to the town.
      4.   Fee: Initial applications for new mobile home parks or camper parks
shall be accompanied by a fee as determined by the town council.
      5.   Review: All new applications for a mobile home park and camper park
business licenses shall be reviewed by the planning and zoning commission and
town council. Review comments and recommendations shall be forwarded to the
applicant within thirty five (35) days after receipt of the original
application.
      6.   Construction: After receipt of approval for construction from the
town council, the applicant may proceed with construction. It is unlawful to
begin any construction on a mobile home park or camper park in the absence of
this approval.
      7.   Inspection: During the time of construction and the completion of
construction, the town shall provide for inspectors to inspect construction as
per specifics set forth in the letter of construction approval. Upon final
completion of the mobile home park or camper park, notice shall be made to the
designated inspector to make final inspection and to file his inspection report
with the commission.
      8.   Granting Of Mobile Home Park Business License: Upon receiving the
final inspection report, the planning and zoning commission shall recommend
granting or denial to the town council. The council shall grant the final
permit and license and shall sign such license and direct its transmittal to
the applicant upon the payment of any inspection fees as may be necessary.
      9.   Appeal: Applicants shall have the right to appeal any ruling or ask
for a variance from any standards as set forth in this article according to the
variance procedure as set forth in chapter 11 of this title.
      10.   Penalty: Failure to obtain approval prior to construction and the
operation of a mobile home park or camper park without a town license shall be
punishable by a fine of not more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for
each offense. Each day's continuance shall be deemed a separate offense. (1987
Code § 17.44.140)
   B.   License Renewal: Each mobile home park or camper park shall be required
to renew the mobile home park or camper park business license on January 1 of
each year.
      1.   Existing Parks: Mobile home parks or camper parks existing at the
time of adoption hereof will be required to apply for a mobile home park or
camper park business license under this subsection.
      2.   Temporary Suspension: Mobile home park business licenses may be
temporarily suspended by the inspector upon violation by the holder of any of
the terms of these town standards or revoked after an opportunity for a hearing
by the town council upon serious or repeated violation. (1987 Code § 17.44.150)
   C.   Changes To Park; Approval Before Licensing: Any changes which have been
made in the mobile home park or camper park during the past year shall have
been approved under new construction. The date of approval shall be noted on
the application for renewal.
      1.   Inspection; Report: Inspection shall be made of the mobile home park
or camper park and reports shall be filed with the planning and zoning
commission.
      2.   Recommendations To Town Council: The planning and zoning commission
shall make recommendations to the town council concerning the granting of
licenses. They may recommend, based upon the inspector's report, that the
license be granted with the provision that certain things be brought up to
standards within sixty (60) days of granting of license.
      3.   Grant Of License: The town council shall, upon recommendation of the
planning and zoning commission, grant a license to the mobile home park or
camper park. (1987 Code § 17.44.160)
   D.   Inspection: Inspection may be made at any time by the town to determine
adherence to standards and recommendations. Such reports may be used in lieu of
the inspection reports in subsection C of this section at the time of
application, if they are considered by the commission to be current and
applicable. All mobile home park or camper park owners and operators shall
grant reasonable access to designated inspectors. (1987 Code § 17.44.170)
   E.   Register Required: Every mobile home park owner or operator shall
maintain a register containing a record of all mobile homes, travel trailers,
truck campers, tent trailers and tents using the mobile home park or camper
park. The register shall be current. (Ord. 16-00, 12-21-2000, eff. 1-1-2001)
12-4K-15: MOBILE HOMES OUTSIDE MOBILE HOME PARKS; STANDARDS:
When the number of mobile home spaces either planned or to be installed will be
less than six (6) spaces, the regulations of the underlying zone shall fully
apply, provided, however:
   A.   Building Permit; Variance: A building permit and a variance from the
planning and zoning commission must be secured prior to setting up the mobile
home on the lot.
   B.   Foundations: Foundations are to be reinforced concrete at least six
inches (6") thick, or equal, and to be continued without interruption around
and under the structure. (1987 Code § 17.44.180)
   C.   Skirting: Skirting on the mobile home shall be continued without
interruption around and under the structure. Skirting shall be completed within
thirty (30) days of placement of the mobile home and shall be constructed of
the same material as the mobile home siding or a previously approved acceptable
substitute approved by planning and zoning at the time of variance. (Ord. 13-
92, 12-17-1992)
   D.   Minimum Width: The mobile home must have a minimum width of twenty feet
(20'). The connection of two (2) single wide, unisectioned mobile home units,
not manufactured, constructed and intended expressly for the purpose of joining
single sections together to provide one continuous living space are strictly
prohibited.
   E.   Sewer Connections: Sewer connections must be of a positive type and the
water hookup must be of an approved type.
   F.   Additions; Alterations; New Structures: Any additions or alterations or
new structures such as accessory buildings shall require a building permit.
   G.   Electrical Service: Electrical service from the maker loop to the
mobile home shall comply with existing national and state electrical codes.
   H.   Siding: Siding shall be house type siding.
   I.   Walls: Walls to be made of at least two inches by four inches (2" x 4")
thickness with firebreaks installed to meet state fire code specifications and
to be sheeted with sheetrock, drywall or equivalent.
   J.   Roofing Material: All roofing material must meet or exceed the
requirements of the Wyoming state fire code, latest edition. (1987 Code §
17.44.180)
   K.   Roof Overhangs: For all other mobile or manufactured homes, the roof
overhangs shall not be less than six inches (6") measured from the vertical
side of the building. (Ord. 11-00, 8-17-2000; amd. Ord. 17-2002, 10-17-2002)
   L.   Finished Floor Height: The finished floor height of the closest to
ground level shall be no more than thirty inches (30") higher than the finished
lot grade measured at the sidewalk next to the street closest to the mobile or
manufactured home. (Ord. 10-98, 2-18-1999)
12-4K-16: CAMPER PARKS; SPECIAL STANDARDS:
   A.   Variance From General Provisions: The following variances from the
general provisions are made only for camper parks or parts of mobile home parks
catering to overnight campers providing facilities for truck campers, travel
trailers, tents and tent trailers:
      1.   Unit Size: Each designated unit space providing for a truck camper,
travel trailer, tent or tent trailer shall contain a minimum of nine hundred
(900) square feet.
      2.   Table; Solid Waste Disposal Facilities: Each designated unit space
provided for tenting units shall be provided with a table and easy access to
both liquid and solid waste disposal facilities.
      3.   Kitchen Or Sink Wastewater: Provisions shall be made for the
approved disposal of kitchen or sink wastewater at each designated unit space
for camper units in a manner approved by the state health department.
      4.   Distance From Service Building: No unit space serving a dependent
travel trailer, truck camper or tent or tenting unit shall be located further
than three hundred feet (300') radially from the service building. Unit spaces
further than this distance must be designated for and used by independent units
only.
   B.   Water Supply: The water supply shall be approved by the state health
department and the water quality division of the department of environmental
quality, where applicable, as per specifications stated in prior sections of
this article.
   C.   Sewage Disposal: Sewage disposal shall be handled in a manner meeting
the requirements of the state health department and the state department of
environmental quality as provided for in prior sections of this article.
   D.   Service Building: Each park which permits dependent "mobile homes" and
dependent "travel trailers", dependent "truck campers" or "tenting units" as
defined in the definitions and each camper park shall provide a service
building equipped and meeting the specifications of the state health
department, with a minimum of one per twenty five (25) spaces. (1987 Code §
17.44.190)
12-4K-17: AGE OVERLAY:
   A.   Designation For Age Overlay: The opportunity for an age overlay
designation in the M zone is hereby created and provided, wherein mobile homes
constructed prior to twenty five (25) years before the date they are moved into
town may be placed for year round residential living. This section does not
prohibit mobile homes constructed more recently than twenty five (25) years
before the date it is moved into town from also being placed in this designated
overlay. (Ord. 2012-09, 12-20-2012)
   B.   Owner To Provide Overlay Map: The owner of the mobile home park
desiring an age overlay must submit a map to the town designating the portions,
lots, spaces or area of the mobile home park proposed for the age overlay, to
be reviewed by the planning and zoning commission and approved by the governing
body by ordinance.
   C.   Conditions For Age Overlay: The following conditions shall apply when
considering any age overlay proposal in the M zone:
      1.   The proposed lots, spaces, portions or areas of the mobile home park
shall be contiguous, excepting roads. The age overlay shall be in one clustered
area.
      2.   The proposed lots, spaces, portions or areas of the mobile home park
shall consist of no more than fifteen percent (15%) of the available space or
area in the mobile home park, excepting roads.
      3.   The proposed lots, spaces, portions or areas of the mobile home park
shall be the available area farthest removed (isolated) from public streets and
rights of way and other residential use areas within and outside the mobile
home park. (Ord. 2-99, 4-8-1999)
      4.   The mobile home park shall consist of no less than seven (7) lots
suitable for placement of individual singlewide mobile homes. (Ord. 2008-16, 8-
21-2008)
12-4K-18: CONFLICTS BETWEEN ORDINANCE AND RULES:
In the event any conflict shall exist between any section of this article and
administrative rules promulgated by the Wyoming department of health and social
services, that ordinance, section or rule requiring the stricter standard shall
apply. (1987 Code § 17.44.210)
12-4K-19: LICENSE TRANSFER OR SUSPENSION; REAPPLICATION:
   A.   Transferability: Business licenses shall not be transferable from one
person to another person or to a different location than originally issued.
(1987 Code § 17.44.250)
   B.   Suspension; Revocation: Town business licenses may be temporarily
suspended by the inspector upon violation by the holder of any of the terms of
these town standards or revoked after an opportunity for a hearing by the town
council upon serious or repeated violations.
   C.   Reapplication: Any mobile home park, the business license of which has
been suspended or revoked, may, at any time, make reapplication for the
reinstatement of the business license. (1987 Code § 17.44.240)
12-4K-20: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4K-21: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4K-22: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the M zone.
No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered or enlarged,
or land used, except for the following purposes:
Educational institutions.
Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
Single-family dwellings (only 1 per lot). (Ord. 2015-05, 12-3-2015)
ARTICLE L. PUD ZONE
SECTION:
12-4L-1: Purpose
12-4L-2: Permitted Uses
12-4L-3: Area
12-4L-4: Boundary Amenities; Open Space; Setbacks
12-4L-5: Only Planned Uses Permitted
12-4L-6: Residential District Screening
12-4L-7: Application; Conditions And Modifications
12-4L-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended to encourage better and more flexible land use
development by allowing such development to be based upon a comprehensive,
integrated and detailed plan rather than upon specific constraints as
applicable to uniform lot by lot development while carrying out the intent and
purpose of the zoning regulations. (1987 Code § 17.48.010)
12-4L-2: PERMITTED USES:
Any use listed as a permitted or conditional use in the R, R-0, R-1, R-1-A, R-
2, R-3, R-4, RS, RS-1, C-1 or C-2 zones may be approved in any planned unit
development if such use, by location, characteristic or design, is deemed
compatible with the character of the planned unit development, and the area in
which the development is proposed, with the following exceptions: (1987 Code §
17.48.020; amd. 2004 Code)
   A.   In areas already zoned RS, RS-1, R or R-1, only those listed as
permitted or special uses in R, R-1, R-2, RS, RS-1 or C-2 may be approved in
any such planned unit development, if such use, by location, characteristic or
design, is deemed compatible with the character of the development, the zone in
which the proposed development exists, and the area in which the development is
proposed.
      1.   In an R, R-1, RS or RS-1 district, no planned unit development shall
have more than a ten percent (10%) increase in total density in the R-1 zone.
      2.   The concessions and retail services provided for the occupants of
the planned unit development in an R or R-1 district shall be located in a
separate building.
   B.   No planned unit development shall have more than a twenty percent (20%)
increase in total density allowed in the zone in which the development is
proposed. (1987 Code § 17.48.020)
12-4L-3: AREA:
The minimum area which may be considered for a planned unit development zone
shall be five (5) acres of contiguous land, unless the town council finds a
district of less than five (5) acres suitable as a planned unit development
district by virtue of its unique character. (1987 Code § 17.48.030)
12-4L-4: BOUNDARY AMENITIES; OPEN SPACE; SETBACKS:
   A.   Boundaries: Around the boundaries of the development, building height,
architecture and coverage shall be arranged to enhance the livability and
attractiveness of adjacent land uses. The yard and height requirements of the
adjacent zone may be required on the immediate periphery.
   B.   Open Area: Not more than eighty percent (80%) of the planned unit
development site shall be devoted to the construction of parking facilities,
streets, buildings, and accessory buildings. The remaining twenty percent (20%)
shall remain open.
   C.   Setbacks, Yard And Area Requirements: All setback, yard and area
requirements shall be determined by the planning and zoning commission. (1987
Code § 17.48.040)
12-4L-5: ONLY PLANNED USES PERMITTED:
All uses shall be restricted to those structures approved for said use in the
final development plan. (1987 Code § 17.48.050)
12-4L-6: RESIDENTIAL DISTRICT SCREENING:
Where a planned unit development adjoins any lot in any residential district,
there may be required along such property lines a fence and/or planting strip
as determined by the planning and zoning commission. (1987 Code § 17.48.060)
12-4L-7: APPLICATION; CONDITIONS AND MODIFICATIONS:
   A.   Amendments; Changes Of District Boundaries: The procedure for
amendments and changes of district boundaries as set forth in chapter 13 of
this title shall apply to the submission and approval of the preliminary
development plan for planned unit development.
   B.   Application; Preliminary Development Plan: The application to the
planning and zoning commission shall consist of a preliminary development plan
for the area showing unified and organized arrangements of buildings and
structures, their proposed uses, provisions for off street parking, internal
and external traffic circulation and service facilities, etc., and schematic
architectural drawings, landscape plans and sketches demonstrating the design
and character of the proposed development.
   C.   Criteria For Approval: No application shall be approved unless the
planning and zoning commission finds that the application:
      1.   Complies with all requirements imposed by this article and the
planning and zoning commission;
      2.   Is consistent with the objectives and purposes of this title;
      3.   Is designed to be compatible with surrounding land uses; and
      4.   Is designed to be compatible with the physical features of the site
upon which the development is proposed.
   D.   Modifications Or Conditions: In considering an application for planned
unit development, the planning and zoning commission may impose modifications
or conditions concerning the following development features to the extent that
such modifications or conditions are necessary to ensure compliance with
criteria in the preceding subsection:
      1.   Size and location of site.
      2.   Street and road capacities in the area.
      3.   Ingress and egress to adjoining public streets.
      4.   Location and amount of off street parking.
      5.   Internal traffic circulation system.
      6.   Fencing, screening and landscaped separations.
      7.   Building bulk, height and location.
      8.   Usable open space.
      9.   Signs and lighting.
      10.   Noise, vibration, air pollution and other environmental influences.
      11.   Setback, yard and area requirements.
   E.   Ability Of Developer To Complete Project: The developer shall submit
all evidence deemed necessary by the planning and zoning commission of his
ability to undertake and complete the proposed project.
   F.   Security: The town council shall also require a reasonable amount to be
provided by the developer, by cash deposit, bond, mortgage, letter of credit,
or other security as approved by the town council on the property to ensure the
completion of the landscaping for the entire plan or phase thereof.
   G.   Changes Or Amendments: No changes or amendments shall be made in the
preliminary development plan after approval of the plan without first
submitting the changes or amendments to the planning and zoning commission and
obtaining their approval. No public hearing shall be required prior to approval
or disapproval of the changes or amendments.
   H.   Final Development Plan, Approval And Building Permit Issuance:
      1.   Issuance Of Building Permits: After the planned unit development has
received a preliminary approval, no building permits shall be issued until
approval of the final development plan.
      2.   Final Development Plan Requirements: A final development plan shall
set forth in detail the following:
         a.   The proposed name of the area and the name and address of the
applicant or applicants.
         b.   Total acreage and the location of the land proposed to be
developed.
         c.   The applicant's interest in the land (the development for sale,
rental, etc.).
         d.   The density of land use allocated to the various parts of the
development.
         e.   The location and size of land, if any, to be retained as common
open space with proposed landscaping plans.
         f.   The form of organization proposed to own and maintain the common
open space.
         g.   The use, dimensions, schematic drawings, and locations of
buildings or other structures.
         h.   Provisions for disposition of storm water or surface runoff.
         i.   The substance of any covenants, grants, easements or any other
restrictions proposed to be imposed upon the land or building(s), including
assessment for public utilities.
         j.   The proposed provision for parking locations and widths of
streets and ways, modifications from the existing ordinances governing streets
and ways or land use being requested.
         k.   Projected schedule for development (construction schedule).
         l.   Existing and proposed contours at five foot (5') intervals.
         m.   Percent of residential and commercial (business) development in
the planned unit development.
      3.   Restrictive Covenants: The council shall require such restrictive
covenants by the developer to be placed or recorded in the office of the county
clerk as are necessary to assure compliance with the approved final development
plan.
      4.   Approval Required For Changes Or Amendments: No changes or
amendments shall be made in the final development plan after approval of the
plan without first obtaining the written approval of the planning and zoning
commission. Copies of the approved final plan shall be kept on file in the
office of the planning and zoning commission. (1987 Code § 17.48.070)
ARTICLE M. RECREATIONAL DEVELOPMENT ZONE
SECTION:
12-4M-1: Purpose
12-4M-2: Permitted Uses
12-4M-3: Area
12-4M-4: Boundary Amenities; Open Space; Setbacks
12-4M-5: Only Planned Uses Permitted
12-4M-6: Application; Conditions And Modifications
12-4M-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended to facilitate and encourage the development and operation
of related and supporting businesses in the recreation and tourism industries
within the town of Lyman. The town of Lyman recognizes that many businesses
that support these related industries may not legally exist within the same
defined zone within the town of Lyman. By allowing development of a plan, that
utilizes interrelated and supporting businesses, and is based on specific,
comprehensive and detailed development, a better use of land and more desirable
economic development will result, while carrying out the intent and purpose of
the zoning regulations. (Ord. 14-2004, 10-21-2004)
12-4M-2: PERMITTED USES:
   A.   Any use that can demonstrate a benefit to development of recreational
and/or tourism within the town of Lyman may be permitted, which includes, but
is not limited to, a list of uses that will be supplied by the clerk upon
request.
Any use must be one of a combination of uses allowed under this article. (Ord.
14-2004, 10-21-2004)
12-4M-3: AREA:
   A.   The minimum area allowed to be designated as an RCD is two (2) lots.
(Ord. 14-2004, 10-21-2004)
12-4M-4: BOUNDARY AMENITIES; OPEN SPACE; SETBACKS:
   A.   Boundaries: Around the boundaries of the development, building height,
architecture and coverage shall be arranged to enhance the livability and
attractiveness of adjacent land uses. The yard and height requirements of the
adjacent zone may be required on the immediate periphery.
   B.   Open Area: Not more than eighty percent (80%) of the planned unit
development site shall be devoted to the construction of parking facilities,
streets, buildings, and accessory buildings. The remaining twenty percent (20%)
shall remain open.
   C.   Setbacks, Yard And Area Requirements: All setback, yard and area
requirements shall be determined by the planning and zoning commission, after
submission of comprehensive plan. (Ord. 14-2004, 10-21-2004)
12-4M-5: ONLY PLANNED USES PERMITTED:
All uses shall be restricted to those structures approved for said use in the
final development plan. (Ord. 14-2004, 10-21-2004)
12-4M-6: APPLICATION; CONDITIONS AND MODIFICATIONS:
   A.   Amendments; Changes Of District Boundaries: The procedure for
amendments and changes of district boundaries as set forth in this title shall
apply to the submission and approval of the preliminary development plan for
planned unit development.
   B.   Application; Preliminary Development Plan: The application to the
planning and zoning commission shall consist of:
      1.   A preliminary development plan for the area showing unified and
organized arrangements of buildings and structures and their proposed uses;
      2.   Provisions for off street parking, internal and external traffic
circulation and service facilities;
      3.   If the buildings are not currently in existence, schematic
architectural drawings;
      4.   A written explanation of how each proposed use will support the
other uses and overall goal of the development;
      5.   Landscape plans and sketches demonstrating the design and character
of the proposed development;
      6.   An explanation of how such a development would enhance and benefit
the recreational or tourism industries in and around the town of Lyman.
   C.   Criteria For Approval: No application shall be approved unless the
planning and zoning commission finds that the application:
      1.   Complies with all requirements imposed by this article and the
planning and zoning commission;
      2.   Is consistent with the objectives and purposes of this title;
      3.   Is designed to be compatible with surrounding land uses; and
      4.   Is designed to be compatible with the physical features of the site
upon which the development is proposed.
   D.   Modifications Or Conditions: In considering an application for
recreational development zone, the planning and zoning commission may impose
modifications or conditions concerning the following development features to
the extent that such modifications or conditions are necessary to ensure
compliance with criteria in the preceding subsection:
      1.   Size and location of site.
      2.   Street and road capacities in the area.
      3.   Ingress and egress to adjoining public streets.
      4.   Location and amount of off street parking.
      5.   Internal traffic circulation system.
      6.   Fencing, screening and landscaped separations.
      7.   Building bulk, height and location.
      8.   Usable open space.
      9.   Signs and lighting.
      10.   Noise, vibration, air pollution and other environmental influences.
      11.   Setback, yard and area requirements.
      12.   If a camping area is part of the plan, conditions of size of
spaces, number of spaces (density), required amenities, and any required
facilities shall be specified.
   E.   Ability Of Developer To Complete Project: The developer shall submit
all evidence deemed necessary by the planning and zoning commission of his
ability to undertake and complete the proposed project.
   F.   Security: If the proposed RDZ needs to be fully developed, all
applicable planning and zoning regulations shall apply, including the town
council shall also require a reasonable amount to be provided by the developer,
by cash deposit, bond, mortgage, letter of credit, or other security as
approved by the town council on the property to ensure the completion of the
landscaping for the entire plan or phase thereof.
   G.   Changes Or Amendments:
      1.   No changes or amendments shall be made in the preliminary
development plan after approval of the plan without first submitting the
changes or amendments to the planning and zoning commission and obtaining their
approval. No public hearing shall be required prior to approval or disapproval
of the changes or amendments.
      2.   If one or more businesses fail after completion of the plan, any new
business or use of the building failed business occupied, shall be the same
type of business allowed by recreational development or have a recreational
development modification granted in a way that would comply with the
recreational development rules on changes.
   H.   Final Development Plan, Approval And Building Permit Issuance:
      1.   Issuance Of Building Permits: After the recreational development
zone has received a preliminary approval, final approval may be pursued, but,
no building permits shall be issued until approval of the final development
plan.
      2.   Final Development Plan Requirements: A final development plan shall
set forth in detail the following:
         a.   The proposed name of the area and the name and address of the
applicant or applicants.
         b.   Total acreage, number and sizes of lots and the location of the
land proposed to be developed.
         c.   The applicant's interest in the land (the development for sale,
rental, etc.).
         d.   The density of land use allocated to the various parts of the
development.
         e.   The location and size of land, if any, to be retained as common
open space with proposed landscaping plans.
         f.   The form of organization proposed to own and maintain the common
open space.
         g.   The use, dimensions, schematic drawings, and locations of
buildings or other structures.
         h.   Provisions for disposition of storm water or surface runoff.
         i.   The substance of any covenants, grants, easements or any other
restrictions proposed to be imposed upon the land or building(s), including
assessment for public utilities.
         j.   The proposed provision for parking locations and widths of
streets and ways, modifications from the existing ordinances governing streets
and ways or land use being requested.
         k.   Projected schedule for development (construction schedule).
         l.   Existing and proposed contours at five foot (5') intervals.
      3.   Approval Required For Changes Or Amendments: No changes or
amendments shall be made in the final development plan after approval of the
plan without first obtaining the written approval of the planning and zoning
commission. Copies of the approved final plan shall be kept on file in the
office of the planning and zoning commission. (Ord. 14-2004, 10-21-2004)
ARTICLE N. R-4 ZONE
SECTION:
12-4N-1: Purpose
12-4N-2: Permitted Uses
12-4N-3: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4N-4: Minimum Floor Area
12-4N-5: Lot Requirements
12-4N-6: Height Limit And Construction
12-4N-7: Setbacks
12-4N-8: Fences And Walls
12-4N-9: Off Street Parking
12-4N-10: Signs
12-4N-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a high density residential area with lots having a
minimum area of ten thousand (10,000) square feet with one or more buildings on
one lot. (Ord. 2-2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
4 zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered, or
enlarged, or land used, except for the following purposes:
Multi-dwelling (4 unit or greater) residential structures.
Planned unit developments, provided such development complies with article L of
this chapter. (Ord. 2-2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-3: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Uniform Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to
use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the R-4 zone must certify, under oath, that
the building, structure or improvement will conform to the uniform building
code as adopted. An improvement which does not comply with the uniform building
code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures which are to be located in the
R-4 zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building and not on jacks or in
the center of the structure. All foundations must meet uniform building code
standards. (Ord. 2-2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-4: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
Each dwelling unit in the R-4 zone shall have a minimum size of seven hundred
(700) square feet, exclusive of one-story open porches and garages. (Ord. 2-
2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-5: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-4 zone shall be ten thousand
(10,000) square feet. An additional one thousand (1,000) square feet shall be
added to the minimum lot size for every dwelling unit above four (4) dwelling
units, located on the lot.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot width in the R-4 zone shall be sixty
feet (60') for interior lots. Corner lots must be large enough to accommodate
setback and yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the R-4 zone shall be
on an adequately improved lot. (Ord. 2-2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-6: HEIGHT LIMIT AND CONSTRUCTION:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4N-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-4 zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-4 zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no
structures located in a required front yard or in a required side yard abutting
a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted to dismantle, repair, or keep
any inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor side yard abutting a street or
driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: There shall be a side yard on each side of the lot,
extending from the front yard, of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides of
an interior lot. A corner lot shall have a side yard abutting a street of not
less than twelve feet (12') and not less than ten feet (10') on the opposite
side yard.
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10').
      4.   Multiple Dwelling Buildings: When multiple dwelling buildings are on
one lot, at least ten feet (10') shall be between each building. (Ord. 2-2005,
6-2-2005)
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings and uses shall be permitted
only to the extent necessary and normal to the limited types of uses permitted
in this zone. Accessory buildings are not to be used for residential purposes.
All accessory buildings which are not a part of the main building shall be
separated from the main building by at least three feet (3').
      ACCESSORY BUILDING SETBACK REQUIREMENTS IN FEET
Portable Accessory Buildings (Easily Moved By Sliding)
Building    Front Side Yard Side Yard  Rear Yard
Square Feet                 Corner Lot
Portable Accessory Buildings (Easily Moved By Sliding)
Building    Front Side Yard Side Yard  Rear Yard
Square Feet                 Corner Lot
0 - 120     201   1         12         1
121 - 250   201   3         12         3
Permanent Accessory Buildings
With Foundation Or Concrete Floor
Building    Front Side Yard Side Yard  Rear Yard
Square Feet                 Corner Lot
0 - 120     201   10        12         10
 
   Note:
      1.    No accessory building may encroach into the front yard beyond the
main structure.
Yard intrusions as provided in section
12-7-5 of this title shall not be considered to apply to accessory buildings of
two hundred (200) square feet or less and portable in nature in residential
zones. (Ord. 2014-01, 4-3-2014)
12-4N-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
12-4N-9: OFF STREET PARKING:
For off street parking requirements in the R-4 zone, see chapter 8 of this
title. (Ord. 2-2005, 6-2-2005)
12-4N-10: SIGNS:
For sign requirements in the R-4 zone, see chapter 9 of this title. (Ord. 2-
2005, 6-2-2005)
ARTICLE O. D ZONE
SECTION:
12-4O-1: Purpose
12-4O-2: Permitted Uses
12-4O-3: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4O-4: Minimum Floor Area
12-4O-5: Lot Requirements
12-4O-6: Height Limit And Construction
12-4O-7: Setbacks
12-4O-8: Fences And Walls
12-4O-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a high density residential area with duplexes,
townhouses and other multiple dwellings, without common areas, within one
building. (Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the D zone.
No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered, or enlarged
or land used except for the following purposes:
Accessory buildings.
Gardens for personal use.
Multiple residences contained within one building without common areas with
separate and individual entrances and exits. (Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-3: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   International Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring
to use a lot for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a
building permit for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All
applicants for building permits for the D zone must certify, under oath, that
the building, structure or improvement will conform to the international
building code as adopted. An improvement that does not comply with the
international building code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures that are to be located in the D
zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building or at the outer perimeter
of each individual dwelling and not on jacks or in any other place within the
building. All foundations must meet international building code standards.
(Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-4: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
Each dwelling unit in the D zone shall have a minimum size of five hundred
seventy five (575) square feet exclusive of one-story open porches and garages.
(Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-5: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the D zone shall be one thousand two
hundred feet (1,200').
   B.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the D zone shall be on
an adequately improved lot. (Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-6: HEIGHT LIMIT AND CONSTRUCTION:
The maximum building height for the dwelling structure (including attached
garage) shall be thirty five feet (35'). The maximum building height for an
accessory building shall be no more than twenty two feet (22'). Building height
is measured from the lowest point of the floor of the structure. The roof pitch
of all buildings over three hundred (300) square feet shall be no less than a
four inch (4") rise to a twelve inch (12") run. (Ord. 2009-10, 10-15-2009)
12-4O-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the D zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the D zone shall have a front yard extending
across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less than twenty
feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no structures located
in the required front yard or in a required side yard abutting a street (corner
lot). It shall not be permitted to keep any inoperative vehicle in the front
yard or side yard abutting a street or driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: When multiple dwellings are contained within one
building, there shall be no required side yard between dwellings. Each
building, however, shall have a side yard on each side of the building
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides. If
the building is on a corner wherein two (2) streets meet, the lot adjacent to
the meeting streets shall have a side yard abutting the street of not less than
twelve feet (12').
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10').
      4.   Multiple Dwelling With One Owner: Each dwelling shall be contained
on a separate lot, even if an individual owner has ownership of multiple
dwellings.
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings shall be regulated pursuant to
subsection 12-4N-7B of this chapter. (Ord. 2007-16, 10-4-2007)
12-4O-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet four inches (6'4") in height, the
height of the flat vertical plane of which shall not exceed six feet (6'), and
where any portion of the same is located within the front yard setback, said
portion shall not exceed forty inches (40"), the height of the flat vertical
plane of which shall not exceed thirty six inches (36"), if said portion is
opaque, and fifty two inches (52"), the height of the flat vertical plane of
which shall not exceed forty eight inches (48"), if said fence is not opaque.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire, unless
the fence borders an agricultural zone established by the town or county.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be lower than six feet (6') above the ground.
   C.   Electric Fences: Electric fences are prohibited.
   D.   Finished Side: Fences having a finished side must be oriented with the
finished side to the street and adjacent lots. If two (2) property owners
jointly construct a fence, the owners may jointly determine on which side to
orient the finished side. (Ord. 2008-17, 8-21-2008)
ARTICLE P. R-S ZONE
SECTION:
12-4P-1: Purpose
12-4P-2: Permitted Uses
12-4P-3: Building Code Certification; Foundations
12-4P-4: Minimum Floor Area
12-4P-5: Lot Requirements
12-4P-6: Height Limit
12-4P-7: Setbacks
12-4P-8: Fences And Walls
12-4P-1: PURPOSE:
This zone is intended as a residential area with stick built single-family
dwellings. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-2: PERMITTED USES:
Only the following buildings, structures and uses are permitted in the R-
S zone. No buildings or structures shall be erected, structurally altered, or
enlarged or land used except for the following purposes:
   Accessory buildings.
   Churches.
   Educational institutions.
   Gardens for personal use.
   Golf courses.
   Public parks, playgrounds and athletic fields.
   Rest and convalescent homes.
Single-family residences wholly constructed in place. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-3: BUILDING CODE CERTIFICATION; FOUNDATIONS:
   A.   Building Code Certification Required: Any person desiring to use a lot
for a permitted or conditionally permitted use must acquire a building permit
for any and all buildings or improvements to the land. All applicants for
building permits for the R-S zone must certify, under oath, that the building,
structure or improvement will conform to the building code currently adopted by
the town of Lyman. An improvement that does not comply with the said building
code will not be permitted.
   B.   Foundations: All residential structures that are to be located in the
R-S zone must be placed on a permanent foundation on which the weight or load
bearing is around the outer perimeter of the building or at the outer perimeter
of each individual dwelling and not on jacks or in any other place within the
building. All foundations must meet said building code standards.
   C.   Stick Built Only: All residential structures that are to be located in
the R-S zone must be new and fully constructed on site. No manufactured,
component or modular home may be placed in an R-S zone. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-
2008)
12-4P-4: MINIMUM FLOOR AREA:
The ground floor area of the main structure in the R-S zone, exclusive of one-
story open porches and garages, shall not be less than one thousand two hundred
(1,200) square feet for one dwelling, nor less than one thousand (1,000) square
feet for a dwelling of more than one story. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-5: LOT REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Lot Area: The minimum lot area in the R-S zone shall be seven thousand
(7,000) square feet.
   B.   Lot Dimensions: The minimum lot width in the R-S zone is seventy feet
(70') for interior lots. Corner lots must be large enough to accommodate
setback and side yard requirements.
   C.   Building Site: The building site for any use in the R-S zone shall be
on an adequately improved lot. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-6: HEIGHT LIMIT:
The maximum building or structural height of the main buildings in the R-S zone
shall be two and one-half (21/2) stories, or thirty five feet (35'). The
maximum building or structural height of accessory buildings shall be one story
or eighteen feet (18'). (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-7: SETBACKS:
Setback requirements in the R-S zone are as follows:
   A.   Main Structure:
      1.   Front Yard: Each lot in the R-S zone shall have a front yard
extending across the full width of the subject property, a depth of not less
than twenty feet (20'). Except for drives and walks, there shall be no
structures located in the required front yard or in a required side yard
abutting a street (corner lot). It shall not be permitted to keep any
inoperative vehicle in this front yard nor side yard abutting a street or
driveway.
      2.   Side Yard: When multiple dwellings are contained within one
building, there shall be no required side yard between dwellings. Each
building, however, shall have a side yard on each side of the building
extending from the front yard of not less than ten feet (10') on both sides. If
the building is on a corner wherein two (2) streets meet, the lot adjacent to
the meeting streets shall have a side yard abutting the street of not less than
twelve feet (12').
      3.   Rear Yard: Each lot shall have a rear yard the full width of the lot
of a depth not less than ten feet (10').
      4.   Multiple Dwellings With One Owner: Each dwelling shall be contained
on a separate lot, even if an individual owner has ownership of multiple
dwellings.
   B.   Accessory Buildings: Accessory buildings shall be regulated pursuant to
subsection 12-4B-8B of this chapter. (Ord. 2008-14, 6-19-2008)
12-4P-8: FENCES AND WALLS:
   A.   Maximum Height: Fences and walls are permitted but not required. Such
fences and walls shall not exceed six feet (6') in height and where the same is
located in the required front yard or side yard abutting a street, the same
shall not exceed forty eight inches (48") in height or less if necessary to
provide an unobstructed view of oncoming traffic.
   B.   Barbed Wire; Chainlink: Fences shall not be made of barbed wire.
However, when special conditions warrant, and when approved by the planning and
zoning commission, security fences may be constructed of chainlink with not
more than three (3) strands of barbed wire on the top of the chainlink. In no
case will barbed wire be closer than six feet (6') above the ground. (Ord.
2008-14, 6-19-2008)
CHAPTER 5
SEXUALLY ORIENTED BUSINESSES
SECTION:
12-5-1: Purpose; Intent
12-5-2: Definitions
12-5-3: Classification
12-5-4: Zoning; Spacing
12-5-5: Operation Standards
12-5-6: Viewing Room Restrictions
12-5-7: Nude Model Studios
12-5-8: Public Nudity
12-5-9: Adult Theaters And Adult Cabarets
12-5-10: Minors
12-5-11: Hours Of Operation
12-5-12: Affirmative Defense
12-5-13: Advertising
12-5-14: Territorial Jurisdiction
12-5-15: Penalty
12-5-1: PURPOSE; INTENT:
   A.   Purpose: It is the purpose of this chapter to regulate sexually
oriented businesses in order to promote the health, safety, morals, and general
welfare of the citizens of the town, and to establish reasonable and uniform
regulations to prevent the deleterious location and concentration of sexually
oriented businesses within the town.
   B.   Intent: The provisions of this chapter have neither the purpose nor
effect of imposing a limitation or restriction on the content of any
communicative materials, including sexually oriented materials. Similarly, it
is not the intent nor effect of this chapter to restrict or deny access by
adults to sexually oriented materials protected by the first amendment, or to
deny access by the distributors and exhibitors of sexually oriented
entertainment to their intended market. Neither is it the intent nor effect of
this chapter to condone or legitimize the distribution of obscene material.
(Ord. 9-99, 1-5-2000)
12-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ADULT ARCADE: Any place to which the public is permitted or invited wherein
coin operated, slug operated or for any form of consideration, electronically,
electrically, or mechanically controlled still or motion picture machines,
projectors, video or laser disc players, or other image producing devices are
maintained to show images to five (5) or fewer persons per machine at any one
time, and where the images so displayed are distinguished or characterized by
the depicting or describing of specified sexual activities or specified
anatomical areas.
ADULT BOOKSTORE, ADULT NOVELTY STORE OR ADULT VIDEO STORE:
   A.   A commercial establishment which devotes a significant or substantial
portion of its stock in trade or interior floor space to, or devotes a
significant or substantial portion of its advertising expenditures to, the
promotion of the sale, rental or viewing, for any form of consideration any one
or more of the following:
      1.   Books, magazines, periodicals or other printed matter, or
