   B.   Americans With Disabilities Act Compliance. All off-street parking
areas must comply with the Americans with Disabilities Act Accessible Parking
Spaces regulations. Each parking area must have a minimum of one marked
accessible ADA compliant space for every twenty-five (25) parking spaces, with
a minimum of one such space. These spaces must be located on the shortest
accessible route to the accessible entrance. An accessible route is the path a
person with a disability takes to enter and move through a building or
facility. Accessible parking spaces must have access aisles. Access aisles
provide a designated area for people who use wheelchairs or other mobility
devices to get in and out of their car or van.
(1987 Code § 17.56.030; amd. Ord. 2025-01, 4-7-2025)
CHAPTER 9
SIGNS
SECTION:
12-9-1: Purpose
12-9-2: Definitions
12-9-3: Exemptions
12-9-4: Exterior Sign Permit; Fee
12-9-5: Height Generally
12-9-6: Portable Or Temporary Signs
12-9-7: Sign Interference With Traffic
12-9-8: Flashing, Blinking Or Animated Signs
12-9-9: Projection Of Signs
12-9-10: Abandoned, Dilapidated And Unsafe Signs
12-9-11: Residential Zones
12-9-12: Agricultural, Commercial And Industrial Zones
12-9-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to provide a reasonable system for control of
signs:
   A.   To encourage signs which are well designed and pleasing in appearance.
   B.   To provide a reasonable system of control of signs and to integrate
within the comprehensive zoning plan.
   C.   To attract and direct persons to various activities and enterprises in
order to provide for maximum public convenience.
   D.   To encourage signs which are compatible with adjacent land uses. (1987
Code § 17.60.010)
12-9-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this section:
ABANDONED SIGN: One which has apparently served its purpose and has no apparent
use or value to its originator or owner.
AREA OF SIGN: Means, and shall be computed as, the entire area within the
exterior boundary of the structure, the perimeter of which shall not be in
excess of eight (8) straight lines. A sign designed with more than one exterior
surface shall have its area computed as including only the maximum single
display surface which is visible from any ground position. The supports,
uprights or structures on which any sign is supported shall not be included in
determining the sign area, unless such supports, uprights or structures are so
designed to form an integral background of the display.
DILAPIDATED SIGN: One which creates an eyesore, needing maintenance, repair or
paint.
FLASHING, ANIMATED OR MOVING SIGN: A sign that intermittently emits or reflects
artificial or natural light, a sign which has movement of any illumination such
as intermittent flashing or varied intensity, or a sign that has any visible
portion in motion.
FREESTANDING OR POLE SIGN: A sign supported by one or more uprights, poles or
braces in or upon the ground, with a clear space of not less than ten feet
(10') between the bottom of the sign and the natural terrain above which the
sign is located. This definition shall not include portable signs.
FRONTAGE: That portion of the property facing and running more or less parallel
to and along a public street or highway right of way.
GROUND SIGN: A sign supported by uprights, poles or braces anchored in the
ground and not attached to any building, with a clearance space of more than
ten feet (10') between the bottom of the face of the sign and the natural
ground level. This definition shall not include portable signs.
OFF PREMISES SIGN: A sign which is located on property separate and apart from
the property on which the advertised activity is carried out.
ON PREMISES SIGN: A sign which is located on the property for the purpose of
advertising its sale or lease, or for advertising an activity conducted on the
property or for advertising a product sold on the property.
OUTDOOR ADVERTISING STRUCTURE: Any outdoor sign, display, light, device,
figure, painting, drawing, message, plaque, poster, billboard or any other
thing which is designed, intended or used to advertise or inform.
PORTABLE TEMPORARY SIGN: A sign, without independent structural support, in
connection with political, school, civic, noncommercial, health, safety, and
welfare campaigns or events provided that in all districts such posters shall
be removed within fifteen (15) days following the conclusion of the campaign or
event.
REAL ESTATE SIGN: A sign placed upon a property advertising that property for
sale, for rent, or for lease.
REAL ESTATE SUBDIVISION SIGN: A sign placed on the premises of a subdivision or
other real estate development.
ROOF SIGN: A sign erected upon the roof of a building or structure.
SIGN: Shall be construed as synonymous with "outdoor advertising structure" as
defined herein.
UNSAFE SIGN AND SUPPORTING STRUCTURE: One which, by reason of the elements,
wear and tear, or having been damaged by a vehicle, projectile or other moving
thing or object, has loose metal or wood parts, or steel structure, loose neon
tubing or lamps, dangling electrical or guy wire, or which obviously needs
repair.
WALL SIGN: A sign attached to or painted on, or erected against a wall of a
building or structure with the exposed face of the sign in a plane
approximately parallel to the plane of the wall. (1987 Code § 17.60.020; amd.
Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
12-9-3: EXEMPTIONS:
Nothing in this chapter shall prevent the erection, construction and
maintenance of the following types of signs:
   A.   Official traffic, fire and police signs, signals, devices and markings
of the state highway department, the county, and other competent public
authorities, nor the posting of notices required by law or signs required by a
public utility for purposes of identification or safety.
   B.   Temporary signs, including political and election issue signs, of no
more than twelve (12) square feet on the property of the person or entity
placing the sign, or on the sidewalk and/or greenspace immediately adjacent to
the property, so long as such signs do not interfere with pedestrian or
vehicular traffic.
   C.   Political and/or election issue signs, up to and including forty-eight
square feet, for one hundred and eighty (180) days prior to the subject
election so long as said signs:
      1.   Are not in a Residential Zone of the Town;
      2.   Are placed with the express consent of the property owner;
      3.   Do not interfere with traffic sight lines or are otherwise
constructed or placed in a way as to present a danger to the community's
safety;
      4.   Such signs shall be removed within fourteen (14) days after the
conclusion of the election for which the candidate or issue was decided.
   D.   Event promotion signs for one hundred and eighty (180) days prior to
the advertised event so long as said signs:
      1.   Are not in a Residential Zone of the Town;
      2.   Are placed with the express consent of the property owner;
      3.   Do not interfere with traffic sight lines or are otherwise
constructed or placed in a way as to present a danger to the community's
safety;
      4.   Such signs shall be removed within fourteen (14) days after the
conclusion of the advertised event. (1987 Code § 17.60.030; amd. Ord. 2021-01,
5-6-2021)
12-9-4: EXTERIOR SIGN PERMIT; FEE:
No exterior sign shall be erected, attached or displayed until a written
application has been made to the planning and zoning commission, and a permit
duly issued. The fee for such permit shall be as set by resolution of the town
council. (1987 Code § 17.60.040)
12-9-5: HEIGHT GENERALLY:
No sign shall be permitted to exceed thirty five feet (35') in height, except
where a conditional use permit is granted. (1987 Code § 17.60.050)
12-9-6: PORTABLE OR TEMPORARY SIGNS:
Persons or organizations desiring to place such signs in any district in the
town, other than those exempted under Ordinance
12-9-3, herein shall first, before such placement commences, apply for a permit
to do so, and may be required to post a bond in addition to the permit fee, to
ensure complete removal of such temporary sign within a period of fifteen (15)
days following the conclusion of the campaign or event. (1987 Code § 17.60.060;
amd. Ord. 2021-01, 5-6-2021)
12-9-7: SIGN INTERFERENCE WITH TRAFFIC:
   A.   No sign may encroach on or hang over the highway right of way.
   B.   No sign may be lighted so it impairs the vision of any motor vehicle
driver.
   C.   No sign may obstruct the view of any road to the extent it makes it
dangerous to use the road.
   D.   No sign may obscure or physically interfere with an official traffic
control sign, signal or device. (1987 Code § 17.60.070; amd. Ord. 2021-01, 5-6-
2021)
12-9-8: FLASHING, BLINKING OR ANIMATED SIGNS:
No sign shall contain components which alternately flash, blink, or rotate in a
rapid manner so as to be similar, both as to color and motion, to any emergency
vehicle, traffic control device or signal. Rotating signs shall be limited to
eight (8) revolutions per minute. (1987 Code § 17.60.080)
12-9-9: PROJECTION OF SIGNS:
   A.   Location; Specifications: No projecting sign shall substantially hide
or obscure another sign as viewed from the least favorable lane of traffic. A
sign so projecting shall not be less than eight feet (8') above the sidewalk
and may project not more than ten feet (10') from the front of the building,
and not closer than two feet (2') to the curb or intended curb line.
   B.   Single Faced Or Flat Signs: Single faced or flat signs or wall signs
may extend over a public sidewalk not more than twelve inches (12").
   C.   Nonconforming Signs: Signs not meeting the provisions of this title in
place on the effective date hereof shall be considered nonconforming. It is the
intent of this chapter to eliminate sign eyesores and to restrict the
proliferation of projecting signs in dense commercial areas.
   D.   Spacing Formula: The planning and zoning commission and the town
council reserve the right to institute a spacing formula for such commercial
areas requiring projecting signs to be placed no closer than forty feet (40')
or fifty feet (50') or whatever spacing best serves the public interest. (1987
Code § 17.60.090)
12-9-10: ABANDONED, DILAPIDATED AND UNSAFE SIGNS:
Abandoned, dilapidated or unsafe signs and supporting structures are to be
removed if not corrected within thirty (30) days after written notice from the
town to the owner of the property on which the sign is installed. Costs of
removal will become a lien against the property if not paid within thirty (30)
days. (1987 Code § 17.60.100)
12-9-11: RESIDENTIAL ZONES:
No sign in a residential zone shall exceed twelve (12) square feet in area
without a conditional use permit. (Ord. 2011-15, 1-5-2012)
12-9-12: AGRICULTURAL, COMMERCIAL AND INDUSTRIAL ZONES:
In agricultural, commercial and industrial zones:
   A.   Off Site Advertising Signs: Off site advertising signs shall be placed
or erected not less than five hundred feet (500') apart and shall not be
erected adjacent to and parallel with another sign.
   B.   On Site Business Signs: On site business signs for any one building
shall not exceed one-third (1/3) of the total square footage of the building
front, including fascia and wall.
   C.   Roof Signs: No roof sign or supporting structure shall extend above the
roofline or fascia more than thirty three and one-third percent (331/3%) of the
height of the building which supports it, and shall not exceed one hundred
(100) square feet per one hundred feet (100').
   D.   Trade Construction Signs: Trade construction signs shall not exceed
thirty two (32) square feet in area, shall not be installed prior to start of
construction, and shall be removed prior to occupancy of the building. (1987
Code § 17.60.120; amd. Ord. 2020-01, 6-4-2020)
CHAPTER 10
NONCONFORMING LOTS, BUILDINGS AND USES
SECTION:
12-10-1: Uses
12-10-2: Repairs And Maintenance
12-10-3: Buildings And Structures
12-10-4: Use Removal
12-10-5: Signs And Billboards
12-10-6: Fences, Hedges And Walls
12-10-7: Mobile Home Park Improvements
12-10-1: USES:
If the use of a building, structure or land exists on the effective date
hereof, and such a use is not allowed in the district under the terms of this
title, the use may be continued so long as it remains otherwise lawful, subject
to the following provisions:
   A.   Enlarged, Extended, Constructed, Reconstructed: Unless a conditional
use permit is granted, no existing building or structure devoted to a use not
permitted in the district in which it is located shall be enlarged, extended,
constructed, reconstructed, moved or structurally altered except in changing
the use of the structure to a use permitted in the district in which it is
located. (Ord. 2007-8, 5-1-2007)
   B.   Reconstruction: An existing residential building or structure in a
commercial (C), light industrial (L-I) or heavy industrial (H-I) zone shall be
allowed to be rebuilt at the same location so long as the reconstructed
building or structure receives proper building permits and conforms to all
other requirements of this code. Such reconstructed residential building shall
conform with all standards, including setbacks, inspections and codes as if
said residence was constructed in an R-1 zone. (Ord. 2013-06, 1-16-2014)
   C.   Extension Outside Building: Any nonconforming use may be extended
through any part of a building which was arranged or designed for such use at
the time of adoption or amendment of this title, but no such use shall be
extended to occupy any land outside such building.
   D.   Changed To Another Nonconforming Use: A nonconforming use may not be
changed to another nonconforming use.
   E.   Superseded By Permitted Use: Any building, structure or land use, in or
on which a nonconforming use is superseded by a permitted use, shall thereafter
conform to the regulations for the district in which it is located and the
nonconforming use may not thereafter be resumed.
   F.   Discontinued Or Abandoned: When a nonconforming use is discontinued or
abandoned for ninety (90) consecutive calendar days, the building, structure or
land shall thereafter only be used in conformance with the regulations of the
district in which it is located. (Ord. 2007-8, 5-1-2007)
12-10-2: REPAIRS AND MAINTENANCE:
   A.   Strengthening Or Restoring To Safe Condition: Nothing in this chapter
shall be deemed to prevent the strengthening or restoring to a safe condition
of any building or part thereof declared to be unsafe by an official charged
with protecting the public safety, but in no event shall such repair or
maintenance prolong the time within which the nonconforming use thereof must
terminate.
   B.   Ordinary Repairs; Extent Of Repairs: On any building devoted in whole
or in part to any nonconforming use, work may be done in any period of twelve
(12) consecutive months on ordinary repairs, or on repair or replacement of
nonbearing walls, fixtures, wiring or plumbing, to an extent not exceeding
fifty percent (50%) of the replacement value of the building or structure;
provided, that the cubic content of the building or structure is not increased
from the size which existed on the effective date hereof. (1987 Code §
17.64.020)
12-10-3: BUILDINGS AND STRUCTURES:
   A.   Removed Or Destroyed: Except as provided for in subsections B and C of
this section, if any nonconforming building or structure in any district
established by this chapter is removed or destroyed voluntarily or
involuntarily, every building, structure or use occupying the premises thereof
shall conform to the regulations of the district in which it is located.
   B.   Damage In Excess Of Sixty Percent: Whenever, in any district, a
nonconforming building or structure is damaged or destroyed by fire or a
calamity other than natural deterioration in excess of sixty percent (60%) of
the replacement value of the building or structure, the building, structure or
use which existed at the time of the destruction may be restored to its
original condition; provided, however, that the restoration must be commenced
within a period of six (6) months from the date of such damage or destruction
and be diligently prosecuted to completion. The planning and zoning commission
may, upon a written request of the applicant, extend the period six (6) months,
but not in excess of twelve (12) months from the date of the damage or
destruction.
   C.   Damage Under Sixty Percent: In the event of such damage or destruction,
by any means, of sixty percent (60%) or less of the replacement value of the
building or structure, only the building structure or use which existed at the
time of partial destruction may be restored and continued; provided, however,
if such restoration is started within a period of six (6) months from the date
of such damage or destruction and is diligently prosecuted to completion. The
planning and zoning commission may, upon a written request of the applicant,
extend the period of six (6) months, but not in excess of twelve (12) months
from the date of damage or destruction. (1987 Code § 17.64.030)
12-10-4: USE REMOVAL:
If the planning and zoning commission determines that the continuance of a
nonconforming use is detrimental to the health, safety or welfare of the
neighborhood, such nonconforming use shall be completely removed or converted
to a conforming use within the time prescribed by the town council. The
planning and zoning commission shall conduct public hearings on the
nonconforming use and set forth an amortization period for its continuance of
not less than six (6) months nor more than one year, depending on the impact of
the use on the neighborhood. The town council shall approve or deny the
amortization period. The planning commission shall then grant a conditional use
permit subject to the procedures set forth in chapter 12 of this title. (1987
Code § 17.64.040)
12-10-5: SIGNS AND BILLBOARDS:
   A.   Existing Signs Or Billboards: On an off site business, signs or
billboards which do not conform to this title, but which lawfully existed and
were properly maintained and kept in good repair on the effective date hereof
shall be permitted to remain as nonconforming signs until such time as:
      1.   The sign becomes dilapidated and run down, creating an eyesore.
      2.   A business name change occurs.
      3.   Extensive remodeling of the sign or structure in excess of seventy
five percent (75%) of the original estimated value of the sign or structure.
   B.   Attention Getting Devices: Attention getting devices which, in the
opinion of the planning and zoning commission, are not in keeping with the
spirit of this title, and all signs with certain components which alternately
flash, blink or rotate in a rapid manner, so as to be similar as to color and
motion to flashing, blinking or rotating of any lights on an emergency vehicle
or traffic control device or signal shall be made to conform within one year of
the effective date hereof. (1987 Code § 17.64.050)
12-10-6: FENCES, HEDGES AND WALLS:
In instances where fences, hedges and walls which do not conform to the corner
cutback provisions of this title exist, the landowner, lessee or tenant shall
be allowed thirty (30) days from the date of delivery of written notice to
remove the nonconformance. (1987 Code § 17.64.060)
12-10-7: MOBILE HOME PARK IMPROVEMENTS:
An owner of a mobile home park in a nonconforming zone may make improvements,
repairs, replacements, additions, enlargements and modifications to the mobile
home park, including utility services which improve the overall appearance and/
or life of the park. (Ord. 6-93, 10-7-1993)
CHAPTER 11
VARIANCES
SECTION:
12-11-1: Purpose; Authority Of Planning And Zoning Commission
12-11-2: Application; Fee
12-11-3: Hearing; Requirements
12-11-4: Conditions
12-11-5: Appeal
12-11-6: Revocation Or Modification
12-11-1: PURPOSE; AUTHORITY OF PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION:
When practical difficulties, unnecessary hardships or results inconsistent with
the general intent and purpose of this title occur through the strict
application of the provisions of this title to the parcel or group of parcels
affected by a common problem, the planning and zoning commission shall have the
power to grant, upon such terms and conditions as it deems necessary and proper
as may be in harmony with its general intent and purpose, so that the spirit of
the title is observed, public safety and general welfare secured, and
substantial justice done, variances as to the use provisions of this title.
(1987 Code § 17.68.010)
12-11-2: APPLICATION; FEE:
   A.   Application:
      1.   Form: Application for variances shall be filed by the owner or his
authorized agent upon forms provided by the planning and zoning commission.
      2.   Required Information: The application shall set forth and state
fully the reasons and grounds for the variance and shall contain such
information as the planning and zoning commission shall prescribe. Accompanying
the application shall be the following:
         a.   A map showing the property described in the application and
adjoining properties and public streets and ways within a radius of three
hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries.
         b.   A list of all property owners whose names and addresses appear on
the latest adopted tax roll as owning property within a distance of three
hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries.
         c.   Photographs, drawings and other supporting documents as may be
required by the planning and zoning commission.
   B.   Filing Fee: Before accepting an application for a variance, the
planning and zoning commission shall charge and collect a filing fee. Such fee
shall be established by a resolution of the town council. (1987 Code §
17.68.020)
12-11-3: HEARING; REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   Notice Of Hearing: The planning and zoning commission shall hold a
public hearing upon the application for a variance. Written notices concerning
hearings on applications for variances shall be mailed to the owners of
property and occupants of the property within a distance of three hundred feet
(300') of the exterior boundaries not less than seven (7) days before the date
of the public hearing. A public notice shall be printed in the official
newspaper at least three (3) days prior to the hearing. The notice shall set
forth the person requesting the variance, the legal description of the
property, the street address, if applicable, any other pertinent information,
and the date, time and place of the public hearing.
   B.   Criteria For Approval: Before it may grant a variance, the following
qualifications must be shown relative to the property or properties involved in
the application for such variance, and the planning commission's approval in
connection with any such application shall contain written findings of fact
showing wherein the following conditions exist, that:
      1.   Because of the special circumstances or unusual hardships applicable
to the subject property, including size, shape, topography, location or
surroundings, the strict application of this title is found to deprive the
subject property of privileges enjoyed by other properties in the vicinity and
under identical zone classifications.
      2.   Publication: A public notice shall be printed in the official town
newspaper at least three (3) days prior to the hearing.
      3.   The granting of the variance will not be materially detrimental to
the public welfare or injurious to property and improvements in the zone and
vicinity in which the property is located.
      4.   The granting of the variance will not adversely affect the
comprehensive general plan.
      5.   An on site inspection shall have been made by the commission or its
authorized representative.
   C.   Grant/Denial: From the facts presented with the application at the
public hearing, the planning and zoning commission may grant the requested
variance in whole or in part. If the findings cannot be made, such application
shall be denied.
   D.   Vote Required: Every action or decision of the planning and zoning
commission authorizing a variance from the regulations established in this
title shall be adopted by an affirmative vote of not less than a majority of
the members attending and voting at a meeting of the planning and zoning
commission at which there is a quorum present, setting forth the written
findings of fact required by subsection B of this section. (1987 Code §
17.68.030; amd. Ord. 2019-12, 12-19-2019)
12-11-4: CONDITIONS:
   A.   Terms And Conditions: The planning and zoning commission, in approving
a variance, may set forth in its decision reasonable terms and conditions which
it deems necessary to protect the health, safety and welfare of the community
and to assure the intent and purpose of this title. It may also require that
such terms and conditions are being or will be complied with.
   B.   Term Of Variance: Every variance from the provisions of this title
granted by the planning and zoning commission as authorized by this chapter
shall contain a condition thereof, as follows:
The variance hereby allowed is conditioned upon the privileges herein being
utilized within one hundred eighty (180) days after the effective date hereof,
and should the privileges authorized hereby fail to be executed or utilized or
where some form of construction has not actually commenced within such one
hundred eighty (180) days, and is not diligently prosecuted to completion, this
authority shall become null and void and any privilege or variance granted
hereby shall lapse unless such variance has not been utilized within such one
hundred eighty (180) day period by reason of delays caused by approval of
plans, in which event the planning and zoning commission may, in its discretion
and with the consent or upon the request of the applicant, for any cause, grant
a reasonable extension of time to the one hundred eighty (180) day time limit
noted above.
   (1987 Code § 17.68.040)
12-11-5: APPEAL:
   A.   Right To Appeal: Written appeals may be reviewed by the town council
for the applicant for the variance or for any person owning property within
three hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries of the variance
applicant's property aggrieved by any determination for variance, or upon
failure of the planning and zoning commission to make its determination on any
application by or at the next regular monthly planning and zoning commission
meeting.
   B.   Hearing: The town council shall hold a public hearing as required by
Wyoming Statutes.
   C.   Board Of Adjustment: The town council shall perform all duties formerly
allocated to the board of adjustment under this code. (1987 Code § 17.68.050)
12-11-6: REVOCATION OR MODIFICATION:
   A.   Grounds For Revocation Or Modification: A variance may be revoked or
modified by the town council, after a public hearing, on any one or more of the
following grounds:
      1.   Approval was obtained by fraud.
      2.   The use for which such approval was granted is not being exercised
within the time specified in such permit.
      3.   The use for which such approval was granted has ceased to exist or
has been suspended for one year or more.
      4.   The permit granted is being, or recently has been, exercised
contrary to the terms or conditions of such approval, or in violation of any
statute, resolution, law or regulation.
      5.   The use for which such approval was granted has been so exercised as
to be detrimental to the public health or safety, or so as to constitute a
nuisance.
   B.   Notice Of Intent To Revoke: Written notices of intention to revoke
shall be mailed to the owners of the property and the occupants of property not
less than fifteen (15) days before the date of the public hearing.
   C.   Appeal: In the event of the revocation by the town council, the
applicant may appeal in the same manner as an appeal from a denial of a
variance in the first instance. (1987 Code § 17.68.060)
CHAPTER 12
CONDITIONAL USE PERMITS
SECTION:
12-12-1: Generally
12-12-2: When Required
12-12-3: Home Occupations
12-12-4: Multiple Animal Permits
12-12-5: Inoperable Motor Vehicles
12-12-6: Gaming
12-12-7: Application; Fee
12-12-8: Hearing
12-12-9: Findings For Approval
12-12-10: Appeals
12-12-11: Revocation Or Modification
12-12-12: Modification Of Approved Structures
12-12-1: GENERALLY:
   A.   Generally: Uses permitted subject to conditional use permits are those
uses necessary for the development of the community, but which uses must be
located, planned and used in such manner as not to be detrimental to the
property abutting such uses and to the community as a whole. In considering a
conditional use permit, the planning and zoning commission shall determine
whether the use is suitable in the area and, if the grant is made, shall
require safeguards necessary to protect the health, safety, morals, order,
convenience and general welfare. In approving such uses, the planning and
zoning commission shall set forth the manner in which the use is to be
conducted, approve the design or plan of the structures, including their
locations and the yards around them, and consider the adequacy of facilities to
serve them. In granting a conditional use permit, the planning and zoning
commission may grant deviations or relief from the yard, fence, sign, height,
parking, loading and open space regulations of this title. (1987 Code §
17.72.010)
   B.   Petition For Zone Change Or Newly Annexed Territory: In the event a
conditional use is proposed in connection with a petition for a zone change or
newly annexed territory, the application for the conditional use shall
accompany the petition. In the event the petition for the zone change or
annexation is required to be considered by the planning and zoning commission
prior to council consideration, the commission may recommend reasonable
conditions be attached to any recommended approval. The commission and council
shall consider the same criteria and make the findings required in the same
manner as those set forth in this chapter.
   C.   Term: In any case in which a conditional use permit has not been
exercised within one year from the date of issuance, such permit shall be void
and have no further force or effect. "Exercise" as used in this section, shall
mean that the holder of the permit has: 1) obtained all necessary building
permits; and 2) executed a binding contract for the construction of the
principal building or other improvement or, in the absence of contracts, that
the principal building or other improvement is under construction to a
substantial degree. When construction is not a part of the conditional use
permit, "exercise" shall mean that the use is operating in compliance with
conditions as designated in the permit. (Ord. 6-94, 10-24-1994)
12-12-2: WHEN REQUIRED:
Uses requiring special use permits are set forth in this title, except that
wherever not specifically referred to, public service uses, including radio or
television transmitters, structures necessary for public utilities, cemeteries
and airports may be located in each zone with a conditional use permit. (1987
Code § 17.72.020)
12-12-3: HOME OCCUPATIONS:
   A.   Permits Required: "Home occupations" or small "home businesses", as
defined in section
12-2-1 of this title, are permitted in any residential zone; provided, that a
conditional use permit as set forth in this chapter and a business permit as
set forth in title 3 of this code are first obtained.
   B.   Specific Conditions: In addition to the general conditions of a
conditional use permit and any special conditions that may be imposed by the
planning and zoning commission, the following specific conditions shall also
apply:
      1.   Not more than one-half (1/2) of one floor shall be used for an
occupation if the occupation is conducted in a family residence.
      2.   An occupation may be conducted in an accessory building if first
approved by the planning and zoning commission.
      3.   No goods, products or manufactured items associated with the home
occupation shall be attached, displayed or stored outside of any buildings or
structures located on the premises or general area. Goods, products or
manufactured items shall be confined to the building or buildings in which an
occupation or home business is being conducted.
      4.   For sign requirements in conjunction with a home occupation or small
business, see section
12-9-11 of this title.
   C.   Not Allowed To Continue: The home occupation or small home business
license shall not be granted or allowed to continue if it is determined by the
planning and zoning commission or the town council that the conduct of such
home occupation or small business infringes upon the residential quality and
life of neighbors or immediate family or when it is determined that such
business or occupation becomes a nuisance and warrants moving to a commercial
area. (1987 Code § 17.72.030)
   D.   Prohibited Occupations:
      1.   Vehicle Repairs: Vehicle repair including the assembly or
disassembly of vehicle parts, paint and body work, and accessory components
installation is not permitted as a home occupation.
      2.   Retail Stores: Business where the primary function is the sale of
retail goods shall not be permitted as a home occupation.
   E.   Exemptions:
      1.   Criteria For Exemption: Any home occupation may be exempt from
obtaining a conditional use permit if the home occupation can meet all of the
following criteria:
         a.   Employees: In addition to family members residing in the dwelling
unit, only one person may be employed by the home occupation. (Ord. 8-94, 12-
15-1994)
         b.   Visual Indicators: No exterior display, no exterior storage of
materials, and no other exterior indication of the home occupation or variation
from the residential character of the principal or accessory building. Signs
for home occupations are allowed not to exceed twelve (12) square feet in size.
(Ord. 2011-15, 1-5-2012)
         c.   Environmental Contaminants: No home occupation shall emit odor,
dust, gas, noise, vibration, smoke, heat, glare, or other environmental
contaminants associated with the home occupation beyond any boundary of the lot
on which the home occupation is conducted.
         d.   Operating Hours: Activity shall be limited to the hours between
seven o'clock (7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M., except for home
occupation childcare facilities and those occupations which do not adversely
impact the neighborhood.
         e.   Operating Equipment: No mechanical equipment shall be used except
that normally used for domestic, hobby, standard office or household purposes.
         f.   Business License: A town business license is required for all
home occupations.
         g.   Parking: Any parking incidental to the home occupation shall be
provided on the site and must be improved.
         h.   Business Area: Not more than fifty percent (50%) of the total
area under the primary residential roof shall be used for any home occupation,
except for home occupation childcare facilities. Accessory buildings may be
used by approval of the planning and zoning commission.
         i.   Increased Traffic: Home occupations which generate business
traffic resulting in excess of eight (8) trips per day, or more than two (2)
vehicles at any one time, shall require approval of the planning and zoning
commission.
         j.   State Licensing: Home occupations requiring Wyoming state
licensing shall require planning and zoning approval. (Ord. 8-94, 12-15-1994)
      2.   Notice To Adjacent Property Owners: If an application for a home
occupation business complies with all the criteria of subsection E1 of this
section, the town shall notify, by letter, all adjacent property owners and
occupants. If no objections from those notified are received within fourteen
(14) days of the notification letter date, the business license may be issued
by the town clerk. (Ord. 8-94, 12-15-1994; amd. 2004 Code)
      3.   Commercial Zone: A home occupation located in the commercial zone is
not required to obtain a conditional use permit. A business license is still
required.
      4.   Criteria Requiring Permit: Any one of the following criteria shall
cause the home occupation to obtain a conditional use permit:
         a.   A written objection from an adjacent property owner when letters
are sent to all adjacent property owners;
         b.   Failure to comply with the criteria listed in subsection E1 of
this section;
         c.   The home occupation is located in an accessory building;
         d.   The home occupation generates business traffic in excess of eight
(8) trips per day, or more than two (2) vehicles at any one time;
         e.   The home occupation requires Wyoming state licensing; or
         f.   A written objection from any interested party who becomes aware
that the business does not comply with the criteria listed in subsection E1 of
this section.
      5.   Appeal: If an application for a business license for a home
occupation is denied, the applicant may appeal to the planning and zoning
commission. (Ord. 8-94, 12-15-1994)
12-12-4: MULTIPLE ANIMAL PERMITS:
Multiple animal permits as described and regulated in title 5, chapter 3,
article B of this code shall be conditionally permitted in any zone; provided,
that a conditional use permit as set forth in this chapter and a business
permit (if required) as set forth in title 3 of this code are first obtained.
Multiple animals shall be permitted in an A zone without a conditional use
permit, however, a business permit may still be required. (Ord. 2011-10, 8-4-
2011)
12-12-5: INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLES 1 :
   A.   Permit Required: Inoperable motor vehicles as described in title 6,
chapter 8 of this code shall be permitted in any zone; provided, that when
required, a conditional use permit as set forth in this chapter is first
obtained.
   B.   Conditions For Approval: A conditional use permit may be granted if the
applicant complies with all the following conditions:
      1.   All inoperable vehicles shall be kept in the rear or side yard;
      2.   All inoperable vehicles are kept in a safe condition;
      3.   All property owners within three hundred feet (300') of the subject
property have been notified and have been given opportunity to comment as
provided in this chapter; and
      4.   All but two (2) inoperable motor vehicles shall remain covered.
   C.   Additional Conditions: The planning and zoning commission may also
require any other reasonable conditions that will ensure that keeping the
inoperable vehicles will not be detrimental to the subject property,
surrounding properties, or the town. Such reasonable conditions may include
time limits, location requirements, coverings, etc. (Ord. 6-97, 1-8-1998, eff.
6-1-1998)
 
Notes
1 1. See also title 6, chapter 8 of this code.
12-12-6: GAMING:
   A.   Generally: No property shall be used as a gaming establishment except
as provided in this title. Any place where one or more gaming devices are found
is presumed to be intended for use as a gambling establishment.
   B.   Commercial Zone: Gaming establishments may only be located in areas
zoned commercial and they shall be a conditional use in that zone.
   C.   Application For Permit: A written application shall be made to the
planning and zoning commission as provided in section
12-12-7 of this chapter.
   D.   Signs; Parking: For sign and parking requirements, see chapters 8 and 9
of this title.
   E.   Exemptions: Gaming activities such as bingo, pulltabs, raffles, etc.,
used by nonprofit groups as fundraising activities where all the proceeds of
such activities go solely to the benefit of that nonprofit organization are
exempt from the conditional use requirements. (Ord. 6-94, 10-2-1994)
12-12-7: APPLICATION; FEE:
   A.   Application: Application for a conditional use permit shall be made by
the property owner or his authorized agent upon forms provided by the planning
and zoning commission. Accompanying an application shall be the following:
      1.   A map showing the property described in the application and
adjoining properties and public streets and ways within a radius of three
hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries.
      2.   A list of all property owners whose names and addresses appear on
the latest adopted tax roll as owning property within a distance of three
hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries.
      3.   Photographs, drawings and other supporting documents as may be
required by the planning and zoning commission.
   B.   Filing Fee: The planning and zoning commission shall charge and collect
a filing fee for each application, as determined by resolution of the town
council. (1987 Code § 17.72.040)
12-12-8: HEARING:
   A.   Required: The planning and zoning commission shall hold a public
hearing upon the application for a conditional use permit.
   B.   Notice Of Hearing:
      1.   Mail: Written notices concerning the hearing on an application for
conditional use permit shall be mailed to the owners of the property, and
occupants of property within a distance of three hundred feet (300') of the
exterior boundaries, not less than seven (7) days before the date of the public
hearing.
      2.   Publication: A public notice shall be printed in the official town
newspaper at least seven (7) days prior to the hearing.
      3.   Contents: The notice shall set forth the person requesting the
conditional use permit, the intent of the conditional use permit, the legal
description of the property, the street address, if applicable, any other
pertinent information, and the date, time and place of the public hearing.
(1987 Code § 17.72.050)
12-12-9: FINDINGS FOR APPROVAL:
The planning and zoning commission, in approving by an affirmative vote of not
less than a majority of the members attending and at which time a quorum is
present, shall find as follows:
   A.   Adequacy Of Site: The site for the proposed use is adequate in size,
shape, location, and topography to accommodate the use, and all yards, spaces,
walls and fences, parking, loading and landscaping are adequate to properly
adjust such use with the land and uses in the vicinity.
   B.   Adverse Effect On Abutting Property: The site for the proposed use will
have no adverse effect upon abutting property from the permitted use thereof,
nor will it conflict with the comprehensive general plan.
   C.   Adverse Effect From Use: The proposed use will have no adverse effect
upon abutting property from the permitted use thereof, nor will it conflict
with the comprehensive general plan.
   D.   General Conditions Imposed: The planning and zoning commission shall,
in addition to any special conditions, impose the following general conditions
upon every conditional use permit granted:
      1.   The right to a use an occupancy permit shall be contingent upon the
fulfillment of all general and special conditions imposed by the conditional
use permit procedure.
      2.   All of the special conditions shall constitute restrictions running
with the land and shall be binding upon the owner of the land, his successors
or assigns.
      3.   All of the special conditions shall be consented to, in writing, by
the applicants and all owners of interest and lien holders.
      4.   The vote granting the application, together with all consent forms,
shall be recorded by the town clerk or his authorized deputy.
      5.   Each permit shall be subject to yearly review.
   E.   Inspection: An on site inspection shall be made by the commission or
its authorized representative prior to a decision being rendered. (1987 Code §
17.72.060)
   F.   Limitations Or Modifications: In addition, and to further clarify those
listed in subsections A through E of this section, and by way of illustration,
but not limitation, the following criteria and such limitations or
modifications may be placed upon the conditional use permit to accentuate or
mitigate their impacts:
      1.   Street And Road Capacities: Street and road capacities on the
property and on public rights of way leading to and from the property.
      2.   Intensification Of Traffic Congestion Or Hazard: Intensification of
traffic congestion or hazard caused by the use which may be over and above
normal traffic for the area, as determined by the town or as advised by the
Wyoming department of transportation. Ingress and egress to adjoining public
streets, location and amount of off street parking, internal traffic
circulation systems.
      3.   Open Space: Usable open space, including area and height to be
occupied by buildings or other structures.
      4.   Density: Density for the proposed use in terms of units per acre and
the number of employees or both.
      5.   Volume Of Business: Volume of business in terms of the number of
customers per day.
      6.   Location And Use: Location and use with respect to the same or
similar uses in the immediate area.
      7.   Performance Standards: Noise, vibration, air pollution, and other
environmental influences.
      8.   Utility Capacity: Capacity of water, sewer, solid waste, electric,
telecommunication and other public and municipal systems.
      9.   Water Drainage: On site and off site surface water drainage
requirements.
      10.   Nearby Structures And Environmental Conditions: Landscaping,
architectural themes, including signs, of nearby structures and environmental
conditions.
      11.   Other Criteria: Any other criteria affecting public health, safety,
and welfare as provided for by the written rules of the planning and zoning
commission or town council. (Ord. 6-94, 10-20-1994)
12-12-10: APPEALS:
   A.   Right To Appeal: Written appeals may be reviewed by the town council,
by the applicant for a conditional use permit, or by any person owning property
within three hundred feet (300') of the exterior boundaries of the conditional
use permit applicant's property, who is aggrieved by a determination for a
conditional use permit, or upon failure of the planning and zoning commission
to make its determination on any application by (or at) the next regular
monthly planning and zoning commission meeting.
   B.   Hearing: The town council shall hold a public hearing as required by
Wyoming Statutes.
   C.   Board Of Adjustment: The town council shall perform all duties formerly
allocated to the board of adjustment under this title of the code. (1987 Code §
17.72.070)
12-12-11: REVOCATION OR MODIFICATION:
   A.   Grounds For Revocation Or Modification: A conditional use permit may be
revoked or modified by the planning and zoning commission, on any one or more
of the following grounds:
      1.   The approval was obtained by fraud.
      2.   The use for which such approval was granted is not being exercised
within the time specified in such permit.
      3.   The use for which such approval was granted has ceased to exist or
has been suspended for one year or more.
      4.   The permit granted is being, or recently has been, exercised
contrary to the terms or conditions of such approval, or in violation of any
statute, resolution, law or regulation.
      5.   The location or address of the use of the conditional use permit has
changed to a different location or address within the corporate limits of the
town.
      6.   The person holding the conditional use permit moves from the
corporate limits of the town.
      7.   The person holding the conditional use permit moves from the
corporate limits of the town, and the successor or assign to the location or
address wishes to continue the use granted by permit.
      8.   The conditional use permit has proven to be, as practiced,
detrimental to the development of the community, to the property abutting the
use, or to the community as a whole.
   B.   Notice Of Intent To Revoke: Written notices of intention to revoke
shall be mailed to the owners of the property and the occupants of property not
less than fifteen (15) days before the date of the planning and zoning
commission hearing addressing the revocation. (Ord. 2011-08, 6-2-2011)
   C.   Effect Of Revocation: The revocation of a conditional use permit shall
have the effect of denying all rights granted by the conditional use permit.
(1987 Code § 17.72.080)
   D.   Appeal: In the event of a revocation by the planning and zoning
commission, the applicant may appeal in the same manner as an appeal from a
denial of a conditional use permit in the first instance. (Ord. 2011-08, 6-2-
2011)
   E.   Annual Review: The planning and zoning commission shall annually review
all the conditional use permits active within the town. Holders of the
conditional use permits shall be notified by mail at the address listed on the
conditional use permit request as to their intentions to maintain the current
permit. Permit holders who do not respond, or respond that the conditional use
permit is no longer needed, may have their conditional use permits revoked
without further notice.
   F.   Grandfathering: No conditional use permit shall be deemed to remain in
effect solely for the reason that the conditional use permit was granted prior
to the date of any new ordinance governing such permits. (Ord. 2008-15, 7-17-
2008)
12-12-12: MODIFICATION OF APPROVED STRUCTURES:
Any proposed additions, enlargements or modifications of the structures
approved in any conditional use permit or any proposed extension of the use
into areas not approved in any such permit shall require a conditional use
permit. No building permit for such additions, enlargements, modifications or
extensions shall be issued unless the planning and zoning commission has
granted a conditional use permit therefor. (1987 Code § 17.72.090)
CHAPTER 13
AMENDMENTS; REZONES
SECTION:
12-13-1: Authority
12-13-2: Initiation
12-13-3: Planning And Zoning Commission Hearing And Action
12-13-4: Town Council Hearing And Action
12-13-1: AUTHORITY:
The town council, after a report thereon by the planning and zoning commission,
and after public hearings as required by law, may amend, supplement or change
the regulations and zoning districts established in this title or subsequently
established, and shall zone new annexed areas and unzoned areas within the
territorial jurisdiction of this title. (1987 Code § 17.76.010)
12-13-2: INITIATION:
   A.   Who May Initiate: An amendment, supplement, change or zoning of newly
annexed areas may be initiated by the town council, by the planning and zoning
commission, or by petition of property owners.
   B.   Request; Fee: Whenever the town council, the planning and zoning
commission, or owner of any land desires a reclassification of his property, or
a change of land use district or regulations pertaining to property, or zoning
of a newly annexed area, or zoning of any unzoned area within the territorial
jurisdiction of the town, a request shall be presented to the planning and
zoning commission. The form setting forth the request and related facts,
circumstances or information shall be filed with the secretary of the planning
and zoning commission, together with a fee as set by the town council. The
secretary shall acknowledge, in writing, receipt of the request and of the fee
and shall thereafter report the request to the planning and zoning commission
at its next regular meeting or special meeting following the date of filing.
(1987 Code § 17.76.020)
12-13-3: PLANNING AND ZONING COMMISSION HEARING AND ACTION:
   A.   Hearing: The planning and zoning commission shall hear the request
filed as provided in section
12-13-2 of this chapter and shall take such action as it deems necessary in
order to proceed with any studies, surveys, investigations or public hearings
as required by section 15-1-602, Wyoming Statutes Annotated, 1977 republished
edition.
   B.   Recommendations To Town Council: Following a public hearing, the
planning and zoning commission shall report its findings and recommendations to
the town council on the request, upon the boundaries of the district involved,
or such other matters as may be related to the request. (1987 Code § 17.76.030)
   C.   Rezoned And Unzoned Areas: All zone changes or zoning of all unzoned
areas shall be by resolution duly adopted by the town council after the town
council has received from the planning and zoning commission its report and
recommendation. (Ord. 2007-10, 5-1-2007)
12-13-4: TOWN COUNCIL HEARING AND ACTION:
The town council, after receipt of the report and recommendation from the
planning and zoning commission, shall hold at least one public hearing and/or
review the proceedings from the public hearing held by the planning and zoning
commission, and shall thereafter proceed by its action on the report and
recommendation, as provided by applicable Wyoming Statutes, and all zone
changes or zoning of all unzoned areas shall be by resolution duly adopted by
the town council. (Ord. 2007-10, 5-1-2007)
CHAPTER 14
ENFORCEMENT
SECTION:
12-14-1: Administrative Duty
12-14-2: Building Permits
12-14-3: Law Enforcement Agency Duties
12-14-4: Penalty
12-14-1: ADMINISTRATIVE DUTY:
It is the responsibility of the town council and its authorized agency, the
planning and zoning commission, to administer this title. (1987 Code §
17.80.010)
12-14-2: BUILDING PERMITS:
The purpose of this section is to provide for the safety, health and public
welfare through proof of structural strength and stability, means of egress,
adequate light and ventilation, and protection of life and property from fire
and hazards incident to the design, construction and alteration of buildings
and structures.
   A.   Building Code: The town council shall enforce the most recent edition
of the building code.
   B.   Application; Term: The building permit application shall be filled out
by the contractor, authorized agent, or owner of land, and submitted to the
town council for all building construction. Such permit becomes null and void
if work or construction authorized is not commenced within one hundred twenty
(120) days. (1987 Code § 17.80.020; amd. 2004 Code)
12-14-3: LAW ENFORCEMENT AGENCY DUTIES:
It is the duty of the law enforcement agency of the town charged with the
enforcement of the law to enforce all provisions of this title. (1987 Code §
17.80.030)
12-14-4: PENALTY:
No person shall locate, erect, construct, reconstruct, enlarge, change,
maintain or use any building or use any land in violation of this title. Unless
specifically set out in this title, any violation of this title constitutes a
class B misdemeanor punishable as set forth in subsection
1-4-1A2 of this code. (Ord. 2012-11, 1-17-2013)
